# E-Filing Technical/Portal Constraints -- Research Pass (50 states + federal)

> Generated 2026-07-02 as a fan-out research pass for the `pdf-suite-jurisdiction-rules` Blueprint.
> Scope: TECHNICAL/PORTAL constraints only (kind: "portal" in the JurisdictionPack schema) -- NOT
> formal rules of court. This file is Stage A + B of the Blueprint's verification pipeline
> (source triage + structured extraction with evidence). Every entry is tagged `needs-review`
> or `unverified` -- NONE are `verified`, because this is a single-pass automated research run.
> Per the Blueprint's decided policy, the extracting pass may never self-certify `verified`;
> that requires a separate independent review pass before any of this is translated into a
> shipped JSON pack and enabled for Prepare for Filing.
>
> Coverage: 51/51 jurisdictions returned a result in this pass (federal folded in from a separately-run, already-verified single-agent pass; see synthesis note below on how it factors into the counts).
>
> **Next step:** independent review (Stage C) of each entry, then translation into the
> per-jurisdiction JSON pack format, then jurisdiction-by-jurisdiction enablement.

## Executive synthesis

# Is "Always Convert to PDF/A + Always Scrub Metadata" a Safe Universal Default?

**No — not as a blind, unconditional default.** The data shows both actions are net-positive in most places but each has documented, named jurisdictions where they actively cause rejection or conflict. Coverage below is **50 jurisdictions, not 51** (50 states, no federal courts, no D.C.) — treat this as incomplete coverage, not a full national picture.

## PDF/A — counts (n=50)

| Stance | Count | Jurisdictions |
|---|---|---|
| Required | 2 | Louisiana, New York |
| Preferred | 5 | Connecticut, Florida, Kentucky, New Hampshire, Oregon |
| Silent | 41 | (no stated position either way) |
| Prohibited | 2 | Missouri, Tennessee |

**Missouri explicitly rejects PDF/A outright** — its own spec says PDF/A's archival protection layer trips the same ban as any encrypted/secured PDF. **Tennessee's Tyler Odyssey platform** rejects PDF/A with the identical error code used for non-PDF files. Beyond these two hard blocks, six more "silent" or "preferred" states carry a **documented technical landmine inside PDF/A conversion itself**: Georgia, Idaho, Minnesota, New Mexico, North Dakota, and Oregon all warn that PDF/A's standard practice of embedding fonts can embed unsupported font types (CID/JBIG), causing outright Format Error rejection — this is not theoretical, it's named in their own troubleshooting docs. Texas's own technical standard bans embedded fonts entirely while separately citing the ISO number for PDF/A-1 — an internal contradiction that makes PDF/A conversion risky there too. **Florida is the standout case**: PDF/A is "preferred," but Florida's own FAQ documents that PDF/A prohibits encryption, form fields, and annotations outright — meaning a naive PDF/A conversion can silently strip signatures, flatten forms, and invalidate redaction-via-annotation workflows.

## Metadata scrubbing — counts (n=50)

| Stance | Count | Jurisdictions |
|---|---|---|
| Required | 6 | Alaska, Arkansas, Indiana, Louisiana, Michigan, Montana |
| Recommended | 5 | Alabama, California, Minnesota, New Hampshire, Wisconsin |
| Silent | 38 | (no stated position either way) |
| Unverified | 1 | Texas |

Metadata scrubbing is much safer than PDF/A as a default — no jurisdiction prohibits it. But **Florida is the one documented conflict**: its own PDF/A conformance verifier requires retaining the `pdfcreator` metadata tag to pass PDF/A conformance checking, meaning a full metadata scrub can itself cause a file to *fail* PDF/A validation. This is the single clearest documented case of the two "always do this" defaults actively contradicting each other.

## Bottom line

Metadata scrubbing: safe as a default everywhere researched, with the single Florida caveat (don't strip `pdfcreator` if also converting to PDF/A). PDF/A conversion: **not safe as an unconditional default** — hard-block in 2 states, real rejection risk (font embedding) in at least 6 more, and a metadata/conformance conflict in a 7th (Florida). A filing tool should gate PDF/A behind jurisdiction-specific logic (allow-list where required/preferred, skip or warn in Missouri/Tennessee, strip non-standard embedded fonts everywhere PDF/A is attempted), not apply it blindly. The 41 "silent" PDF/A jurisdictions and 38 "silent" metadata jurisdictions are **unresearched-objection, not confirmed-safe** — absence of a found rule is not evidence no rule exists.

**Addendum on federal (added after this synthesis was written):** the PDF/A and metadata-scrub counts above are states-only (n=50); federal is reported separately below rather than folded into those tables, since the true CM/ECF constraint that matters -- maximum file size -- varies per court and has no single national number, and its PDF/A and metadata stances are both `silent` (accepted but not required, and unaddressed, respectively) at the national level. `silent` is not evidence of safety there either -- see the federal section for two additional rejection causes (un-flattened form fields, embedded vendor logo/links) that PDF/A conversion and metadata scrubbing would likely help avoid in practice, even though neither is a stated national requirement.


---

# Federal

## Federal (CM/ECF national baseline)

- **E-filing system:** CM/ECF (Case Management/Electronic Case Files), current generation "NextGen CM/ECF" (vendor: Administrative Office of the U.S. Courts (AOC) — developed and maintained in-house, not a third-party commercial e-filing vendor)
- **Statewide system:** yes (national baseline)
- **Notes:** CM/ECF is not one single monolithic portal -- it is standardized software developed and issued nationally by the AOC, but deployed as a separate instance per court (each of the 94 district courts, the bankruptcy courts, and the courts of appeals runs its own CM/ECF instance, with some parameters -- notably maximum file size -- individually configurable per court). This research targeted only the AOC's own national technical documentation and PACER's national FAQ, and deliberately excluded any single district's local rules or general orders, consistent with the Blueprint's decision to ship one national baseline pack for v1 rather than per-district precision.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://pacer.uscourts.gov/sites/default/files/files/AC_DC_BC_0160ECF_PDF_Functionality.pdf)
  > The AOC's own national PDF-content-criteria list explicitly places PDF/A on the ACCEPTED side (not the rejected side) of the system's upload check, with no caveats about encryption conflicts, form-field stripping, or redaction/annotation problems. It does not affirmatively recommend or prefer PDF/A over an ordinary PDF -- it is simply one of several listed content types that will not be rejected.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://pacer.uscourts.gov/sites/default/files/files/AC_DC_BC_0160ECF_PDF_Functionality.pdf)
  > The AOC's national PDF-Related Functionality document does not mention metadata at all. Note: near-identical metadata-scrubbing advisory language recurs verbatim across several individual district/court CM/ECF FAQ pages (e.g. D.N.J., Court of International Trade, C.D. Cal.), suggesting widely shared boilerplate -- but that recurring text was excluded here as evidence for the national baseline since it is court-local, not national.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size (per document)**: No fixed national number -- each individual court configures its own maximum PDF file size in its CM/ECF instance; any PDF larger than that court's configured limit is rejected by the system itself. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://pacer.uscourts.gov/sites/default/files/files/AC_DC_BC_0160ECF_PDF_Functionality.pdf)
    > Each court determines the maximum file size for the PDF. Any PDF larger than the maximum file size will be rejected by the system. To find the current file size limit: In CM/ECF, from the Startup Page, click the Court Information link.
  - **Oversize-document workaround**: No separate envelope-level cap is defined nationally. The prescribed mechanism for an oversized filing is to split it into smaller PDFs filed together as one docket event: one main document plus the rest attached as separate attachments. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://pacer.uscourts.gov/sites/default/files/files/AC_DC_BC_0160ECF_PDF_Functionality.pdf)
    > If you have a document or filing that is larger than the maximum file size defined by the court, you can break the document or filing into smaller PDF documents and file those smaller PDF documents together in one event, with a main document and the remaining documents as separate attachments to the main document.
  - **Corroborating file-size guidance (PACER national FAQ)**: PACER's own national FAQ confirms the same decentralized model directly to filers: courts, not the national system, set the number, and the remedy for an oversized document is to split it. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://pacer.uscourts.gov/help/faqs/there-limit-size-pdf-files-which-cmecf-will-accept)
    > Each court sets a limit on the size of PDF files submitted for electronic filing. ... If a document exceeds the limit, the recommendation is to break the document into separate, smaller documents.
  - **Accepted file format**: CM/ECF only accepts PDF. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.uscourts.gov/court-records/file-a-case-cm-ecf/faqs-case-management-electronic-case-files-cm-ecf)
    > CM/ECF systems are designed to accept only documents in PDF format.
  - **PDF version / format-compliance requirement**: No specific PDF version number is named (e.g. 1.4, 1.7, 2.0). The spec only requires that a PDF "comply with PDF format standards" generally -- version-agnostic, not a pinned number. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://pacer.uscourts.gov/sites/default/files/files/AC_DC_BC_0160ECF_PDF_Functionality.pdf)
    > PDFs with the following content will be rejected: Does not comply with PDF format standards
  - **PDF/A acceptance (content-criteria list)**: PDF/A-standard files are explicitly listed among content the system WILL accept, alongside OCR'd text and plain scanned documents -- with no caveat noted about encryption, forms, redaction, or annotations being affected by PDF/A conversion specifically. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://pacer.uscourts.gov/sites/default/files/files/AC_DC_BC_0160ECF_PDF_Functionality.pdf)
    > PDFs with the following content will be accepted: ... Meets the PDF-A standard ... Contains optical character recognition (OCR) meta-data ... Comprised of scanned documents.
  - **Searchable text / OCR requirement**: Not required nationally -- both OCR'd (searchable) content and plain (non-OCR) scanned documents are explicitly listed as accepted content types. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://pacer.uscourts.gov/sites/default/files/files/AC_DC_BC_0160ECF_PDF_Functionality.pdf)
    > Contains optical character recognition (OCR) meta-data ... Comprised of scanned documents. NOTE: Local courts may stipulate acceptable dots-per-inch (dpi) standards.
  - **Prohibited PDF content (rejected on upload)**: The national system itself -- not merely local court rules -- technically rejects a PDF that: does not comply with PDF format standards; contains JavaScript; is encrypted or password-protected; contains scripts that can launch an external application; contains internal (embedded) attachments; contains audio/video content; or was created via specific Mac OS X Safari-fillable-form or Word "Best for printing" export paths. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://pacer.uscourts.gov/sites/default/files/files/AC_DC_BC_0160ECF_PDF_Functionality.pdf)
    > PDFs with the following content will be rejected: Does not comply with PDF format standards; Contains JavaScript; Encrypted or password-protected; Contains scripts which can launch an external application; Contains internal attachments; Contains audio and video content; Created with Mac OS X using a fillable form in the Safari browser; Created with Mac OS X using MS Word and selecting the option, "Best for printing"
  - **Editable/fillable forms -- flattening requirement**: Fillable-form PDFs are accepted by the CM/ECF system itself, but a common cause of the "system does not recognize my PDF" upload error is exactly an un-flattened form field -- PACER's own troubleshooting FAQ instructs filers to flatten the form before filing. The appellate CM/ECF instance in particular can additionally be configured to reject editable forms outright regardless of flattening. This is directly relevant to Prepare for Filing: form-flattening (which PDF/A conversion effectively performs as a side effect) removes one of the most common real-world rejection causes. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://pacer.uscourts.gov/help/faqs/trying-e-file-getting-error-message-does-not-recognize-my-pdf-why-error-occurring)
    > The PDF may be form-fillable and needs to be flattened so that it cannot be edited or altered by other users. / Contains editable forms will be accepted by the system but may be rejected by court policy. NOTE: Appellate CM/ECF may be configured to reject PDFs with editable forms.
  - **Embedded vendor marks/logos with links -- rejection cause**: The same national troubleshooting FAQ names a second common rejection cause distinct from file-size or form issues: a PDF containing an embedded mark or logo that links back to the site of the software that produced the file. This is exactly the kind of producer/vendor artifact that a metadata-and-embedded-object scrub would remove. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://pacer.uscourts.gov/help/faqs/trying-e-file-getting-error-message-does-not-recognize-my-pdf-why-error-occurring)
    > make sure the PDF does not contain marks or logos with links to the site of the company that developed the product, as the court will not accept these files.
  - **Attachment count / multi-part filing mechanism**: No fixed national cap on the number of attachments is stated. The mechanism is: one main document plus any number of additional PDF attachments in the same docket event, each still bound by that court's per-document size limit. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://pacer.uscourts.gov/sites/default/files/files/AC_DC_BC_0160ECF_PDF_Functionality.pdf)
    > you can break the document or filing into smaller PDF documents and file those smaller PDF documents together in one event, with a main document and the remaining documents as separate attachments to the main document

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Exact numeric maximum attachment count per filing -- appears to be per-court configuration, not a system-wide number., Filename character-set and length restrictions -- no national AOC document found stating a specific limit., Bookmark or table-of-contents requirements -- not addressed in national CM/ECF technical documentation., A codified national metadata policy -- the AOC's national document is silent; a scrub-recommendation recurs on individual district FAQ pages but is out of scope as non-national.

---

# States

## Alabama (statewide)

- **E-filing system:** AlaFile (vendor: On-Line Information Services (OLIS), Mobile, AL — under a long-term (15-year) contract with the Alabama Administrative Office of Courts covering the Alacourt/AlaFile/AlaVault/AlaPay suite (per news reporting; not independently confirmed against an AOC primary source, so treat as background context rather than a verified constraint))
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Alabama runs ONE mandatory statewide e-filing system, not a county-by-county model. AlaFile (at alafile.alacourt.gov, with policy/FAQ/manual hosted at efile.alacourt.gov) is administered by the Alabama Administrative Office of Courts (AOC) and governs civil-division electronic filing across the entire Alabama Unified Judicial System. Electronic filing was authorized statewide by a 2008 amendment to the Alabama Rules of Civil Procedure, and e-filing (registration and use) was made mandatory for licensed Alabama attorneys by an April 12, 2011 administrative order, effective as an E-filing Mandate on October 1, 2012. The canonical governing document is 'Administrative Policies and Procedures for Electronic Filing in the Civil Divisions of the Alabama Unified Judicial System,' most recently revised February 27, 2026 — this is the closest thing Alabama has to a technical-specifications page and was the primary source for this research, supplemented by the live FAQ and the AlaFile User Manual (most recent copy found dated January 29, 2020; an older 2018 and 2012 revision also exist online, and manual content on file-size limits should defer to the newer, authoritative Administrative Policies doc). Note: certain document types are categorically barred from e-filing regardless of technical compliance (documents filed under seal, Rule 32 post-conviction petitions, exhibits offered at trial, documents/exhibits that cannot be scanned into PDF such as video/audio tapes or large maps, etc.) — this is a filing-eligibility rule, not a PDF/portal technical constraint, but worth flagging for RaioPDF's e-filing-prep feature so it doesn't imply universal e-filing eligibility.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://efile.alacourt.gov/media/1118/administrative-policies-and-procedures-02-27-2026.pdf)
  > PDF/A is never mentioned in any of the three official sources reviewed — not the Administrative Policies and Procedures document (which does define plain 'PDF' and lays out a dedicated 'TECHNICAL SPECIFICATIONS' section), not the FAQ, and not a full-text search of the 113-page AlaFile User Manual. The system's own definition of accepted format stops at generic PDF: 'The term "PDF" refers to portable document format. A PDF document allows anyone to open the converted document across a broad range of hardware and software, with layout, format, links, and images intact.' There is no requirement, preference, or warning of any kind regarding the PDF/A archival substandard, and correspondingly no indication that PDF/A conversion causes encryption, form-field, or redaction/annotation problems in AlaFile — that scenario is simply never raised.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** recommended -- [source](https://efile.alacourt.gov/faqs/)
  > The official FAQ has a dedicated question instructing filers to strip hidden metadata from word-processor files before conversion/filing, pointing to Microsoft's own metadata-removal documentation. This is guidance/best-practice framing, not a stated mandatory filing requirement enforced by the portal (i.e., AlaFile does not reject a file for having metadata) — but it is an explicit, official recommendation to scrub, with no countervailing warning that scrubbed files cause any problem.

**Constraints found:**
  - **maxFileSizePerDocument**: 10 MB maximum per uploaded document/attachment. Files over 10MB are rejected by AlaFile and must either be filed conventionally (paper) with the clerk or split into multiple 10MB segments, each filed as a separate attachment. The rule is stated per-document/per-file; no distinct, separately-stated 'envelope' or whole-submission cap was found beyond this per-file limit. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efile.alacourt.gov/media/1118/administrative-policies-and-procedures-02-27-2026.pdf)
    > Because large documents may not upload properly to the system or download within a reasonable amount of time for users with a 56K modem, documents over ten (10) megabytes will be rejected by the system and must be filed conventionally, or in ten (10) megabyte segments as attachments.
  - **maxFileSizePerDocument_corroboration**: The public FAQ independently states the same 10MB ceiling in plain terms, confirming this is the live, current-operation number (not just legacy policy-doc text). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efile.alacourt.gov/faqs/)
    > What is the size limit of the document that can be filed? The maximum size limit that can be filed is 10MB.
  - **acceptedFileFormatPdfVersion**: PDF is the required upload format — documents must be converted from word-processing software to PDF, or scanned and converted to PDF. No specific PDF version (e.g., 1.4, 1.7) or PDF sub-standard is specified anywhere in the reviewed official materials. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efile.alacourt.gov/media/1118/administrative-policies-and-procedures-02-27-2026.pdf)
    > The ability to convert documents from word processing software to PDF. ... The term "PDF" refers to portable document format. A PDF document allows anyone to open the converted document across a broad range of hardware and software, with layout, format, links, and images intact.
  - **searchableTextOcrRequirement**: No searchable-text/OCR requirement exists. The only image-quality rule governs visual legibility of scanned pages, not text-searchability: scanners must be set to 200 dpi, black-and-white (not color), and the filer bears responsibility for legibility. A document that can't be made legible must be filed on paper instead of e-filed — there is no instruction anywhere to run OCR or to ensure the resulting PDF contains a text layer. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efile.alacourt.gov/media/1118/administrative-policies-and-procedures-02-27-2026.pdf)
    > When scanning documents to be filed electronically, filing parties should make certain their scanners are configured for 200 dpi and black and white, rather than color, scanning. The filing party is responsible for the legibility of the scanned document. If for any reason a document cannot be easily read after scanning, the filing party should not electronically file the document. Instead, the filing party must file the document conventionally with the clerk's office.
  - **attachmentCountLimit**: No explicit numeric cap on the number of attachments per filing was found in any reviewed source. The governing document affirmatively contemplates multiple attachments per envelope — it directs filers to split an oversized document into several 10MB segments 'as attachments' rather than capping how many pieces that can become — and the AlaFile User Manual's per-case-type workflows likewise route ancillary documents (e.g., a Waiver of Service, a Proposed Order) in as additional attachments alongside a primary filing without stating a maximum count. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efile.alacourt.gov/media/1118/administrative-policies-and-procedures-02-27-2026.pdf)
    > ...documents over ten (10) megabytes will be rejected by the system and must be filed conventionally, or in ten (10) megabyte segments as attachments.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Filename character/length restrictions — not addressed in the Administrative Policies and Procedures for Electronic Filing (Rev. 2026-02-27), the AlaFile FAQ (efile.alacourt.gov/faqs), or a full-text search of the AlaFile User Manual (Rev. 2020-01-29, 113 pages). None of the three official sources impose or even mention a filename convention., Bookmark or table-of-contents requirements — no mention found in any of the three official AlaFile sources reviewed (Administrative Policies and Procedures, FAQ, or User Manual). Given the manual walks through document upload for dozens of filing types without ever raising bookmarks, this looks like a genuinely unaddressed topic rather than a search miss, but no source affirmatively states 'no bookmarks required,' so it is listed as a gap rather than a confirmed 'silent' constraint., Separate per-envelope/whole-submission size cap distinct from the per-document 10MB limit — sources state the 10MB ceiling applies to each uploaded document/attachment; whether AlaFile also enforces a separate aggregate cap across all attachments in one filing was not found.

---

## Alaska (statewide — Alaska Court System / Administrative Office of the Courts, all Trial Courts)

- **E-filing system:** TrueFiling — Alaska's branded instance of the platform is called "AKFile" (akfile.truefiling.com) (vendor: TrueFiling, with technical support delivered through i3Verticals (the User Guide names "i3Verticals, the TrueFiling vendor"))
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Confirmed: Alaska runs ONE single, mandatory, statewide e-filing platform (TrueFiling/AKFile) operated centrally by the Alaska Court System — this is NOT a fragmented county-by-county model like California's Electronic Filing Service Provider system. Alaska's unified judiciary (no separate county trial courts) makes a single statewide vendor the natural architecture, and the User Guide confirms this ("The Alaska Court System is in the process of deploying TrueFiling... This user guide provides additional instructions on how to use TrueFiling for filing cases and documents with the Alaska Trial Courts"). Rollout is phased BY CASE TYPE AND COURT LOCATION, not by jurisdiction-selected vendor — e.g., Delinquency cases went statewide 2026-03-09, CINA cases transition 2026-08-17, Probate is planned by end of 2026, and confidential/sealed/not-published case types are permanently excluded from TrueFiling (must be filed by email/mail/hand-delivery). Attorneys registered with the Alaska Bar and most self-represented litigants are mandated to use TrueFiling (Administrative Bulletin 92), under Supreme Court Order 1943's provisional eFiling rules.

Terminology note: TrueFiling uses "bundle" (not "envelope") for a collection of documents submitted together in one transaction.

Important scoping note: A separate, OLDER, non-TrueFiling channel exists — "File New Cases and Motions by Email or Fax" (courts.alaska.gov/courtdir/efiling.htm) — for court locations/situations where TrueFiling isn't used. That page states its OWN limits (10MB per email, PDF "if possible," and a 30-page fax limit for exhibits) which are NOT TrueFiling portal constraints and must not be conflated with them; I deliberately excluded those from the constraints below since they describe a different (legacy, non-portal) submission channel, not the TrueFiling software itself. The 30-page figure also appears inside the TrueFiling User Guide itself only in the context of faxing trial exhibits that were never accepted into TrueFiling in the first place ("physically mailed... faxed (30-page limit)... " — Section "Proposed Jury Instructions and Exhibits"), again not a TrueFiling upload constraint.

Primary source used throughout: Alaska TrueFiling User Guide, Version Date: March 6, 2026, https://courts.alaska.gov/efile/docs/userguide.pdf — read in full (all 25 pages, Sections 1 through 31 and Appendices A-C).
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://courts.alaska.gov/efile/docs/userguide.pdf)
  > PDF/A is never mentioned anywhere in the 25-page TrueFiling User Guide (Version Date: March 6, 2026), which was read in full — every numbered section and all three appendices. The guide's only file-format guidance is: avoid scanning when possible and instead upload the native electronic file "in its original file format (i.e., Microsoft Word or Adobe PDF)," and if scanning is genuinely unavoidable, scan at a minimum of 300 DPI. There is no statement requiring, preferring, or warning against PDF/A conversion, and no mention of encryption conflicts, form-field stripping, or annotation/redaction issues tied to PDF/A specifically. The only format-adjacent prohibition found is unrelated to PDF/A: "Document Management Rights must be removed before filing through TrueFiling. The court is unable to view documents with management rights and the filings will be rejected" (see metadata field below) — this is about DRM/permission locks, not PDF/A.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** required -- [source](https://courts.alaska.gov/efile/docs/userguide.pdf)
  > The User Guide requires removal of "Document Management Rights" before filing, framed as an outright filing-rejection risk: "IMPORTANT: Document Management Rights must be removed before filing through TrueFiling. The court is unable to view documents with management rights and the filings will be rejected." (Section 9, "Document Size and Quality," p.10). Caveat for RaioPDF's purposes: this is specifically about DRM/permission-lock removal (e.g., Microsoft Information Rights Management or PDF security restrictions that block the court's viewer from opening the file) — it is NOT a statement about scrubbing ordinary descriptive metadata fields (author, company, revision history, comments/tracked changes, GPS/creation data). The Guide never separately addresses whether descriptive metadata should be removed, preserved, or is a non-issue; only the DRM/permission-lock removal is explicitly mandatory.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size (per document)**: 10.0 MB per individual document. Documents that exceed this must be split and filed as separate documents labeled 'Part 1, Part 2,' etc. No separate/distinguished limit is stated for a total bundle (Alaska's term for an envelope) beyond the sum of its per-document parts. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://courts.alaska.gov/efile/docs/userguide.pdf)
    > A single document filed in TrueFiling may not exceed 10.0 megabytes. Documents exceeding that size must be filed as separate documents labeled Part 1, Part 2, etc.
  - **Accepted PDF version / file format requirements**: No specific PDF version number (e.g., 1.4/1.7/2.0) is specified anywhere. Native electronic files should be uploaded 'in its original file format' — explicitly naming both Microsoft Word and Adobe PDF as acceptable formats (i.e., Word documents are accepted directly, not just PDF). Scanning is discouraged in favor of native files; where scanning is unavoidable, minimum 300 DPI resolution is required. Electronic signatures use the '/s/ [name]' convention rather than a digital-certificate signature block. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://courts.alaska.gov/efile/docs/userguide.pdf)
    > Avoid filing scanned documents when possible. If the document is generated electronically, apply an electronic signature (/s/ [name]) and upload it directly into TrueFiling in its original file format (i.e., Microsoft Word or Adobe PDF). If you must scan the document, scan it at a high-quality resolution (minimum 300 DPI).
  - **Searchable-text / OCR requirement**: No requirement for OCR or text-searchability is stated anywhere. The Guide instead pushes filers away from scanned images entirely ('Avoid filing scanned documents when possible'), and only imposes a quality floor — minimum 300 DPI — for the cases where scanning genuinely cannot be avoided. There is no mention of a searchable-text mandate, an OCR pass, or rejection for non-searchable scans. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://courts.alaska.gov/efile/docs/userguide.pdf)
    > Avoid filing scanned documents when possible... If you must scan the document, scan it at a high-quality resolution (minimum 300 DPI).
  - **Filename character restrictions**: The 'Filing Name' field accepts only: A-Z, 0-9, underscores (_), spaces, periods (.), hyphens (-), and apostrophes ('). Mixed case is required — filers are told not to capitalize every word. Filers must also replace their saved document's filename with the actual document title if the two differ (e.g., replace 'Smith.Modification' with 'Motion to Modify Alaska Child Support Order'). No numeric length/character-count limit is stated (see gaps). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://courts.alaska.gov/efile/docs/userguide.pdf)
    > Filing Names can only include certain characters: A to Z, 0 to 9, underscores (_), spaces, periods (.), hyphens (-), and apostrophes ('). ... Do not capitalize all words in the Filing Name, used mixed case.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Maximum file size per envelope/'bundle' (as distinct from the confirmed 10.0 MB per-document cap) — not addressed anywhere in the User Guide; only the per-document limit is stated., Filename length limit (maximum character count) — the User Guide specifies an allowed character SET (see constraints) but never states a maximum length., Bookmark or table-of-contents requirement — not mentioned anywhere in the 25-page User Guide (no bookmark, TOC, or document-navigation requirement of any kind was found)., Attachment/document count limit per filing or per bundle — no maximum is stated; the Guide describes multi-document 'bundles' (e.g., motion + confidential attachment + proposed order as three separate uploads) without ever capping how many documents a bundle may contain.

---

## Arizona

- **E-filing system:** Fragmented by court level/case type, not one unified portal. Two applications are each labeled "statewide" by the AOC: (1) eFileAZ (efile.azcourts.gov) — the primary Superior Court e-filing application, used for most case types (civil, family, probate, some criminal/juvenile) in all counties except certain Maricopa case types; (2) AZTurboCourt (azturbocourt.gov, run on the TurboCourt platform) — mandatory for the Arizona Supreme Court and Court of Appeals, Division One, and separately available statewide as an optional path for Superior Court civil-case filings, for Maricopa County tax cases, and for process-server filings in Maricopa/Pima. On top of those two: (3) the Court of Appeals, Division Two runs its own "e-filer" application (appeals2.az.gov) that is explicitly NOT statewide and is managed independently by that court; and (4) Maricopa County Superior Court runs its own local e-filing system for criminal and juvenile-delinquency filings, the two case types eFileAZ does not cover there. So: no single statewide mandatory portal — a filer's system depends on court level, county, and case type. (vendor: Mixed / not fully identified. AZTurboCourt runs on the "TurboCourt" platform (hosted at dss.turbocourt.com — a commercial legal-forms/e-filing vendor used by multiple states). eFileAZ's underlying vendor is not named in its own User's Guide (the cover page has a "Powered by:" line with a vendor logo that did not extract as text); no vendor attribution was found in the guide body. Court of Appeals Division Two's "e-filer" vendor was not researched in this pass.)
- **Statewide system:** no -- fragmented/county-by-county
- **Notes:** Arizona is a middle case between "one statewide portal" (e.g., Florida) and "fully county-procured" (e.g., California): it has multiple AOC-sanctioned statewide-scope applications rather than per-county vendor choice, but which application a filer uses depends on court level and case type, and two carve-outs (COA Division Two, Maricopa criminal/juvenile) sit entirely outside the two main statewide apps. Primary sources for this research: the official azcourts.gov eFiling Information pages (current, last updated April 2026) for system identification/availability, plus the AOC's own eFileAZ User's Guide (V2.0, Jan 2017) and AZTurboCourt Statewide User Manual (V3.9, 2015) / FAQ (2012) for technical specs — the latter two are dated but are still the live, linked documentation on the official azcourts.gov/turbocourt.com domains and were the only primary technical-spec sources found. The AZTurboCourt manual reproduces two Arizona Supreme Court Administrative Orders (2011-40 for Maricopa Superior Court, 2012-02 for the Supreme Court/Court of Appeals Div. One) as appendices; these are cited here only for their "Technical Format and Size" / bookmark provisions (portal-technical content), not for any substantive filing-procedure rule.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://efile.azcourts.gov/Help/eFile%20Users%20Guide%20V2-0%20Jan%202017.pdf)
  > No source mentions PDF/A anywhere. Both eFileAZ's "Document Formats and Size" section and AZTurboCourt's "Technical Format and Size" provisions (in the FAQ, the Statewide User Manual, and the reproduced Administrative Orders 2011-40/2012-02) describe format requirements in detail — container format, size caps, password prohibition — without a single PDF/A reference, positive or negative. Treated as genuine silence rather than an unresearched gap because these are the sections that would be expected to state a PDF/A rule if one existed.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://dss.turbocourt.com/manuals/az/AZTurboCourt%20Statewide%20User%20Manual%20No%20Pima%203.9_HF.pdf)
  > No mention of metadata (inclusion or removal) appears in the eFileAZ User's Guide, the AZTurboCourt Statewide User Manual, or the AZTurboCourt FAQ — including within the detailed "Technical Format and Size" provisions of the reproduced Administrative Orders governing e-filing format for Maricopa Superior Court and the appellate courts. Neither a requirement nor a warning against metadata-scrubbed files was found.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Max file size per document — eFileAZ (Superior Court, most counties/case types)**: 9.5 MB per document per the detailed submission instructions (repeated three times in the guide); the guide's own general summary section states 9 MB instead — a minor internal inconsistency in the same document _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efile.azcourts.gov/Help/eFile%20Users%20Guide%20V2-0%20Jan%202017.pdf)
    > Documents may not be larger in size than 9.5mb.
  - **Max file size per submission/envelope — eFileAZ**: 100 MB total per submission _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efile.azcourts.gov/Help/eFile%20Users%20Guide%20V2-0%20Jan%202017.pdf)
    > Submission’s total size may be no larger than 100MB.
  - **Max file size per document/attachment — AZTurboCourt (AZ Supreme Court, Court of Appeals Div. One, and optional statewide Superior Court civil filings)**: 10 MB per lead document and per attachment; no separate combined-envelope/total cap was found documented for AZTurboCourt _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.azcourts.gov/Portals/0/21/AZTC%20FAQs/2ndAMENDED%20AZTC%20ADDITIONAL%20FREQUENTLY%20ASKED%20QUESTIONS_NM.doc)
    > Each lead document and required attachment cannot exceed 10 MB.
  - **Accepted file formats — eFileAZ**: PDF, DOCX, or ODT for standard documents; Proposed Orders, Proposed Judgments, and Proposed Notices of Hearing must be DOCX or ODT (PDF not accepted for those). No password protection or other security devices allowed; documents must be virus-free or the submission is auto-rejected. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efile.azcourts.gov/Help/eFile%20Users%20Guide%20V2-0%20Jan%202017.pdf)
    > Documents may be in PDF, DOCX or ODT formats. Proposed Orders, Proposed Judgments, and Proposed Notice of Hearing documents must be in DOCX or ODT.
  - **Accepted file formats — AZTurboCourt (Maricopa County Superior Court civil filings)**: Main/lead document must be PDF; a proposed order must instead be submitted as MS Word 97-2003 .DOC (not .DOCX, not PDF) _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://dss.turbocourt.com/manuals/az/AZTurboCourt%20Statewide%20User%20Manual%20No%20Pima%203.9_HF.pdf)
    > The document must be in PDF (except proposed order must be in DOC).
  - **Accepted file formats — AZTurboCourt (Arizona Supreme Court / Court of Appeals Division One)**: DOCX, PDF, or ODT accepted; courts prefer DOCX. The reproduced Administrative Order 2012-02 states the same rule as a formal technical-format requirement. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://dss.turbocourt.com/manuals/az/AZTurboCourt%20Statewide%20User%20Manual%20No%20Pima%203.9_HF.pdf)
    > The document must be in DOCX, PDF, or ODT. The courts prefer documents be filed in DOCX.
  - **Searchable-text / OCR requirement — AZTurboCourt**: AZTurboCourt's own FAQ lists creating a text-searchable PDF/DOCX/ODT as a required step in its summary of "the process for filing a document electronically," and separately walks filers through converting scanned documents into text-searchable PDFs. Framed as a mandatory workflow step rather than an explicit auto-rejection rule. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.azcourts.gov/Portals/0/21/AZTC%20FAQs/2ndAMENDED%20AZTC%20ADDITIONAL%20FREQUENTLY%20ASKED%20QUESTIONS_NM.doc)
    > Create a document that is either a text searchable .pdf, .docx or .odt format.
  - **Filename / field character limits — AZTurboCourt (Maricopa Superior Court and AZ Supreme Court / COA Div. One filings)**: Document title/description field: 256-character limit. Attach-main-document filename field: 75-character limit — exceeding it requires renaming the file locally and reattaching. Filers are told not to use special characters or abbreviations in the filename. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://dss.turbocourt.com/manuals/az/AZTurboCourt%20Statewide%20User%20Manual%20No%20Pima%203.9_HF.pdf)
    > The title/description field has a character limit of 256. Attach main document field has a character limit of 75. If you exceed this limit, you need to save your document with a shorter title and reattach. Do not add any special characters or abbreviate.
  - **Bookmark / table-of-contents requirement — AZTurboCourt (Arizona Supreme Court / Court of Appeals Division One)**: Bookmarking to another page within the same document is permitted but optional in general. However, when a single document contains multiple exhibits or attachments, a bookmarked index or table of contents to those exhibits/attachments is REQUIRED. This mandatory clause is in the appellate-court Administrative Order (2012-02); the parallel Maricopa Superior Court order (2011-40) reproduced in the same manual contains only the permissive bookmark sentence, without the mandatory-TOC clause — i.e., the requirement differs by court within the same AZTurboCourt platform. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://dss.turbocourt.com/manuals/az/AZTurboCourt%20Statewide%20User%20Manual%20No%20Pima%203.9_HF.pdf)
    > When multiple exhibits or attachments are contained in a document, the document shall contain a bookmarked index or table of contents to these exhibits or attachments.
  - **Attachment count limit — AZTurboCourt (Maricopa County Superior Court filings)**: One main/lead document per submission in this flow, plus up to 25 supporting-attachment slots for exhibits and/or a proposed order, each capped at 10 MB _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://dss.turbocourt.com/manuals/az/AZTurboCourt%20Statewide%20User%20Manual%20No%20Pima%203.9_HF.pdf)
    > You have 25 attachment options for exhibits and or proposed orders. Each attachment can be up to 10 MB.
  - **Lead-document count limit — AZTurboCourt (general / appellate filings)**: Up to 4 lead documents may be included in a single submission, each with its own required attachments _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.azcourts.gov/Portals/0/21/AZTC%20FAQs/2ndAMENDED%20AZTC%20ADDITIONAL%20FREQUENTLY%20ASKED%20QUESTIONS_NM.doc)
    > A submission may include up to 4 lead documents plus their required attachments such as a certificate of service.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Exact accepted PDF version number (e.g. PDF 1.4 / 1.7 / 2.0) — neither eFileAZ nor AZTurboCourt documentation specifies a PDF version; both only require the PDF container format generally., eFileAZ: filename character/length restrictions — not addressed anywhere in the official eFileAZ User's Guide (only AZTurboCourt documents a 75-character filename limit and a 256-character title/description limit)., eFileAZ: fixed numeric attachment-count limit — the guide instructs filers to split an oversized document into a 'lead' document plus separate 'connected' documents, but never states a maximum number of attachments per submission., eFileAZ: bookmark/table-of-contents requirement — not addressed in the eFileAZ User's Guide., eFileAZ: searchable-text/OCR requirement — not addressed in the eFileAZ User's Guide (only AZTurboCourt's FAQ raises text-searchability)., Court of Appeals, Division Two's independent 'e-filer' application (appeals2.az.gov) — explicitly not a statewide system; its technical specs (file size, format, OCR, filenames, bookmarks, attachment limits, metadata) were not located within this pass's bounded search effort., Maricopa County Superior Court's own local e-filing system for criminal and juvenile-delinquency filings (the case types eFileAZ does not cover there) — a distinct system from eFileAZ/AZTurboCourt; its technical specs were not located within this pass's bounded search effort., Whether the AZTurboCourt Statewide User Manual (dated 2015, v3.9) and FAQ (dated 2012) reflect the platform's current technical limits, or whether these figures have since changed — no more recent AOC-published version of either document was found during this search.

---

## Arkansas

- **E-filing system:** eFlex — Arkansas's single statewide e-filing platform run by the Administrative Office of the Courts (AOC), reached via efile.arcourts.gov / eflex.arcourts.gov (legacy domain: efile.aoc.arkansas.gov) (vendor: Tybera Development Group, Inc. (per copyright line on the official filer's guide))
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Arkansas is NOT fragmented like California. Administrative Order 21 established one statewide e-filing system (eFlex, built by Tybera) that the AOC contracts for and rolls out court-by-court — a court becomes eligible once it's on the "Contexte" case management system (with Contexte internal imaging and accounting). Per an official AOC training slide (quoting AO 21 itself): "This order establishes statewide policies and procedures governing the electronic filing process in all the courts in Arkansas." An AOC press release (March 2023) states electronic filing is "now available statewide in circuit courts," and district courts are also onboarding onto the same eFlex platform. So: one system, one vendor, statewide-mandated policy, with a rolling per-court activation schedule (a target of "all Judicial Circuits on eFiling by 2025" was cited in AOC training materials) — the architecture matches Florida/Texas's single-portal model, not California's per-county-vendor model.

Two official primary sources were used, both hosted directly on arcourts.gov/eflex.arcourts.gov (not vendor marketing):
1. "eFlex Electronic Filing – Filer Interface Arkansas User's Guide for Filers" (the canonical 60-page filer manual AOC links from its own eFile Instructions and eFlex Resources pages) — https://eflex.arcourts.gov/eflexResources/ArkansasFilerInterface.pdf
2. "Are You Smarter Than an eFiler?" — an AOC staff training deck (Business Analyst + Applications Specialist, both @arcourts.gov) with a "Technical Requirements for Scanned Images" slide that corroborates the manual's numbers and adds detail — https://www.arcourts.gov/sites/default/files/Smarter%20than%20an%20eFiler%20Presentation%20(2).pdf
A companion "eFlex Electronic Filing – Clerk Review Arkansas User's Guide for Clerks" (https://eflex.arcourts.gov/eflexCRResources/ArkCourtReviewManual.pdf) was also checked and contains no additional detail on any of the 8 requested fields.

Extra technical constraints found that fall outside the 8 requested fields but are relevant to RaioPDF's e-filing-prep feature, straight from the AOC training slide's "Technical Requirements for Scanned Images" list: standard fonts only (Times New Roman, Arial, Helvetica, Courier — TrueType); "Only one document type on a single document" (don't combine multiple document types into one PDF); "Hyperlinks are not allowed"; scanned images should be 300 DPI or less, black-and-white preferred to keep file size down; "Proposed Orders" must be filed as an editable Word/WordPerfect file, never as PDF, so the clerk/judge can convert it into a signed order. Also, the filer's guide separately imposes mandatory redaction of SSNs/tax-ID/financial account numbers to last-four-digits, minor children reduced to initials, and DOB reduced to year — a redaction rule, not a portal/technical constraint, so not included in "constraints" above, but worth flagging since it's adjacent to RaioPDF's redaction feature.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://eflex.arcourts.gov/eflexResources/ArkansasFilerInterface.pdf)
  > Full-text review (all 60 pages, converted to text and keyword-searched) of the official eFlex Filer Interface User's Guide — the only detailed technical-requirements document the AOC publishes for filers — contains zero occurrences of "PDF/A" in any form. The guide discusses ordinary PDF format requirements at length (accepted formats, conversion behavior, fonts) and separately bans form-fillable fields and metadata, but never invokes an archival/PDF-A standard, and the companion AOC training slide and Clerk Review manual likewise never mention it. No evidence PDF/A is required, preferred, or causes problems — the system appears indifferent to whether an uploaded PDF is PDF/A-conformant.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** required -- [source](https://eflex.arcourts.gov/eflexResources/ArkansasFilerInterface.pdf)
  > The official filer's guide states this twice, in near-identical language, once in the main body and once in Appendix A: "PDF files submitted to the court should not be form fillable or contain any metadata," and "Filers should not upload documents that are form fillable, include metadata, or are locked in any way." No exception, threshold, or method is given — just a blanket instruction to strip metadata (and form fields, and any file locking) before upload. No mention anywhere that a metadata-scrubbed file causes problems; the direction runs entirely the other way (metadata presence is the thing to avoid).

**Constraints found:**
  - **maxFileSize**: 10 MB maximum per individual document; 30 MB maximum for an entire eFiled submission (multiple documents can make up one submission, but the whole submission must stay under 30 MB). Corroborated verbatim by a separate AOC training slide. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://eflex.arcourts.gov/eflexResources/ArkansasFilerInterface.pdf)
    > Note: Individual document size is limited to 10 MB. Multiple documents can be included in a single submission. The size limitation for an entire submission is 30 MB.
  - **acceptedFileFormat**: Accepted upload formats per the filer's guide: PDF (Adobe Acrobat), Microsoft Word 2003+ (.doc/.docx), Corel WordPerfect 10+ (.wpd). A separate AOC training slide's 'Document file format' line lists a broader set: doc, docx, pdf, wpd, txt, rtf. No specific PDF version number (e.g., 1.4/1.7/2.0) is specified anywhere. The system always converts and permanently stores the final record as PDF, EXCEPT 'Proposed Orders,' which must be filed only as an editable Word or WordPerfect file (not PDF) so it can be turned into a signed order. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://eflex.arcourts.gov/eflexResources/ArkansasFilerInterface.pdf)
    > For the most part, those documents and any additional documents that are submitted at a later time need to be submitted as Adobe Acrobat PDF files (Portable Document Format), Microsoft® Word 2003 or higher, or Corel WordPerfect® 10 or higher files.
  - **metadataPolicy**: Metadata removal is required before upload — the guide instructs filers not to submit PDFs containing metadata (stated alongside a parallel ban on form-fillable fields and locked/secured files). See metadataScrubStance/metadataScrubEvidence above for the full analysis; duplicated here because it's also one of the 8 requested technical fields. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://eflex.arcourts.gov/eflexResources/ArkansasFilerInterface.pdf)
    > PDF files submitted to the court should not be form fillable or contain any metadata.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Searchable-text / OCR requirement — no source found (official filer's guide, AOC training deck, and Clerk Review manual all checked) states whether scanned/image-only PDFs need OCR or a searchable text layer; the guide's only scan-related guidance concerns DPI/color for legibility and file size, not text-searchability., Filename character/length restrictions — no source found imposes any restriction on uploaded document filenames (length, allowed characters, etc.)., Bookmark or table-of-contents requirements — no source found requires or even mentions PDF bookmarks or a table of contents for filings or exhibits., Attachment count limits — no source found states a maximum number of documents/attachments per submission; only a total submission SIZE cap (30 MB) is documented, not a document COUNT cap.

---

## California

- **E-filing system:** No single statewide trial-court e-filing system. California's 58 Superior Courts each independently approve their own Electronic Filing Service Providers (EFSPs); e-filing is mandatory for represented civil litigants but the "system" a filer touches varies by county. Separately, TrueFiling IS a single statewide portal — but only for the Supreme Court of California and the six District Courts of Appeal (appellate cases), not for Superior Court trial-level filings. (vendor: Varies by county. Each Superior Court publishes its own approved-EFSP list (e.g., Los Angeles, Alameda, San Bernardino, San Diego, Orange each maintain separate lists). Common backend Electronic Filing Managers/vendors seen across counties include Tyler Technologies' Odyssey eFileCA, File & ServeXpress, and GreenFiling/One Legal, among others — no single vendor is state-mandated. Appellate courts use TrueFiling (Journal Technologies) statewide, a separate system from any trial-court EFSP.)
- **Statewide system:** no -- fragmented/county-by-county
- **Notes:** CONFIRMED FRAGMENTATION: California has no single statewide e-filing portal for Superior Court (trial-level) filings — this is explicit in the courts' own FAQs. The LA Superior Court's own Civil eFiling FAQ states the court "may not accept electronic filings directly" (citing Code Civ. Proc. §1010.6(e)) and instead requires filers to go through any EFSP "listed on the Court's website" — and each county maintains its own separate list. Alameda, Los Angeles, and San Bernardino Superior Courts each publish their own "Technical Requirements"/FAQ documents, and they are not identical: e.g., Los Angeles states the *court itself* imposes no file-size limit (EFSPs set their own), while San Bernardino's own published requirement is a specific 25MB/50MB rule enforced by the court/system itself. This is a genuine county-by-county (or at least county-EFSP-by-EFSP) technical landscape, not a single spec — any RaioPDF "e-filing prep" feature for California should treat these numbers as representative examples, not a universal California constant, and should ideally let the user pick their county/EFSP profile. Separately and for contrast: California DOES have one true statewide portal, TrueFiling, confirmed via the courts' own appellate.courts.ca.gov page to be used by "The Supreme Court of California" and all six District Courts of Appeal — but that only covers appellate proceedings, not the Superior Court civil/family/probate filings that are RaioPDF's likely target use case.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://sanbernardino.courts.ca.gov/online-services/efiling/civil-efiling/civil-efiling-requirements)
  > None of the three official Superior Court technical-requirements documents examined (Alameda County's "Technical E-Filing Requirements," Los Angeles County's "Civil eFiling FAQ," and San Bernardino County's "Civil eFiling Requirements") mentions PDF/A at all — they specify plain PDF (San Bernardino: "Adobe Acrobat version 7 or higher") plus a text-searchable requirement, with no reference to the PDF/A archival subset. No source found stating PDF/A causes encryption, form-field, or redaction/annotation problems either. Two adjacent, possibly relevant data points: (1) San Bernardino prohibits password-protected/encrypted documents outright ("Documents should not be password protected and will be rejected if the content cannot be viewed" — LA FAQ Q63 says the same for LA), which would apply regardless of PDF/A; and (2) San Bernardino separately requires that interactive/fillable PDF form fields be flattened ("fields must be inactivated and no longer fillable before submission") — again a general portal rule, not something tied to PDF/A conversion specifically. Given the fragmented, county-by-county/EFSP-by-EFSP landscape, silence in these three counties' documents cannot be extrapolated with certainty to all 58 Superior Courts.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** recommended -- [source](https://sanbernardino.courts.ca.gov/online-services/efiling/civil-efiling/civil-efiling-requirements)
  > San Bernardino County Superior Court's own official "Civil eFiling Requirements" page explicitly recommends stripping metadata before filing: "To maintain confidentiality and ensure all redactions are appropriately applied, it is important that the submitting party remove all metadata," and separately defines metadata as information that "may reveal a document's revision history, earlier drafts, information about the document's author, file name, file path, date of creation, etc." This is a recommendation/best-practice framed around confidentiality and redaction integrity, not a system-enforced technical gate (no source found saying the portal checks for or rejects files containing metadata). Neither Alameda's nor Los Angeles's own technical-requirements documents mention metadata at all (silent), so — consistent with the fragmented landscape — "recommended" is confirmed for at least one county (San Bernardino) rather than established as a uniform statewide policy.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Statewide system structure**: No single statewide trial-court e-filing portal; the court cannot accept e-filings directly and each Superior Court maintains its own approved-EFSP list. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.lacourt.org/division/efiling/pdf/Civilefiling_FAQ.pdf)
    > The Judicial Council has mandated that all Courts accepting electronically filed documents use independent EFSPs. Pursuant to Code of Civil Procedure Section 1010.6(e) the Court may not accept electronic filings directly.
  - **Statewide system (appellate contrast, not trial court)**: TrueFiling is a genuine single statewide e-filing portal, but only for the Supreme Court of California and the six District Courts of Appeal — not for Superior Court civil/family/probate filings. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://appellate.courts.ca.gov/truefiling)
    > TrueFiling offers users a secure and reliable way to electronically submit case files... The Supreme Court of California [and all six District Courts of Appeal use TrueFiling]
  - **Max file size — San Bernardino County Superior Court**: 25 MB per document; 50 MB per submission (envelope) — this is the court/system's own stated limit, not merely an EFSP guideline. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://sanbernardino.courts.ca.gov/online-services/efiling/civil-efiling/civil-efiling-requirements)
    > There is a 25 MB document limit and a 50 MB file limit for eFile submissions.
  - **Max file size — Los Angeles County Superior Court**: The court itself imposes no file-size limit; any effective limit (guideline of ~25MB/document, ~60MB/transaction) is set by the filer's chosen EFSP, not the court. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.lacourt.org/division/efiling/pdf/Civilefiling_FAQ.pdf)
    > The Court technically has no limit. However, the EFSPs may have restrictions. As a general rule of thumb, 25 megabytes per document and 60 megabytes per e-filing transaction is a good guideline.
  - **Accepted PDF version / format**: PDF format required; specifically 'Adobe Acrobat version 7 or higher.' _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://sanbernardino.courts.ca.gov/online-services/efiling/civil-efiling/civil-efiling-requirements)
    > All documents eFiled must be submitted in pdf format using Adobe Acrobat version 7 or higher
  - **Searchable text / OCR requirement**: Required, with a 'when technologically feasible' carve-out per Alameda's own wording; Los Angeles treats non-text-searchable filings as a rejectable defect. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.alameda.courts.ca.gov/system/files/general/e-filing-technical-requirements.pdf)
    > Electronic documents must be electronically filed in PDF, text searchable format when technologically feasible without impairment of the document's image.
  - **Searchable text / OCR requirement (rejection consequence)**: Los Angeles Superior Court lists a non-text-searchable/non-bookmarked document as a stated common reason for outright rejection. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.lacourt.org/division/efiling/pdf/Civilefiling_FAQ.pdf)
    > Document is not bookmarked and/or text searchable.
  - **Bookmark / table of contents requirement**: Exhibit bookmarking is mandatory (links to first page of each exhibit, titled with exhibit letter/number and description) for represented parties; whole-document table-of-contents bookmarking is only 'preferred,' not mandatory. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.alameda.courts.ca.gov/system/files/general/e-filing-technical-requirements.pdf)
    > Preferably, the table of contents for any filing should be bookmarked to each referenced section... electronic exhibits must include electronic bookmarks with links to the first page of each exhibit and with bookmark titles that identify the exhibit number or letter and briefly describe the exhibit.
  - **Bookmark requirement — self-represented exemption**: The mandatory exhibit-bookmark requirement applies to represented parties; self-represented filers are explicitly exempt from it. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://sanbernardino.courts.ca.gov/online-services/efiling/civil-efiling/civil-efiling-requirements)
    > No electronic bookmark requirements exist for self-represented parties.
  - **Metadata policy**: Recommended (not system-checked) to strip all metadata before filing, framed around confidentiality and redaction integrity — not a hard technical gate. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://sanbernardino.courts.ca.gov/online-services/efiling/civil-efiling/civil-efiling-requirements)
    > To maintain confidentiality and ensure all redactions are appropriately applied, it is important that the submitting party remove all metadata.
  - **Password protection / encryption**: Prohibited — an encrypted/password-protected PDF will be rejected because the clerk cannot open/view it. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.lacourt.org/division/efiling/pdf/Civilefiling_FAQ.pdf)
    > Documents should not be password protected and will be rejected if the content cannot be viewed.
  - **Interactive/fillable PDF form fields**: Judicial Council fillable-form fields must be flattened/deactivated before filing (a related but PDF/A-independent form-handling rule); San Bernardino also rejects negative images and images saved as PDF 'objects.' _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://sanbernardino.courts.ca.gov/online-services/efiling/civil-efiling/civil-efiling-requirements)
    > When using Judicial Council fillable forms, fields must be inactivated and no longer fillable before submission... The court also cannot accept documents with certain characteristics including, but not limited to forms with fillable fields, a negative image, or an image that is saved as an object on the filed document.
  - **Document naming (system field, not filename restriction)**: The EFSP-entered 'Filing Document Name' (a metadata field describing the document type, e.g. 'Motion,' 'Answer') must match the document's actual caption — this is a data-entry-field requirement, not a restriction on the underlying computer filename's characters/length. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.alameda.courts.ca.gov/system/files/general/e-filing-technical-requirements.pdf)
    > The document title entered on the EFSP system must be the same as that reflected in the caption of the document.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Filename character/length restrictions on the underlying computer file (as opposed to the EFSP's 'Filing Document Name' metadata field) — not addressed in any of the official Alameda, Los Angeles, or San Bernardino Superior Court e-filing documents reviewed., Attachment/exhibit count limits per envelope (a numeric cap, as opposed to the unlimited 'multiple documents can be uploaded in one envelope' language found) — not stated in any of the three counties' official documents reviewed; Riverside Superior Court's e-filing FAQ PDF could not be accessed (403 Forbidden) and may have addressed this., Whether San Diego County Superior Court's own civil e-filing FAQ page states different numbers than the counties reviewed — page returned 403 Forbidden and could not be directly verified against an official quote within the bounded research effort., A true statewide baseline for PDF/A stance and metadata policy across all 58 Superior Courts — only three counties' official technical-requirements documents were directly read; given the confirmed county-by-county/EFSP-by-EFSP fragmentation, other counties or EFSPs could plausibly diverge from what was found here.

---

## Colorado

- **E-filing system:** Colorado Courts E-Filing (CCE) — formerly ICCES (Integrated Colorado Courts E-Filing System), renamed effective November 1, 2016 (vendor: Operated by the Colorado Judicial Branch / State Court Administrator's Office as a self-funded, in-house-developed statewide platform (launched 2011 as ICCES). Credit-card payment processing that rides on top of the filing system is run through the Statewide Internet Portal Authority (SIPA) and "operated by Tyler Technologies" per the official FAQ — but that is the payment layer, not necessarily the filing engine itself, so I would not present "Tyler Technologies" as the confirmed core e-filing vendor without further verification. One documented statewide exception: Denver County Court (not Denver District Court) does not use CCE at all — it requires filing and service through a separate commercial vendor platform, File & ServeXpress, per the official CCE FAQ ("Denver County Court cases are not available in the Colorado Court's E-Filing system. Organizations should continue to file and serve in Denver County Court through File & Serve Xpress.").)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Colorado runs ONE mandatory statewide e-filing system — Colorado Courts E-Filing (CCE), formerly branded ICCES — covering district court (civil, domestic relations, probate, water), county court (civil, small claims/FED, name changes, misdemeanor/traffic), criminal/juvenile delinquency, and the Court of Appeals and Supreme Court. It is NOT fragmented county-by-county the way California is. There is exactly one documented carve-out: Denver County Court (the county-level small-claims/civil court, distinct from Denver District Court and Denver Probate Court, which ARE on CCE) is not on CCE at all — filers must use the separate commercial vendor platform File & ServeXpress for Denver County Court cases specifically. Source: CCE FAQ, https://www.coloradojudicial.gov/e-filing-attorneys, Q: \"Can organizations E-File into Denver County Court?\" A: \"Denver County Court cases are not available in the Colorado Court's E-Filing system. Organizations should continue to file and serve in Denver County Court through File & Serve Xpress. Denver District and Probate Court cases can be submitted through the Colorado Court's E-Filing system.\"

Numeric discrepancy worth flagging for the reviewer: the Colorado Judicial Branch's own \"Attorney Training Manual\" PDF (hosted at courts.state.co.us, revised May 2017, still linked from current training resources as of this research) shows on-screen UI text reading \"Total Upload: 0.25 MB of 50 MB limit\" and \"Max Document Size: 3.0 MB,\" plus a supported-filetype list (doc, docx, gif, html, jpeg, msg, odp, odt, pdf, ppt, pptx, rtf, text, tiff, wp, wpd, xls, xlsx, png). Those numbers are far smaller than the 15MB/150MB figures on the live FAQ page and referenced by the current (effective Jan 1, 2026) CJD 11-01. The training manual is nearly a decade old and its screenshots almost certainly reflect a since-increased limit; I treated the live FAQ + current CJD 11-01 as authoritative and did not use the training manual's numbers as a constraint, but flagging the conflict in case a human reviewer wants to double check whether the manual has simply never been updated.

The governing technical document is Chief Justice Directive 11-01 (\"Directive Concerning Statewide Electronic Filing Standards\"), most recently amended effective January 1, 2026 — this is explicitly a directive about the operation of the e-filing system (its stated purpose is \"to make uniform the means by which documents are electronically transmitted and accepted through the State's E-Filing system\"), not a rule of civil/appellate procedure, so I treated it as an in-scope primary technical source for this research rather than excluding it as a \"formal rule of court.\"
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.coloradojudicial.gov/sites/default/files/2025-12/CJD%2011-01%20Effective%20January%201%202026%20WEB%20A11Y.pdf)
  > No mention of PDF/A (as required, preferred, or problematic) appears anywhere in the three primary sources reviewed: Chief Justice Directive 11-01 (the Colorado Supreme Court's governing directive on statewide e-filing document-format standards, amended effective January 1, 2026), the official Colorado Courts E-Filing FAQ page for attorneys, or the (2017) Attorney Training Manual. CJD 11-01's Document Format Standards section (III-IV) only requires that filings be uploaded either as native word-processing files or as PDFs converted directly from a word-processing file — not as scanned/graphic images — with no PDF version or PDF/A profile specified either way. No evidence was found of PDF/A causing (or being warned against for) encryption conflicts, form-field issues, or redaction/annotation stripping in this system; the topic simply is not addressed.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.coloradojudicial.gov/sites/default/files/2025-12/CJD%2011-01%20Effective%20January%201%202026%20WEB%20A11Y.pdf)
  > No mention of document metadata — neither a requirement to include specific metadata, nor a requirement/recommendation to remove it, nor any warning that metadata-scrubbed files cause upload problems — appears in CJD 11-01, the official CCE FAQ page, or the Attorney Training Manual. The only adjacent, non-metadata concept found is CJD 11-01 Section X, which requires the *Document Title* field entered in the web filing form (not file metadata) to be descriptive of the document's contents (e.g., "Motion to Suppress Statements" rather than just "Motion").

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size — per document**: 15 MB per document _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.coloradojudicial.gov/e-filing-attorneys)
    > Yes, the system allows up to 15MB per document, with a total of 150MB per filing submission.
  - **Maximum file size — per filing submission/envelope**: 150 MB total per filing submission _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.coloradojudicial.gov/e-filing-attorneys)
    > Yes, the system allows up to 15MB per document, with a total of 150MB per filing submission.
  - **Accepted file format for upload**: A filing must be uploaded either directly in its native word-processing format (Word or WordPerfect) or as a PDF converted directly from a word-processing file; no specific PDF version number is specified, and image/scan-based files are barred except where the directive specifically allows them (e.g., true-and-correct scanned exhibits). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.coloradojudicial.gov/sites/default/files/2025-12/CJD%2011-01%20Effective%20January%201%202026%20WEB%20A11Y.pdf)
    > All documents must be submitted by either (1) directly uploading the document from a word processing format (such as Word or Word Perfect) to the E-Filing system, or (2) electronically converting the document from a word processing format into a PDF format and then directly uploading the PDF document to the E-Filing system.
  - **Searchable-text / OCR requirement**: Filed documents (other than the specifically-permitted scanned exhibits) must not be uploaded as scanned or graphic images, and must not be uploaded in any way that blocks the court from copying/pasting text or using enhanced search within the document — i.e., filings other than exhibits must be genuine, searchable text, not image-only scans. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.coloradojudicial.gov/sites/default/files/2025-12/CJD%2011-01%20Effective%20January%201%202026%20WEB%20A11Y.pdf)
    > Parties shall not upload documents into the E-Filing system in any manner that prevents the Court from copying/pasting text or employing enhanced search functionality within the document. Except as specifically provided in this directive, parties shall not upload documents into the E-Filing system as scanned or graphic images.
  - **Attachment / exhibit count limit**: No numeric cap on the number of attachments or exhibits was found. Instead, the system is governed structurally and by size: each exhibit must be its own separate file within a single filing submission (bundling multiple documents/exhibits into one file is a rejection ground), and if a filing submission's total size (all documents plus exhibits) would exceed the size limit, the filer must split it into an additional filing submission, or, if an individual exhibit can't be split, place it on a CD/DVD for physical filing instead. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.coloradojudicial.gov/sites/default/files/2025-12/CJD%2011-01%20Effective%20January%201%202026%20WEB%20A11Y.pdf)
    > Each exhibit shall be a separate file (for example, PDF file, Excel Spreadsheet) within the filing submission. ... If the total size of all documents, including exhibits, exceeds the size limits of a filing submission, an additional filing submission must be created.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Filename character/length restrictions on the uploaded file itself — no official CCE technical spec, FAQ, or CJD was found addressing filesystem-level filename characters or length. (Note: CJD 11-01 Section X does require the web-form "Document Title" field to be a descriptive label of the document's contents, e.g. not just "Motion" — but that is a metadata/title-field content rule, not a restriction on the actual uploaded filename, so it was not used to fill this field.), Bookmark or embedded PDF table-of-contents requirement at the technical/portal level — none found. The only 'table of contents' requirement located in Colorado sources is a substantive content requirement for appellate briefs under Colorado Appellate Rules 28/32 (table of contents and table of authorities as part of the brief's own required content), which is a rule of appellate procedure rather than an e-filing system/portal technical spec, and was excluded per the research scope.

---

## Connecticut

- **E-filing system:** E-Services (Connecticut Judicial Branch) — encompassing Superior Court E-Filing (civil, family, housing, small claims) and Appellate E-Filing under one enrollment/login system (vendor: Not publicly disclosed in any official document reviewed. The system appears to be operated directly by the Connecticut Judicial Branch (in-house) rather than through a named third-party e-filing vendor/platform brand (no Tyler/Odyssey/File&ServeXpress branding appears anywhere on the official portal or manuals). Not independently confirmed — treat as unverified.)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Confirmed: Connecticut runs ONE statewide mandatory e-filing system called "E-Services," operated directly by the Connecticut Judicial Branch (not a county-by-county or district-by-district patchwork — Connecticut has no county governments, and the Judicial Branch/Superior Court is a single unified statewide court system). E-filing has been mandatory (not optional) for civil and housing matters since December 5, 2009 (docket numbers beginning with 5 or 6 signal e-filable/mandatory cases), extended to newly-initiated family matters of listed case types on/after December 15, 2014, and to small claims/housing small claims on/after September 1, 2017. A structurally separate 'Appellate E-Filing' application exists for the Supreme and Appellate Courts (same E-Services login, its own Procedures and Technical Standards document) — its specific technical limits were not independently re-verified in this pass; do not assume they are identical to the Superior Court civil/family figures above without checking that document directly. Do NOT confuse this with the U.S. District Court for the District of Connecticut's federal CM/ECF e-filing system (ctd.uscourts.gov) — that is a completely separate federal system with its own rules, irrelevant to state-court RaioPDF e-filing-prep logic. Primary sources used: e-standards.pdf (Civil & Family Procedures and Technical Standards, effective 2026-01-23 — very current), ATTY_FAQs.pdf (Attorney/Law Firm FAQ, last revised 2023-09-18), Atty_UserManual.pdf (E-Filing Manual for Attorneys, effective 2018-04-30, still the live linked manual), and PDF-A-FAQ.htm / How-to-Save-or-Convert-to-PDFA.htm (PDF/A-specific guidance pages, undated but currently linked from the live E-Services FAQ index).
- **PDF/A stance:** preferred -- [source](https://www.jud.ct.gov/external/super/e-services/efile/PDF-A-FAQ.htm)
  > Connecticut Judicial Branch PDF/A FAQ states PDF/A is encouraged/anticipated but not yet mandatory: 'The Judicial Branch has not yet set a deadline for requiring all electronic files to be uploaded in a PDF/A format, however all users are encouraged to begin to transition their filings to this new standard as soon as possible.' Where used, PDF/A-1a is 'preferred' and PDF/A-1b 'meets the minimum requirement.' The same page frames PDF/A as a fix for standard-PDF security/font/long-term-readability issues, not as a source of new problems — no mention of PDF/A breaking encryption, forms, or redactions was found anywhere in official CT materials.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.jud.ct.gov/external/super/e-services/e-standards.pdf)
  > No mention of document metadata (properties, author fields, revision history, etc.) — neither a requirement to include it, a recommendation to remove it, nor any warning that scrubbed/metadata-stripped files cause rejection — appears anywhere in the three core official sources checked: the 2026 Civil & Family E-Services Procedures and Technical Standards, the Attorney E-Filing Manual, and the Attorney FAQ (which has a dedicated 'Format and Size of Documents' section covering PDF format, PDF/A, and the 50MB limit but says nothing about metadata). This reads as genuine silence in the primary sources, not a failure to locate them.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size (per document)**: 50 MB per PDF document (Judicial Branch describes this as 'in excess of 1000 pages of unformatted text'). If an exhibit or document exceeds 50 MB, the filer must split it into multiple smaller PDF files and file them as separate items — there is no single-envelope override for one oversized file. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.jud.ct.gov/external/super/e-services/efile/ATTY_FAQs.pdf)
    > The e-filing system will accept documents up to 50 MB, which is in excess of 1000 pages of unformatted text. Be sure that you are not scanning your documents in color and avoid using colored paper since color scanning and colored paper will use up a tremendous amount of space.' ... '65. How do I file exhibits that are over 50 MB in size? Exhibits that are over 50 MB in size can be broken down into sections and filed separately.
  - **Accepted file format / PDF version**: Only PDF is accepted for e-filed documents — Word/WordPerfect and other native formats are rejected.
