For document creation, the Branch's technical standards recommend Adobe Acrobat 9.0 through 11.0 (and Adobe Reader 9.0+ for viewing), but no specific PDF spec version (e.g., 1.4 vs 1.7) is mandated for ordinary (non-PDF/A) filings. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.jud.ct.gov/external/super/e-services/e-standards.pdf)
    > No, you can only file a PDF document. PDF is a universal file format that preserves the fonts, images, graphics, and layout of any source document, regardless of the application and platform used to create it.' (ATTY_FAQs.pdf, Q9) ... 'If you are using Adobe Acrobat ® for PDF document creation, it is recommended that you use Adobe Acrobat® 9.0 through 11.0; and if you are using Adobe Acrobat® Reader ® for viewing documents, it is recommended that you use Adobe Acrobat® Reader ® 9.0 or higher.
  - **PDF/A requirement**: Not required. The Judicial Branch actively encourages transition to PDF/A and calls it a 'future required standard,' but as of the current PDF/A FAQ page has 'not yet set a deadline' for mandating it — plain PDF remains fully acceptable today. If a filer does use PDF/A, PDF/A-1a is preferred and PDF/A-1b 'meets the minimum requirement' (1b is recommended specifically for scanned documents). No CT source found states PDF/A causes encryption conflicts, form-field breakage, or redaction/annotation stripping; the Branch's own framing is the opposite — PDF/A was adopted specifically to eliminate security and long-term-readability problems found in ordinary PDF. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.jud.ct.gov/external/super/e-services/efile/PDF-A-FAQ.htm)
    > When will the Judicial Branch require that all documents filed in e-filing be in PDF/A format? The Judicial Branch has not yet set a deadline for requiring all electronic files to be uploaded in a PDF/A format, however all users are encouraged to begin to transition their filings to this new standard as soon as possible. ... Which PDF/A format should filers use: 1a or 1b? PDF/A-1a is preferred; PDF/A-1b meets the minimum requirement.
  - **Filename restrictions**: No enforced naming convention or length limit is stated, but the Attorney E-Filing Manual instructs filers to avoid special characters and not to include spaces in the PDF's file name. (Separately, for E-Services account User IDs — not document filenames — symbols/punctuation such as @, #, & or * are expressly disallowed and passwords must be 8-10 characters.) _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.jud.ct.gov/external/super/E-Services/efile/Atty_UserManual.pdf)
    > Note: The Judicial Branch does not require any particular format when you name the PDF documents. However, avoid using special characters and do not include spaces in the name of your document.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Per-envelope/submission aggregate file-size limit distinct from the confirmed 50 MB per-document cap — no official source found describing a total-submission ceiling (oversized exhibits are simply split into additional 50MB-or-under documents with no stated cap on how many)., Searchable text / OCR requirement — no official CT Judicial Branch source (e-standards.pdf, Attorney/SRP manuals, ATTY_FAQs, PDF/A FAQ) mentions any requirement or preference for OCR'd/searchable text., Bookmark or table-of-contents requirement — not mentioned in any official source; the only related convention found is a non-binding suggestion to insert a plain divider page with a reference number before each exhibit in a combined exhibit PDF, which is not a PDF-bookmark technical requirement., Attachment count limit (maximum number of documents/attachments per single e-filing transaction) — not stated in any official source reviewed., Whether the Appellate E-Filing sub-system (Supreme/Appellate Court) shares the same 50MB/PDF-only/PDF/A-optional constraints as the Superior Court civil/family/housing/small-claims system verified above — it has its own separate 'Appellate E-Filing Procedures and Technical Standards' document that was not independently pulled and checked line-by-line in this pass.

---

## Delaware (state courts)

- **E-filing system:** File &amp; ServeXpress ("FSX") — used by the Delaware Supreme Court, Court of Chancery, Superior Court, and Register of Wills. (Delaware is NOT a single-statewide-system state — see systemNotes and statewideSystem below.) (vendor: File &amp; ServeXpress, LLC)
- **Statewide system:** no -- fragmented/county-by-county
- **Notes:** Delaware does NOT have one single mandatory statewide e-filing portal. It is fragmented by COURT LEVEL/TYPE (not by county, and not fully unified like Florida/Texas, but also not a California-style "each county picks its own vendor" model either — each of the three systems below, once you know which court you're in, applies the same way across all three counties):

1. File &amp; ServeXpress (FSX) — Delaware Supreme Court, Court of Chancery, Superior Court, and Register of Wills. This is the system covering the courts most relevant to substantive civil/business litigation (including Delaware's famous Chancery corporate docket), so this report focuses primarily on FSX. Confirmed via the official courts.delaware.gov/efiling/ overview and the Court of Chancery's own current (July 26, 2023) "Best Practices and Procedures for E-Filing" manual, which is the most authoritative and current primary source found.
2. File &amp; Serve Delaware — a separate, distinct e-filing system used only by the Court of Common Pleas. NOT independently researched here (effort-budget tradeoff) — treat as a fully separate system with its own specs if CCP filings matter.
3. eFlex ("State of Delaware Judiciary eFiling System") — a third, separate system used by the Justice of the Peace Court. Its official technical standards document ("EFILING STANDARDS") is the most granular technical document found in this research, but it is dated May 2010 (revised 3/18/2010) — still the current document officially posted on courts.delaware.gov, but its age should be flagged; it may not reflect subsequent portal changes.
4. Family Court currently has NO e-filing capability at all (per courts.delaware.gov/efiling/).

Given this fragmentation, constraints below are labeled by which system they come from. FSX (Chancery/Superior/Supreme) is the practically important one for most Delaware litigation; eFlex (JP Court) constraints are included because that document is unusually specific but apply only to that court.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://courts.delaware.gov/forms/download.aspx?id=157098)
  > Read in full: the Court of Chancery's current 39-page "Best Practices and Procedures for E-Filing/Filing with the Register in Chancery" (updated July 26, 2023) specifies accepted formats (Word/TIFF/PDF), auto-conversion behavior, and document/transaction size limits in detail — but never mentions PDF/A anywhere: no requirement, no preference, and no caution about PDF/A causing encryption, form-field, or redaction/annotation problems. The eFlex "EFILING STANDARDS" document (Justice of the Peace Court, 2010) is likewise completely silent on PDF/A. No official Delaware court e-filing document found in this research mentions PDF/A in any capacity.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://courts.delaware.gov/forms/download.aspx?id=157098)
  > Same full-document review as above: neither the Court of Chancery's "Best Practices" manual nor the eFlex "EFILING STANDARDS" document contains any instruction to include, preserve, or strip document metadata before filing, and neither warns that metadata-scrubbed (or metadata-laden) files cause rejection or other problems. The Chancery document does address a related-but-distinct topic — redacting Social Security numbers/dates of birth from document *content* and confidential-filing/"Sealed, electronic" designation — but that is a content-redaction rule, not a file-metadata policy.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size per document — File & ServeXpress (Supreme Court, Court of Chancery, Superior Court)**: 10 megabytes per eFiled document _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://courts.delaware.gov/forms/download.aspx?id=157098)
    > The size of any eFiled document shall not exceed 10 megabytes.
  - **Maximum file size per envelope/transaction — File & ServeXpress**: 35 megabytes per eFiled transaction (a transaction can bundle a main document plus supporting documents) _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://courts.delaware.gov/forms/download.aspx?id=157098)
    > The size of any eFiled transaction shall not exceed 35 megabytes.
  - **Maximum file size per document — eFlex (Justice of the Peace Court, a SEPARATE system from FSX)**: 2 megabytes per document. Note: this figure comes from a document dated May 2010 (revised 3/18/2010) — the current officially-posted standard, but old enough that it should be treated with caution pending confirmation the JP e-filing portal hasn't since changed this limit. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://courts.delaware.gov/forms/download.aspx?id=42198)
    > 2 megabyte size of document
  - **Accepted file format — File & ServeXpress (Supreme Court, Court of Chancery, Superior Court)**: Word, TIFF, or PDF accepted at upload. Word/TIFF files are automatically converted to PDF by the system (original also stays downloadable); the PDF version becomes the official court record. Exception: briefs and proposed orders must specifically be filed in EDITABLE Word format, not a flat/scanned PDF. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://courts.delaware.gov/forms/download.aspx?id=157098)
    > Each electronically filed document shall be filed in Word, TIFF, or .PDF format, except that each electronically filed brief, and proposed order shall be filed in editable Word format... Any Word or TIFF file will automatically be converted to .PDF format by File & ServeXpress, but the original format also will be available for downloading. The official record of the court is the .PDF version.
  - **Accepted file format / page-splitting & scan-quality rules — eFlex (Justice of the Peace Court)**: PDF format only. Any document exceeding 10 pages must be broken into multiple PDF files unless the court has granted leave (with a 2-page tolerance for pages added purely by the scan/conversion process). Scans should be 150-300 DPI, black & white for text (grayscale permitted for photos); scanning at too high a resolution is itself a stated cause for rejection because it inflates file size past the limit. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://courts.delaware.gov/forms/download.aspx?id=42198)
    > FORMAT IS .PDF ... Each electronically filed document shall be filed in .PDF format ... Any document that exceeds ten (10) pages must be broken into multiple .PDF files, unless prior leave has been granted by the Court. A document may exceed page limitation rules to a maximum of two (2) additional pages when the additional pages are attributed to the electronic conversion or filing process. ... No more than 10 pages per document ... Please use 150-300 DPI black and white for documents
  - **Document title / naming convention within the portal — File & ServeXpress**: The portal requires a structured descriptive 'document title' entered at upload for every filed document — this is an in-system title/metadata field, NOT a restriction on the underlying computer filename. It must state who is filing, a descriptive title of the document, who relief is sought against (if any), and a description of the relief sought. No numeric character-count limit is given for this title field, and no separate restriction on the actual uploaded computer filename was found anywhere in the document (see gaps). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://courts.delaware.gov/forms/download.aspx?id=157098)
    > The title of each electronically filed document shall include: Party or parties filing the document; Descriptive title of the document; Party or parties against whom relief, if any, is sought; and Description of the relief sought.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Searchable-text / OCR requirement — not addressed anywhere in either official document reviewed (FSX/Chancery Best Practices 2023, or eFlex Standards 2010); no statement requiring, recommending, or forgoing OCR/text-layer PDFs was found., Filename character/length restriction on the actual uploaded computer file (distinct from the in-system 'document title' metadata field, which IS documented) — no source found addressing OS-level filename constraints., Bookmark or table-of-contents requirement at the PORTAL/technical level — Court of Chancery Rule 171 requires a Table of Contents and Table of Authorities as document CONTENT for Briefs specifically, but that is a rule-of-court content requirement, not a technical PDF-bookmark constraint imposed by the e-filing system itself, and per the research brief's scope this was not counted as a qualifying technical finding., Attachment count limit per filing/envelope — no numeric cap on the number of supporting/linked documents in a single FSX transaction was found (only the 35MB total transaction size cap, which indirectly limits attachment count)., Specific required PDF version number (e.g., PDF 1.4, 1.7, 2.0/PDF 2.0) — neither official document specifies an ISO PDF version; both only specify 'PDF format' generically., Court of Common Pleas' 'File & Serve Delaware' system's technical specs — a system entirely distinct from File & ServeXpress; not independently researched within this pass's effort budget.

---

## Florida (statewide)

- **E-filing system:** Florida Courts E-Filing Portal ("the Portal" / "ePortal"), at myflcourtaccess.com (vendor: Developed and operated by the Florida Courts E-Filing Authority — a public entity whose membership is "All Clerks of the Circuit and Appellate Courts" and whose Board is composed of eight Circuit Court Clerks plus the Clerk of the Supreme Court — under standards set by the Florida Supreme Court in consultation with the Florida Courts Technology Commission. It is not a single named commercial COTS e-filing product (e.g., not confirmed to be Tyler Technologies or Odyssey); the Authority does separately certify third-party "Filing Agent"/practice-management integrations that submit into this same central Portal, analogous to Texas's EFSP model, but the back-end Portal itself is a single statewide system, not a per-county procurement.)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Confirmed via multiple official sources (Florida Supreme Court Administrative Order AOSC20-77, the Florida Courts Technology Standards, and the Florida Courts E-Filing Authority's own FAQ/manual documents) that Florida runs ONE mandatory statewide e-filing system — the Florida Courts E-Filing Portal at myflcourtaccess.com — used by all 67 counties' trial courts, the District Courts of Appeal, and the Florida Supreme Court alike. This is NOT a fragmented county-by-county model like California. E-filing by attorneys was made mandatory statewide by Florida Supreme Court order in 2012. The only jurisdiction-level variance found is cosmetic/administrative (e.g., individual counties can customize document-type naming lists, and some counties do not yet accept criminal case-initiation e-filings, and some counties require exhibits combined into the main document rather than filed separately) — the underlying e-filing system and its technical constraints (file size, format, PDF/A rules, filename rules) are uniform statewide. The governing standards have gone through several versions: originally AOSC09-30 (2009), superseded by AOSC20-77 (2020) adopting the "Florida Courts E-Filing Portal Standards," which were folded into the broader "Florida Courts Technology Standards" (v1.0 Nov 2020, most current version found: v4.0 adopted May 2025) — all versions checked contain materially identical language for the fields researched here, indicating these constraints have been stable for several years.
- **PDF/A stance:** preferred -- [source](https://flcourts-media.flcourts.gov/content/download/2484497/file/florida-courts-technology-standards-v4%20(adopted%20May%202025).pdf)
  > PDF/A (specifically PDF/A-2a for born-digital documents, PDF/A-2b for scanned documents) is explicitly the "preferred" format, not a hard requirement — the Portal continues to accept Word and plain PDF and will itself convert those server-side to PDF/A once/where the receiving clerk's system can handle it. Critically for RaioPDF's default-behavior question: PDF/A is NOT a universally safe drop-in conversion target. The official standard flatly prohibits several things a PDF/A converter can accidentally strip: (1) any encryption/password protection — "a compliant PDF/A file must be open and available to anyone... User IDs and passwords may not be embedded," so an encrypted PDF cannot become compliant PDF/A without first removing the password; (2) interactive form fields and form actions — explicitly listed as a "prohibited" PDF/A document-intelligence element, meaning fillable-form PDFs will have their form fields flattened/invalidated in the filing workflow; (3) comments and annotations — also explicitly prohibited, which is directly relevant to any redaction or markup workflow implemented via PDF annotations rather than true content removal; (4) digital signatures/notarizations using an encryption key — the Portal will not pass these through at all, PDF/A or not. On the upside, the Portal is forgiving about non-conformant files: a Florida Courts E-Filing Authority FAQ states "The Portal will check each document submitted and display an error message if the document is not in PDF/A format. This will not disrupt the filing of your document. At this time, this is informational only" — meaning a mislabeled or imperfectly-converted PDF/A does not currently cause outright rejection, only a warning.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://documents.myflcourtaccess.com/uploads/2021/08/PDF_FAQS_Apr_2021-2.pdf)
  > The binding, adopted standards (Florida Courts Technology Standards / AOSC20-77) impose no general filer-facing requirement to either include or strip document metadata before filing — they are silent on this beyond the encryption-related rule (no embedded user IDs/passwords) noted above. However, the Florida Courts E-Filing Authority's own published "PDF/A Frequently Asked Questions" document contains a dedicated "Metadata Scrub" section that surfaces a real, documented conflict directly relevant to RaioPDF's question of whether scrubbing metadata is a safe universal default. It states: "To be a true PDF/A, we may need to modify the metadata rules a bit. As the rules read right now, they require ALL metadata to be scrubbed to be truly compliant with the Portal. Perhaps a slight modification to 'any metadata that is not required for compliance standards shall be removed from submission'... " and separately, under "PDF/A Conformity": "You basically cannot scrub any metadata for it to pass [PDF/A conformance verification]. For example: if you take a file that has had its metadata scrubbed and run it through the 'VERIFY CONFORMITY' [check] it will fail. The reason it will 'fail' is because when you scrub metadata part of that is the metadata 'pdfcreator' which can be scrubbed. The 'pdfcreator' tag, apparently is required to pass the CONFORMITY test." In short: this Portal-published FAQ describes an unresolved internal tension between a general expectation of scrubbing all metadata and the PDF/A standard's own requirement to retain certain identifying metadata tags to pass formal conformance verification — i.e., a full, blanket metadata scrub can itself cause a file to fail PDF/A conformity checking. This is documented evidence but comes from an informal, dated FAQ/training document (dated Feb. 2019, last revised Aug. 2021) rather than an adopted binding standard, so it is reported as "silent" at the formal-standard level with this caveat surfaced for review rather than elevated to "required"/"prohibited."

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size — Trial Court (per submission/envelope)**: 50 MB aggregate per submission (covers a single document or multiple documents together in one filing envelope) _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://flcourts-media.flcourts.gov/content/download/2484497/file/florida-courts-technology-standards-v4%20(adopted%20May%202025).pdf)
    > A single submission, whether consisting of a single document or multiple documents, shall not exceed 50 megabytes (50 MB) in size.
  - **Maximum file size — Appellate Court / Florida Supreme Court (per submission/envelope)**: 200 MB aggregate per submission _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://documents.myflcourtaccess.com/uploads/2024/08/FAQ_For_Filers_Nov_2021-tagged.pdf)
    > The aggregate size for the Appellate Court and The Florida Supreme Court cannot exceed 200 megabytes for one submission.
  - **Accepted file formats**: Word, PDF, and PDF/A are all accepted for new filings (WordPerfect was formally removed as an acceptable format); PDF/A is the preferred format _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://flcourts-media.flcourts.gov/content/download/2484497/file/florida-courts-technology-standards-v4%20(adopted%20May%202025).pdf)
    > The Portal will accept new filings in Word, PDF, and PDF/A formats. The preferred format for filing is the PDF/A format where original document intelligence has been maintained.
  - **Preferred PDF/A conformance level**: PDF/A-2a preferred for born-digital documents (or current equivalent); PDF/A-2b acceptable for scanned/non-born-digital documents _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://documents.myflcourtaccess.com/uploads/2021/08/PDF_FAQS_Apr_2021-2.pdf)
    > The preferred format for document submission is PDF/A-2a (or current equivalent). ... PDF/A-2b (basic). When the filer is unable to create a born-digital document, the document may be scanned, and the filer should use the PDF/A-2b format.
  - **PDF/A vs. encryption — direct conflict**: An encrypted or password-protected PDF cannot be a compliant PDF/A file; no user IDs or passwords may be embedded _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://flcourts-media.flcourts.gov/content/download/2484497/file/florida-courts-technology-standards-v4%20(adopted%20May%202025).pdf)
    > Encryption Prohibited. A compliant PDF/A file must be open and available to anyone or any software that processes the file. User IDs and passwords may not be embedded.
  - **PDF/A vs. form fields, annotations, comments, JavaScript**: Interactive form fields/actions, comments, annotations, embedded attachments, hidden/deleted content, non-persistent hyperlinks, thumbnails, JavaScript, and non-display data are prohibited in PDF/A submissions and are expected to be flattened, invalidated, modified, or deleted during the filing workflow _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://flcourts-media.flcourts.gov/content/download/2484497/file/florida-courts-technology-standards-v4%20(adopted%20May%202025).pdf)
    > The following elements must not be used in PDF/A documents submitted to the Florida Courts: embedded attachments, comments, annotations, hidden deleted items (these should be purged), embedded non-persistent external hyperlinks, embedded thumbnails, form fields and actions, JavaScript, and embedded non-display data. These elements are prohibited because they might be flattened, invalidated, modified, or deleted during the document workflow process.
  - **PDF/A vs. digital signatures**: Encryption-key-based digital signatures and digital notarizations are not passed through by the Portal (including when a filing is server-side converted to PDF/A); Florida's own s/-Name signature block is the format actually preserved _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://documents.myflcourtaccess.com/uploads/2021/08/PDF_FAQS_Apr_2021-2.pdf)
    > Will digital signatures be accepted in a PDF/A document? The Portal will not pass digital signatures and digital notarizations which require an encryption key.
  - **Searchable-text requirement**: Required — PDF documents filed with the Portal must be text-searchable; non-searchable PDFs are not rejected outright but are rasterized into a bitmap-image PDF/A on ingestion _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://flcourts-media.flcourts.gov/content/download/2484497/file/florida-courts-technology-standards-v4%20(adopted%20May%202025).pdf)
    > PDF documents filed with the Portal must be searchable. Documents filed in non-searchable PDF format will be rasterized (i.e., converted into bitmap file format) as an approved PDF/A format.
  - **OCR / scan quality requirement**: Scanned documents should be run through OCR and scanned at a minimum of 300 DPI, in black and white (non-color) _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://flcourts-media.flcourts.gov/content/download/2484497/file/florida-courts-technology-standards-v4%20(adopted%20May%202025).pdf)
    > Scanned documents should be scanned using Optical Character Recognition ("OCR"). The scanning process should use a minimum resolution of 300 DPI.
  - **Filename — disallowed characters**: File names may not contain: " # % & * : < > ? \ / { } | ~ . (period — the Portal appends the extension automatically) , ' _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://flcourts-media.flcourts.gov/content/download/2484497/file/florida-courts-technology-standards-v4%20(adopted%20May%202025).pdf)
    > The following special characters are not allowed in a file name: Quotation mark ("), Number sign (#), Percent (%), Ampersand (&), Asterisk (*), Colon (:), Angle brackets (less than, greater than) (< >), Question mark (?), Backslash (\), Slash (/), Braces (left and right) ({ }), Pipe (|), Tilde (~), Period (.) The filer should not add an extension... Comma (,), Apostrophe (').
  - **Filename — length limit**: 150 bytes maximum including spaces; each space counts as 3 bytes (so effectively well under 150 plain characters once any spaces are used) _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://flcourts-media.flcourts.gov/content/download/2484497/file/florida-courts-technology-standards-v4%20(adopted%20May%202025).pdf)
    > In addition, file names cannot exceed 150 bytes in length, including spaces. Spaces must be counted as three (3) bytes each.
  - **Bookmarks / table of contents**: Not required by the Portal. Bookmarks appear only on the list of permitted (optional) PDF/A document-intelligence elements — no provision mandates including bookmarks or a table of contents _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://flcourts-media.flcourts.gov/content/download/2484497/file/florida-courts-technology-standards-v4%20(adopted%20May%202025).pdf)
    > The following PDF/A document intelligence elements are permitted in documents submitted to the Florida Courts: bookmarks, electronic signatures, attachments created using the Insert feature to append pages to a document, internal links, embedded internal hyperlinks, embedded persistent external hyperlinks, and embedded images.
  - **Attachment / exhibit count limit**: No numeric cap on the number of exhibits/attachments per submission was found in official sources; exhibits are instead governed purely by the aggregate submission size ceiling (50MB trial / 200MB appellate) and each exhibit must carry its own cover page _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://flcourts-media.flcourts.gov/content/download/2484497/file/florida-courts-technology-standards-v4%20(adopted%20May%202025).pdf)
    > Multiple exhibits can be filed in one submission as long as each exhibit is accompanied by a cover page and does not exceed submission file size. On each cover page, the number of pages should be noted for that exhibit.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Specific minimum/maximum PDF version number (e.g., PDF 1.4 vs 1.7 vs 2.0) accepted for non-PDF/A 'plain PDF' submissions is not stated in any official source found — the standards only say 'PDF' and 'PDF/A' are accepted, without pinning a version number for the former., Whether PDF/A has, in practice, already flipped from 'preferred' to a hard mandatory requirement in any specific circuit/clerk as of 2026 could not be confirmed — the most current adopted standard found (Technology Standards v4.0, May 2025) still frames PDF/A as conditionally converted 'when the clerk is able to receive and store a PDF/A document,' and an official FAQ noted repeated extensions of the clerks' PDF/A storage-readiness deadline (last extension found on record was to June 2022) with no later official statement located confirming full statewide completion.

---

## Georgia (state trial courts — Superior and State Courts, civil filings)

- **E-filing system:** Fragmented between two vendor platforms: PeachCourt and Odyssey eFileGA (branded 'File & Serve'). No single statewide e-filing portal exists. (vendor: PeachCourt (its own dedicated Georgia platform/knowledge base at peachcourt.com) and Tyler Technologies' Odyssey File & Serve product, branded for Georgia as 'eFileGA' (efilega.tylerhost.net / georgia.tylerhost.net). Two separate commercial vendors, not one statewide-built system.)
- **Statewide system:** no -- fragmented/county-by-county
- **Notes:** CONFIRMED: Georgia does NOT have one single statewide mandatory e-filing portal (unlike Florida's ePortal or Texas's eFileTexas/Tyler). Instead, Georgia law (SB 407, effective Jan. 1, 2019) made e-filing MANDATORY statewide for civil cases in Superior and State Courts, but left each county/circuit court free to choose which of two competing commercial platforms to adopt: PeachCourt or Odyssey eFileGA (Tyler Technologies). Per the Georgia Bar's own description, 'the vast majority of counties with both a state and superior court' use the same provider for both, but 'a few Georgia courts allow attorneys to file using both eFileGA and PeachCourt' (e.g., Oconee County). This is a narrower, two-vendor fragmentation — not the fully open county-by-county marketplace seen in California — but it is still fragmented: there is no single technical spec sheet that governs 'Georgia e-filing.' A tool like RaioPDF that wants to give attorneys reliable pre-flight guidance for Georgia needs to know which of the two platforms a given county/circuit uses, because the two systems' documented specs differ (e.g., eFileGA explicitly accepts PDF/A; PeachCourt's own FAQ only mentions plain PDF). Separately, Georgia's two appellate courts (Supreme Court, Court of Appeals) run their own distinct e-filing systems (SCED and EFAST respectively) that were not researched in depth here — see gaps.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](http://content.tylerhost.net/docs/GA/OFSFrequentllyAskedQuestions.pdf)
  > Odyssey eFileGA explicitly accepts PDF/A as one of two allowed formats ('File & Serve only accepts documents in PDF or PDF-A formats') — it is permitted, not required, and the source is otherwise silent on whether attorneys should prefer it. However, the same official document flags a genuine, specific PDF/A risk in its troubleshooting chapter: PDF/A's standard behavior of embedding font resources can embed an unsupported font (their named example is 'JBig'), which breaks the system's document-conversion process and produces a 'Format Error' rejection that must be manually diagnosed and refiled. PeachCourt's own official FAQ (Georgia Statewide Business Court page) does not mention PDF/A at all — it only says 'You may only upload documents as a PDF,' silent on the /A variant.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](http://content.tylerhost.net/docs/GA/OFSFrequentllyAskedQuestions.pdf)
  > Neither the Odyssey eFileGA FAQ (which otherwise devotes a full chapter to document-format troubleshooting: security settings, fonts, image compression, OCR, corrupt files) nor the PeachCourt-related official Georgia Statewide Business Court FAQ says anything about metadata — no requirement to include it, no instruction to scrub it, and no warning that scrubbed files cause problems. This reads as genuine silence in the primary sources reviewed, not merely an unsuccessful search, given how thorough the eFileGA troubleshooting chapter is on adjacent technical PDF issues.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size — Odyssey eFileGA (Tyler File & Serve)**: Court-recommended limits: documents should not exceed 5 MB per document and 25 MB per envelope (submission). Framed as a recommendation for manageability, not stated as a hard technical block in this document. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](http://content.tylerhost.net/docs/GA/OFSFrequentllyAskedQuestions.pdf)
    > For optimal manageability, the court recommends that files do not exceed 5 MB per document and 25 MB per envelope. There are practical limits to the size of an electronic document that judges and staff can quickly and easily retrieve and read within the case management system.
  - **Maximum file size — PeachCourt**: Recommended limit: total file size of documents should not exceed 25 MB. Not explicitly broken out as per-document vs. per-envelope in this source. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.georgiabusinesscourt.com/faq/)
    > You may only upload documents as a PDF... it is recommended that you limit the total file size of your documents to 25 MB.
  - **Accepted PDF version / file format — Odyssey eFileGA**: PDF or PDF/A only. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](http://content.tylerhost.net/docs/GA/OFSFrequentllyAskedQuestions.pdf)
    > File & Serve only accepts documents in PDF or PDF-A formats.
  - **Accepted PDF version / file format — PeachCourt**: PDF only; this source does not mention PDF/A one way or the other. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.georgiabusinesscourt.com/faq/)
    > You may only upload documents as a PDF.
  - **PDF/A — documented risk factor (Odyssey eFileGA)**: PDF/A is an accepted format alongside plain PDF (not required over it), but the system's own troubleshooting guidance flags a specific, real interoperability problem: PDF/A's mandatory embedded-font behavior can pull in an unsupported font (named example: JBIG/'JBig'), which causes the filing to fail conversion and be rejected with a 'Format Error.' Separately (not PDF/A-specific but relevant to any PDF/A workflow that also applies security), any encrypted/password-protected/secured PDF is rejected outright regardless of PDF/A status. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](http://content.tylerhost.net/docs/GA/OFSFrequentllyAskedQuestions.pdf)
    > Font resources are included in newly created documents. This is a standard with PDF/A files. Document generating tools use non-supported fonts when creating documents, which results in the inability to convert the document into the standard e-filing format... The JBig font is not a supported font. / PDF files have security settings that can prevent documents from being e-filed... The document security can include a number of different options, any of which will prevent the document file from being processed. To ensure successful document processing, recreate the PDF file with no security options.
  - **Searchable-text / OCR requirement — Odyssey eFileGA**: OCR is NOT required and is not treated as a benefit by the system's own documentation — it is listed as one of the typical causes of automated 'Format Error' rejections, apparently because OCR'd files tend to be larger and/or carry non-standard compression the converter chokes on. This cuts against 'always OCR everything' as a safe default for this specific portal. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](http://content.tylerhost.net/docs/GA/OFSFrequentllyAskedQuestions.pdf)
    > Format errors are typically caused by the following submissions: ... A document that has Optical Character Recognition (OCR) associated with it; usually determined by a larger file size.
  - **Attachment / document count limits — Odyssey eFileGA**: No numeric cap on attachments or documents-per-envelope is stated. The system supports bundling multiple documents into one 'envelope' via 'Add Another Filing.' Functional guidance (not a hard rule) is that anything that will be docketed separately should be its own PDF, and exhibits/appendices should be separate PDF attachments rather than merged into the main pleading file. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](http://content.tylerhost.net/docs/GA/OFSFrequentllyAskedQuestions.pdf)
    > Yes, if all of the documents pertain to the same case, multiple documents can be submitted together by selecting Add Another Filing. The documents will be submitted to the court in a single File & Serve envelope. ... The basic rule of thumb is that anything that will be docketed separately should be in its own separate PDF file. To facilitate internal handling, the court prefers that an appendix or exhibit be created as a separate PDF document from the primary pleading and submitted as an attachment to the e-filing.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Filename character/length restrictions: could not confirm from a primary source I could directly read. A Tyler 'Odyssey File and Serve Cloud' Zendesk support article (ERROR 104: File Name Contains Invalid Characters) appears to describe an alphanumeric-only, short filename limit, but the page returned HTTP 403 on direct fetch (bot-blocked) both times, so I could not read/quote it myself, and it is unclear whether that 'Cloud' product's error page is the same platform build Georgia's classic eFileGA (efilega.tylerhost.net / georgia.tylerhost.net) runs versus a newer product tier used by other states. Not reporting a specific character count given that uncertainty., Bookmark / table-of-contents requirements: no PeachCourt or eFileGA official documentation found (in this bounded pass) requiring or recommending bookmarks/TOC in filed documents. (Only hits were unrelated federal-court context.), Metadata policy: no PeachCourt or eFileGA official documentation found addressing whether metadata should be included, removed, or whether metadata-scrubbed files cause any processing problems. Note: a 'Metadata Redaction Guide' exists for the U.S. Bankruptcy Court for the Northern District of Georgia, but that is a federal CM/ECF system, not a Georgia state-court e-filing system, so it is out of scope and was not used as a source., Georgia's two appellate e-filing systems — the Supreme Court's SCED (efile.gasupreme.us) and the Court of Appeals' EFAST (efast.gaappeals.gov) — were identified as existing but their technical/portal specs were not researched in this pass; only the two mandatory civil trial-court platforms (PeachCourt and Odyssey eFileGA) were covered in depth, since those are what the vast majority of attorney e-filing volume runs through., The Tyler eFileGA FAQ document I was able to read directly (content.tylerhost.net/docs/GA/OFSFrequentllyAskedQuestions.pdf) is dated April 2015 and references outdated browser guidance (Microsoft Silverlight, IE7-10), suggesting it may be stale relative to the live 2026 system even though it is still the document currently hosted/linked at that official Tyler URL for Georgia. Treat its specifics as needing a currency check, not as confirmed-current.

---

## Hawaii (statewide)

- **E-filing system:** Judiciary Electronic Filing and Service System (JEFS) (vendor: Not identified in the official sources reviewed. JEFS is presented as an in-house module of the Hawai‘i Judiciary's own Judiciary Information Management System (JIMS), administered by the Judiciary's Information Technology and Communication Division (ITCD) — no third-party e-filing platform vendor (e.g., Tyler/Odyssey) is named anywhere in the rules, manuals, or FAQs. Online credit-card payment processing (a separate function) is contracted to Hawaii Information Consortium / NIC Hawaii's "Kala" platform, but that is a payments vendor, not the filing platform itself.)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Hawaii has ONE single statewide, mandatory e-filing system — JEFS — not a county-by-county or vendor-fragmented model. JEFS is the attorney/firm-facing filing module of JIMS (Judiciary Information Management System); the other two JIMS-family applications are the internal JIMS Portal (court staff) and eCourt Kōkua (public case lookup/purchase). JEFS covers the Hawaii Supreme Court and Intermediate Court of Appeals (since 2010), District Court criminal (since 2012), Family Court criminal, and — the relevant scope for civil practice — District Court Civil, Circuit Court Civil, Family Court Civil, Land Court, and Tax Appeal Court (added October–November 2019). Governed by the Hawai‘i Electronic Filing and Service Rules (HEFSR). System is available Mon–Sat 4:00 a.m.–midnight HST and Sunday noon–midnight HST (down for nightly maintenance). Self-represented litigants may register for JEFS access but most still file conventionally at the courthouse.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.courts.state.hi.us/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/JEFS_Working_with_PDFs.pdf)
  > The Hawai‘i AOC's own "JEFS Efiling – Working with PDF Files" guide directly and explicitly answers the PDF/A question: "Is PDF/a format required? PDF/a is a specific PDF format used for archiving. It is not required at this time." No other reviewed official source (HEFSR Rules 2.1-2.6, the JEFS Civil User Manual, or the 53-question Civil JEFS FAQ) mentions PDF/A at all, and none flag any encryption/form-field/redaction conflict with it — so there is no documented problem with using it, it is just not mandated. Separately and importantly: JEFS DOES outright reject any password-protected/encrypted PDF regardless of PDF/A status ("Password protected PDFs cannot be uploaded in JEFS") — a redaction/scrub tool targeting Hawaii must ensure the output PDF carries no encryption at all, independent of the PDF/A question.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.courts.state.hi.us/wp-content/uploads/2024/09/hefsr_ada.htm)
  > No reviewed official source — HEFSR Rules 2.1-2.6, the JEFS Civil User Manual (2022), the Civil JEFS Frequently Asked Questions (as of 02/14/20, 53 Q&As covering everything from file size to sealed documents to Bates numbering), or the AOC's own "Working with PDF Files" guide — mentions document metadata in any form: no requirement to include specific metadata, no instruction or recommendation to scrub/remove metadata before filing, and no warning that metadata-scrubbed files cause problems. The technical guidance that exists is narrowly focused on file size (10MB cap), format (PDF only), and removing password/encryption security (which IS required) — metadata hygiene is simply never addressed one way or the other in any of these documents.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size per document (rule text)**: 10 megabytes maximum per PDF document filed through JEFS; the same 10 MB cap applies separately to each exhibit. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.state.hi.us/wp-content/uploads/2024/09/hefsr_ada.htm)
    > the size of each document shall not exceed 10 megabytes
  - **File size limit is per-PDF, not a separate envelope/submission-wide cap**: The 10MB cap is enforced per uploaded PDF file, not as an aggregate 'envelope' limit across a whole submission. A single filing commonly bundles a lead document plus several supporting/exhibit PDFs, each independently capped at 10MB; oversized documents must be split into multiple sequentially-labeled parts (e.g., 'Exhibit A, Part 1 of 3') and uploaded as separate attachments. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.state.hi.us/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/JEFS_Working_with_PDFs.pdf)
    > JEFS Efiling accepts Portable Document Format (PDF) documents up to 10 megabytes (MB). A PDF which exceeds this limit can be split into smaller files for submission... Separate your files to keep the size down. The court allows you to efile your documents in sections as long as each file is under 10 MB.
  - **Accepted file format**: Only PDF (Adobe PDF format) is accepted for documents filed through JEFS; no other file types may be uploaded. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.state.hi.us/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/JEFS_User_Manual.pdf)
    > a JEFS User shall file each document as a PDF document through JEFS for docketing and storage in JIMS... Documents must be in Adobe PDF format as required per Rule 2.2 of the Hawaii Electronic Filing and Service Rules (HEFSR).
  - **Encrypted / password-protected PDFs are rejected**: JEFS will not accept a password-protected or otherwise security-encrypted PDF; the filer must strip the password/security before upload (e.g., Acrobat Pro's 'Remove Security', or print-to-PDF from Chrome as a workaround). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.state.hi.us/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/JEFS_Working_with_PDFs.pdf)
    > Password protected PDFs cannot be uploaded in JEFS.
  - **PDF/A requirement**: PDF/A is explicitly NOT required for JEFS filings ('not required at this time'); the guidance neither recommends nor prohibits it, and no source flags any encryption/form-field/redaction conflict with PDF/A specifically. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.state.hi.us/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/JEFS_Working_with_PDFs.pdf)
    > Is PDF/a format required? PDF/a is a specific PDF format used for archiving. It is not required at this time.
  - **Searchable text / OCR requirement**: No searchable-text or OCR requirement is documented anywhere in JEFS's official rules or guides. The AOC's own PDF-preparation guide affirmatively treats scanning a paper-only document into an image PDF as a normal, accepted filing method, and even gives scanner-resolution guidance (200-300 dpi) without ever mentioning OCR or text-searchability as a requirement. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.state.hi.us/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/JEFS_Working_with_PDFs.pdf)
    > Only documents that exist as paper-only must be scanned to create a PDF... Resolution of scanned documents should be set no less than 200 dpi and no greater than 300 dpi (dots per inch).
  - **In-portal 'Document Name' field length (distinct from the actual PDF filename)**: The Document Name typed into the JEFS filing form (displayed on the Notice of Electronic Filing) is capped at 400 characters. This is a metadata/label field entered in the web UI, not a restriction on the actual filename of the PDF the filer selects from their own computer — no official source restricts the uploaded file's own filename. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.state.hi.us/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/JEFS_User_Manual.pdf)
    > Enter the Document Name* (up to 400 characters) for this document. The name entered will be displayed on the Notice of Electronic Filing (NEF).
  - **Bookmark requirement — narrow, agency-appeal-only**: There is no general bookmark or table-of-contents requirement for ordinary JEFS filings. A bookmark requirement exists only for the Certified Record on Appeal filed by a government agency in an agency appeal, which must be bookmarked and Bates-stamped. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.state.hi.us/wp-content/uploads/2019/10/Civil_JEFS_-FAQ.pdf)
    > In eFiling the Certified Record on Appeal, the Agency shall comply with the submission requirements of HRAP Rule 10 and 11. In addition, the bookmarked PDF created by the agency shall include Bates stamping/numbering.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** PDF version compatibility range (e.g., minimum/maximum PDF spec version such as 1.4-1.7) accepted by JEFS — not stated in any official source reviewed, Filename character/length restrictions on the actual uploaded PDF file itself — not found; only the separate in-portal 'Document Name' metadata field (400-character cap) is documented, Attachment/exhibit count limit per filing — no maximum number of attachments/exhibits is stated anywhere; only the per-file 10MB size cap is documented

---

## Idaho

- **E-filing system:** Odyssey File &amp; Serve (the e-filing module of Idaho's statewide "iCourt" court-modernization project; end-user portal at idaho.tylertech.cloud/OfsWeb) (vendor: Tyler Technologies)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Idaho has ONE mandatory statewide e-filing system, not a fragmented county-by-county model like California. In 2013 the Idaho Supreme Court/Administrative Office of the Courts selected Tyler Technologies' Odyssey platform under the "iCourt" modernization initiative and rolled it out county-by-county (pilot: Twin Falls, early adopter: Ada, then three regional waves) until it covered all counties. E-filing/e-service is now mandatory for all active members of the Idaho State Bar (self-represented litigants may opt in). The live portal (confirmed by direct fetch, version banner "2024.6.4.11424", 2026 copyright, no migration notice) is idaho.tylertech.cloud/OfsWeb. The binding technical rules are the Idaho Rules for Electronic Filing and Service (I.R.E.F.S.), promulgated directly by the Idaho Supreme Court specifically to govern the e-filing system's format/size/technical behavior (distinct from the Idaho Rules of Civil Procedure, which were not used here) — Rule 6 was most recently amended Dec. 18, 2024, effective Jan. 1, 2025, so it reflects the current, live configuration. I.R.E.F.S. Rule 6(d) also incorporates-by-reference a Court-approved "Electronic Filing Guide," which is still hosted at icourt.idaho.gov but is internally dated "Draft: October 19, 2016" — I used it only for details not superseded by the current Rule 6 text (e.g., the font-compatibility warning). I also found an older Tyler-hosted FAQ PDF (content.tylerhost.net) citing 25MB/document and 35MB/envelope caps — this is stale/superseded; the current, amended Rule 6 explicitly states 50MB/document and 100MB/envelope, and I treated the Idaho Supreme Court's own current rule page as authoritative over the older vendor FAQ. A separate-looking portal at efileid.tylertech.cloud ("eFile - Idaho") also appears live but only rendered a loading screen on fetch; I could not confirm whether it is a newer parallel "Odyssey File and Serve Cloud" front end or an EFSP-integration endpoint, so I did not rely on it for any constraint.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://isc.idaho.gov/IREFS6)
  > Rule 6(a)(1) names "text-searchable Portable Document Format (PDF)" and "text-searchable Portable Document Format/A (PDF/A)" as two equally acceptable ways to satisfy the searchable-text requirement — neither is called out as required, preferred, or discouraged relative to the other, so there is no stated PDF/A preference either way. Separately, the Court's own Electronic Filing Guide (incorporated by reference via Rule 6(d)) flags a concrete technical risk that surfaces more often in PDF/A workflows: "Documents should contain standard fonts... This is a standard with PDF/A files. Document generating tools use fonts not supported when creating documents, which results in the inability to convert the document into the standard efiling format. (CID and JBig fonts may lead to technical problems and rejection)." So PDF/A is not unsafe as a rule, but a naive PDF/A conversion that embeds non-standard/CID/JBIG2 fonts (common in some OCR and scan-to-PDF/A tools) is called out by name as a rejection risk.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://isc.idaho.gov/IREFS15)
  > I reviewed the full I.R.E.F.S. rule list (Rules 1–21, https://isc.idaho.gov/irefs) plus Rule 6 (format/size) and Rule 20 (appellate record) directly. None mention document metadata (XMP/document-properties) at all — no requirement to include specific metadata, no instruction to scrub it before filing, and no statement that metadata-scrubbed files cause upload/acceptance problems. The only privacy-oriented filing rule is Rule 15, "Privacy Protections for Filings Made with the Court," and it governs redacting personal identifiers that are visible in the document's content (SSNs to last 4 digits, DOB to year only, minors to initials, financial/DL account numbers to last 4 digits) via omission or a filed reference list — a content-redaction rule, not a file-metadata rule: "It is the responsibility of the filer to ensure that protected personal data identifiers are omitted or redacted from documents before the documents are filed, whether filed electronically or conventionally."

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size**: 50 MB maximum per PDF document; if a document exceeds that it must be split into parts of ≤50 MB each. Separately, the whole envelope (all documents/files submitted together in one filing transaction) is capped at 100 MB — a filer must split into multiple envelopes if the combined submission would exceed that. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://isc.idaho.gov/IREFS6)
    > ...not exceed 50 megabytes. A document that exceeds the size limit must be broken down and submitted as separate files that do not exceed 50 megabytes each... An envelope cannot exceed 100 megabytes. A filer may submit multiple envelopes at the same time if a singular submission would exceed 100 megabytes.
  - **Accepted PDF version / file format**: PDF only (no other file types for the document itself). Must be text-searchable, and should be produced by direct PDF conversion from the source file rather than scanned, whenever that's possible. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://isc.idaho.gov/IREFS6)
    > A document...submitted electronically to the court must be in the form of a text-searchable Portable Document Format (PDF) or a text-searchable Portable Document Format/A (PDF/A) file, be directly converted to PDF rather than scanned (if possible), and not exceed 50 megabytes.
  - **Searchable-text / OCR requirement**: Text-searchability is required for filed documents (motions, briefs, memoranda, etc.) by default. Two carve-outs don't need to be searchable: (1) attachments/exhibits that are scanned images of an original, and (2) current Court Assistance Office forms pre-approved by the Idaho Supreme Court. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://isc.idaho.gov/IREFS6)
    > A document that is an attachment or exhibit (not motion, brief, memorandum, etc.) that is a scanned image of its original form, may be in standard PDF format and need not be text searchable as required in subsection (1) above.
  - **Bookmark / table-of-contents requirement**: Not required for ordinary trial-court e-filings — Rule 6 says nothing about bookmarks. Electronic bookmarks ARE specifically required, but only when compiling the Clerk's Record or an Agency Record for an appeal to the Idaho Supreme Court. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://isc.idaho.gov/IREFS20)
    > The record must contain electronic bookmarks that link to each document in the electronic record.
  - **Attachment count limits**: No stated numeric cap on the number of attachments/documents. Instead, the rule pushes the opposite direction: attachments must be merged into one unified PDF 'to the extent practicable,' with named exceptions that must be filed as their own separate document — a proposed order/judgment needing court signature, a sealed/confidential/exempt-from-disclosure attachment, and a fee-waiver application. The practical ceiling is the 100 MB per-envelope size cap, not a count of files. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://isc.idaho.gov/IREFS6)
    > ...a document that includes attachments must be submitted as a unified single PDF file to the extent practicable... (A) A proposed order, judgment, or other document that requires court signature must be submitted as a separate document. (B) An attachment that is exempt from public disclosure, was previously ordered sealed, or is the subject of a motion to seal must be submitted...as a separate document...(C) An application for fee waiver must be submitted as a separate document.
  - **PDF/A requirement**: Neither required nor preferred over a standard text-searchable PDF — the rule lists PDF/A as a co-equal alternative that satisfies the same searchable-text requirement. However, the Court's own Electronic Filing Guide separately warns that non-standard embedded fonts — which it specifically calls out as more of a PDF/A phenomenon — can make a document unconvertible into the e-filing system's accepted format and lead to rejection. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://icourt.idaho.gov/docs/Electronic-Filing-Guide.pdf)
    > Documents should contain standard fonts. Font resources are included in newly created documents. This is a standard with PDF/A files. Document generating tools use fonts not supported when creating documents, which results in the inability to convert the document into the standard efiling format. (CID and JBig fonts may lead to technical problems and rejection).
  - **Metadata policy**: Silent on file-level metadata entirely — no rule requires adding specific metadata, no rule instructs scrubbing metadata before filing, and nothing indicates metadata-scrubbed files cause upload or acceptance problems. The system's only privacy-protection rule (Rule 15) is about redacting personal identifiers that are visible in the document's content, not about the PDF's metadata/document-properties fields. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://isc.idaho.gov/IREFS15)
    > It is the responsibility of the filer to ensure that protected personal data identifiers are omitted or redacted from documents before the documents are filed, whether filed electronically or conventionally.
  - **Other technical constraints (bonus, from the Court's Electronic Filing Guide)**: Documents may not be secured/password-protected or otherwise access-restricted; must be self-contained with all hyperlinks/shortcuts to external documents or websites removed; use 8.5x11" portrait orientation; scanned images should be set above 200 DPI and in black-and-white unless color is legible-necessary. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://icourt.idaho.gov/docs/Electronic-Filing-Guide.pdf)
    > Access - Documents may not be secured, password-protected, or have other features limiting access. Documents shall be self-contained – Remove all hyperlinks or shortcuts to external documents or websites.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Filename character/length restrictions — could not confirm an Idaho-specific limit from a directly-read primary source. I.R.E.F.S. Rule 6 and the Court's Electronic Filing Guide say nothing about filename format. A generic Tyler 'Odyssey File and Serve Cloud' help-center article (filenames ≤24 characters, letters/numbers only, no punctuation) turned up in search results, but the page returned HTTP 403 on direct fetch so I could only read a secondhand search-index summary of it, not the primary source itself — and that same summary states filename rules are configured per-court/per-state, so I can't confirm it reflects Idaho's actual Odyssey File & Serve configuration (idaho.tylertech.cloud/OfsWeb) rather than a different state's instance or the separate 'Cloud' product line. Not reporting a number without being able to verify it against Idaho's own instance.

---

## Illinois

- **E-filing system:** eFileIL (the Illinois Supreme Court's statewide Electronic Filing Manager / EFM) — the filer-facing implementation is Tyler Technologies' Odyssey File & Serve platform, accessed through court-certified third-party "Electronic Filing Service Providers" (EFSPs) (vendor: Tyler Technologies (Odyssey File & Serve is the EFM backend; multiple certified EFSPs — e.g. Odyssey File & Serve Cloud itself, and other approved vendors — serve as filer-facing portals that all route through this single statewide EFM))
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Confirmed: Illinois is NOT fragmented county-by-county like California. Pursuant to Illinois Supreme Court Order M.R. 18368 (In re: Mandatory Electronic Filing in Civil Cases), a single statewide "Electronic Filing Manager" (EFM) — implemented as Tyler Technologies' Odyssey File & Serve — is the mandatory backend for the Supreme Court, all Appellate Court districts, and all 87 circuit courts. E-filing became mandatory in civil cases in the Supreme Court/Appellate Court on July 1, 2017, and in all circuit courts on January 1, 2018. Filers register with any court-approved "Electronic Filing Service Provider" (EFSP) — a third-party web portal — and every EFSP transmits through the same statewide EFM to the intended court. So there is genuine vendor choice at the front-end-portal layer (similar in flavor to California's multiple-EFSP model), but a single unified statewide technical backend/rule set (unlike California, where each Superior Court independently approves its own providers and rules). All primary sources below are official Illinois Supreme Court / Administrative Office of the Illinois Courts (AOC) documents, hosted on efile.illinoiscourts.gov or the courts' own Azure resource storage (ilcourtsaudio.blob.core.windows.net), not vendor marketing.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://efile.illinoiscourts.gov/wp-content/uploads/2022/10/2022_eFileIL_Electronic_Document_Standards_Revised.pdf)
  > No official Illinois eFileIL document located — including the comprehensive statewide "eFileIL Electronic Document Standards" (which affirmatively covers PDF format, OCR, scan DPI, page size, font, margins, security/encryption, and embedded audio/video/executable content) — mentions PDF/A anywhere, positively or negatively. The Circuit Court and Reviewing Court Rejection Standards, the Supreme Court e-filing manual, and the Record on Appeal standards likewise never use the term. The Standards do flatly state that e-filed documents "cannot contain any security or encryption," which is a related-but-distinct rule (it bars password/security-encrypted PDFs; PDF/A itself is not an encryption format, so this does not amount to an implicit PDF/A prohibition, but it's the closest adjacent rule found).
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://efile.illinoiscourts.gov/wp-content/uploads/2022/10/2022_eFileIL_Electronic_Document_Standards_Revised.pdf)
  > No official Illinois eFileIL document located requires, recommends, or prohibits removing/scrubbing metadata from e-filed documents, nor mentions document metadata at all — despite the "eFileIL Electronic Document Standards" and the Circuit/Reviewing Court "Electronic Filing Rejection Standards" (the latter updated as recently as April 1, 2026) being reasonably thorough on adjacent technical-hygiene topics (viruses/malware certification, embedded files, security/encryption, tracking tags in the Record-on-Appeal standard). Separately, Illinois DOES have a strong, well-documented rule requiring redaction of personal-identifying information/SSNs from the visible content of filings (Supreme Court Rules 15 & 138 — a defined rejection reason, CodeID 264866), but that is a content-redaction rule, not a file-metadata-scrubbing rule, and is arguably closer to "rules of court" than a portal/technical constraint, so it is not reported here as the answer to the metadata question.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size — trial (circuit) courts**: 25 MB maximum per individual document; 50 MB maximum per envelope/transaction for Illinois circuit (trial) courts. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efile.illinoiscourts.gov/wp-content/uploads/2022/10/2022_eFileIL_Electronic_Document_Standards_Revised.pdf)
    > The maximum file size for a document e-filed through eFileIL is 25mb., with a maximum envelope size of 50mb.
  - **Maximum file size — Supreme Court & Appellate Court (reviewing courts)**: 150 MB maximum per envelope for filings to the Illinois Supreme Court and Appellate Court districts (no separate lower per-document cap is stated for reviewing courts in this standard). The companion Record-on-Appeal standard separately instructs that each PDF volume of an appellate record be assembled at no more than 150 MB. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efile.illinoiscourts.gov/wp-content/uploads/2022/10/2022_eFileIL_Electronic_Document_Standards_Revised.pdf)
    > The maximum file size for an envelope e-filed through eFileIL to the Supreme Court and Appellate Court Districts is 150mb.
  - **Accepted PDF format / file requirements**: Must be submitted as PDF; OCR PDF is called for; if scanned, minimum 300 DPI / maximum 600 DPI in black-and-white mode; page size 8.5x11 inches. Documents cannot contain any security or encryption, and cannot contain embedded audio or video files. Separately, a fillable/interactive PDF form that is still fillable at submission ('unflattened') is a defined, named rejection reason under the circuit court rejection standards — it must be flattened first. No official source specifies a specific PDF version number (e.g., 1.4, 1.7, 2.0) — only that the file must be 'PDF' (defined generically as 'Portable Document Format, a proprietary file format developed by Adobe Systems, Inc.'). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efile.illinoiscourts.gov/wp-content/uploads/2022/10/2022_eFileIL_Electronic_Document_Standards_Revised.pdf)
    > E-filed documents cannot contain any security or encryption. Embedded audio or video files in PDF document are not allowed.
  - **Fillable/interactive PDF must be flattened**: A PDF form submitted while still fillable/interactive is a standardized, named rejection reason statewide for circuit court e-filings; the filer must flatten it and resubmit. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://ilcourtsaudio.blob.core.windows.net/antilles-resources/resources/44154505-ae47-43f5-ad2c-542ef24d39fc/Circuit_Court_eFiling_Rejection_Standards.pdf)
    > 10. Unflattened PDF. ... The submitted form is still fillable. Please flatten and resubmit.
  - **Searchable-text / OCR requirement**: OCR/searchable text is called for 'when possible' — framed as a strong preference/soft requirement rather than an absolute mandate that blocks filing outright. The standard explicitly prefers generating the PDF natively from the authoring program over scanning specifically so it will be text-searchable: scan-based OCR is the fallback, not the preferred path. Separately, an illegible/unreadable/blank document is a defined statewide rejection reason for circuit courts. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efile.illinoiscourts.gov/wp-content/uploads/2022/10/2022_eFileIL_Electronic_Document_Standards_Revised.pdf)
    > When possible, the following parameters apply to e-filed documents submitted through eFileIL: a. Optical Character Recognition (OCR) PDF. ... The OCR PDF document should be created directly from the program creating that document, rather than from a scanned image of the document.
  - **Filename / file-description character limit**: The statewide Electronic Filing Manager (EFM) caps both a document's 'file name' and its 'file description' field at 150 characters each; exceeding either causes the filing to fail outright. This is documented in the Illinois Supreme Court's own e-filing manual; because the EFM is the single shared statewide backend for all Illinois courts (not a Supreme-Court-specific system), this reads as a system-wide technical limit rather than a Supreme-Court-only policy choice, though it was not independently found restated in a circuit-court-specific manual. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://ilcourtsaudio.blob.core.windows.net/antilles-resources/resources/05df0957-c20a-441d-9f79-fd16e65dc7d2/SCt_efiling_user_manual.pdf)
    > The EFM limits a document's "file name" and "file description" to 150 characters. Any document with a name or description exceeding 150 characters will fail to e-file.
  - **Bookmark / table-of-contents requirement**: For ordinary attorney-filed documents (motions, pleadings, briefs) under the general eFileIL Electronic Document Standards, no bookmark or table-of-contents requirement was found. A detailed, mandatory scheme of Tables of Contents plus PDF bookmarks DOES exist, but it applies specifically and only to the Record on Appeal — the circuit-clerk-assembled case record transmitted to a reviewing court on appeal, not a document an attorney prepares and files as a normal matter of course. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efile.illinoiscourts.gov/wp-content/uploads/2022/10/IL-Record-on-Appeal-Standards.pdf)
    > Where possible, each PDF section shall include bookmarks, immediately viewable when the document is opened, to individual sections and documents in the same order as they appear in the corresponding Table of Contents to facilitate navigation and location of specific contents within the record.
  - **Attachment / document count limits per envelope**: No numeric cap on the number of attachments or documents per envelope/transaction was found. Instead the portal enforces structural rules: each individual document must be submitted as its own single PDF (multiple distinct documents combined into one PDF are rejected as 'Multiple documents submitted as one PDF'; conversely splitting one document across multiple PDFs is also rejected, unless required by file-size limits); exhibits/attachments must travel in the same envelope or the same PDF as the document they support; and documents for different case numbers must go in separate envelopes. In practice, the ceiling on what fits in one envelope is the file-size cap (50 MB trial court / 150 MB reviewing court), not a document-count limit. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://ilcourtsaudio.blob.core.windows.net/antilles-resources/resources/44154505-ae47-43f5-ad2c-542ef24d39fc/Circuit_Court_eFiling_Rejection_Standards.pdf)
    > 11. Multiple documents submitted as one PDF. ... Multiple documents cannot be submitted in a single .PDF file. Please separate the documents and resubmit each separately.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Exact PDF version/spec number (e.g. PDF 1.4, 1.7, 2.0) — no official Illinois eFileIL source specifies one beyond generically requiring 'PDF' (Adobe's Portable Document Format)., Independent circuit-court-specific confirmation of the 150-character filename/file-description limit — it is documented in the Illinois Supreme Court's own e-filing manual (describing an EFM-level system limit that should apply statewide) but was not separately located restated in a circuit-court-specific manual or the circuit court rejection standards.

---

## Indiana

- **E-filing system:** Indiana E-Filing System (IEFS) — statewide mandatory system, per the Indiana Office of Judicial Administration's official "E-filing User Guide, Indiana Statewide E-filing System." Confirmed live and current as of the guide's last update (May 15, 2026). Note: Indiana's judiciary has been developing a new state-built platform called "INfile" intended to eventually replace IEFS, but the AOC's own most-recently-updated user guide (dated 2026-05-15) still describes IEFS as the live system — so IEFS is what is actually in force today, not INfile. (vendor: Tyler Technologies operates the back-end e-filing manager (EFM) — the central hub, historically branded "Odyssey File & Serve" — that all approved E-Filing Service Providers (EFSPs) submit through. Indiana runs a multi-vendor front-end model: attorneys/filers pick from a list of Supreme-Court-approved EFSPs (third-party paid vendors, or the state's own no-cost EFSP at efile.incourts.gov, itself Tyler-built) to actually prepare and submit filings into the single statewide IEFS backend.)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Indiana is NOT fragmented like California. It is architecturally closer to the Texas eFileTexas/Tyler model: ONE statewide mandatory system (IEFS) that all Indiana trial, appellate (Court of Appeals, Supreme Court), and Tax Court filings funnel through, with a marketplace of interchangeable EFSP front-end software vendors sitting on top of the same backend. E-filing is mandatory for all attorneys in all Indiana courts (Trial Rules 86-88; Appellate Rule 68); self-represented litigants may e-file but aren't required to. A small number of counties (Allen, Howard, Johnson, Lake, LaPorte, Madison, Porter, St. Joseph, Tippecanoe) use more than one back-end Case Management System and require the filer to pick the right one for the case type — this is a CMS-routing quirk, not a separate e-filing portal, and doesn't change the single-IEFS-backend picture. Primary source used for all findings below: the Indiana Office of Judicial Administration's official "E-filing User Guide, Indiana Statewide E-filing System" (https://www.in.gov/courts/files/efiling-user-guide.pdf), last updated 2026-05-15, which states on its cover it is "prescribed by the Chief Administrative Officer of the Indiana Office of Judicial Administration" and that "the instructions in this guide must be followed per Indiana Rules of Trial Procedure 87(F)" — i.e., this is binding technical/portal guidance, not a summary.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.in.gov/courts/files/efiling-user-guide.pdf)
  > The official 24-page E-filing User Guide has a dedicated "Formatting documents" section (pp. 21-24) covering PDF creation methods, scanned-PDF settings, file-size limits, page layout, a "Prohibited items" list, bookmarks/hyperlinks, special characters, filenames, and signatures — and never mentions "PDF/A," "ISO 19005," or "archival" format anywhere in the document. The guide's "Prohibited items" list bars "encryption, password protection, or other features that limit access" and "embedded files" generally (not PDF/A-specifically) — relevant context if a PDF/A conversion tool were to introduce either, but this is a generic prohibition unconnected to any PDF/A discussion. No separate technical-specifications page distinct from this guide was found on the courts.in.gov e-filing help site. Net: PDF/A is neither required, preferred, nor prohibited by name — the AOC's guidance is simply silent on it.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** required -- [source](https://www.in.gov/courts/files/efiling-user-guide.pdf)
  > Scoped requirement, not a blanket "strip all metadata from every filing" instruction. In the "Confidential information in filings" section, the guide states as a mandatory (must-level) instruction: "When you redact confidential information from a document you must make sure the confidential information cannot be retrieved. Redaction methods that were sufficient for paper documents will not always be sufficient for electronic documents," followed by a boxed warning: "Covering text with a black rectangle, highlighting it in black, reducing its size, or changing its color to white does not constitute redaction. You must also ensure that there is no confidential information in the document properties, also called metadata." This makes metadata-scrubbing mandatory specifically wherever a filing contains confidential information (redacted content) — not stated as a universal requirement for every ordinary filing regardless of content. No language anywhere in the guide suggests scrubbed/stripped metadata itself ever causes rejection or a technical problem, so nothing found conflicts with treating metadata-scrubbing as a safe universal default.

**Constraints found:**
  - **maxFileSize**: 50 MB limit per document; 75 MB total limit per envelope (submission). Exception: in the appellate courts, each volume of a brief's appendix is limited to the lesser of 250 pages or 50 MB. Oversized documents must be split into clearly labeled volumes ("Volume 1 of 3," etc.) rather than submitted as one file. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.in.gov/courts/files/efiling-user-guide.pdf)
    > Trial and Appellate Courts: 50 MB limit on each document* / 75 MB total limit on each envelope ... Filings that exceed these limits cannot be submitted. If a document exceeds the limit, you must break it into separate documents with each file clearly labeled in order ("Volume 1 of 3," "Volume 2 of 3," etc.) in the comments field. *Note that in the appellate courts, each volume of an appendix to a brief is limited to the lesser of 250 pages or 50 MB.
  - **fileFormatAndPdfVersion**: All e-filed documents must be submitted as PDF; no other file format is accepted. The guide does not specify a required PDF version number (e.g., 1.4/1.7/2.0) — any standard PDF is acceptable subject to the other rules (no encryption/password protection, no embedded files, readable/legible). Creating the PDF by exporting/saving directly from the source document is described as "Ideal"; scanning a paper original is only "Acceptable." _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.in.gov/courts/files/efiling-user-guide.pdf)
    > All documents must be submitted as PDF ... Creating the PDF: Ideal: Save or export the source document to PDF format electronically. Acceptable: Scan paper documents to PDF. ... Documents must not contain: Encryption, password protection, or other features that limit access / Unreadable words or images / Invalid or corrupted tables / Embedded files / Any other form of information that cannot be readily viewed in its entirety with PDF viewing software.
  - **searchableTextOcr**: OCR is instructed as a mandatory step whenever a document is scanned ("Always apply optical character recognition (OCR)"), listed alongside other required scanning settings (300 DPI, TIFF/G4 for black-and-white, etc.). Digitally-created (non-scanned) PDFs are separately favored precisely because exporting preserves searchable text. The guide does not state that a non-searchable/non-OCR'd PDF will be outright rejected by the portal, but frames OCR as a required scanning setting, not an optional nicety. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.in.gov/courts/files/efiling-user-guide.pdf)
    > Use the following settings when scanning: Resolution of 300 DPI ... For black and white: Scan to PDF or Tagged Image File Format with Group 4 compression (TIFF with G4 compression) ... Always apply optical character recognition (OCR). ... Unlike scanning a document, exporting to PDF preserves the text of the source document, making it searchable and resulting in smaller file size.
  - **filenameRestrictions**: The e-filed document's file name must not exceed 100 characters, counting spaces and the ".pdf" extension. A non-compliant filename blocks processing outright (this is enforced at the portal level, not just a style guideline). No specific character/symbol blacklist for filenames is given (the guide's special-character discussion is about in-document text, not filenames). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.in.gov/courts/files/efiling-user-guide.pdf)
    > The name of the document you are e-filing must not exceed 100 characters. This includes any spaces and the file extension (.pdf). Filings with documents that do not comply cannot be processed by the e-filing system.
  - **bookmarksTableOfContents**: PDF bookmarks are optional for all filings — never a portal requirement, only encouraged for reader navigation. However, appellate appendices carry a distinct, mandatory structural TOC rule: an appendix must be split into at least 2 PDF volumes, and Volume 1 must always be the table of contents for the entire appendix (and must never contain confidential information); failing to submit the appendix TOC as its own separate volume is explicitly listed as a common error that triggers a Notice of Defect under Appellate Rule 51(F). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.in.gov/courts/files/efiling-user-guide.pdf)
    > Bookmarks help the reader navigate a PDF, so they are welcome, though not required. ... You will always divide your appendix document into at least 2 PDF files (2 volumes). Each volume is limited to the lesser of 250 pages or 50 MB. Volume 1 will always be the table of contents for the entire appendix, and it should never contain confidential information. ... Common errors in documents e-filed so far include ... Appendix table of contents isn't submitted as a separate volume – App. R. 51(F)
