**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Attachment count limit — the official guide describes an envelope as able to contain "multiple filings" and a filing as able to contain a lead document plus attachments, but nowhere states a maximum NUMBER of attachments/documents per filing or per envelope. The only enforced ceilings found in the primary source are size-based (50 MB per document, 75 MB total per envelope), not count-based. Could not confirm a hard numeric attachment-count cap from the AOC's guide or its linked EFSP tutorials within the bounded research effort — do not assume one exists.

---

## Iowa (statewide)

- **E-filing system:** EDMS (Electronic Document Management System), publicly branded to filers as "eFile" — one mandatory system covering both Iowa District Court and the Iowa Supreme Court / Court of Appeals (appellate), used in all 99 counties (vendor: Not confirmed by an official Iowa Judicial Branch source. A 2015 press release from vendor Tybera Systems states Iowa's statewide e-filing rollout was completed using its platform ("Iowa Completes Statewide eFiling Implementation" — tybera.com), but this is vendor marketing, not a court-issued statement, so treat as unverified context only, not a sourced fact.)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Confirmed: Iowa is NOT fragmented by county — it runs ONE statewide mandatory e-filing/case-management portal (EDMS, filer-facing name "eFile") administered by the Iowa Judicial Branch, used for both district court and appellate filings statewide. Two current, dated primary manuals were located and read in full: (1) the 'eFile User Guide' (district court, updated September 23, 2024, https://www.iowacourts.gov/static/media/cms/E0002_569890E51EF7C.pdf) and (2) the 'Electronic Document Management System Appellate eFiler User Guide' (https://www.iowacourts.gov/static/media/cms/ACP_EDMS_eFiler_Full_2D77D488A8499.pdf). NOTE ON A STALE SOURCE: an older legacy help site still live on the court's own domain (https://www.iowacourts.state.ia.us/Efile/manual/fiPreFile.htm, undated) states much smaller and conflicting limits — "2 MB limit for each document" and a "10 MB per submission" cap. These figures directly contradict the current, dated (Sept 2024) eFile User Guide's limits (20 MB per submission for district court; 150 MB per submission / 50 MB per document for appellate) and appear to be an unmaintained holdover from an earlier system version. All constraint values below rely on the current, dated 2024 guides, not the stale legacy page. The FAQ page and the 'eFile Instructions' / 'eFile Resources' landing pages on iowacourts.gov were also checked and contain no additional technical/portal specifications beyond what the two manuals already cover (mostly registration/account FAQs and links to the same PDFs).
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.iowacourts.gov/static/media/cms/E0002_569890E51EF7C.pdf)
  > Neither current official manual (the district 'eFile User Guide' nor the 'EDMS Appellate eFiler User Guide') contains the string "PDF/A" anywhere, despite both having a dedicated, fairly detailed "Formatting and Technical Requirements" / "Prepare Documents" section covering document type, page format, size limits, color, scan resolution, viewability, protected information, and password-protection. The requirement is simply "submitted as PDF (.pdf) files" with no version or archival-format qualifier. No indication of PDF/A being required, preferred, or causing problems was found in any official source searched.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.iowacourts.gov/static/media/cms/E0002_569890E51EF7C.pdf)
  > No official Iowa source (the 2024 eFile User Guide, the EDMS Appellate eFiler User Guide, or the eFile FAQ/Instructions/Resources pages) mentions file-embedded metadata (e.g., Word/PDF document properties, author, revision history) at all — neither a requirement to include it, a recommendation to scrub it, nor any warning that scrubbed files cause problems. The only "metadata" concept documented is the filer-entered case/document data on the system's own web-form "Electronic Cover Sheet" (title, category, party info) used for docket routing — an unrelated concept from embedded file metadata. Protected personal identifiers (SSNs, financial account numbers, etc.) must be redacted from document content, but this is a content-redaction rule, not a file-metadata-scrubbing rule.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size — District Court, per submission/envelope**: 20 MB per single submission; any number of individual documents may be bundled into that submission as long as the aggregate does not exceed 20 MB _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.iowacourts.gov/static/media/cms/E0002_569890E51EF7C.pdf)
    > The size limit for District Court filings is 20 MB per single submission. ... Any number of individual documents may be included in a submission, as long as they do not exceed the size limit.
  - **Maximum file size — Appellate Court, per submission/envelope**: 150 MB per single submission _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.iowacourts.gov/static/media/cms/E0002_569890E51EF7C.pdf)
    > The size limit for Appellate Court filings is 150 MB per single submission.
  - **Maximum file size — Appellate Court, per individual document**: 50 MB per document (separate from, and nested within, the 150 MB per-submission cap) _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.iowacourts.gov/static/media/cms/ACP_EDMS_eFiler_Full_2D77D488A8499.pdf)
    > Document Size – There is a 50 MB limit per document. Multiple documents can be submitted per case. The submission size limit is 150 MB.
  - **Accepted file format / password protection**: All filed documents must be PDF (.pdf) except proposed orders, which must be a Microsoft Word-editable file; documents must not be password-protected. No specific PDF version number (e.g. 1.4 vs 1.7) is specified. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.iowacourts.gov/static/media/cms/E0002_569890E51EF7C.pdf)
    > All documents must be submitted as PDF (.pdf) files except for proposed orders. ... Proposed orders must be filed in a Microsoft Word editable format. ... Password Protected: Documents for filing must not be password protected.
  - **Searchable text / OCR requirement**: Searchable PDF is required 'whenever possible.' Scanned paper documents must be OCR'd. Non-searchable PDF is permitted only as a fallback when a searchable version genuinely isn't possible (e.g., handwritten documents, photographs). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.iowacourts.gov/static/media/cms/E0002_569890E51EF7C.pdf)
    > PDFs must be searchable whenever possible. ... When it is necessary to scan printed (paper) documents for filing, you must convert the scanned image to text using OCR. ... If submitting a document (or portion of a document) in searchable PDF format is not possible, the document or portion may be scanned and submitted in non-searchable PDF format. Handwritten documents and photographs not available in electronic form are examples of documents that may be submitted in non-searchable PDF format.
  - **Scan resolution guidance / rejection threshold**: Recommended scanner resolution is 200 dpi; documents scanned above 300 DPI 'may be rejected for filing.' _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.iowacourts.gov/static/media/cms/E0002_569890E51EF7C.pdf)
    > The scanner resolution should be set to 200 dpi. Higher resolution increases the file size. Documents scanned at resolutions higher than 300 DPI may be rejected for filing.
  - **Bookmark / hyperlink policy**: Bookmarks and hyperlinks are permitted but not required. In-document bookmarks (internal navigation aids) and external hyperlinks to public sources of law/opinions are allowed. The system does not support hyperlinking from one filed document to a separate document/attachment within the case file. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.iowacourts.gov/static/media/cms/E0002_569890E51EF7C.pdf)
    > It is not possible to hyperlink between one document in an electronic court file to another document or attachments within the electronic court file. Documents may contain these types of hyperlinks: • Bookmarks: Hyperlinks to a destination within the same document that help the reader navigate a long document. • External hyperlink: Link to a destination outside the document that provide convenient access to publicly available sources of law or court opinions.
  - **Attachment / document count limit per submission**: No fixed numeric cap on the number of documents per submission — the constraint is purely the aggregate size limit (20 MB district / 150 MB appellate), not a document count. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.iowacourts.gov/static/media/cms/E0002_569890E51EF7C.pdf)
    > Any number of individual documents may be included in a submission, as long as they do not exceed the size limit.
  - **Document-bundling prohibition**: Each distinct document must be uploaded as its own separate PDF file within a submission — multiple documents (e.g., a motion and its proposed order) may not be combined into one PDF, and public and confidential documents may never be combined into the same file. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.iowacourts.gov/static/media/cms/E0002_569890E51EF7C.pdf)
    > If you want to submit multiple documents simultaneously, each document must be submitted as a separate PDF file and should not be combined with another file. Motions and proposed orders must be submitted separately... Do not combine public and confidential documents. ... Do not combine multiple documents in one pdf.
  - **Oversize-document handling**: If a document would exceed the size limit, it must be split into smaller parts filed as sequential separate submissions, labeled 'Part 1 of 3,' 'Part 2 of 3,' etc., filed one after another, with the clerk alerted that the parts are one document. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.iowacourts.gov/static/media/cms/E0002_569890E51EF7C.pdf)
    > If a document exceeds the size limit, it can be split into smaller parts and filed in separate submissions. File the submissions one after the other, so that they can be docketed together. Clearly label the separate documents in order ("Part 1 of 3", "Part 2 of 3", etc.) in the Comments field when you file them.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Filename character/length restrictions for uploaded documents — not addressed anywhere in the official Iowa Judicial Branch eFile User Guide, the EDMS Appellate eFiler User Guide, the EDMS FAQ page, or the eFile Instructions/Resources pages. No official source found stating a character limit, forbidden characters, or a max filename length; could not verify., Specific PDF version/spec number (e.g., PDF 1.4, 1.7, or a minimum/maximum version) — the manuals only require 'PDF (.pdf)' format generically with no version qualifier; unable to confirm whether the underlying system enforces or rejects any particular PDF version.

---

## Kansas

- **E-filing system:** Kansas Courts eFiling (built on the "eFlex" platform), accessed via the shared Portal Interface at filer.kscourts.org/portal which then routes to a District Interface or Appellate Interface (vendor: Tybera Development Group, Inc. (eFlex electronic filing platform), administered by the Kansas Office of Judicial Administration (OJA))
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Kansas Courts eFiling is a single, centrally-administered, mandatory statewide system (Kansas Supreme Court Rule 206 requires all licensed Kansas attorneys to e-file in all case types in all state courts) run on Tybera's "eFlex" software and governed technically by Kansas Supreme Court Administrative Order No. 268. It covers appellate courts and district courts in essentially all 105 Kansas counties (all 31 judicial districts) through one shared portal. The one confirmed exception: Johnson County District Court (10th Judicial District, the state's most populous county) maintains its own separate, independently-procured e-filing system outside Kansas Courts eFiling — attorneys must contact that court directly for access, and the technical constraints documented here (sourced from Kansas Courts eFiling / eFlex materials) should not be assumed to apply to Johnson County's system without separate verification. This is a much more unified model than a fully fragmented county-by-county state (e.g., California), but it is not literally 100% single-system statewide, so RaioPDF's Kansas-targeting logic should special-case or flag Johnson County rather than silently assuming statewide uniformity. Historical note: the underlying case-management system moved to Tyler's Odyssey CMS for most counties via the "Centralized Case Management System" (CCMS) project (Johnson County was reportedly the last to join Odyssey CMS in 2020 per secondary sources), but Tybera's eFlex remains the e-filing front end/vendor as confirmed by current (2024) OJA support contacts (kansassupport@tybera.com) and document-upload screenshots referencing "eFlex."
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://kscourts.gov/KSCourts/media/KsCourts/Orders/Admin-order-268.pdf)
  > No Kansas eFiling source reviewed — Administrative Order 268 (the AOC's own technical-standards order), the OJA's 2017 "Hints and Tips for EFlex – Attorneys" guide, the January 2024 "What's New for Attorneys and External Stakeholders" filer-interface guide, or Douglas County District Court's own eFiling FAQ — mentions PDF/A at all, in any direction (not required, not preferred, not flagged as causing problems). Administrative Order 268 does require documents be "stored in, or convertible to, a format that can be archived in accordance with specifications set forth in Kansas Supreme Court Rule 108," which could theoretically implicate PDF/A-style archival formats, but Rule 108 itself is a records-retention rule, not a filer-facing technical spec, and no eFlex/OJA filer document operationalizes it as a PDF/A requirement for attorneys uploading documents. Targeted searches for "PDF/A" combined with Kansas eFiling/eFlex/kscourts terms returned no hits.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://kscourts.gov/KSCourts/media/KsCourts/eCourt/Updates/Certificate_of_Compliance_Checkbox.pdf)
  > No Kansas eFiling source reviewed — Administrative Order 268, the OJA's 2017 Hints and Tips guide, the January 2024 filer-interface guide, or Douglas County's eFiling FAQ — says anything about document metadata: no requirement to include particular metadata, no instruction or recommendation to strip metadata before filing, and no indication that metadata-scrubbed files cause upload or processing problems. The only privacy-adjacent control found is the filer-side "Sealed" / "Confidential" checkbox and date-of-order fields (used to mark a document as sealed/confidential in the case record) and the 2019 "Certificate of Compliance" checkbox, where the filer self-certifies compliance with the Kansas Supreme Court's personally-identifiable-information redaction rules (Rules 22(d)/23(b)/24 for Odyssey-CMS courts, Rule 123 for non-Odyssey courts) — those are PII-redaction-in-document-content rules, not a file-metadata (XMP/document-properties) policy. Targeted searches for Kansas eFiling + metadata "remove"/"scrub" returned no hits.

**Constraints found:**
  - **System scope / Johnson County exception**: Kansas Courts eFiling (the eFlex platform) is the single OJA-run e-filing system used by all Kansas district and appellate courts EXCEPT Johnson County District Court (10th Judicial District), which runs its own separate, independently-accessed e-filing system outside Kansas Courts eFiling. So Kansas is very close to a single statewide system (104 of 105 counties, all appellate courts) but not literally 100% unified — do not assume Johnson County follows the same technical constraints documented here without separately checking with that court. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://kscourts.gov/eCourt/Kansas-Courts-eFiling/Register)
    > Johnson County District Court maintains an electronic filing system that is separate from Kansas Courts eFiling and you must contact the court directly to gain access to it. ... Currently, only Johnson County District Court does not operate on the Kansas eCourt case management system.
  - **Maximum file size**: Per the Kansas Office of Judicial Administration's own attorney guidance for the eFlex platform: maximum document size is 10 MB per document, and maximum submission (envelope) size is 30 MB per filing session. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://kscourts.gov/KSCourts/media/KsCourts/eCourt/Updates/Hints_and_Tips_20170328.pdf)
    > Document Size Info   Maximum Document Size is 10 Mb and maximum submission size is 30 Mb per session.
  - **Maximum file size — conflicting older figure found**: Douglas County District Court's own eFiling FAQ page (content dating to the 2013-2015 eFlex pilot rollout, still posted with no visible update date) states a 3 MB per-submission cap, which conflicts with the statewide OJA document's 10 MB/30 MB figures. This looks like stale county-page language that was never updated after the platform-wide limit was raised, but no single current OJA source explicitly reconciles the two numbers, so flag this as an open discrepancy rather than picking one with full confidence. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.dgcoks.gov/district-court/clerk-of-the-district-court/efiling)
    > There is no page limit on the documents that you file, though each submission can be no larger than 3 MB.
  - **Accepted file format**: Standard filings must be uploaded as PDF. The current (as of January 2024) filer-interface screenshot in the Kansas Judicial Branch's own attorney guide shows the upload control restricted to PDF. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://kscourts.gov/KSCourts/media/KsCourts/eCourt/Updates/What-s-New-Attorney-External-Stakeholders.pdf)
    > Acceptable File Format Type(s) (*.pdf)
  - **Proposed orders / judge-signature documents must be Word, not PDF**: Documents that require a judge's or clerk's signature (e.g., proposed orders) must be filed as Word-family files (.doc/.docx or .rtf), not PDF, so the judge/magistrate can edit them directly — a notable exception to the platform's otherwise PDF-only rule. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.dgcoks.gov/district-court/clerk-of-the-district-court/efiling)
    > Proposed Orders must be in Word format with a document file extension of doc or docx in order to be editable for the judge/magistrate. All other document types must be PDFs.
  - **Encryption / password protection prohibited**: Password-protected or encrypted PDFs are rejected — if any document in a submission is encrypted or password protected, the ENTIRE submission is returned unfiled. RaioPDF should never encrypt a file destined for Kansas e-filing. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://kscourts.gov/KSCourts/media/KsCourts/eCourt/Updates/Hints_and_Tips_20170328.pdf)
    > Documents may not be password protected or encrypted. If a submission contains any of these types of documents the submission will be returned unfiled.
  - **General document format standard (AOC technical standard, not a procedural rule)**: The Kansas Supreme Court's own technical-standards order for e-filing requires that e-filed documents be printable as paper without loss of content/appearance, and be in (or convertible to) an archivable format per the court's records-retention rule. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://kscourts.gov/KSCourts/media/KsCourts/Orders/Admin-order-268.pdf)
    > All documents filed electronically must be capable of being printed as paper documents without loss of content or appearance. Electronic documents must be stored in, or convertible to, a format that can be archived in accordance with specifications set forth in Kansas Supreme Court Rule 108.
  - **Filename character/length restriction**: No symbols are permitted in uploaded file names, and file names must not exceed 80 characters including spaces; noncompliant file names cause processing errors and rejection. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://kscourts.gov/KSCourts/media/KsCourts/eCourt/Updates/Hints_and_Tips_20170328.pdf)
    > Please do not include any symbols in your file names. Max file name length is 80 characters including spaces. Items will not process correctly and will be rejected if these guidelines are not followed.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Searchable text / OCR requirement — no mention found in Administrative Order 268 (the AOC's technical standards order), the OJA's 2017 'Hints and Tips' attorney guide, the January 2024 filer-interface guide, or Douglas County District Court's eFiling FAQ. Could not confirm whether eFlex checks for or requires text-searchable PDFs., Bookmark or table-of-contents requirement — no mention found in any Kansas eFiling technical document reviewed. Kansas district-court eFiling appears to have no bookmark/TOC portal requirement, but this is an absence-of-evidence finding, not a confirmed 'no requirement' from an FAQ that directly addresses the question., Attachment count limit distinct from the aggregate size cap — the OJA's own guidance documents an aggregate 30 MB/submission size ceiling and note that 'multiple documents can be included in a single submission,' but no numeric cap on the *number* of documents/attachments per submission was found in any source reviewed., Whether the 10 MB/30 MB size figures (last restated in an OJA document dated 2017, and not contradicted in the January 2024 interface guide) are still literally current in 2026, versus the 3 MB figure still posted on Douglas County's own FAQ page — no single current OJA source was found that explicitly reconciles or re-states these numbers as of 2025-2026.

---

## Kentucky (statewide) — Kentucky Court of Justice state courts (Circuit, District, Family, Probate, Court of Appeals, Supreme Court). Scope note: this does NOT cover Kentucky's two federal district courts (Eastern District of Kentucky / Western District of Kentucky), which run their own separate federal PACER/CM-ECF e-filing systems entirely outside AOC control and with their own local-rule technical requirements.

- **E-filing system:** eFiling (Kentucky Court of Justice eFiling system, administered by the AOC; public help portal branded "KCOJ eCourts Help" at ehelp.kycourts.net). This legacy system is in the early stages of being replaced statewide by Tyler Technologies' "File & Serve," whose go-live is scheduled to begin in 2027 (per AOC's own May 2026 Fast Facts sheet), rolling out to 28-30 counties per region per month until statewide. (vendor: Not clearly identified in official sources for the currently-live "eFiling" platform — AOC materials describe it only as the Court of Justice's own in-house-branded "eFiling" system (paired with the "KYCourts" case management system), explicitly contrasted with the incoming Tyler Technologies-built replacement ("File & Serve" eFiling UI + "Enterprise Justice" case management system). Do not assume the current live system is a Tyler/Odyssey product — the AOC's own FAQ says the "Odyssey" name found in some materials refers only to the legacy branding of the NEW Tyler product line, not the current system.)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** CONFIRMED SINGLE STATEWIDE SYSTEM (not fragmented like California). Kentucky runs one statewide court e-filing system, "eFiling," under the Kentucky Court of Justice / Administrative Office of the Courts (AOC), governed by uniform statewide rules adopted by the Kentucky Supreme Court — the "Administrative Rules of Practice and Procedure for the Kentucky Court of Justice Electronic Filing" ("eFiling Rules"), originally adopted and most recently comprehensively amended as Order 2025-02 (entered Jan. 3, 2025). A subsequent Order 2025-41 (entered Oct. 30, 2025) amended ONLY Section 15 (Court Record / clerk-processing timing) and left Section 7 (Format and Technical Requirements) — the section all constraints above are drawn from — completely untouched, so 2025-02's Section 7 remains the current controlling text as of this research (July 2026). I confirmed no order postdating 2025-41 supersedes Section 7.

TRANSITION IN PROGRESS, NOT YET LIVE: Kentucky is mid-migration to a new, also-statewide platform: Tyler Technologies' "File & Serve" (eFiling UI) paired with "Enterprise Justice" (case management, replacing "KYCourts"). Per the AOC's own May 2026 "Fast Facts" sheet, File & Serve go-live is scheduled to begin in 2027 (not 2026, despite some secondary/search-summary sources saying "Fall 2026" — the primary AOC document is explicit: "File & Serve Go-Live Implementation is scheduled to begin in 2027"), rolling out to 4 regions of 28-30 counties per month until statewide, with both systems running in parallel ("dual systems") during the transition. This means: (1) the constraints reported here describe the system that is actually live and mandatory for essentially the entire state today, and (2) RaioPDF should plan to re-verify these constraints against Tyler's File & Serve / Odyssey File & Serve platform technical specs once that rollout reaches general availability, since Tyler's "Odyssey File & Serve" product in other states typically layers its own portal-level file rules on top of (or instead of) a state's civil-procedure-derived rules, and Kentucky's new system could diverge from what's reported here.

CIVIL-PROCEDURE VS. PORTAL DISTINCTION HELD: I deliberately excluded page/word-count limits, caption requirements (CR 10.01), and the CR 7.03 redaction substantive rule from the technical constraints (those are Rules of Civil Procedure, not portal/system tech specs) except where CR 7.03 was relevant context to correctly answer the metadata question (i.e., to show that the "redaction" concept in Kentucky's rules is about visible content, not file metadata, so it should not be mistaken for a metadata-scrubbing policy).
- **PDF/A stance:** preferred -- [source](https://www.kycourts.gov/Courts/Supreme-Court/Supreme%20Court%20Orders/202502.pdf)
  > "Documents must be converted to PDF/A or PDF format before they are filed in the eFiling system. PDF/A is the preferred format for purposes of these rules." (Section 7(1)(a)). Plain PDF is equally acceptable; PDF/A is merely preferred, not mandatory. No language anywhere in the 23-page order (or the amending Order 2025-41, which touched only Section 15/Court Record and left Section 7 untouched) suggests PDF/A ever causes encryption conflicts, form-field problems, or redaction/annotation stripping — the topic simply isn't addressed beyond stating the preference.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.kycourts.gov/Courts/Supreme-Court/Supreme%20Court%20Orders/202502.pdf)
  > The eFiling Rules' "Format and Technical Requirements" section (Section 7) is an exhaustive, numbered list covering page size, DPI, image quality, password-protection, corruption, and completeness — and never mentions document metadata (e.g., XMP/document-properties fields) in either direction. The AOC's separate public help site (ehelp.kycourts.net "Filing Basics" and "Rules for eFiling" pages) likewise contains no metadata guidance. The Rules do address a related-but-distinct topic — redacting visible protected content per CR 7.03 (Section 11) — but that is a content-redaction rule under the Rules of Civil Procedure, not a file-metadata policy, and is explicitly the filer's sole responsibility with no clerk review.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size (per document / per envelope)**: No separate per-document limit is stated. The binding limit is per-envelope (i.e., per submission): the entire eFiling envelope, including all attachments combined, must not exceed 50 MB. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.kycourts.gov/Courts/Supreme-Court/Supreme%20Court%20Orders/202502.pdf)
    > Envelope size limitation. eFiling envelopes, including all attachments, must not exceed fifty (50) megabytes.
  - **Accepted PDF version / file format requirements**: Documents must be converted to either PDF or PDF/A before filing (both are accepted; no specific PDF version number such as 1.4/1.7/2.0 is specified). Documents must also be 8.5x11" size, at least 200 DPI, not secured/password-protected, not corrupted/0-byte, and must comprise the complete file. Anything that can't be converted (video/audio, large maps, etc.) must be filed conventionally on paper instead. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.kycourts.gov/Courts/Supreme-Court/Supreme%20Court%20Orders/202502.pdf)
    > Documents must be converted to PDF/A or PDF format before they are filed in the eFiling system... Documents filed electronically must comply with the following format requirements: (a) 8 1/2" x 11" size; (b) At least 200 dot-per-inch (DPI) resolution... (d) Documents must not be secured, password-protected, or have other features limiting access... (f) Documents must not be corrupted (e.g., a corrupt file having -0- bytes of data).
  - **PDF/A requirement (required / preferred / silent / prohibited)**: PDF/A is explicitly the PREFERRED format but is not mandatory — plain PDF is equally accepted. Nothing in the Rules or the AOC's eFiling help site indicates PDF/A ever causes problems (no mention of encryption conflicts, form-field stripping, or redaction/annotation issues). The only format prohibition that could interact with PDF/A conversion is that files must not be 'secured, password-protected, or have other features limiting access' — a general rule against encrypted files, not a PDF/A-specific complaint. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.kycourts.gov/Courts/Supreme-Court/Supreme%20Court%20Orders/202502.pdf)
    > Documents must be converted to PDF/A or PDF format before they are filed in the eFiling system. PDF/A is the preferred format for purposes of these rules.
  - **Searchable-text / OCR requirement**: No searchable-text or OCR requirement exists. Section 7(3) is the Rules' exhaustive, numbered list of every document-format requirement (page size, DPI, no all-black/unintelligible images, no password protection, readability, no corruption, completeness) and it does not mention text-layer searchability or OCR anywhere. The AOC's separate eFiling help pages (ehelp.kycourts.net) likewise never mention OCR. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.kycourts.gov/Courts/Supreme-Court/Supreme%20Court%20Orders/202502.pdf)
    > Documents filed electronically must comply with the following format requirements: (a) 8 1/2" x 11" size; (b) At least 200 dot-per-inch (DPI) resolution; (c) No unintelligible images (e.g., no all-black images); (d) Documents must not be secured, password-protected...; (e) Only readable word and viewable pictures or images, and valid, noncorrupted tables shall be included; (f) Documents must not be corrupted...; and (g) Documents must comprise the complete image or file.
  - **Attachment count limits**: No numeric cap on the number of attachments per envelope is stated anywhere in the Rules. The only constraint governing how much can go into one submission is the 50 MB total envelope-size cap (Section 7(2)) — attachments are limited by cumulative size, not by count. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.kycourts.gov/Courts/Supreme-Court/Supreme%20Court%20Orders/202502.pdf)
    > Envelope size limitation. eFiling envelopes, including all attachments, must not exceed fifty (50) megabytes.
  - **Metadata policy (include / remove / silent)**: Silent. Nothing in the eFiling Rules (Section 7's technical-requirements list, or anywhere else in the 23-page order) requires including specific document metadata, requires or recommends stripping metadata before filing, or warns that metadata-scrubbed files cause rejection or problems. The Rules do impose a separate content-redaction obligation (Section 11, incorporating CR 7.03, "Privacy protection for filings made with the court") that requires redacting visible protected information like SSNs/account numbers — but that is a Rule-of-Civil-Procedure-based content rule about what's visible on the page, not a rule about file/document metadata, and responsibility for it rests solely on the filer with no clerk review. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.kycourts.gov/Courts/Supreme-Court/Supreme%20Court%20Orders/202502.pdf)
    > All eFilers must comply with the redaction requirements set out in CR 7.03, "Privacy protection for filings made with the court." These requirements apply to all documents, including attachments and exhibits. The clerk will not review filings for compliance with this rule. The responsibility to redact filings rests solely with the eFiler.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Filename character/length restrictions for eFiled documents or attachments — not addressed anywhere in the eFiling Rules (Supreme Court Orders 2025-02 / 2025-41) or the AOC's eFiling help site (ehelp.kycourts.net); no official source found after targeted searching., Bookmark or table-of-contents requirements for eFiled documents — not addressed anywhere in the eFiling Rules or the AOC's eFiling help site; no official source found.

---

## Louisiana

- **E-filing system:** Fragmented — there is no single statewide e-filing portal. (1) The Louisiana Supreme Court runs its own system, "CDX" (Court Data/Document Exchange, cdx.lasc.org), governed by its own Rule XLII. (2) Each of Louisiana's 5 Courts of Appeal runs its own separate e-filing program under its own local rule (e.g., the 4th Circuit's program under Local Rule 25; the 5th Circuit's "eCourt" at ecourt.fifthcircuit.org). (3) District (trial) courts e-file through parish-specific systems: many (not all) parish clerks of court use the Tyler Technologies "Odyssey File & Serve" platform branded "eFileLA" (efilela.tylertech.cloud), while other parishes run their own portal (e.g., Jefferson Parish's "JeffNet"). Each venue sets its own technical specs; they are not uniform. (vendor: Varies by venue. Louisiana Supreme Court's CDX vendor was not identified from the sources reviewed. Many (not all) Louisiana district/parish courts run on Tyler Technologies' "Odyssey File & Serve" platform (branded "eFileLA"). Courts of Appeal and some parishes appear to run independently procured or in-house portals.)
- **Statewide system:** no -- fragmented/county-by-county
- **Notes:** Louisiana's e-filing landscape is fragmented similarly to California's — but split by court level/circuit rather than purely by county. The Supreme Court (Rule XLII, effective 2012) and the 4th Circuit Court of Appeal (Local Rule 25) each publish their own binding technical specs for their own e-filing system, and the two disagree materially: the Supreme Court requires PDF/A + text-searchability with a 175MB per-filing cap, while the 4th Circuit requires plain PDF (200dpi minimum, no PDF/A mandate) with a 20MB per-document cap. District (trial) courts — where the bulk of civil/criminal filing volume happens — are further fragmented by parish and by e-filing vendor (eFileLA/Tyler Odyssey File & Serve is common but not universal). A secondary (non-primary, marketing-blog) source claimed a January 1, 2026 mandatory e-filing rollout for Louisiana civil/criminal filings generally, but this could not be verified against an official AOC/court source within the research budget and is not included as a constraint.
- **PDF/A stance:** required -- [source](https://cdx.lasc.org/Public%20Documents/COURTRULES/RULE%20XLII.pdf)
  > The Louisiana Supreme Court's own e-filing rule (Rule XLII §4(b), current text posted on the court's own e-filing portal cdx.lasc.org) explicitly mandates PDF/A: "An electronically filed document must be in text-searchable PDF-A format." This is the single strongest, most authoritative verified data point found. By contrast, the Louisiana 4th Circuit Court of Appeal's own Local Rule 25 (§7) requires only plain PDF ("submitted in a portable document format (PDF)...") and never mentions PDF/A — i.e., silent, not prohibited. No source reviewed (Supreme Court rule or 4th Circuit rule) indicated PDF/A causes any technical problem — no mention of encryption conflicts, form-field stripping, or redaction/annotation issues. Note Rule XLII §4(g) separately bars encryption/password/rights-management on uploaded documents, which is consistent with (not in tension with) PDF/A's own no-encryption constraint. Because the state's highest court affirmatively requires PDF/A and nothing found treats it as unsafe, "required" is reported as the overall stance, with the caveat that other Louisiana venues (4th Circuit COA, and presumably other circuits/district courts not verified here) are simply silent on the question rather than agreeing with the requirement.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** required -- [source](https://www.la4th.org/downloads/Local%20Rule%2025.pdf)
  > The Louisiana 4th Circuit Court of Appeal's Local Rule 25 (§8, published on the court's own site la4th.org) explicitly requires metadata removal before filing: "Before transmitting an e-filed document, the party filing the document shall remove any confidential information or metadata that may be embedded in the e-filed document." The same rule (§7) separately bars embedded files, scripts, tracking tags, or executable files in the PDF. The Louisiana Supreme Court's Rule XLII (§4(f)) has an adjacent-but-distinct requirement — filers must redact/omit "personal data identifiers" from the visible content of filed documents and exhibits (a content-redaction rule, not explicitly framed as embedded-metadata scrubbing). No source reviewed suggested that removing metadata causes any problem with filing. Given the fragmentation, "required" reflects the clearest verified instance (4th Circuit) rather than a confirmed uniform statewide rule.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size — Louisiana Supreme Court (CDX / Rule XLII)**: 175 MB per single electronic filing (the whole envelope, not stated as per-document) _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://cdx.lasc.org/Public%20Documents/COURTRULES/RULE%20XLII.pdf)
    > The size of any single electronic filing shall not exceed 175 megabytes.
  - **Maximum file size — Louisiana 4th Circuit Court of Appeal e-filing**: 20 MB per document; documents over 20MB must be broken into separate parts filed within the same envelope, in sequence, noted in the Filing Comments field _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.la4th.org/downloads/Local%20Rule%2025.pdf)
    > The size of an e-filed document is limited to 20MB. Documents exceeding 20MB must be divided into separate parts. ... A party e-filing a document over 20MB in size shall separately deliver three copies to the Clerk of Court within twenty-four hours of the e-filing.
  - **Accepted PDF format — Louisiana Supreme Court (CDX / Rule XLII)**: Must be PDF/A and text-searchable; scanned appendix/exhibit material should be at least 300 dpi _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://cdx.lasc.org/Public%20Documents/COURTRULES/RULE%20XLII.pdf)
    > An electronically filed document must be in text-searchable PDF-A format. Appendix and/or exhibit materials may be scanned if necessary, but should maintain 300 dots per inch when scanned.
  - **Accepted PDF format — Louisiana 4th Circuit Court of Appeal e-filing**: Plain PDF (PDF/A not specified), minimum 200 dpi resolution, must not be password-protected or secured, must not contain embedded files/scripts/tracking tags/executables _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.la4th.org/downloads/Local%20Rule%2025.pdf)
    > An e-filed document must be submitted in a portable document format (PDF) with a minimum resolution of 200 dpi (dots per inch) that is not password protected or secured. ... An e-filed document must not contain any embedded files, scripts, tracking tags, or executable files.
  - **Searchable text / OCR requirement — Louisiana Supreme Court (CDX / Rule XLII)**: Required — the filed document itself must be text-searchable PDF/A; scanned appendix/exhibit pages are allowed but should be scanned at 300 dpi _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://cdx.lasc.org/Public%20Documents/COURTRULES/RULE%20XLII.pdf)
    > An electronically filed document must be in text-searchable PDF-A format.
  - **Metadata policy — Louisiana 4th Circuit Court of Appeal e-filing**: Required: filer must strip confidential information and any embedded metadata before transmitting the e-filed document; embedded files, scripts, tracking tags, and executables are separately barred _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.la4th.org/downloads/Local%20Rule%2025.pdf)
    > Before transmitting an e-filed document, the party filing the document shall remove any confidential information or metadata that may be embedded in the e-filed document.
  - **Personal data identifier redaction — Louisiana Supreme Court (CDX / Rule XLII)**: Filers must omit, or partially redact where inclusion is necessary, personal data identifiers from all e-filed documents and exhibits, absent a court order otherwise. This is a content-redaction rule (visible text), distinct from — but adjacent to — embedded-file metadata scrubbing. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://cdx.lasc.org/Public%20Documents/COURTRULES/RULE%20XLII.pdf)
    > A Registered User must refrain from including, or must partially redact where inclusion is necessary, any personal data identifiers from all documents electronically filed, including exhibits, unless otherwise ordered by the Louisiana Supreme Court.
  - **Encryption/DRM prohibition — Louisiana Supreme Court (CDX / Rule XLII)**: E-filed documents must not contain any virus, malware, encryption, PKI, password, or other rights-management when uploaded — relevant because it confirms PDF/A's own no-encryption constraint does not create friction with this portal's rules _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://cdx.lasc.org/Public%20Documents/COURTRULES/RULE%20XLII.pdf)
    > An electronically filed document must not contain a virus, malware, encryption, public key infrastructure, password or any other type of rights management when uploaded.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Filename character/length restrictions — no reliable primary source found for any Louisiana e-filing venue (Supreme Court Rule XLII and 4th Circuit Local Rule 25 are both silent on this)., Bookmark / table-of-contents requirements — not addressed in either verified rule; no reliable primary source found for any Louisiana venue., Attachment count limits — Rule XLII (§4(c)) and Local Rule 25 both allow multiple documents in one filing but neither states a maximum count; no reliable source found with a numeric cap., District (trial) court-level technical specs for the vendor system used by many Louisiana parishes (Tyler Technologies Odyssey File & Serve, branded 'eFileLA') — could not confirm a Louisiana-specific technical user guide/FAQ from a reliable primary source within the research budget. Two documents found at a Tyler-hosted URL pattern that appeared to be Louisiana-specific (path '/docs/LA/...') were excluded: one (a Frequently Asked Questions PDF) explicitly cited Oregon's Uniform Trial Court Rules and referenced the 'Oregon Judicial Department,' indicating it was not actually Louisiana-specific content despite the URL, so no numeric claims from it (e.g., a 25MB/document figure, PDF-or-PDF/A acceptance) were used., PDF/A stance, metadata policy, OCR requirement, file size, filename rules, bookmarks, and attachment limits for Louisiana's other four Courts of Appeal (only the 4th Circuit was verified) and for individual district/parish courts were not independently verified within the research budget., A secondary source (non-primary, marketing/blog page) claimed a January 1, 2026 mandatory e-filing rollout for Louisiana civil and criminal filings; this could not be verified against an official AOC or court source and was not included as a constraint.

---

## Maine

- **E-filing system:** eFileMaine (vendor: Tyler Technologies (Odyssey File & Serve, now marketed as part of Tyler's "Enterprise Justice" platform))
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Confirmed rather than assumed: Maine runs ONE statewide, AOC-selected e-filing system — eFileMaine, built on Tyler Technologies' Odyssey File & Serve platform — governed uniformly by the Maine Rules of Electronic Court Systems (MRECS), adopted by the Supreme Judicial Court. This is NOT a fragmented county-by-county vendor model like California's Electronic Filing Service Provider system. It IS being rolled out in phases court-by-court / region-by-region (news coverage describes "Western Maine courts lead rollout," a 2026 expansion, etc.), so not every courthouse has it live yet, but every region that goes live uses the identical eFileMaine platform and identical MRECS rule set — phased geographic rollout of one system, not multiple independent systems. County probate courts are explicitly carved out of MRECS/EFS scope (MRECS Rule 1(A)(2)). The MRECS document itself (last amended effective January 31, 2026) is the closest thing Maine has to an AOC "technical specification" for the e-filing system and was the primary source used here, supplemented by the Judicial Branch's own one-page "eFileMaine Submission Requirements" and FAQ.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.courts.maine.gov/rules/text/mrecs.pdf)
  > The controlling technical rule (MRECS Rule 34, "Document Requirements") states only that filings must be PDF — preferably natively converted rather than scanned — and must not exceed the EFS size limit; it never mentions PDF/A in any direction. The Judicial Branch's separate "eFileMaine Submission Requirements" one-pager and its eCourts FAQ are likewise completely silent on PDF/A. No Maine source treats PDF/A as required, preferred, or prohibited, and none describes PDF/A causing encryption, form-field, or redaction/annotation problems. The one adjacent, verified requirement is that PDFs must not be password-protected/secured (official court forms ship secured and that protection must be stripped before upload) — a general anti-encryption rule, not a PDF/A-specific finding, but worth flagging since encrypted PDFs and PDF/A conversion can interact.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.courts.maine.gov/rules/text/mrecs.pdf)
  > No Maine e-filing source addresses file-level metadata (author, XMP/Info dictionary, revision history, etc.) in either direction — no requirement to include it, no instruction to strip it. MRECS does impose a separate and unrelated redaction duty on filers (Rules 4(E), 5(E), 12, and 38) to omit or redact nonpublic *content* appearing in the document itself — Social Security numbers, financial account numbers, victim addresses, and other statutorily nonpublic information — but this is about visible document content, not embedded file metadata, and nothing in the rules, the Submission Requirements page, or the FAQ discusses metadata scrubbing as a filing-prep step.

**Constraints found:**
  - **maxFileSizePerDocument**: 54.1 MB maximum per document/file (current figure, published on the Judicial Branch's EFS website per the rule's Jan. 2026 advisory note). A document that exceeds the cap must be broken into multiple separate PDF files, each individually within 54.1 MB. No distinct 'per envelope' (whole-submission) cap separate from this per-file limit was found. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.maine.gov/rules/text/mrecs.pdf)
    > The size limit for document submissions can be found on the Judicial Branch's EFS website and is currently 54.1 MB.
  - **acceptedFileFormat**: PDF is the only accepted format. Files should be natively/digitally converted to PDF rather than scanned, where that is possible (scanning is allowed when a native PDF isn't available). No specific PDF version number (e.g., 1.4 vs 1.7) is specified. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.maine.gov/rules/text/mrecs.pdf)
    > A document submitted electronically to the court must be in the form of a file in Portable Document Format (PDF) directly converted to PDF rather than scanned (if possible), and not exceeding the maximum size allowed by the EFS.
  - **acceptedFileFormat_FAQConfirmation**: The Judicial Branch's own FAQ separately confirms PDF is the sole acceptable submission format. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.maine.gov/ecourts/faqs.html)
    > PDF format is the only acceptable format for submitting documents to the court when eFiling.
  - **documentsMustBeSeparateFiles**: Each pleading/document generally must be filed as its own separate PDF file (own filing code/lead document) rather than bundled into one PDF — the opposite of a combined-PDF or single-envelope-file practice. Narrow exceptions require the opposite (must be combined into one file): proposed orders accompanying a motion, and motions to revoke criminal bail with their attachments. No general numeric cap on the number of separate files/attachments per submission was found. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.maine.gov/ecourts/efilemaine-submission-requirements.pdf)
    > All documents must be submitted as separate PDFs (MRECS 34(A)(2))
  - **filenameMustMatchCaption**: No numeric character-count or length limit on filenames is published for Maine specifically. What is required: the PDF file's title/filename must substantially match the document's own caption/title as used in the filing. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.maine.gov/rules/text/mrecs.pdf)
    > For each separate document submitted, the detailed caption title and PDF file title must be substantially identical.
  - **pdfMustNotBeSecured**: Documents must not be password-protected or otherwise security-protected. Official court forms ship with PDF security/protection enabled by default, and that protection must be manually stripped before the form can be uploaded to eFileMaine (the court publishes separate PC and Mac walkthroughs for removing it). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.maine.gov/ecourts/efilemaine-submission-requirements.pdf)
    > Not be protected by passwords or other security — Please note: All court forms are protected. The protection must be removed before uploading.
  - **selfContainedNoLiveLinks**: Filed PDFs must be self-contained; they may not contain live/active hyperlinks pointing to external papers or websites. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.maine.gov/rules/text/mrecs.pdf)
    > All electronic documents shall be self-contained and must not contain live links to external papers or websites.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** PDF/A requirement — no mention of PDF/A (required, preferred, or prohibited) found anywhere in MRECS, the eFileMaine Submission Requirements one-pager, or the Maine eCourts FAQ., Searchable-text / OCR requirement — no official Maine source found requiring or recommending that filed PDFs be text-searchable or OCR'd., Filename character/length restriction (specific numeric limit) — MRECS requires the filename to substantially match the caption title, but no character-count or length cap is published for Maine. A generic (non-Maine-specific) Tyler 'Odyssey File & Serve HTML5 Quick-Reference Guide' notes the underlying software lets a court configure a max document-name length, but does not state what value, if any, Maine has configured., Bookmark or table-of-contents requirement — no source found requiring or recommending PDF bookmarks/TOC structure in e-filed documents (the 'Bookmarks' feature referenced in Tyler's generic guide is a saved-case-list UI feature unrelated to in-document PDF bookmarks)., Attachment count limit — no numeric cap found on the number of attachments per lead document or per submission/envelope., Metadata policy — no source found addressing file-level metadata (author, XMP/Info dictionary, revision history, etc.) in either direction; this is distinct from MRECS's separate, unrelated requirement to redact nonpublic case *content* (SSNs, account numbers) from the visible document., Per-envelope (whole-submission) file size cap distinct from the 54.1 MB per-document limit — only a per-document/per-file limit is published; whether a separate aggregate envelope cap exists was not found.

---

## Maryland

- **E-filing system:** MDEC (Maryland Electronic Courts) — filings are submitted through the "Odyssey File & Serve" portal (court-facing brand name: "File & Serve"), hosted at maryland.tylertech.cloud/OfsWeb (vendor: Tyler Technologies (Odyssey File & Serve / Odyssey case management))
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Confirmed: Maryland has ONE mandatory statewide e-filing system, not a county-by-county patchwork. MDEC rolled out county-by-county starting fall 2014 and reached full statewide coverage when Baltimore City joined in May 2024 (per the Judiciary's own MDEC news release). It now runs in every District Court, every Circuit Court, the Appellate Court of Maryland, and the Supreme Court of Maryland. E-filing is mandatory for attorneys everywhere MDEC has launched (i.e., statewide) for civil, family, criminal, traffic, and all appellate filings; self-represented litigants may opt in voluntarily but must continue e-filing once they start. Maryland also allows third-party "E-filing Service Providers" (EFSPs) as alternate front-ends ("open" filing model), but all filings still land in the same MDEC/Odyssey backend and are governed by the same State Court Administrator (SCA) technical policies documented here.

Product-relevant flag for RaioPDF's "Combine with Exhibits" binder feature: Maryland's own portal rules cut against bundling a motion and its exhibits into one merged/bound PDF for e-filing. MDEC defines a "submission" as "a single document contained in a single PDF file within an envelope" (Rule 20-101(w), restated in the Policies & Procedures manual), and the SCA's clerk-facing deficiency policy states "All submissions (including proposed orders) that are filed together at one time shall be included in a single envelope as separate PDF files" (Rule 20-201(e)). The Attorney FAQ likewise instructs filers to scan every exhibit as its own file ("each exhibit should be scanned separately and entered into the system by the type of document"). A Maryland-aware exhibit workflow should keep exhibits as separate per-document uploads (each its own submission/filing code within one envelope) rather than flattening a motion + exhibits into a single bound PDF, unless a specific local practice or court order says otherwise. Also note: MDEC does not permit "omnibus motions" combining multiple motions into one document — another place a "combine documents" feature could accidentally create a deficient filing if pointed at MDEC use cases.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.mdcourts.gov/mdec/efilingattyfaqs)
  > Read in full: the MDEC Policies and Procedures Manual, the Maryland Courts "E-filing FAQ for Attorneys" page, the SCA "Best Practices for Attorneys" and "Deficiencies/Strikings/Rejections for Clerks" policy documents, and Tyler's Odyssey File & Serve Filers User Guide and Firm Administrator Guide. None of these mention "PDF/A" (or any archival-PDF standard) anywhere, positively or negatively. The complete official statement on file format is simply the plain-PDF requirement: "All documents are required to be filed in PDF format." There is no stated preference for or against PDF/A, and no documented warning about PDF/A causing encryption, form-field, or redaction/annotation problems.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.mdcourts.gov/sites/default/files/import/mdec/pdfs/manualh5.pdf)
  > Same document set reviewed for PDF/A (MDEC Policies & Procedures Manual, Attorney FAQ, both SCA best-practices/deficiency policies, Odyssey File & Serve Filers User Guide and Firm Administrator Guide) contains zero mention of file metadata — no requirement to include specific metadata, no instruction or recommendation to scrub/remove metadata before filing, and no warning that metadata-scrubbed files cause upload or acceptance problems. The only document-hygiene instructions found relate to content redaction of confidential information within the visible document (Rule 20-201.1 / Rule 20-203), which is a substantive confidentiality rule, not a metadata-scrubbing instruction.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size (per document)**: 25 MB per document. If a document exceeds that, the filer is instructed to split it into multiple volumes/files. The FAQ ties this rule-of-thumb to a ~300-page document (documents of 300 pages or fewer typically fit within 25MB, 'however many factors can affect the file size'). No numeric byte-count formula is given beyond the 25MB figure. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.mdcourts.gov/mdec/efilingattyfaqs)
    > The system allows documents that are 25MB or smaller to be uploaded. If you have a document that is larger than that, you will want to break it up into multiple volumes. Typically, documents that are 300 pages or less will meet the file size requirements, however many factors can affect the file size.
  - **Maximum size per envelope/submission (aggregate)**: Not numerically published. The Policies & Procedures manual confirms a cap exists ('maximum envelope size') and instructs filers to split unrelated filings across multiple envelopes only once that ceiling is hit, but no MB figure for the aggregate envelope is stated anywhere in official MDEC documentation. Only the 25MB per-document figure is quantified. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.mdcourts.gov/sites/default/files/import/mdec/pdfs/manualh5.pdf)
    > Do not use separate envelopes for submissions being filed at the same time in the same case unless the maximum envelope size has been reached.
  - **Accepted file format / PDF requirement**: PDF format is required for every electronic submission. No specific PDF version (e.g., 1.4–1.7) or PDF variant is specified — 'PDF format' is the entirety of the stated format rule. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.mdcourts.gov/mdec/efilingattyfaqs)
    > All documents are required to be filed in PDF format. Most word processing systems have PDF converters in them now; however, there are many free online tools that can help you create a PDF document if you are unable to do so through your word processing software.
  - **Filename requirements — content/relation rule**: No character-set or length rule is published, but there IS a substantive naming-convention requirement enforced as a deficiency ground: the electronic file name must relate to the title of the submission, and if the submission relates to another submission already filed, the file name must reference that relationship. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.mdcourts.gov/sites/default/files/import/mdec/pdfs/scabestpractices-attorneys.pdf)
    > File Names: Make sure that the electronic file name for each submission relates to the title of the submission. If a submission relates to another submission, refer to it in the file name. In other words, show that they're related. Rule 20-201(i).
  - **Filename requirements — system-enforced length limit**: The underlying Tyler Odyssey File & Serve portal (the same e-filing application Maryland's own attorney e-filing page directs users to for 'technical requirements') does enforce some maximum file-name length and throws an error if exceeded, but the Maryland-specific documentation set does not publish the actual character count. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://content.tylerhost.net/docs/MD/OFSFilersUserGuide.pdf)
    > Error on Long File Name Submission. The system now displays an error message when the lead document file name is too long.
  - **Attachment / document count limit per envelope**: No published cap on the number of documents (submissions) per envelope. The portal's own FAQ states filers may include as many documents as needed in one envelope for the same case at the same time; the only ceiling is the unpublished aggregate 'maximum envelope size' (see file-size constraint above), not a document-count number. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.mdcourts.gov/mdec/efilingattyfaqs)
    > Can you file more than one document in a filing? Yes. The e-filing system has an envelope concept, which means you may file as many documents as you need to for the same case at the same time.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Searchable-text / OCR requirement — no MDEC/Odyssey official source (Policies & Procedures manual, Attorney FAQ, SCA best-practices/deficiency policies, or Tyler Odyssey File & Serve user guides) addresses whether filed PDFs must contain a text layer or be OCR'd., Bookmark or table-of-contents requirement — no official MDEC technical source addresses PDF bookmarks or an in-document table of contents for e-filed submissions (note: this is distinct from the Rule 8-504 appellate-brief table-of-citations content requirement, which is a substantive briefing rule, not a portal/technical spec)., Exact maximum aggregate envelope/submission size in MB — the Policies & Procedures manual references a 'maximum envelope size' ceiling by name but does not publish the numeric value anywhere in official documentation.

---

## Massachusetts

- **E-filing system:** eFileMA (vendor: Tyler Technologies (Odyssey File &amp; Serve))
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Massachusetts runs ONE statewide e-filing system called eFileMA (public entry point efilema.com; filer portal at massachusetts.tylertech.cloud/ofsweb), built on Tyler Technologies' Odyssey File & Serve platform. It is used by all Trial Court departments (Boston Municipal, District, Housing, Juvenile, Land, Probate & Family, Superior), the Appeals Court, and the SJC Clerk's Office for the Commonwealth -- this is NOT a fragmented county-by-county system like California. However, e-filing is mandatory only for specific case types/courts (varies by department and case type) and optional or unavailable for others. IMPORTANT CAVEAT for downstream review: Massachusetts does not appear to publish a single unified 'technical specifications' or portal FAQ page covering all 8 requested constraints in one place. Instead, the technical/portal requirements are codified directly into the SJC's own 'Massachusetts Rules of Electronic Filing' (S.J.C. Rule 1:25, Rules 1-16, adopted 2018) plus court-specific standing orders/guides (Superior Court Standing Order 1-23, adopted 2023; the Appeals Court's 'Electronic Filing at the Appeals Court' guide). These are official court/AOC-authored technical-requirement documents governing the e-filing SYSTEM itself (file size, PDF format, searchability, filenames) rather than general rules of civil procedure -- but they are still promulgated as court rules/standing orders, which is simply how Massachusetts chose to document its e-filing system's technical constraints (as opposed to a separate vendor-style user manual). Per-document/per-envelope size limits differ by court (Superior Court: 25MB/50MB; Appeals Court: 50MB/75MB), confirming the limits are Provider-configured per court rather than one fixed statewide number. Research note: www.mass.gov blocks direct automated fetches (403 'Not allowed', likely a bot-detection WAF) for nearly all content pages while allowing its homepage; a text-extraction proxy (r.jina.ai) was used to read the live official pages' actual rendered content, and figures were cross-checked against independent web-search snippets before inclusion. Two vendor-hosted PDFs (Tyler's Massachusetts-specific 'Odyssey File & Serve User Guide' at content.tylerhost.net/docs/MA/, and Tyler's Zendesk help center linked directly from the official Superior Court guide page) were also consulted as genuine platform technical documentation (not marketing pages) but added little beyond what the official Rules/guides already covered.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.mass.gov/supreme-judicial-court-rules/massachusetts-rules-of-electronic-filing-rule-9-format-and-content-of-documents)
  > No Massachusetts e-filing rule, standing order, or official court guide (Rules of Electronic Filing Rules 1-16, Superior Court Standing Order 1-23, or the Appeals Court's Electronic Filing guide) mentions PDF/A at all -- the only format requirement stated anywhere is generic 'searchable PDF' that is not locked/password-protected. The single incidental appearance of 'PDF/A' found anywhere in official MA e-filing materials is a screenshot of Adobe Acrobat's standard 'Save as PDF' dialog box (reproduced in a CPCS/Appeals-Court e-filing training guide) showing an unchecked 'Create PDF/A-1a:2005 compliant file' checkbox as one of Acrobat's normal save options -- it is not accompanied by any instruction to select or avoid it, so it reflects the software's default UI, not a Massachusetts requirement or prohibition. No source discusses PDF/A causing encryption conflicts, form-field issues, or redaction/annotation stripping.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.mass.gov/supreme-judicial-court-rules/massachusetts-rules-of-electronic-filing-rule-12-protection-of-personal-identifying-information)
  > No rule, standing order, or official guide found anywhere in the Massachusetts Rules of Electronic Filing (Rules 1-16), the Superior Court Standing Order 1-23, or the Appeals Court/Superior Court e-filing guides addresses document metadata (XMP/document-properties) inclusion or removal in any way. The only metadata-adjacent requirement located is content-level, not file-metadata: Rule 12 requires filers to redact personal identifying information (PII) from the visible text/content of a document per S.J.C. Rule 1:24, which is a distinct concept from scrubbing a PDF's embedded document-properties metadata. No source indicates metadata-scrubbed files cause any problem, and none recommends or requires scrubbing metadata before filing.

**Constraints found:**
  - **jurisdiction_system_confirmation**: Massachusetts has ONE statewide e-filing system: eFileMA, running on Tyler Technologies' Odyssey File & Serve platform (portal at massachusetts.tylertech.cloud/ofsweb, public-facing at efilema.com). It is used by all Trial Court departments (Boston Municipal, District, Housing, Juvenile, Land, Probate & Family, Superior), the Appeals Court, and the SJC Clerk's Office for the Commonwealth. This is NOT a county-by-county/fragmented system like California -- it is a single statewide platform, though e-filing is mandatory only for certain case types/courts and optional/not-yet-available for others. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.mass.gov/info-details/learn-about-efiling-in-the-trial-court)
    > The Massachusetts Trial Court has engaged with Tyler Technologies to deliver electronic filing ("eFiling") for all who may wish to submit court filings electronically. ... Which courts accept eFiling? [table lists Boston Municipal Court, District Court, Housing Court, Juvenile Court, Land Court, Probate and Family Court, Superior Court]
  - **max_file_size_superior_court**: Superior Court (civil actions, via Standing Order 1-23): 25 MB maximum per single e-filed document; 50 MB maximum per envelope (total of all documents in one submission). Oversized filings are auto-rejected and must be split into labeled parts (e.g. 'Volume 1 of 2'). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.mass.gov/superior-court-rules/superior-court-standing-order-1-23-e-filing-policies-and-procedures-for-civil-actions)
    > The size limit for a single e-filed document is 25 megabytes (MB), and for a single e-filed envelope is 50MB. If a filing exceeds the limit, eFileMA automatically rejects the filing and notifies the filer of the problem. The filer may divide a large document or envelope into smaller parts to fall within the limit.
  - **max_file_size_appeals_court**: Appeals Court: 50 MB maximum per individual PDF document; 75 MB maximum per envelope. This differs from the Superior Court's 25MB/50MB limits, confirming the per-document/per-envelope cap is Provider- and court-configured rather than a single fixed statewide number. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.mass.gov/guides/electronic-filing-at-the-appeals-court)
    > EFileMA.com imposes size limits on filings. No individual PDF document may be more than 50 MB in size, and no “envelope” (which can contain multiple PDF documents) may be more than 75 MB in size.
  - **max_file_size_generic_rule**: The statewide Rules of Electronic Filing (Rule 10(a)) establish that the Provider (Tyler) sets a maximum per-document megabyte size and a maximum per-envelope size, but the rule itself does not hard-code a single statewide number -- the actual figure is set per Provider configuration and varies by court (see Superior Court vs. Appeals Court entries above). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.mass.gov/supreme-judicial-court-rules/massachusetts-rules-of-electronic-filing-rule-10-file-size-limitations-and-legibility)
    > The Provider has set a maximum megabyte size for each document, and a maximum envelope size for all documents contained in one envelope. A User must limit the size of each electronically filed document, and the total size of all the documents filed within one envelope, to comply with the maximum file size and envelope size permitted by the Provider.
  - **accepted_file_format**: Only PDF is accepted (no other file types can be uploaded through the eFileMA/Tyler portal). Documents must be uploaded as flattened PDF files (interactive/fillable form fields should be flattened, e.g. via 'Print to PDF', before upload). No specific PDF version number (e.g., 1.4/1.7/2.0) is specified anywhere in the rules or guides -- the requirement is generically 'PDF'. PDFs must not be locked or password-protected. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.mass.gov/guides/efiling-in-the-superior-court)
    > After registering, the filer will need to upload the documents to be eFiled as flattened PDF files. ... What type of files can I submit through Tyler? Only PDFs can be uploaded through Tyler.
  - **pdf_locked_password_prohibition**: Documents shall not be locked or password protected -- stated as a blanket rule (Rule 9(a)) and repeated verbatim in the Superior Court Standing Order 1-23. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.mass.gov/supreme-judicial-court-rules/massachusetts-rules-of-electronic-filing-rule-9-format-and-content-of-documents)
    > Except where specifically provided, all documents submitted for e-filing must be in searchable Portable Document Format (PDF). Documents should be submitted as electronically converted PDFs rather than scanned PDFs whenever possible. Scanned PDFs shall be made searchable using optical-character-recognition software, such as Adobe Acrobat. Documents shall not be locked or otherwise password protected.
  - **searchable_text_ocr_requirement**: Searchable PDF / OCR is REQUIRED statewide. Word-processed documents must be converted directly to PDF (not scanned) whenever possible. Any scanned PDF must be run through OCR software (e.g. Adobe Acrobat's 'Recognize Text'). The Superior Court Standing Order additionally specifies scan settings of 200 dpi, black-and-white. The Appeals Court explicitly lists 'PDF is not searchable using optical character recognition' as a common rejection reason. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.mass.gov/superior-court-rules/superior-court-standing-order-1-23-e-filing-policies-and-procedures-for-civil-actions)
    > E-filed text documents must be in searchable Portable Document Format (PDF). Word-processed documents should be electronically converted to PDFs, not scanned. Any scanned PDF must be made searchable using optical-character-recognition software, such as Adobe Acrobat, with a resolution of 200 dots per inch (dpi), in black and white.
  - **filename_character_restrictions**: There is no required PDF naming convention, but a specific list of special characters is prohibited in filenames because they cause a transmission error in the e-filing system itself (not merely a court preference) and the filing cannot be accepted: square brackets [ ], @, #, $, %, ^, &, ?, backslash \, forward slash /, +, =, straight/curly quotation marks, :, ;, comma, <, >, curly braces { }, and the vertical bar |. Documented specifically on the Appeals Court's e-filing guide, but framed as a system-level (transmission) failure rather than an Appeals-Court-only rule, suggesting it reflects the underlying Tyler Odyssey platform behavior. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.mass.gov/guides/electronic-filing-at-the-appeals-court)
    > There is no required PDF naming convention for e-filed documents. Do not use any of the following special characters when naming a PDF. Using these characters will cause a transmission error in the e-filing system, and the Appeals Court will not be able to accept the PDF. [list includes] Square brackets: [ and ]; At sign: @; Pound sign: #; Dollar sign: $; Percent sign: %; Caret: ^; Ampersand: &; Question mark: ?; Backslash: \; Forward slash: /; Plus sign: +; Equals sign: =; Quotation marks...; Colon: :; Semicolon: ;; Comma: ,; Less-than sign: <; Greater-than sign: >; Curly braces: { and }; Vertical bar (pipe): |
  - **bookmark_toc_requirement**: Bookmarks and internal links are NOT required by court rule anywhere found in the statewide Rules of Electronic Filing. The Appeals Court explicitly and affirmatively encourages (but does not mandate) bookmarks and internal links in briefs/appendices, and justices are said to find them helpful. No requirement or recommendation was found for Trial Court (Superior Court, etc.) filings specifically. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.mass.gov/guides/electronic-filing-at-the-appeals-court)
    > Although not required by court rule, the Appeals Court encourages all parties filing any brief or record appendix in the Appeals Court to include both bookmarks and internal links.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Exact per-document / per-envelope file size limits for Trial Court departments other than Superior Court (e.g., Probate & Family, Housing, Land, District/BMC, Juvenile) -- only Superior Court (25MB/50MB) and Appeals Court (50MB/75MB) figures were confirmed from primary sources; other departments may share Superior Court's limit or have their own Provider-configured limit, but no department-specific page was found stating it explicitly., Numeric attachment/document count limit per envelope -- no rule or guide states a maximum number of documents/filing codes per envelope; the only constraint documented is total envelope file size, and one page (via secondary search synthesis only, not independently confirmed via a primary source I could read directly) suggested there is no cap on number of filings., SJC / Supreme Judicial Court and other individual Trial Court department (Probate & Family, Land, Housing, Juvenile, District/BMC) specific technical FAQ pages were not individually fetched due to mass.gov's bot-blocking WAF limiting how many pages could be reached in the bounded research window; their PDF/A, metadata, and filename rules were assumed (based on the shared Rules of Electronic Filing) to mirror Rule 9/10, but this was not independently verified per department.

---

## Michigan (state trial courts) — e-filing system: MiFILE

- **E-filing system:** MiFILE (vendor: TrueFiling, a product originally developed by ImageSoft and now owned/operated by i3 Verticals (per i3 Verticals' own press materials; not independently confirmed on courts.michigan.gov, which never names the underlying vendor company — it only surfaces the "TrueFiling" product name in filer-facing screens, e.g. the "TrueFiling username," "TrueCertify" certified-document system, and the mifile.courts.michigan.gov login redirecting to a TrueFiling-branded portal).)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Michigan runs ONE dominant, SCAO-administered statewide e-filing platform — MiFILE (built on the TrueFiling product) — which is closer to Florida's ePortal/Texas's eFileTexas model than to California's fully-fragmented county-by-county model. However, it is not 100% universal: a formal carve-out under Administrative Order 2019-4 lets the 3rd (Wayne/Detroit), 6th (Oakland), 13th (Antrim/Grand Traverse/Leelanau), 16th (Macomb), and 20th (Ottawa) Circuit Courts continue operating "their current e-Filing system" pending full MiFILE integration — the official Policies and Standards No. 2 document (rev. 7/17/2020) explicitly says "These standards do not apply to filings in the 3rd, 6th, 13th, 16th, and 20th Circuit Courts until these courts are fully implemented on MiFILE." As of this research pass, Wayne County's own 3rd Circuit Court e-filing guidance page brands its system as "MiFile" and states an aligned 25MB/document limit and PDF-or-TIFF format list, suggesting substantial convergence toward the same TrueFiling backend even for these five courts — but I could not confirm whether their document-preparation rules (OCR, metadata-removal, filename limits) are identical to the statewide Policies and Standards No. 2 or a locally-varied set, since their court rules are issued under a separate Administrative Order. Also out of scope for this pass: Michigan's appellate courts (Court of Appeals, Michigan Supreme Court) layer additional format standards from their own Appellant/Appellee Manuals on top of the trial-court standards referenced here; and Michigan's federal district courts (Eastern/Western Districts) use the unrelated federal CM-ECF/PACER system, not MiFILE.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.courts.michigan.gov/4aa06a/siteassets/mifile/electronicdocument_stds.pdf)
  > Michigan's official MiFILE document-preparation standards ("Policies and Standards: No. 2 — E-Filing in Michigan Courts") devote an entire section to "File Format, Quality, Metadata, Orientation" — covering permissible file formats, OCR/searchability, scan DPI, and mandatory metadata stripping — but never mention PDF/A anywhere in the document. Permissible formats are listed simply as "PDF, DOC and DOCX, RTF, TIFF, TXT, JPG, and PNG" with no PDF version (e.g., 1.4/1.7/2.0) or archival-format specification of any kind. The companion Filer FAQ likewise never mentions PDF/A, and confirms that whatever format is uploaded, "the document is converted to PDF" by the TrueFiling system itself on submission — meaning the portal produces its own PDF regardless of what the filer chose to upload, without any stated PDF/A conversion or requirement. No language anywhere suggests PDF/A is required, preferred, or causes problems — the standard is silent on PDF/A as a concept entirely.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** required -- [source](https://www.courts.michigan.gov/4aa06a/siteassets/mifile/electronicdocument_stds.pdf)
  > The official standards flatly require metadata removal from every e-filed document, with no caveat or exception noted, and no mention anywhere of metadata scrubbing causing any downstream problem (form fields, signatures, redaction, etc. are treated as separate, unrelated topics in the same standards document).

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size (per document)**: 25 MB per document/file. No numeric limit on total page count. Files exceeding 25 MB must be split by the filer into multiple 25-MB-or-smaller segments (a 'multiple-part document'), each labeled sequentially (e.g., '1 of 3, 2 of 3, 3 of 3'). No separate, distinct envelope/submission-level total cap was found — the limit is applied per uploaded file, and a submission is simply built from multiple individually-capped files. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.michigan.gov/4aa06a/siteassets/mifile/electronicdocument_stds.pdf)
