    > File size shall not exceed 25 MB. Files larger than 25 MB may be filed electronically in separate 25 MB (or smaller) segments.
  - **Accepted file formats for upload**: Filers may upload: PDF, DOC, DOCX, RTF, TIFF, TXT, JPG, PNG. No specific PDF version (e.g. 1.4, 1.7, 2.0) is specified anywhere. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.michigan.gov/4aa06a/siteassets/mifile/electronicdocument_stds.pdf)
    > Permissible formats are PDF, DOC and DOCX, RTF, TIFF, TXT, JPG, and PNG.
  - **Portal-side PDF conversion and bookmark stripping**: The TrueFiling/MiFILE portal automatically converts every uploaded document to PDF on submission, regardless of the original uploaded format. This server-side conversion strips any bookmarks that existed in an uploaded Word file. MiFILE itself imposes no blanket bookmark requirement, but the FAQ warns that individual participating courts may require bookmarked PDFs, and instructs filers to pre-convert to a bookmarked PDF themselves (rather than rely on the portal's own DOC/DOCX-to-PDF pipeline) if that's the case. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://info.courts.mi.gov/hubfs/Filer%20FAQ.pdf)
    > Regardless of a document's original file format, upon upload, the document is converted to PDF. Bookmarks that exist in a Word file are not retained in the converted PDF. If the court you are filing in requires bookmarked PDF files, convert the Word document to a PDF file in a manner that will keep the bookmarks and then upload the PDF.
  - **Searchable text / OCR requirement**: Required. All e-filed documents must be searchable/OCR'd PDFs. If the filer authored the document electronically (a 'born-digital' document), it must be converted straight to PDF from the authoring program — scanning a document the filer created electronically is explicitly prohibited. Scanning is permitted only for documents the filer did not create electronically, or where a wet-ink signature requires it, and any such scan must be at least 300–400 DPI, black/white mode. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.michigan.gov/4aa06a/siteassets/mifile/electronicdocument_stds.pdf)
    > Documents must be searchable/Optical Character Recognition (OCR) PDF and capable of being printed. When the filing party has control of the creation of a document, the document must be converted to PDF directly from the program used to create the document. A scanned image of a document is prohibited except for documents the filing party did not create electronically or when a required signature on the document was signed by hand. Scanned documents must be a minimum 300-400 dpi, black/white mode.
  - **Filename character/length restrictions**: 100-character limit on the filename. The filename must identify the document's title. Abbreviations are permitted. Special characters are not permitted (no specific disallowed-character list given). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.michigan.gov/4aa06a/siteassets/mifile/electronicdocument_stds.pdf)
    > The file name must identify the title of the document. There is a 100 character limit. Abbreviations are permitted. Do not use special characters.
  - **Bookmark / table-of-contents requirement**: No universal PDF-bookmark requirement from MiFILE itself (see the portal-conversion entry above for the individual-court caveat). What IS required: any lead document with attachments must carry a manually-authored 'Index to Attachments' on its last page, listing each attachment's title and file name, and each attachment must be labeled/numbered (e.g., 'Attachment 1 [title] for [lead document name]'). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.michigan.gov/4aa06a/siteassets/mifile/electronicdocument_stds.pdf)
    > The last page of the lead document to which attachments pertain must contain an index subtitled "Index to Attachments" and must list the title of each attachment and its associated file name(s).
  - **Attachment structuring rules (distinct from a numeric count limit — see gaps)**: Attachments the filer creates must be separately attached/'connected' to the lead document (not merged into one PDF, except in Landlord-Tenant/Summary Proceedings case types, where lead document + attachments must be combined into a single file). Each attachment individually must stay within the same 25 MB cap; an oversized attachment is split into labeled parts (e.g., 'Part 1 of 3'). Multiple like-kind documents (e.g., a run of account statements) may be combined into one attachment. Hyperlinks in a filed document may only point to locations within that same document — external links and embedded audio/video are prohibited. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.michigan.gov/4aa06a/siteassets/mifile/electronicdocument_stds.pdf)
    > Multiple documents (including attachments) cannot be combined into a single PDF unless authorized in these standards... Each filed document must be self-contained. Hyperlinks embedded within a document must refer only to information within the same document. Embedded audio or video files are prohibited.
  - **Metadata policy**: Metadata removal is mandatory for every e-filed document — not merely recommended. The standard names drafter/reviewer info, JavaScript, and macros specifically as metadata that must be stripped. No exception, and no indication metadata-scrubbing itself creates any filing problem. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.michigan.gov/4aa06a/siteassets/mifile/electronicdocument_stds.pdf)
    > All metadata must be removed from the document, including information referencing drafters, reviewers, javascript, or macros.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Attachment COUNT limit (max number of attachments/exhibits per filing or envelope) — no numeric cap found in either the official Policies and Standards No. 2 document or the Filer FAQ; only structural/formatting rules for attachments (indexing, per-attachment 25MB cap, like-kind combination) were found, not a maximum quantity., A distinct envelope/submission-level total size cap (as opposed to the documented 25 MB per-document/per-file limit) — not found; unclear whether MiFILE/TrueFiling imposes any aggregate cap across all documents in one filing transaction., Whether the 3rd (Wayne), 6th (Oakland), 13th, 16th (Macomb), and 20th (Ottawa) Circuit Courts — which operate under a separate Administrative Order (2019-4) rather than the statewide Policies and Standards No. 2 — apply identical OCR/metadata/filename/bookmark rules, or their own locally-varied technical rules; Wayne County's own 3rd Circuit Court page brands its system 'MiFile' and states matching file-size/format rules, but its OCR and metadata-removal policy specifically was not independently confirmed., Current (July 2026) authoritative count and identity of which specific courts remain off MiFILE entirely — the definitive periodically-updated court list PDF (courts.michigan.gov .../mifilecourtlist.pdf) was not fetched in this pass; the 3rd/6th/13th/16th/20th carve-out language in the Standards doc is dated 7/17/2020 and may be partially stale.

---

## Minnesota

- **E-filing system:** eFile and eServe (eFS) -- for Minnesota's district (trial) courts. NOTE: Minnesota's appellate courts (Supreme Court and Court of Appeals) use a separate, different system called E-MACS, not covered by this research. (vendor: Tyler Technologies -- Odyssey File & Serve (accessed via minnesota.tylerhost.net), administered by the Minnesota State Court Administrator's Office (SCAO))
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Minnesota is a clean single-vendor, single-portal statewide case: NOT county-fragmented like California. eFS (built on Tyler's Odyssey File & Serve) is mandatory for attorneys, government agencies, and guardians ad litem in all 87 counties for district (trial) court filings, per Minn. Gen. R. Prac. 14.01. The one real split is by court LEVEL, not by county: district/trial courts use eFS (this research's subject); the Minnesota Supreme Court and Court of Appeals use a separate system, E-MACS, governed by different rules not covered here. The authoritative technical-requirements document is the SCAO-published "Minnesota District Court Registered User Guide for Electronic Filing," last revised 4/15/2026 (33 pages) -- current as of this research (2026-07-02). A vendor-hosted Tyler FAQ (content.tylerhost.net/docs/mn/help/OFS_Minnesota_FAQ_3051.pdf) also exists but is materially stale (dated 2013, cover page updated only to 2020) and cites superseded figures (5MB/document, 25MB/envelope) -- do not rely on it over the current Registered User Guide. Both of the two current mncourts.gov PDF URLs are now behind a Cloudflare bot-challenge that blocks direct automated fetch (returns a "Just a moment..." JS-challenge page); content was retrieved via a text-extraction reader proxy of the same official URLs and is presented here as read from mncourts.gov, but a human or browser-based follow-up fetch of the direct URL is recommended for independent verification.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://mncourts.gov/mncourtsgov/media/scao_library/eFS/Minnesota-District-Court-Registered-User-Guide.pdf)
  > The term "PDF/A" does not appear anywhere in the current (4/15/2026) Minnesota District Court Registered User Guide for Electronic Filing, the Best Practices document, or the Tyler FAQ -- so there is no explicit stance naming PDF/A specifically. However, the guide's mandatory "Prohibited Formatting" rules are practically hostile to a naive PDF/A conversion: PDF/A conformance requires embedding every font used in the document, and this guide states "Do not use character identifier (CID) fonts or embedded fonts. Documents with these fonts may fail to submit" and separately prohibits any "Encryption or password protection, or other features that limit access." A PDF/A converter that embeds fonts (as the standard requires) risks tripping the embedded-font rejection rule. Net effect: PDF/A is not safe to apply as a blind universal default for Minnesota eFS filings -- at minimum, a tool would need to verify the specific PDF/A output doesn't trigger the embedded-font rejection, which contradicts the normal assumption that PDF/A is a strictly "more archival-safe, no downside" conversion.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** recommended -- [source](https://mncourts.gov/mncourtsgov/media/scao_library/eFS/Minnesota-District-Court-Registered-User-Guide.pdf)
  > The Registered User Guide does not command a blanket "strip all metadata from every filing" rule, but it does impose an affirmative, sanctionable duty specific to confidential content: "Filers must also ensure that confidential information is not stored in a document's metadata. Any filer who fails to properly redact confidential information may be sanctioned by the courts." This sits inside the guide's broader Redaction section, which also warns that common paper-era redaction tricks (blacking out, highlighting black, white-text) "are generally not effective for electronic documents" and text "can often be recovered." Practical read for RaioPDF: a metadata scrub is not a required step for every single filing regardless of content, but is effectively mandatory (and court-enforced via sanctions) any time a filing could carry confidential data in its metadata -- which is common. No indication was found that a metadata-scrubbed file itself causes any technical/portal problem (i.e., scrubbing appears to be purely safe/beneficial from the system's perspective, unlike PDF/A).

**Constraints found:**
  - **system_identification**: Minnesota has ONE statewide, mandatory e-filing system for all district (trial) courts: eFile and eServe (eFS), which runs on Tyler Technologies' Odyssey File & Serve platform (accessed at minnesota.tylerhost.net). It is administered centrally by the Minnesota State Court Administrator's Office (SCAO), not procured county-by-county. Attorneys, government agencies, and guardians ad litem are required to use it in all 87 counties. IMPORTANT CARVE-OUT: this system covers trial/district courts only. Minnesota's appellate courts (Supreme Court and Court of Appeals) use a SEPARATE, different e-filing system called E-MACS, which has its own distinct rules not covered by the district-court guide. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://mncourts.gov/mncourtsgov/media/scao_library/eFS/Minnesota-District-Court-Registered-User-Guide.pdf)
    > Attorneys, government agencies, and guardians ad litem are required to use eFS to electronically file documents in Minnesota trial courts. ... This Guide applies only to Minnesota's district courts. The Minnesota Supreme Court and Minnesota Court of Appeals use a different electronic filing system called E-MACS. This Guide does not apply to E-MACS.
  - **max_file_size**: Single document limit: 26.21 MB. Envelope (submission) limit: 36.70 MB. Filer is responsible for compliance; oversized documents may fail to upload and must be split into clearly labeled parts (e.g., 'Part 1 of 3'). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://mncourts.gov/mncourtsgov/media/scao_library/eFS/Minnesota-District-Court-Registered-User-Guide.pdf)
    > The filer is responsible for ensuring that all filings comply with the following file size limits: Single document: 26.21 megabytes / Envelope of documents: 36.70 megabytes. If a document is too large, it may not upload successfully. If a filing is over the size limit, try compressing the file or splitting the document into smaller parts that meet the file size limit.
  - **accepted_pdf_format_version**: Only PDF format is accepted ('All documents filed electronically must be submitted as PDF files'). No specific PDF version number (e.g., 1.4/1.7/2.0) is specified anywhere in the guide. Text-based PDFs are preferred over scanned/image-based PDFs ('When possible, use text-based PDFs'). Multiple documents may never be combined into a single PDF, PDF Portfolio, or PDF Package. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://mncourts.gov/mncourtsgov/media/scao_library/eFS/Minnesota-District-Court-Registered-User-Guide.pdf)
    > PDF Format. All documents filed electronically must be submitted as PDF files. When possible, use text-based PDFs. ... Do not combine separate documents into a single PDF, PDF Portfolio, or PDF Package.
  - **pdfa_practical_conflict_embedded_fonts_and_encryption**: The guide never names 'PDF/A' anywhere in the document (36 pages), so there is no explicit PDF/A requirement or prohibition. However, the system's own mandatory technical requirements directly conflict with what PDF/A conversion typically produces: PDF/A standards require embedding all fonts, and PDF/A tooling sometimes applies encryption/permissions or CID font substitution -- and this guide explicitly PROHIBITS embedded fonts, CID fonts, and any encryption/password protection, stating documents with these features 'may fail to submit' or will not be accepted at all ('Prohibited Formatting: No document shall contain any: Embedded files. Encryption or password protection...'). This is a strong practical signal that running a naive PDF/A conversion (which typically embeds fonts) is NOT a safe default for this portal, even though the letters 'PDF/A' never appear in the source. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://mncourts.gov/mncourtsgov/media/scao_library/eFS/Minnesota-District-Court-Registered-User-Guide.pdf)
    > Do not use character identifier (CID) fonts or embedded fonts. Documents with these fonts may fail to submit. ... Before filing, make sure your PDF does not include embedded fonts. [and, separately, under Prohibited Formatting:] No document shall contain any: Embedded files. Encryption or password protection, or other features that limit access.
  - **searchable_text_ocr_requirement**: OCR is explicitly NOT required and is in fact discouraged/can cause outright rejection. Text-based (natively digital) PDFs are preferred specifically because they are searchable without OCR. For documents that must be scanned, filers are instructed to save them as non-searchable image-based PDFs and turn OFF any auto-OCR setting on their scanner, because OCR text layers can cause the eFS system to reject the filing. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://mncourts.gov/mncourtsgov/media/scao_library/eFS/Minnesota-District-Court-Registered-User-Guide.pdf)
    > Scanned PDFs cannot be searched unless OCR (optical character recognition) is added. OCR is not allowed for court filings because it can cause technical issues. ... If you must scan a document, follow these guidelines: Save it as a non-searchable, image-based PDF. Do not include OCR (optical character recognition). Some scanners add OCR automatically, so make sure this setting is turned off. Including OCR can cause eFS to reject your document, which could lead to missed deadlines.
  - **filename_restrictions**: File names longer than 24 characters are prohibited. File names containing special characters such as a comma, apostrophe, or dash are also prohibited. Both are listed under the guide's 'Prohibited Formatting' section as things that will keep a document from being accepted. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://mncourts.gov/mncourtsgov/media/scao_library/eFS/Minnesota-District-Court-Registered-User-Guide.pdf)
    > Prohibited Formatting. No document shall contain any: ... File names that are longer than 24 characters. File names that include special characters, such as a comma, an apostrophe, or a dash.
  - **bookmark_toc_requirement**: Bookmarks are optional, not required. No table-of-contents requirement is mentioned anywhere in the guide. Internal (in-document) hyperlinks/bookmarks are permitted and encouraged for long documents; active/clickable EXTERNAL hyperlinks are prohibited and can cause a submission to fail (citations must still be written out in full, not replaced by a link). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://mncourts.gov/mncourtsgov/media/scao_library/eFS/Minnesota-District-Court-Registered-User-Guide.pdf)
    > Bookmarks and Hyperlinks. Documents can include bookmarks to help readers move through the document more easily. Bookmarks are optional, but many judges find them helpful, especially in longer documents. ... Active external links, meaning links that go to a source outside the document, can cause a document to fail to submit. ... Do not include active (clickable) external links in your documents.
  - **metadata_policy**: The system does not require blanket removal of all metadata from every filing, but it does impose a clear duty: confidential/non-public information (SSNs, financial account numbers, protected identities, etc.) must not be left sitting in a document's metadata, and a filer who fails to catch that can be sanctioned. This is presented as part of the filer's broader redaction obligation, not a standalone 'strip all metadata' technical rule, but in practice it functions as a mandatory pre-filing metadata check/scrub whenever a document could contain confidential data (which is effectively most filings). No requirement to ADD or preserve any particular metadata field was found. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://mncourts.gov/mncourtsgov/media/scao_library/eFS/Minnesota-District-Court-Registered-User-Guide.pdf)
    > Filers must also ensure that confidential information is not stored in a document's metadata. Any filer who fails to properly redact confidential information may be sanctioned by the courts.
  - **additional_page_and_document_formatting_rules_relevant_to_pdf_tooling**: Beyond the 8 requested fields, several other portal-enforced technical rules matter for a PDF tool: page size must be 8.5x11in portrait; top margin must be at least 1 inch and entirely blank (needed for the system to apply its electronic file stamp); page numbers must be consecutive and continue through attachments; scans must be 200-300 DPI (above 300 DPI 'may fail to submit'); color scans are discouraged (black & white preferred, color 'may not display properly in appellate courts'); each distinct document must be its own separate PDF file (no combining into one PDF, PDF Portfolio, or Package); and no embedded file attachments, encryption, or password protection of any kind is allowed. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://mncourts.gov/mncourtsgov/media/scao_library/eFS/Minnesota-District-Court-Registered-User-Guide.pdf)
    > Page Size: 8.5-by-11-inch pages. Orientation: Portrait. Margins: The top margin must be at least one inch and be entirely blank. ... Resolution ... Minimum: 200 DPI. Recommended maximum: 300 DPI. If a document is scanned above 300 DPI, the document may fail to submit.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Attachment count limit (maximum number of attachments/documents per filing envelope) -- no explicit numeric cap was found in the official Registered User Guide, the Best Practices document, or the Tyler Odyssey File & Serve FAQ; the guide only says related documents should share an envelope and each distinct document must be its own separate PDF, with no stated ceiling on how many can go in one envelope beyond the aggregate 36.70 MB envelope size limit., The two older mncourts.gov-hosted PDFs (Best-Practices-eFile-and-eServe-for-Minnesota-District-Court-Filers.pdf and an earlier Registered User Guide filename) are now Cloudflare-protected and returned 403/challenge pages to direct fetch; content was instead recovered via a text-extraction proxy of the same official mncourts.gov URLs, and cross-checked against the vendor-hosted Tyler FAQ (content.tylerhost.net), which is visibly stale (dated March 2013/2020, citing an outdated 5MB/document, 25MB/envelope figure superseded by the current 26.21MB/36.70MB limits) -- flagging in case an independent verification pass wants to re-fetch the primary PDF directly rather than via proxy.

---

## Mississippi

- **E-filing system:** Mississippi Electronic Courts (MEC) — one statewide, mandatory e-filing/case-management system, with a companion public read-only portal called PAMEC (Public Access to Mississippi Electronic Courts) (vendor: None in the commercial-vendor sense. MEC is self-developed and state-owned by the Mississippi Administrative Office of Courts — built on the federal judiciary's CM/ECF codebase (donated by the Administrative Office of the U.S. Courts) and developed with the National Center for State Courts and the Mississippi Dept. of Information Technology. It is explicitly NOT a third-party e-filing vendor platform like Tyler/Odyssey or File & ServeXpress — coverage notes Mississippi is the only state running this model statewide.)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Confirmed as ONE statewide system, not fragmented by county — MEC now operates in all 82 Circuit Courts, all 24 County Courts, and (since Chancery Courts joined June 19, 2023) all Chancery Courts, i.e. all 188 trial courts, plus appellate courts, under a single unified e-filing system per courts.ms.gov and contemporaneous press coverage. This is the opposite pattern from California's per-county EFSP model.

Two caveats for the human reviewer: (1) FILE SIZE DISCREPANCY — the current MEC Attorney User Guide (PDF metadata shows it was last modified March 2026) and the Administrative Procedures for Mississippi Electronic Courts (APMEC, current version effective 10-25-2018) both independently state a 10 MB per-document limit with matching bundling language, so I'm reporting 10 MB as the constraint. However, the live "General Information" page on the same official courts.ms.gov/mec domain still displays a "Creation of PDFs" / scanning-tips section that says "The size limit is 5 MB per document." That page's surrounding content (floppy disks, WordPerfect 9/10, "pdfFactory", "Textbridge" OCR software) reads as long-unrevised legacy content that was likely never scrubbed after a system upgrade — but because it is still live on an official .gov URL as of today, I'm flagging rather than silently discarding it. (2) The same legacy-looking General Information page is also the source for the OCR guidance below — treat its currency with appropriate skepticism even though no newer official source contradicts it.

Also worth noting for scope discipline: APMEC Section 9 imposes a CONTENT-redaction duty (partially redact SSNs, financial account numbers, minors' identifiers, driver's license numbers, etc., from the visible document) — this is a rules-of-procedure-style obligation about document content, not a technical PDF-metadata (file-properties/XMP) requirement, and I've excluded it from the constraints below per the research brief's scope (it is analogous to Fla. R. Jud. Admin. 2.425, not a portal spec).
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://courts.ms.gov/mec/MEC%20Attorney%20User%20Guide.pdf)
  > PDF/A is not mentioned anywhere in the MEC Attorney User Guide (current), the Administrative Procedures for Mississippi Electronic Courts (current version), the MEC General Information/FAQ page, the MEC Tip Sheet, or the Attorney E-Filing Events List. All of these official sources speak only of generic "PDF format," never an ISO-archival subset, and never flag encryption/form-field/annotation conflicts with any particular PDF flavor.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://courts.ms.gov/mec/MEC%20Administrative%20Procedures%20Revised%20Effective%2010-25-18.pdf)
  > None of the reviewed official MEC sources mention PDF document metadata (file properties, XMP, author/producer fields) at all — no requirement to include specific metadata, no instruction to scrub it, and no warning that metadata-scrubbed files cause problems. The only privacy-adjacent filing duty documented is APMEC Section 9's content-redaction requirement (redact partial SSNs, financial account numbers, minors' names/DOB, etc. from the visible document), which is a rules-of-procedure-style obligation about document content, not a technical statement about the PDF file's metadata — and is out of scope per the research brief.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size (per document/attachment)**: 10 MB per PDF document/attachment. No distinct 'envelope'/submission-level cap is documented — the limit is expressed only per attachment. Exhibits that would otherwise exceed 10 MB must be split into sequential 10 MB 'bundles,' each filed as a separate, labeled attachment (e.g. 'Exhibit 1 - Pages 1-43'). See systemNotes for a conflicting '5 MB' figure found on an apparently stale legacy page of the same official site. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://courts.ms.gov/mec/MEC%20Administrative%20Procedures%20Revised%20Effective%2010-25-18.pdf)
    > In filing documents and attachments to documents, a filing party should electronically image, i.e., "scan," the paper exhibit that is less than ten megabytes (10 MB) and submit the exhibit as an attachment in PDF format. Some attached documents, whether a scanned exhibit or other evidence, may exceed the 10MB size requirement on the system. When this occurs, the document shall be reduced to as many 10MB "bundles" as required to file the entire document.
  - **Accepted PDF version / file format requirements**: PDF is the only accepted format — uploading any non-PDF file produces a filing error. No specific PDF version (e.g., 1.4-1.7) or profile is pinned in official guidance; conversion via Word 'Save As PDF' or WordPerfect 'Publish to PDF' is the only method described. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://courts.ms.gov/mec/MEC%20Attorney%20User%20Guide.pdf)
    > The MEC system only accepts documents in PDF format, and any attempt to upload a file that is in a format other than PDF will result in a filing error.
  - **Searchable-text vs. image PDF (conventional-filing conversion)**: MEC's own definitions section distinguishes a searchable 'text PDF' from a non-searchable 'image PDF' produced by scanning, and directs that conventionally-filed hard copies be accompanied by a text PDF 'if possible' but otherwise will simply 'be scanned for inclusion as an image PDF' — meaning non-searchable scanned PDFs are explicitly anticipated and accepted, not merely tolerated as an edge case. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://courts.ms.gov/mec/MEC%20Administrative%20Procedures%20Revised%20Effective%2010-25-18.pdf)
    > The hard or paper copy should be accompanied by an electronic storage device with the document in a text PDF file(s), if possible. If not, the document will be scanned for inclusion as an image PDF unless otherwise provided in these procedures. The "image" is not a searchable document; a text PDF is a searchable document.
  - **OCR guidance for scanned documents**: A live official MEC page instructs filers to affirmatively AVOID running OCR when scanning a document for filing — the opposite of a searchable-text mandate; it wants a plain image only. Caveat: this page's surrounding content (references to floppy disks, WordPerfect 9/10, 'pdfFactory,' 'Textbridge') reads as long-unrevised legacy guidance, so its current authoritativeness is uncertain even though it remains live on the official domain and no newer official statement contradicts it. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://courts.ms.gov/mec/GeneralInformation.php)
    > Do not use OCR or Textbridge. These options scan the document for altering or word processing. For filing purposes, we need only an image of the document.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Filename character/length restrictions on uploaded PDFs — no official MEC source (Attorney User Guide, APMEC, General Information page, Tip Sheet, Attorney E-Filing Events List) specifies any naming convention or restricted/disallowed characters for the file being uploaded., Bookmark or table-of-contents requirements for filed PDFs — not addressed in any official source reviewed; no requirement or recommendation found either way., Numeric attachment-count limit per filing/envelope — only a file-size-triggered splitting rule (documents over 10 MB become sequential 10 MB 'bundles,' each its own attachment) was found; no maximum count of attachments or exhibits per filing event/submission is documented., Distinct envelope/submission-level aggregate file-size cap (as opposed to the per-document 10 MB cap) — not addressed anywhere; all official guidance frames the size limit strictly per document/attachment.

---

## Missouri (statewide)

- **E-filing system:** Missouri Electronic Filing (eFiling) System — accessed through the Case.net portal at courts.mo.gov (vendor: Not confirmed. No official Missouri Courts page names a third-party e-filing portal vendor (unlike, e.g., Tyler Technologies/Odyssey in other states). The system is operated directly by the Office of State Courts Administrator (OSCA) and is presented as an OSCA/Case.net-integrated platform, not a branded vendor product. Do not assume Tyler/Odyssey — that was not verified.)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Missouri has ONE mandatory, statewide e-filing system — the "Missouri Electronic Filing (eFiling) System," reached via the Case.net portal (courts.mo.gov) and operated by the Office of State Courts Administrator (OSCA). It is used uniformly for circuit court and appellate court (Court of Appeals) filings statewide — this is NOT a county-by-county vendor-fragmented model like California's. Individual circuit/county court websites (e.g., 16th Circuit/Jackson County, Clay County/Circuit 7) that appear in search results merely republish or link to the same statewide OSCA guidance rather than running independent e-filing portals. Note: the courts.mo.gov site is Cloudflare-protected and returns HTTP 403 to automated fetch tools (including this session's WebFetch and curl); all page content below was retrieved either via the Wayback Machine's cached copies of courts.mo.gov (confirmed live-site URLs, recent captures) or via a text-extraction proxy (r.jina.ai) hitting the live current pages — not via vendor marketing pages or blog summaries.
- **PDF/A stance:** prohibited -- [source](https://www.courts.mo.gov/file.jsp?id=48975)
  > The official "eFiling Guidelines on Documents" spec directly answers this in an FAQ-style item: "Will the Missouri eFiling System accept PDF/A documents? No. The Missouri eFiling System cannot accept PDF/A formatted documents. The creation of a PDF/A document includes protecting it for archival storage. The Missouri eFiling System cannot accept any PDF document with any form of protection, security, encryption or digital certificate." This ties directly to the system's blanket ban on any document security/encryption/digital signatures — PDF/A's archival protection layer trips the same rejection rule. For RaioPDF: converting to PDF/A before filing in Missouri is affirmatively unsafe, not just unnecessary.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.courts.mo.gov/file.jsp?id=48975)
  > Neither of the two official documents that specifically govern document/file technical formatting for the Missouri eFiling System — the "eFiling Guidelines on Documents" spec (courts.mo.gov/file.jsp?id=48975) and the "Document and Attachment Help" page (courts.mo.gov/page.jsp?id=39916) — mentions file metadata (author/title/XMP properties, revision history, etc.) at all. There is no requirement to include specific metadata, no instruction or recommendation to scrub metadata before filing, and no warning that metadata-scrubbed files cause problems. (Missouri does have a separate, unrelated requirement — Court Operating Rule 2's redaction certification, effective July 1, 2023 — but that concerns visible personal-identifier content in the document body, not file metadata, and is a rule of court/procedure rather than a portal technical constraint, so it's out of scope here.) Treat this as genuine silence rather than an unresearched gap — both authoritative formatting docs were read in full and neither raises the topic.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size — per document**: 7.0 MB (7,000 KB) per individual PDF document, regardless of whether the PDF was converted or scanned. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.mo.gov/file.jsp?id=48975)
    > Document File Size: Documents are limited to 7MB per document and up to 21MB per submission into the Missouri eFiling System. This limit applies regardless if the document is converted or scanned to PDF.
  - **Maximum file size — per submission/envelope**: Two official Missouri Courts pages give slightly different figures for the total-submission cap: the eFiling Guidelines/FAQ say 21.0 MB combined; the current 'Document and Attachment Help' screen-help page says the total submission limit is 20 MB. Both are live, current OSCA pages — flagging the 1MB discrepancy rather than picking one. Per-document cap (7 MB) is consistent across both. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.mo.gov/page.jsp?id=39916)
    > The size limit for each individual document is 7 MB. The size limit for the total submission is 20 MB. When documents and attachments exceed the size limit (over 5 MB per document and over 20 MB per submission), the user should divide the documents into files of 5 MB or less and submit additional filings, or file a notice with the court to submit attachments by other approved media.
  - **Accepted file format / PDF requirements**: PDF is the only accepted format for documents filed into the system (Word/.doc/.docx is only acceptable for out-of-band items sent by e-mail, not through the portal). No specific PDF version number (e.g., 1.4/1.7/2.0) is specified anywhere in official guidance — 'PDF format' is required generically. Additional hard constraints: the PDF must have NO document security/password protection, NO digital signatures or digital certificates, and NO encryption of any kind; it must not contain HTML references, URLs, or hyperlinks (these break once accepted into the system); pages must be standard letter-size 8.5" x 11" (portrait or landscape). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.mo.gov/file.jsp?id=48975)
    > Document File Type: All documents filed into the Missouri eFiling System must be in PDF (portable document format). ... Document Security: Documents submitted to the Missouri eFiling System must have NO document security. ... Digital Encryption: No form of digital encryption is permitted in PDF documents filed in the Missouri eFiling System. ... Internal Links and References: Documents shall NOT include HTML references, URLs or hyperlinks.
  - **PDF/A requirement**: Explicitly prohibited, not merely unsupported. The system flatly rejects PDF/A because the archival-protection layer PDF/A embeds counts as 'protection/security,' which is banned outright. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.mo.gov/file.jsp?id=48975)
    > Will the Missouri eFiling System accept PDF/A documents? No. The Missouri eFiling System cannot accept PDF/A formatted documents. The creation of a PDF/A document includes protecting it for archival storage. The Missouri eFiling System cannot accept any PDF document with any form of protection, security, encryption or digital certificate.
  - **Searchable text / OCR requirement**: Not a system requirement. It is described only as a judicial preference ('many judges prefer' text-searchable filings), and the guidance actively steers filers AWAY from running OCR on scanned documents, because OCR inflates file size and risks blowing past the 7MB per-document cap. Converting the original electronic file (rather than scanning + OCR) is the recommended path to get searchable text. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.mo.gov/file.jsp?id=48975)
    > Many judges prefer electronically filed documents be "text searchable," meaning essentially that it is possible to find individual words within the document. Electronic documents converted directly to PDF are generally text searchable. Documents scanned to PDF are not text searchable. Using OCR software to create searchable text adds significantly to the file size and may make the file too large. It is preferable to convert the file rather than scan it.
  - **Filename / document-title character and length restrictions**: The system does not document any restriction on the underlying OS-level filename of the uploaded file. It does, however, restrict the in-portal 'Document Title' metadata field entered at upload time: capped at 160 characters, alphanumeric, with all special characters stripped except commas, hyphens, and ampersands. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.mo.gov/page.jsp?id=39916)
    > Document Title – Enter the title of the document from the first page of the document you wish to upload. This will accept all alphanumeric characters up to 160 characters in length. All special characters with the exception of commas, hyphens, and ampersands will be stripped from titles.
  - **Document security / encryption prohibition (relevant to redaction and signature tooling)**: Confirmed a second time via the current portal-help page (not just the 2014 guidelines doc): uploaded PDFs cannot be password-protected, and error messages like 'data corruption' when submitting typically mean the PDF is password-protected or otherwise encrypted and must have all security features disabled before upload. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.mo.gov/page.jsp?id=46525)
    > This message typically means you are trying to file a PDF document that is password protected or has other encryption. To unprotect the document, while the document is open, go to 'Security' in the PDF menu. Enter the document password. Deselect the 'Password Protected' or any other Encryption checkboxes.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Bookmark / table-of-contents requirement — no official Missouri eFiling source imposes any bookmark or TOC requirement on filed documents. The only mention of 'bookmarks' in official materials is as an optional feature of a third-party desktop PDF tool's file-splitting utility (used to divide oversized files), not a court filing requirement — do not report a bookmark mandate for Missouri., Attachment count limit (max number of attachments/exhibits per document or per envelope) — no official source specifies a numeric cap. Missouri's stated limits are size-based only (7MB per document, 20-21MB per submission per the two official pages); no page addresses how many separate document/attachment entries a single submission may contain., Specific PDF version/spec number — official guidance requires 'PDF format' generically and never cites a version number (e.g., PDF 1.4, 1.7, 2.0) or an ISO standard.

---

## Montana

- **E-filing system:** Montana Courts E-Filing (portal at mtefile.courts.mt.gov, information hub at courts.mt.gov/courts/efile) (vendor: Built and administered directly by the Montana Judicial Branch's Office of the Court Administrator (not a third-party nationwide e-filing brand like Tyler/Odyssey or File & ServeXpress that appears anywhere in the official documentation reviewed). It integrates with the trial courts' case-management system, FullCourt — Montana's trial courts are in a multi-year transition from FullCourt V5 to FullCourt Enterprise (FCE), rolling out court-by-court (e.g., Cascade County converted Feb/Mar 2023). This CMS-transition detail is corroborating/background context, not itself a portal technical constraint, so it is not in the constraints array.)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Confirmed: Montana runs ONE statewide, state-administered e-filing system (Montana Courts E-Filing, mtefile.courts.mt.gov) — this is NOT a fragmented county-by-county vendor situation like California. However, two nuances matter: (1) Not every court/case-type is a 'participating court' yet, and whether e-filing is mandatory vs. voluntary for e-filing-eligible attorneys is set by each court's own local rules ('Consult trial courts' local rules to determine if e-filing is mandatory' — Best Practices doc); (2) as of the Technical Policy Manual v2.4 (Nov. 2023), only attorneys/government attorneys/authorized staff/case participants/court reporters can register and e-file — self-represented litigants cannot e-file at all today, so 100% of the system's user base is attorneys. Also worth flagging: an older, undated 'Best Practices' document tells Mac users to save combined PDFs 'in PDF/X format' rather than mentioning PDF/A directly — PDF/X is a print-production standard, not an archival one, and this looks like either a typo/legacy artifact or confusion with PDF/A. I did not treat this as authoritative for the PDF/A question because the more current, versioned Technical Policy Manual v2.4 (Nov. 2023) explicitly and unambiguously lists 'pdf, pdf/a' side-by-side as accepted formats with no caveat, so that is the governing statement I used for the pdfaStance field.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://courts.mt.gov/external/efile/docs/operations-manual.pdf)
  > The governing, current source (Technical Policy Manual v2.4, Nov. 2023) explicitly names PDF/A as one of the accepted file formats side-by-side with plain PDF ('portable document format (pdf, pdf/a)'), with no language suggesting it is required, preferred over plain PDF, or ever problematic. No mention anywhere in the manual of PDF/A causing encryption conflicts, form-field issues, or redaction/annotation stripping. Separately, the manual DOES require that submitted files be 'Not password-protected' — which is naturally compatible with PDF/A (PDF/A itself disallows encryption), so converting to PDF/A introduces no additional friction against that rule. Net effect: PDF/A reads as a safe, explicitly-accepted optional format on this system, not a requirement and not a landmine — hence 'silent' (no stance requiring or discouraging it) rather than 'preferred' (no language favors it over plain PDF) or 'prohibited'.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** required -- [source](https://courts.mt.gov/external/efile/docs/bestpractices.pdf)
  > Official 'Best Practices' guidance from the Office of the Court Administrator explicitly directs filers to strip metadata before submission, but the instruction is scoped specifically to Proposed Orders (which trial courts ask to be submitted as editable Word/WordPerfect files, not PDF, so a judge can modify before signing) — not stated as a universal rule for every filed document/PDF (briefs, exhibits, etc. are not covered by this specific line). The Technical Policy Manual v2.4 (the more general, current technical manual) does not separately mention metadata at all. So: for the one document type it addresses, the stance is an unambiguous 'required' with no caveat about scrubbing causing problems — which supports (for that document type) that metadata-scrubbing is a safe default, but it should not be over-generalized as a blanket portal-wide requirement for all document types since no other official source discusses metadata for PDFs/exhibits/briefs.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size (per document)**: 20 MB per individual document. There is no separate, distinctly-stated 'envelope/submission' aggregate cap — the rule is applied per document, and oversized documents must be split into multiple sub-20MB files uploaded together within the same filing/envelope (no stated ceiling on how many split-parts or how large the combined filing may be). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://courts.mt.gov/external/efile/docs/operations-manual.pdf)
    > Documents larger than 20 megabytes must be split up into segments less than 20 megabytes, with the second (and subsequent) documents filed as additional documents. Submit additional documents by clicking the link(s) on the Upload Document page. Documents which must be split up due to file size should be split into as few files as reasonable.
  - **Maximum file size (per document) — corroborating source**: Same 20 MB per-document limit, corroborated in a second official document. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://courts.mt.gov/external/efile/docs/bestpractices.pdf)
    > Document size is limited to about 20 MB. If you have a file that is larger than this, split it into multiple parts and upload the parts as individual documents in the same filing.
  - **Accepted PDF version / file format requirements**: The portal accepts three format families: recent-version Word (.doc/.docx), recent-version WordPerfect (.wpd), and PDF — with PDF/A explicitly named as an acceptable PDF sub-type alongside plain PDF. No specific PDF version number (e.g., PDF 1.4/1.7/2.0) is specified. Files must also be virus-free and must NOT be password-protected. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://courts.mt.gov/external/efile/docs/operations-manual.pdf)
    > Word processing software with the ability to save documents in recent-version Word (doc, docx), Word Perfect (wpd) or portable document format (pdf, pdf/a). Documents submitted through the E-Filing system must be in one of these formats. ... Documents must be able to be processed by the E-Filing system: Virus-free / Not password-protected.
  - **Searchable-text / OCR requirement**: Required for scanned documents: a scanned document must be submitted as an OCR-recognizable (text-readable) PDF, not a flat 'picture'-format image converted to PDF. The filer does not have to actually run OCR themselves, but the resulting PDF must be text-recognizable. If a submitted scan can't be read as text/viewed properly, the clerk will require re-scan and resubmission, and if that fails, may require traditional paper filing instead. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://courts.mt.gov/external/efile/docs/operations-manual.pdf)
    > Scanned documents must be submitted in pdf format that is recognized by OCR (optical character recognition) processing to the extent possible. In other words, a document should not be originally saved in a "picture" format and subsequently converted to pdf. The e-filer does not have to perform OCR on a submitted document; the document needs only be OCR-recognizable, i.e., readable as text. ... If for any reason a document cannot be easily viewed after scanning and electronic submission, the filing party will be instructed to re-scan and resubmit the document. If the issue cannot be resolved by re-scanning, the party will be asked to traditionally file the document within a specified period of time.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Filename character/length restrictions — no technical filename character-set or length limit is stated in either the Technical Policy Manual v2.4 or the Best Practices guide. The only related text is non-technical naming-convention advice ('Name your documents appropriately. Refrain from using acronyms in document titles.') from the Best Practices doc, which is about clerk-facing document labeling, not an enforced filename restriction — not reliable enough to report as a constraint., Bookmark or table-of-contents requirements — no requirement for PDF navigational bookmarks (or a court-imposed TOC on filed documents/exhibits) was found. The only TOC reference in official material is generic word-processing housekeeping advice ('Update the Table of Contents and "save" the document before attaching it,' Appendix B) about a document's own internal Word/WordPerfect TOC field, unrelated to PDF bookmark/navigation requirements., Attachment count limit (max number of documents/attachments per single filing/envelope) — no explicit numeric cap found. The Technical Policy Manual confirms multiple documents can be added to one filing ('You can submit multiple documents in a single filing') via 'Add Another Lead Document' / 'Add Supporting Document' links, but never states a maximum count., Envelope/submission-wide aggregate file-size ceiling distinct from the per-document 20 MB cap — not found. Only a per-document 20 MB limit is documented; there is no stated total-filing-size limit when multiple documents/split-segments are combined into one filing.

---

## Nebraska

- **E-filing system:** Nebraska.gov eFiling (public-facing portal), backed by JUSTICE (trial courts: county, district, separate juvenile, Workers' Compensation Court) and SCCALES (Supreme Court and Court of Appeals) case management systems (vendor: Nebraska.gov, operated by NIC Inc. (Nebraska's official state portal operator, acquired by Tyler Technologies in April 2021))
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** CONFIRMED: Nebraska has a single statewide mandatory e-filing system — not a fragmented, county-procured model like California. One portal (nebraska.gov/apps-EFILE) serves every trial court (county, district, juvenile, Workers' Compensation Court, via the JUSTICE case management system) and both appellate courts (Supreme Court and Court of Appeals, via SCCALES). E-filing has been mandatory for Nebraska attorneys statewide since the rules took effect Jan. 1, 2022 (Neb. Ct. R. § 2-202), though that mandatory-status fact is a rule-of-court citation included only for system-identification context, not counted as a technical/portal constraint.

IMPORTANT RESEARCH TRAP FOUND: A widely-repeated '35MB per file / 100MB aggregate' file-size figure shows up across web search results when querying Nebraska e-filing limits. Tracing it to its actual source (https://www.ned.uscourts.gov/news/maximum-pdf-file-size) shows it is the FEDERAL U.S. District Court for the District of Nebraska's CM/ECF limit — a completely different, federal court system — not the state JUSTICE/SCCALES portal. None of the official state pages (nebraska.gov/faqs/eFileFAQ.html, nebraska.gov/faqs/appellate/, nebraskajudicial.gov/e-services/efiling) mention any file-size number at all. This looks like exactly the kind of AI/search-engine conflation the research brief warned about, so it was deliberately excluded from constraints and filed as a gap instead.

No official state e-filing user manual or technical-specifications PDF (distinct from the FAQs and the one-page 'Converting a Word Document to a Searchable PDF' handout) could be located despite multiple targeted searches — the state's public-facing documentation is limited to two FAQ pages (trial and appellate) plus the eFiling landing page.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.nebraska.gov/faqs/appellate/)
  > PDF/A (as an archival format distinct from plain text-searchable PDF) is never mentioned in any official source reviewed — the trial-court FAQ, the appellate FAQ, the eFiling landing page, or the official Word-to-searchable-PDF conversion handout. All of these consistently describe the requirement only as 'text-searchable' / 'text-based' PDF (as opposed to a scanned image PDF); none reference PDF/A conformance, and none flag any problem with encryption, form fields, or redaction/annotations tied to PDF/A specifically. Absence was confirmed across every official document found, not merely unaddressed by a single page.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://nebraskajudicial.gov/e-services/efiling)
  > No official Nebraska e-filing source reviewed (trial-court FAQ, appellate FAQ, eFiling landing page, or the searchable-PDF conversion guide) mentions document metadata at all — neither a requirement to include specific metadata, nor guidance to scrub/remove metadata before filing, nor any indication that metadata-scrubbed files cause upload or acceptance problems.

**Constraints found:**
  - **systemScope_statewide**: Nebraska runs ONE statewide, mandatory e-filing system — not a fragmented county-by-county model. A single web-based portal (Nebraska.gov eFiling) covers county courts, district courts, separate juvenile courts, the Workers' Compensation Court, the Court of Appeals, and the Supreme Court, backed by two case-management systems: JUSTICE (trial courts) and SCCALES (Supreme Court/Court of Appeals). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://supremecourt.nebraska.gov/administration/media-releases/completion-nebraska-appellate-courts-efiling-system-connects-all-state-courts-one-single-system)
    > the county and district courts, separate juvenile courts, Workers' Compensation Court, Court of Appeals and Supreme Court are all now accepting electronic filings through a single web-based system
  - **pdfFormat_searchableText_appellate**: For appellate filings (Supreme Court and Court of Appeals, via SCCALES), scanned/image-only PDFs are explicitly rejected for pleadings — documents must be converted, text-based (searchable) PDFs. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.nebraska.gov/faqs/appellate/)
    > Can I use scanned PDFs for pleadings? No. Pleadings must be in text-based (searchable) PDF files.
  - **pdfFormat_searchableText_statewidePage**: The Judicial Branch's own eFiling landing page restates the searchable-text requirement for Supreme Court/Court of Appeals filings and recommends the conversion method (Word→PDF) over scanning to satisfy it. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://nebraskajudicial.gov/e-services/efiling)
    > Documents eFiled in the Supreme Court and Court of Appeals must be in text-searchable PDF format. This is best achieved by converting the document directly from a word processing file rather than scanning a printed copy.
  - **trialCourt_pdfConversionGuidance_scopeCaveat**: The trial-court (JUSTICE) FAQ only instructs filers generically to convert documents to PDF using free converter software — it does not restate the explicit 'no scanned PDFs' rule the appellate FAQ states. It is unclear from official portal-facing text whether the searchable-text mandate is enforced identically for county/district/juvenile/Workers' Compensation Court filings as it is for appellate filings; treat searchable-text as required for appellate and as strongly recommended (uncertain enforcement) for trial-court filings. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.nebraska.gov/faqs/eFileFAQ.html)
    > There are many free software applications available for download on the Internet. Installing and using a PDF converter takes only minutes.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Maximum file size (per document and per envelope/submission) — no primary source found on the actual state Nebraska.gov/JUSTICE/SCCALES eFiling portal. Search engines and secondary summary sites (e.g. LegalClarity) repeatedly surface a '35MB per file / 100MB aggregate' figure, but tracing it to its source shows it actually comes from the FEDERAL U.S. District Court for the District of Nebraska's CM/ECF system (ned.uscourts.gov/news/maximum-pdf-file-size) — a completely separate federal court system, not the state portal. Do not apply that number to the state system., Specific accepted PDF version/spec (e.g. PDF 1.4/1.7/2.0) — not specified anywhere in official state sources found. Only a general 'converted, text-searchable, not-scanned' PDF format requirement is documented (see constraints)., Filename character/length restrictions — not addressed in any official trial-court FAQ, appellate FAQ, eFiling landing page, or the official 'Converting a Word Document to a Searchable PDF' guide., Bookmark or table-of-contents technical/portal requirement — the only requirement touching bookmarks/hyperlinks found anywhere (Nebraska Court Rules of Appellate Practice § 2-103) is a formal rule of court, not a portal technical-spec/FAQ/user manual, so per this research's scope it is excluded; no portal-enforced bookmark requirement or rejection behavior was found in any FAQ/manual source., Attachment count limits (per filing/envelope) — not addressed in any official source found (eFileFAQ.html, appellate FAQ, eFiling landing page, or the searchable-PDF conversion guide).

---

## Nevada

- **E-filing system:** No single statewide e-filing portal. Trial courts split mainly between two separate platforms: "eFileNV" (Odyssey File & Serve) — used by the Eighth Judicial District Court (Clark County/Las Vegas, Nevada's most populous county) and many Justice Courts (Las Vegas, North Las Vegas, Henderson, Sparks, etc.) — and "eFlex" — used by the Nevada Supreme Court & Court of Appeals (appellate, efile.nvsupremecourt.us), the Second Judicial District Court (Washoe County/Reno), the Nevada Department of Administration Hearings Division, and other participating courts/counties (e.g., Lyon County). All courts must comply with one overarching statewide rule (the Nevada Electronic Filing and Conversion Rules) that sets baseline procedural requirements, but that rule does not itself mandate a single vendor or portal. (vendor: Two separate commercial vendors operate in parallel rather than one statewide platform: Tyler Technologies (product: Odyssey File & Serve, branded "eFileNV") and Tybera Development Group, Inc. (product: "eFlex").)
- **Statewide system:** no -- fragmented/county-by-county
- **Notes:** Nevada is a hybrid/fragmented case, not a single mandatory statewide portal like Florida's ePortal or Texas's eFileTexas, and not fully county-by-county like California either. There are two major, separately-built vendor platforms running in different Nevada courts (Tyler's Odyssey/eFileNV mainly in Clark County + many Justice Courts; Tybera's eFlex in the Supreme Court, Washoe County, and other courts), plus one umbrella statewide court rule — the Nevada Electronic Filing and Conversion Rules (NEFCR, formerly cited as ADKT 404) — that both platforms must comply with. Critically, the NEFCR was substantially rewritten effective July 26, 2024: the pre-2024 version contained EFS-level technical language (e.g., a soft text-searchability requirement, a "self-contained documents / no external hyperlinks" rule), but the current live rule (verified at leg.state.nv.us, HTTP 200 at research time) removed that technical layer and now only sets high-level baseline requirements (mandatory registration/e-filing for attorneys, service rules, redaction of personal information per NRS 603A.040/239B.030, document formatting "to the extent practicable" per existing paper-pleading rules, and a more permissive hyperlink policy). Current Rule 3(c) explicitly delegates the applicability of technical specifics to each court's "locally operated EFS," which is exactly why the concrete numbers (file size limits, PDF requirements) live only in each vendor's own filer guide/FAQ rather than in the statewide rule. Separately, secondary sources indicate the Odyssey/eFileNV portal was mid-migration to a new URL (efilenv.tylertech.cloud) around mid-2026, deprecating the older nevada.tylertech.cloud/tylerhost.net portal — flagged as a lower-confidence, non-official data point in the gaps list. The Nevada Supreme Court's own eFlex FAQ page (efile.nvsupremecourt.us) returned a live HTTP 502 error during this research session; its content was instead confirmed via an Internet Archive Wayback Machine snapshot of that same official URL.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.leg.state.nv.us/courtrules/NEFCR.html)
  > No mention of PDF/A — as a requirement, a preference, or a source of problems (encryption conflicts, form-field issues, redaction/annotation stripping) — appears anywhere in the four official sources checked: the current statewide NEFCR (effective July 26, 2024), the Tyler eFileNV/Odyssey Filer's User Guide, the Tybera eFlex User's Guide for Filers, or either court's own e-filing FAQ (Las Vegas Justice Court; Nevada Supreme Court eFlex). All of these sources otherwise document plain-PDF format requirements in specific detail (e.g., minimum 200 dpi, must be .pdf not .jpg/.jpeg, 8.5x11 page size, 10-25 MB size caps), which makes the total absence of any PDF/A reference read as a genuine silence rather than a documentation gap.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.leg.state.nv.us/courtrules/NEFCR.html)
  > None of the same four official sources (current statewide NEFCR, Tyler eFileNV/Odyssey Filer's User Guide, Tybera eFlex User's Guide for Filers, and the two courts' own e-filing FAQs) mentions document metadata, file properties, revision history, or tracked changes at all — there is neither a requirement/recommendation to preserve or include metadata, nor one to strip it before filing, nor any indication that scrubbed files cause acceptance problems. The one adjacent statewide rule found is about visible content, not file metadata: current NEFCR Rule 14(d) requires that personal information (as defined by NRS 603A.040, e.g. SSNs, account numbers) be redacted from a document's visible content before submission to an EFS, or else the document must be filed under temporary seal — this is a content-redaction rule, not a PDF-properties/metadata-scrubbing rule, and should not be conflated with it.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Max file size — eFileNV / Odyssey File & Serve (Eighth Judicial District Court, Clark County/Las Vegas, and many Justice Courts e.g. Las Vegas JC, North Las Vegas JC, Henderson JC, Sparks JC)**: 25 MB maximum per individual document; 35 MB combined maximum per filing envelope _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.lasvegasjusticecourt.us/divisions/civil_division/e-file_faq.php)
    > There is no limit to the number of documents you may submit however; each document cannot be larger than 25MB or a combined total of 35MB per envelope.
  - **Max file size — eFlex (Tybera Development Group), used by the Second Judicial District Court (Washoe County/Reno) and other Tybera-network Nevada courts**: 10 MB maximum per individual document; 30 MB maximum for the entire submission _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efiling-nv.com/eflexResources/manual/UsersGuide.pdf)
    > Individual document size is limited to 10 MB. Multiple documents can be included in a single submission. The size limitation for an entire submission is 30 MB.
  - **Accepted file format — eFileNV / Odyssey File & Serve**: PDF required for documents submitted to the court; page size must not exceed 8.5 x 11 inches. Other formats (Word, JPG, PNG, GIF, TIF) are generally converted to PDF on upload, except specific court-designated document types that must stay in Word format (e.g., certain proposed orders). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.lasvegasjusticecourt.us/divisions/civil_division/e-file_faq.php)
    > Any original document submitted to the court, such as a motion or a brief, must be in a Portable Document Format (PDF). Each document must not be larger than 8½ by 11 inches as set out in the Nevada Rules of Court.
  - **Accepted file format — eFlex (Tybera)**: PDF (.pdf) required for all filed documents and exhibits, including scanned exhibits (scan to PDF, not JPG/JPEG). The sole documented exception is Proposed Orders/Documents, which must be submitted as an editable Word document (.doc/.docx) so court staff can edit it to issue the order. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efiling-nv.com/eflexResources/manual/UsersGuide.pdf)
    > Documents need to be submitted in .pdf format (the exception to this rule is for Proposed Documents which must be submitted as a word document, doc or docx). This enables court personnel to make appropriate changes to create an order... Using only .pdf format also applies to exhibits such as copies of contracts, copies of cancelled checks, etc. Scan and save these items as a .pdf instead of .jpg or .jpeg.
  - **Accepted file format / scan resolution — Nevada Supreme Court's own eFlex instance (appellate filings, efile.nvsupremecourt.us)**: PDF required, minimum 200 dpi scan resolution, black text on a white background only (no colored brief/appendix covers permitted electronically) _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efile.nvsupremecourt.us/eflexResources/footer/faqs.html)
    > An electronic document must be submitted in a portable document format (PDF) with a minimum resolution of 200 dpi (dots per inch). Only black text on a white background is permitted. Otherwise, the format of an electronic document must conform to the applicable NRAPs.
  - **Attachment / document count limit — eFileNV / Odyssey File & Serve**: No stated cap on the number of documents in a filing/envelope; the only real ceiling is the 25 MB per-document / 35 MB per-envelope size limit _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.lasvegasjusticecourt.us/divisions/civil_division/e-file_faq.php)
    > There is no limit to the number of documents you may submit however; each document cannot be larger than 25MB or a combined total of 35MB per envelope.
  - **Attachment / document count limit — eFlex (Tybera)**: No stated numeric cap; the guide affirmatively says multiple documents may be included in one submission, bounded only by the 30 MB total-submission size ceiling _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efiling-nv.com/eflexResources/manual/UsersGuide.pdf)
    > Individual document size is limited to 10 MB. Multiple documents can be included in a single submission. The size limitation for an entire submission is 30 MB.
  - **Hyperlink / document-assembly policy under the current statewide rule (relevant to exhibit-binder / citation-linking features; effective July 26, 2024)**: Hyperlinks are permitted within a filed document to (a) other portions of the same document, and (b) an internet location containing the source of a citation — but a hyperlink can never substitute for a full standard-format citation in the text, and if hyperlinked material is meant to be part of the official court record it must be separately attached as an exhibit, not just linked. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.leg.state.nv.us/courtrules/NEFCR.html)
    > Electronic documents may contain hyperlinks to other portions of the same document and to a location on the internet that contains a source document for a citation. Hyperlinks to cited authority may not replace standard citation format. Complete citations must be included in the text of the filed document... When a party intends to make any hyperlinked material part of the official court record, the party must attach the material as an exhibit.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Filename character/length restrictions: neither the Tyler eFileNV/Odyssey Filer's User Guide nor the Tybera eFlex User's Guide for Filers states a specific allowed character set or length limit for uploaded document filenames, even though the Tyler guide's table of contents references a 'Document File Name Error' screen — the underlying text describing the actual rule was not present in the extractable manual content., Bookmark / table-of-contents requirement for the PDF document itself: not addressed by the current statewide NEFCR or by either vendor's filer guide. Both portals use the word 'Bookmarks' only for a user's saved/favorited case list inside the web app (a navigation feature), which is unrelated to PDF-internal bookmarks or a table of contents inside the filed document — so this is a true gap, not a 'no requirement' finding., Searchable-text / OCR requirement under the CURRENTLY effective statewide rule: the prior Nevada Electronic Filing Rules (ADKT 404, in force 2007–2024) stated the EFS 'must support text searches wherever practicable' and that documents should be searchable and tagged 'when possible.' That language does not appear anywhere in the rewritten NEFCR effective July 26, 2024, and neither the eFileNV/Odyssey nor the eFlex/Tybera filer guide states an independent OCR/searchable-text requirement. It is unclear whether this was an intentional removal (deferred to per-court/AOC technical standards under current Rule 3(c)) or an oversight, so this is flagged as a gap rather than asserted as 'no requirement' with confidence., File-size limits specific to the newer 'efilenv.tylertech.cloud' portal: secondary (non-official) sources indicate Nevada's Odyssey-based trial-court portal was mid-migration to a new URL/interface around July 2026, deprecating the older nevada.tylertech.cloud/tylerhost.net portal. The 25 MB/35 MB figures reported above come from an official court FAQ but could not be independently re-confirmed against the newest portal interface, since no official migration announcement or updated technical-requirements page was found.

---

## New Hampshire (statewide)

- **E-filing system:** Odyssey File &amp; Serve — branded "File &amp; Serve" for attorneys/represented parties, plus "TurboCourt" for self-represented litigants. Both are part of the single statewide "NH e-Court" initiative and both run on Tyler Technologies' Odyssey platform. (vendor: Tyler Technologies)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Confirmed: New Hampshire has ONE statewide mandatory e-filing system, not a county-by-county patchwork (unlike California). The NH Judicial Branch selected Tyler Technologies' Odyssey e-filing solution for a "Statewide E-Court Initiative" (2014), and courts.nh.gov/resources/electronic-services is the single canonical portal entry point covering both Superior Court and Circuit Court. Within that one platform there are two distinct front-ends with DIFFERENT technical limits, which is why several fields below are split: (1) "File & Serve" for attorneys/law firms (the relevant track for RaioPDF's audience), and (2) "TurboCourt" for self-represented parties. I drew on four real courts.nh.gov-hosted PDFs (the current "What You Need to Know Before e-Filing" FAQ, the Superior Court "Civil e-Filing FAQs for Attorneys," the Superior Court "7 Steps to Prepare for E-Filing," and an older 2015 Tyler-authored "NH e-Court FAQ" also linked from courts.nh.gov's resources) plus one Tyler/Odyssey vendor support-KB page that names New Hampshire by name in a state-by-state size table (used only to fill in the per-envelope figure the .gov FAQ doesn't state). Two of the courts.nh.gov PDFs (ofsfilersuserguide.pdf and attorney-faq-superior.pdf/what_you_need_to_know.pdf) are blocked from direct fetch by an Akamai WAF (403) even to a browser-like user agent; I recovered readable text for the ones cited via a text-extraction proxy and cross-checked the numbers against independent Google-indexed snippets of the same PDFs, which matched. NOTE: the 2015 Tyler NH e-Court FAQ's own file-size numbers (5 MB/doc, 25 MB/envelope) are superseded by the current (dated 04/01/2026 per its header) "What You Need to Know" FAQ (25 MB/doc for File & Serve) — I only used the 2015 doc for items the current doc is silent on (embedded-attachment rejection, OCR/PDF-A font-embedding caution, internal-vs-external-link risk).
- **PDF/A stance:** preferred -- [source](https://www.courts.nh.gov/sites/g/files/ehbemt471/files/documents/2021-07/what_you_need_to_know.pdf)
  > The current official FAQ affirmatively names PDF/A as an accepted format on equal footing with plain PDF for the attorney "File & Serve" track: "File & Serve only accepts documents in PDF or PDF‐A formats." (TurboCourt, the self-represented track, is documented as PDF-only with no PDF/A mention.) This is genuinely good news for a "safe default" question — PDF/A is not merely tolerated, it's explicitly whitelisted. However, an older (2015) Tyler-authored NH e-Court FAQ flags a specific PDF/A-associated failure mode under its "Format Errors" chapter: "Font resources are included in newly created documents. This is a standard with PDF/A files. Document generating tools use non–supported fonts when creating documents, which results in the inability to convert the document into the standard e-filing format." The same document's screenshot of a "Document Security Message" shows a PDF/A-mode viewing banner alongside an encrypted/"SECURED" document in the same figure, suggesting (though not proving conclusively — it's one illustrative screenshot, not a stated rule) that PDF/A output from some tools can co-occur with the security-restriction rejections the system separately warns about. Net read: PDF/A is explicitly sanctioned today, but a RaioPDF PDF/A export path should avoid embedding non-standard/unsupported fonts and should never carry password/permission security when producing PDF/A for NH filing.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** recommended -- [source](https://www.courts.nh.gov/sites/g/files/ehbemt471/files/documents/2021-07/attorney-faq-superior.pdf)
  > The Superior Court's own attorney-facing FAQ directly addresses metadata and puts the burden on the filer to proactively protect against it, rather than the system removing it or requiring a specific scrub tool: Q: "I have to convert my Word document to PDF to file. I'm concerned that a reverse process may be available, subjecting my information to metadata collection." A: "Check with your IT department to see if there are any safeguards. View your settings in Word, prior to converting to a pdf, to set a level of protection." There is no stated system-side metadata requirement, no stated prohibition on metadata, and no confirmation that the portal itself strips metadata — the court's guidance is a self-help recommendation to the filer, not a system behavior. Scrubbing metadata before filing is therefore consistent with the court's own advice, but is filer responsibility, not portal-enforced.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Max file size — per document (File & Serve / attorneys)**: 25 MB per document. Documents larger than 25 MB must be split into separate documents/filings rather than uploaded as one file. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.nh.gov/sites/g/files/ehbemt471/files/documents/2021-07/what_you_need_to_know.pdf)
    > You can upload any single file up to 25 MB. Documents greater than 25MB must be broken down and submitted as separate documents.
  - **Max file size — per envelope (File & Serve / attorneys)**: 35 MB per envelope for New Hampshire. Not stated in the courts.nh.gov FAQ itself; this figure comes from Tyler's (the platform vendor's) own support knowledge base, which names New Hampshire specifically in a 50-state size table, and whose 25 MB per-document figure for NH matches the official courts.nh.gov number exactly, supporting reliability of the paired envelope figure. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://odysseyfileandservecloud.zendesk.com/hc/en-us/articles/4402363973389-Max-PDF-File-Size-by-State)
    > New Hampshire — Per Document: 25 MB — Per Envelope: 35 MB
  - **Max file size — TurboCourt (self-represented filers)**: 10 MB per single file (uploads over this fail outright); maximum 15 documents/attachments per submission. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.nh.gov/sites/g/files/ehbemt471/files/documents/2021-07/what_you_need_to_know.pdf)
    > You may upload a single file up to 10 MB in size. Files larger than 10 MB will fail to upload. You may attach up to 15 documents per submission.
  - **Accepted file format**: File & Serve (attorney track) accepts only PDF or PDF/A. TurboCourt (self-represented track) accepts only plain PDF (no PDF/A mention). No other formats (Word, TIFF, etc.) are accepted for standard pleadings on either track. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.nh.gov/sites/g/files/ehbemt471/files/documents/2021-07/what_you_need_to_know.pdf)
    > File & Serve only accepts documents in PDF or PDF‐A formats. ... TurboCourt accepts only Portable Document Format (PDF) documents as attachments.
  - **Searchable text / OCR requirement**: Not a hard requirement, but the Superior Court's own attorney onboarding checklist states PDFs should "preferably" be searchable — phrased as a recommendation, not a rejection condition. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.nh.gov/sites/g/files/ehbemt471/files/documents/2021-07/7-steps-to-prepare-for-e-filing.pdf)
    > Documents submitted through the e-filing system must be in portable document format (.pdf), preferably searchable
  - **Bookmarks / hyperlinks**: Not required, but supported and preserved: bookmarks/hyperlinks added to a pleading transfer into the court's case management system, provided they are internal (same-document) links included in that same PDF file — they stop working if the linked content is in a separately-uploaded attachment. A separate, older Tyler-authored NH FAQ further warns that external links (to other documents, websites, or legal sources) are risky and should be avoided because they can trigger format-error rejections. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.nh.gov/sites/g/files/ehbemt471/files/documents/2021-07/attorney-faq-superior.pdf)
    > You can add bookmarks or hyperlinks to your pleading; they will transfer to the Court's case management system. The bookmarks or hyperlinks will only function properly if they are included in the same PDF file.
  - **Attachment count — TurboCourt (self-represented)**: Maximum 15 documents/attachments per submission. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.nh.gov/sites/g/files/ehbemt471/files/documents/2021-07/what_you_need_to_know.pdf)
    > You may attach up to 15 documents per submission.
  - **Attachment bundling guidance — File & Serve (attorneys)**: No numeric attachment-count cap was found for the attorney track. Instead there is conflicting official/vendor guidance on HOW to bundle attachments: the current Superior Court attorney FAQ says attachments to a pleading should be uploaded together with the pleading in one PDF (so bookmarks/hyperlinks survive); an older (2015) Tyler NH e-Court FAQ instead instructs filers to make an exhibit or appendix its OWN separate PDF attached to the e-filing, and never combine a document that will be docketed separately (e.g. a docketing statement) into another document's PDF. RaioPDF's exhibit-binder feature should treat this as a case-specific judgment call, not a fixed rule. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.nh.gov/sites/g/files/ehbemt471/files/documents/2021-07/attorney-faq-superior.pdf)
    > Any attachment(s) to a pleading should be uploaded with the pleading in one PDF. [2021, Superior Court Attorney FAQ] — vs. — "the court prefers that an appendix or exhibit be created as a separate PDF document from the primary pleading and submitted as an attachment to the e-filing. Distinct documents, such as a docketing statement, should not be combined with another document into a single PDF file." [2015, NH e-Court FAQ]
