  - **Embedded PDF file-attachments (Acrobat "Attach a File" feature)**: Rejected as a format error. Using a PDF-native embedded-file-attachment object (e.g. Acrobat's Document > Attach a File) inside a filed PDF causes File & Serve to reject the filing with a "File Format Error." To combine multiple source documents into one PDF, pages must be merged/inserted into a single flat PDF, not attached as embedded file objects. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](http://content.tylerhost.net/docs/NH/OFSFrequentllyAskedQuestions.pdf)
    > No, it is not acceptable to use the file attachment option within a PDF document. If you create a PDF document that includes embedded file attachments, a "File Format Error" message is displayed when you view the filing status after submittal. If your filing contains a format error, it will be rejected by the system.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Filename character/length restrictions specific to NH's actual File & Serve or TurboCourt deployment — the only source found (a Tyler "eFile" support-KB article: "under 24 characters, only letters and numbers") is on a generic multi-state Tyler product page, not confirmed to correspond to NH's specific portal, so it was left out of constraints rather than presented as an NH-specific rule., A hard numeric attachment-count ceiling for the attorney-facing File & Serve system (as distinct from TurboCourt's confirmed 15-document cap) — no NH-specific number was found; only bundling-style guidance (see the 'Attachment bundling guidance' constraint) was available.

---

## New Jersey

- **E-filing system:** eCourts — the New Jersey Judiciary's statewide electronic filing system, administered by the NJ Administrative Office of the Courts. It is not one single monolithic application but a family of modules by case type/division under the same "eCourts" umbrella: eCourts Civil (DC, F, L docket types), eCourts Criminal, eCourts Appellate, eCourts Tax, plus NJMCDirect (municipal) and JEDS (Judiciary Electronic Document Submission, for self-represented litigants). All are centrally run by the state Judiciary — there is no county-by-county procurement model. (vendor: Not identified in any official NJ Courts page reviewed. No document names a commercial e-filing vendor (e.g., Tyler Technologies) as the platform provider; NJ Courts materials refer to it only as "eCourts," suggesting Judiciary-run/in-house administration, but this is not confirmed either way by a primary source.)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Confirmed: New Jersey has ONE statewide, Judiciary-administered e-filing system (eCourts) — it is not fragmented by county the way California's system is. However, it is internally modular by case type, and the two official technical documents I could locate give DIFFERENT numeric file-size limits for different modules: the 2018 "Guidelines for Preparing Documents for e-Filing" (covers eCourts Civil DC/F/L docket types) sets 7 MB/document and 25 MB/submission, while the current "eCourts Appellate — Common Filing Deficiencies" page sets 28 MB/document and a suggested 200-page/upload cap. Treat any single number as module-specific, not universal-statewide, until a unified specifications page is found. I could not locate a single consolidated "eCourts technical specifications" page covering Criminal, Family, or Tax filings specifically — those modules likely follow the Civil-guide numbers by default but this is not confirmed.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.njcourts.gov/sites/default/files/attorneys/ecourts/training/submissionguidelines.pdf)
  > No mention of PDF/A (as a required, preferred, or prohibited format) appears anywhere in the three official eCourts documents I reviewed in full: the 2018 "Guidelines for Preparing Documents for e-Filing," the eCourts FAQ, or the "eCourts Appellate Common Filing Deficiencies" page. The Guidelines document is specifically about PDF preparation for e-filing and would be the natural place for a PDF/A requirement to appear if one existed — its complete silence on the standard, combined with its explicit ban on password/encryption and warning against comments/Track-Changes/form annotations, is the best evidence available that NJ eCourts has no PDF/A policy either way.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.njcourts.gov/sites/default/files/attorneys/ecourts/training/qrg-efile-confidential-docs.pdf)
  > No official eCourts document addresses embedded PDF metadata (e.g., XMP/Document Properties — author, company, revision history, file path) or instructs filers to scrub it before submission. The only metadata-adjacent official material found is (1) a content-level certification under Rule 1:38-7 — "I certify that I have redacted all confidential personal identifiers from all documents included in this electronic submission pursuant to Rule 1:38-7" — which is about redacting confidential identifiers from document TEXT, not stripping file metadata, and (2) a portal-level "Confidential" vs. "Public" access-restriction flag applied per-attachment in the upload UI, which controls who can view the filed document in the case jacket — again a portal workflow feature, not a PDF-metadata operation. Neither addresses whether scrubbing a PDF's internal metadata fields is required, recommended, or ever causes upload problems.

**Constraints found:**
  - **maxFileSize_eCourtsCivil (DC/F/L docket types)**: 7 MB per document; 25 MB cumulative per filing submission. Oversized documents must be split into labeled volumes. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.njcourts.gov/sites/default/files/attorneys/ecourts/training/submissionguidelines.pdf)
    > File size limit of 7 MB for each document. Cumulate file size limit of 25 MB for each filing submission. ... Filings that exceed these limits will not be accepted. If a document exceeds the limit, user should break the document into volumes with each file clearly labeled ("1 of 3," etc.).
  - **maxFileSize_eCourtsAppellate**: 28 MB per document; suggested cap of ~200 pages per upload/transaction; an appendix volume cannot exceed 200 pages. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.njcourts.gov/sites/default/files/filingdeficiencies.pdf)
    > Each document submitted should not exceed 28 MB. It is suggested that the total transaction should not exceed over 200 pages per upload. If necessary, you should break up your filings into volumes. An appendix volume cannot be over 200 pages in length.
  - **acceptedFileFormat**: PDF is required for all documents except Proposed Documents (Orders, Writs, etc.), which are alternatively accepted as Microsoft Word files. No specific PDF version number (e.g., 1.4/1.7/2.0) is specified anywhere in the official guidance. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.njcourts.gov/sites/default/files/attorneys/ecourts/training/submissionguidelines.pdf)
    > All documents, other than Proposed Documents (Orders, Writs, etc.), should be submitted as PDF. Proposed Documents will be alternatively accepted in Microsoft Word format.
  - **pageSizeAndOrientation**: US Letter only, no larger than 8.5 x 11 inches; portrait orientation only. Landscape-oriented documents are rejected outright. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.njcourts.gov/sites/default/files/attorneys/ecourts/training/submissionguidelines.pdf)
    > US Letter, no larger than 8.5 x 11 inches. Portrait orientation. Landscape orientation will not be accepted.
  - **searchableTextOcrRequirement**: Not a hard/enforced requirement, but strongly steered toward via best-practice guidance: the 'Ideal' method is exporting a native electronic PDF (which stays searchable); scanning paper is only 'Acceptable' as a fallback, with 200x200 DPI, bi-tonal, straight-scan settings recommended. Legibility IS enforced — illegible scanned documents are a stated ground for rejection in eCourts Appellate. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.njcourts.gov/sites/default/files/attorneys/ecourts/training/submissionguidelines.pdf)
    > Ideal: Save or export the source document to PDF format with the Microsoft Word "Save as Adobe PDF" option or with PDF software. Acceptable: If you do not have an electronic source document, use a scanner to convert paper documents to PDF. Note: Electronically converting documents to PDF preserves the text of the source document, making it searchable and resulting in smaller file size. [...] Scanned document is not legible. Review scanned documents before transmitting, illegible documents are rejected.
  - **prohibitedDocumentFeatures (encryption / annotations / form fields)**: Documents MUST NOT contain password protection or any access-limiting feature, unreadable text/images, or invalid/corrupted formatting. Documents SHOULD NOT contain fillable form values or software markup layers (comments, Track Changes, redaction annotations) because eCourts may render the form entries missing or leave them editable; the guide recommends flattening via print-to-PDF instead of save-to-PDF before filing. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.njcourts.gov/sites/default/files/attorneys/ecourts/training/submissionguidelines.pdf)
    > Documents must not contain: Password protection or features that otherwise limit access. ... Documents should not contain: Fillable PDF values or software markups such as: comments, "Track Changes" objects, redaction, etc. While it may be possible to upload such documents, one of the following problems could occur: The form entries will be missing, OR The form entries will be editable. To prepare marked-up documents or fillable PDFs for e-filing, it is best practice to first flatten the document by printing a copy to PDF instead of saving it to PDF format.
  - **confidentialityWorkflow (adjacent to, but distinct from, PDF metadata)**: Filers must certify redaction of confidential personal identifiers (Rule 1:38-7) at upload time, and may separately flag any individual attachment as 'Confidential' (vs. the 'Public' default) in the upload UI, which restricts case-jacket visibility to court staff and case-associated attorneys/parties. This is a content-redaction certification plus a portal access-control flag — it is NOT a PDF embedded-metadata (XMP/Info dictionary) scrubbing requirement, and no such embedded-metadata policy was found. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.njcourts.gov/sites/default/files/attorneys/ecourts/training/qrg-efile-confidential-docs.pdf)
    > I certify that I have redacted all confidential personal identifiers from all documents included in this electronic submission pursuant to Rule 1:38-7, unless otherwise required by statute, rule, administrative directive or court order.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Filename character/length restrictions — no official eCourts document, FAQ, or user guide found that specifies allowed characters, a maximum filename length, or naming conventions for uploaded files., Bookmark or table-of-contents requirements — no official guidance found requiring or even recommending PDF bookmarks or a table of contents, including for lengthy appendices in eCourts Appellate filings., Attachment/document count limit per filing — no official document found imposing a maximum number of attached files per submission. The only enforced caps located are aggregate/per-document file-size limits (7MB/doc + 25MB/submission for eCourts Civil DC/F/L; 28MB/doc + a suggested ~200-page/upload guideline for eCourts Appellate) — count-based limits specifically were not found., A single unified 'technical specifications' page covering all eCourts modules (Civil beyond DC/F/L, Criminal, Family, Tax) was not located — the numeric constraints found are module-specific (2018 Civil DC/F/L guide vs. current Appellate deficiencies page) and may not generalize to Family or Tax filings., Confirmed identity of the underlying e-filing software vendor/platform (in-house AOC build vs. a named commercial e-filing product) — not stated in any official page reviewed.

---

## New Mexico

- **E-filing system:** Odyssey File &amp; Serve (vendor: Tyler Technologies)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** New Mexico runs ONE statewide, mandatory e-filing/e-service platform for attorneys — Odyssey File & Serve, built and hosted by Tyler Technologies — used by the NM Supreme Court, Court of Appeals, and all 13 District Courts statewide (mandatory since Oct 1, 2019) plus Magistrate Courts and the Bernalillo County Metropolitan Court for subsequent criminal filings (mandatory since Oct 14, 2024). This is NOT a fragmented county-by-county vendor model like California — it is a single AOC-selected, single-vendor system, governed by statewide procedural rules (Rule 1-005.2 / 5-103.2 NMRA) with each judicial district layering its own local e-filing user guide on top of the same shared Tyler platform. Only attorneys may e-file; self-represented (pro se) litigants cannot use the system.

The most detailed official technical FAQ found (Tyler-authored, hosted at content.tylerhost.net and linked from nmcourts.gov's own "e-Filing for Attorneys" resources page) is dated February 2013 (document version "v.12") — it is the best available primary source for portal-level technical constraints, but its age means some particulars could be stale relative to the platform's current release (the generic Tyler Odyssey product user guide found elsewhere is dated 2016 at "Release 3.14," so the underlying software has iterated since 2013 even if NM's FAQ text was not correspondingly republished).

One discrepancy worth flagging: the 13th Judicial District's own 2015 local e-filing user guide states a stricter 6 MB hard per-document size ceiling ("documents that exceed allowable document size of 6 megabytes... will need to be divided into logical segments"), versus the statewide FAQ's 25 MB recommended ceiling. This may reflect a district-specific technical configuration that diverges from the current shared statewide instance — treat 25 MB as the documented statewide figure but be aware some districts may enforce something stricter in practice.

Also directly relevant to RaioPDF's default output behavior: PDFs bearing an Adobe/Acrobat digital signature are rejected outright (the court's system needs to apply its own timestamp, which a digital signature blocks from modification), and any "secured"/password-protected PDF is likewise rejected as a format error. RaioPDF should not apply encryption, permission restrictions, or digital signatures to a file destined for this portal.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://content.tylerhost.net/docs/nm/help/OFS_NewMexico_FAQ_3047.pdf)
  > No official New Mexico Odyssey File & Serve documentation reviewed requires, prefers, or explicitly prohibits PDF/A. However, the official statewide FAQ's own troubleshooting section flags PDF/A specifically as a source of real processing failures: under "Causes of Typical Format Errors" / "Unsupported Fonts," it explains that font-embedding — described as "a standard with PDF/A files" — can include font types (the example given is the JBig font) that the e-filing conversion engine does not support, causing the document to fail conversion into "the standard e-filing format." The same page's "Document Security" troubleshooting example groups a "You are viewing this document in PDF/A mode" screenshot together with a "(SECURED)" password-protected PDF example, in the context of documents that get rejected. So PDF/A is not banned or required by rule, but the vendor's own documentation names it as a documented cause of filing rejections via unsupported embedded fonts — not a safe universal default to assume works.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://content.tylerhost.net/docs/nm/help/OFS_NewMexico_FAQ_3047.pdf)
  > The official statewide FAQ and the generic Tyler Odyssey File & Serve user guide (both reasonably comprehensive documents that specifically enumerate "causes of format errors" and document-preparation dos/don'ts) do not mention document metadata at all — no requirement to include specific metadata fields, and no instruction or recommendation to scrub/remove metadata before filing. They do address document *security* (encryption/password-protection), which is adjacent but distinct from metadata: "Secured or password-protected PDFs" is listed as a cause of automatic format-error rejection, and the guidance to avoid this is to "use non-secured document properties (i.e., not password-protected)." No source found addresses metadata (author, title, XMP fields, revision history) specifically in either direction.

**Constraints found:**
  - **max_file_size_per_document**: Court-recommended practical ceiling of 25 MB per document (framed as a recommendation for manageability, not stated as an absolute hard technical cap in this source). No distinct per-envelope/submission size limit was found. Caution: an older, district-specific local guide (13th Judicial District, 2015) cites a stricter 6 MB hard limit for that district — see systemNotes for the discrepancy. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://content.tylerhost.net/docs/nm/help/OFS_NewMexico_FAQ_3047.pdf)
    > For optimal manageability, the court recommends that files do not exceed 25 MB per document. There are practical limits to the size of an electronic document that judges and staff can quickly and easily retrieve and read within the case management system.
  - **accepted_file_format**: PDF only for standard e-filed documents (lead documents and attachments); no specific PDF version number (e.g., 1.4, 1.7) is specified in the official documentation reviewed. A separate 'Auxiliary Filing' feature in the underlying Odyssey product allows an editable RTF companion file specifically for proposed orders a judge may need to modify, submitted alongside the required PDF. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://content.tylerhost.net/docs/nm/help/OFS_NewMexico_FAQ_3047.pdf)
    > File & Serve only accepts documents in PDF format.
  - **searchable_text_ocr_requirement**: Not required by rule or by the portal. OCR is explicitly documented as an actual cause of format-error rejections on this platform — the opposite of a requirement or safe default — because OCR'd documents tend to produce the larger file sizes that trigger processing failures. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://content.tylerhost.net/docs/nm/help/OFS_NewMexico_FAQ_3047.pdf)
    > Causes of Typical Format Errors... A document that has Optical Character Recognition (OCR) associated with it; usually determined by a larger file size.
  - **document_security_password_encryption**: PDFs must be non-secured: the portal automatically rejects secured/password-protected PDFs as a format error, and separately rejects any PDF bearing an Adobe/Acrobat digital signature, because a digitally-signed file cannot be modified and the system cannot apply its own filing timestamp to it. Directly relevant to whether RaioPDF should ever encrypt, permission-restrict, or digitally sign output destined for e-filing. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://content.tylerhost.net/docs/nm/help/OFS_NewMexico_FAQ_3047.pdf)
    > Acrobat digital signatures are not allowed. Parties who are capable of applying digital signatures with or without enabled security must omit this process from electronic filings submitted through File & Serve. If such a signature is applied, the document cannot be modified and thus the system cannot time-stamp the PDF document when it arrives. Documents that include this type of digital signature will be rejected.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Per-envelope/submission-level file size limit distinct from the 25 MB per-document figure (not addressed in any source reviewed), Filename character-set or length restrictions specific to the e-filing portal upload step (only naming convention found applies to proposed orders emailed separately to judges, not to the portal itself), PDF bookmark or table-of-contents requirement for filed documents — the only 'Bookmarks' feature documented in the Tyler Odyssey user guide is a portal UI feature for the filer's own saved case list, unrelated to PDF document structure, A stated numeric limit on the number of attachments per filing/envelope (multiple attachments are clearly supported, but no cap number was found), Specific accepted PDF version number (e.g., PDF 1.4/1.7/2.0) — sources confirm 'PDF only' but do not specify a version

---

## New York (statewide) — trial-level courts (Supreme Court, County Court, Court of Claims, Surrogate's Court, Family Court, and NYC Civil/Criminal Courts as authorized) via NYSCEF

- **E-filing system:** NYSCEF — New York State Courts Electronic Filing (vendor: Not identified in official sources checked. NYSCEF appears to be developed and operated directly by the NY State Unified Court System's Office of Court Administration (OCA) rather than a named third-party e-filing vendor (e.g., no Tyler/Odyssey branding found on the portal or its documentation). Do not treat this as confirmed — it is an absence-of-evidence finding, not a sourced statement.)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** NYSCEF is confirmed as ONE single, centrally-operated statewide e-filing portal (https://iapps.courts.state.ny.us/nyscef/HomePage) — not a fragmented, county-by-county vendor model like California's. All research below is against this one system's own official Filing Requirements and FAQ pages. The nuance to flag: e-filing MANDATE varies by county and case type (the Chief Administrative Judge designates mandatory vs. voluntary e-filing counties/case-types by administrative order — e.g., mandatory in New York, Westchester, and Rockland counties for certain case types, with others added over time), but this is a coverage/rollout variance, not a different portal or vendor per county — everyone still files through the same NYSCEF system and the same technical constraints apply everywhere it's used. Separately, New York's four Appellate Division departments also file through NYSCEF but layer on additional formatting rules (22 NYCRR Part 1245) and department-specific pages (e.g., AD1's "Formatting Specifications and Guidelines for Electronically Filed Documents"). That AD1 page returned a Cloudflare bot-challenge (HTTP 403 / "Just a moment...") during this research and could not be read, so any appellate-specific requirements (which might include bookmark/TOC rules for briefs) are NOT reflected below and would need separate verification. This report covers the general/trial-court NYSCEF technical requirements — the common-denominator portal constraints that apply statewide.
- **PDF/A stance:** required -- [source](https://iappscontent.courts.state.ny.us/NYSCEF/live/requirements.htm)
  > NYSCEF's official Filing Requirements page states PDF/A conformance in mandatory terms ("NYSCEF requires that all e-filed documents conform to PDF/A specifications") and lists PDF/A as a "GOOD" format criterion opposite an explicit "BAD" list. Critically for the "is PDF/A a safe universal default" question: NYSCEF's own documentation states that encryption/password-protection actively CONFLICTS with PDF/A and is banned because of it ("Documents should NOT be password-protected or encrypted; documents which include these features violates PDF/A specification compliance" / FAQ: "Password protection and encryption are prohibited. Documents that are protected in this manner will not pass validation, thus will not be submitted."). Separately (not strictly a PDF/A rule, but a related object-content rule enforced the same way) NYSCEF prohibits commenting/annotation/highlighting layers, multi-layer content unless flattened, embedded JavaScript/active content, multimedia, and file attachments as unrenderable "Object Content" — so any annotation or redaction-marker layer must be flattened/removed before filing, independent of the PDF/A conversion itself. No "preferred only" or conditional language was found anywhere in the official pages — the stated posture is mandatory with rejection risk.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://iappscontent.courts.state.ny.us/NYSCEF/live/faq.htm)
  > The two authoritative NYSCEF technical-requirements sources (Filing Requirements page and FAQ) were read in full. Both comprehensively enumerate document-level "GOOD"/"BAD" format criteria (PDF/A, text-searchability, margins, resolution, flattening, no encryption, no active content/objects, filename length) and separately address confidentiality of sensitive CONTENT (SSNs / confidential personal information, citing 22 NYCRR 202.5(e), GBL 399-ddd(6), and Public Officers Law 96-a). Neither page — nor the summarized user manual — contains any requirement, recommendation, prohibition, or troubleshooting note about document METADATA (author/title/XMP/custom properties) or metadata-scrubbing software. This reads as a genuine silence in comprehensive official documentation rather than a search failure, since these are the exact pages that would host such a rule if one existed (they cover every other file-property constraint in detail).

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size per document**: 100 MB per PDF document. No separate/distinguishable per-envelope (multi-document submission) aggregate limit was found in official documentation. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://iappscontent.courts.state.ny.us/NYSCEF/live/faq.htm)
    > Is there a limitation on the size of documents that can be filed electronically? Yes. 100 megabytes per PDF document.
  - **Accepted file format**: PDF only, and specifically PDF/A-conformant; must have 1-inch margins on all sides, 200 dpi minimum for scanned images, and be flattened if it contains multiple layers. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://iappscontent.courts.state.ny.us/NYSCEF/live/requirements.htm)
    > When uploading a document into NYSCEF, your document must comply with the following: GOOD Document Format: PDF/A, Text Searchable, 1 Inch Margins, Resolution of 200 Dots per inch, Flattened (if multi-layered)
  - **PDF/A requirement (portal enforcement)**: Required, with stated rejection risk for non-conformance; no embedded JavaScript or open-action tags allowed as part of this compliance. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://iappscontent.courts.state.ny.us/NYSCEF/live/requirements.htm)
    > NYSCEF requires that all e-filed documents conform to PDF/A specifications. NYSCEF will not accept documents that contain open action tags or javascript. If these specifications are not met, those documents may not be accepted.
  - **Encryption / password-protection vs. PDF/A**: Explicitly prohibited, and the portal's own documentation attributes the prohibition directly to PDF/A incompatibility -- direct evidence that PDF/A conversion and encryption/security features conflict. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://iappscontent.courts.state.ny.us/NYSCEF/live/requirements.htm)
    > Documents should NOT be password-protected or encrypted; documents which include these features violates PDF/A specification compliance. ... Password protection and encryption are prohibited. Documents that are protected in this manner will not pass validation, thus will not be submitted.
  - **Annotation / commenting / object-content prohibition**: Highlighting, annotations, comments, and notes (i.e., PDF markup/commenting layers) are explicitly disallowed as non-printable 'Object Content,' alongside multimedia, 3D models, file attachments, and multi-page embedded objects. Relevant to any RaioPDF annotation or redaction-marker workflow: such layers must be flattened/removed, not merely converted to PDF/A. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://iappscontent.courts.state.ny.us/NYSCEF/live/requirements.htm)
    > Content that cannot render (be viewed) directly or completely to a printed page, including: multimedia (e.g., sound, video, animations, slideshows), 3-dimensional models (e.g., CAD drawings), file attachments, multi-page objects (e.g., Microsoft Excel spreadsheets, multi-page TIFF images), and commenting/reviewing features (highlighting, annotations, comments, notes, and the like) are prohibited.
  - **Searchable text / OCR requirement**: Required for any PDF generated from an original word-processing file (must be text-searchable). For scanned image PDFs, the documentation frames non-searchability as a problem to fix (recommends third-party OCR software) rather than an outright rejection criterion -- i.e., mandatory for word-processor-origin documents, strongly recommended (not stated as an automatic rejection trigger) for scans. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://iappscontent.courts.state.ny.us/NYSCEF/live/requirements.htm)
    > All PDF documents generated from an original word processing file must be text-searchable and compatible with the latest version of Adobe Reader®. ... If a document has any images that contain text, those images may not be searchable. ... If you have a scanned PDF that is not searchable, there are several third party software packages that can make your PDF searchable.
  - **Filename restrictions**: No specific filename format/pattern is mandated, but the portal warns that long file names cause upload failures. No exact character-count threshold is published. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://iappscontent.courts.state.ny.us/NYSCEF/live/requirements.htm)
    > No specific file name is required, BUT long names will not upload properly.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Bookmark or table-of-contents requirement for trial-court NYSCEF filings -- no mention found in the official Filing Requirements page, FAQ, or user manual overview checked., Attachment / document count limit per filing transaction (envelope) -- no official NYSCEF statement found specifying a maximum number of documents or exhibits per submission., Exact numeric filename character-length limit -- NYSCEF states long filenames fail to upload but publishes no specific character-count threshold., Appellate Division-specific technical/formatting requirements (22 NYCRR Part 1245 and department pages, e.g. AD1's TechnicalRequirementsEfiling.pdf) -- the AD1 source page was blocked by a Cloudflare bot-challenge during this research and could not be verified; any appellate-specific bookmark/attachment/metadata rules remain unconfirmed.

---

## North Carolina

- **E-filing system:** eCourts File &amp; Serve (front-end for Tyler Technologies' Odyssey File &amp; Serve, feeding into the Odyssey/Enterprise Justice case management system) (vendor: Tyler Technologies)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** CONFIRMED LIVE SYSTEM: As of October 13, 2025, North Carolina completed a statewide rollout — all 100 counties now run on ONE unified, mandatory e-filing/case-management platform for District and Superior trial courts: Tyler Technologies' "Enterprise Justice (Odyssey)" system, publicly branded "eCourts" with the filing front-end called "File & Serve" (efilenc.tylertech.cloud). This is a genuine single statewide system, NOT a county-by-county fragmented model like California's approved-ESP-per-county approach. Attorneys are required to e-file (General Rules of Practice, Rule 5); pro se litigants may opt in but are not required to. IMPORTANT CARVE-OUTS outside this platform: (1) the NC Business Court (a single specialized statewide court for complex business litigation) runs its own entirely separate e-filing portal at ncbc.nccourts.org/filer, with materially different technical specs (110 MB per-document cap vs. 26.21 MB, no envelope cap vs. 36.7 MB, unlimited attachments); (2) the NC Supreme Court and Court of Appeals (appellate courts) run a distinct, separate legacy portal at ncappellatecourts.org that has not been migrated into Odyssey — NCAOC's own FAQ states "Appellate activities will continue outside of Odyssey." All constraints above are scoped to the primary statewide File & Serve/Odyssey platform used by the 100 counties' trial courts, except where explicitly labeled "NC Business Court." Research relied on two source classes: (a) NCAOC's own official PDFs published at nccourts.gov (FAQs, filer process guides, "Additional Information for Filers," the Business Court quick-reference guide), and (b) Tyler Technologies' own product support knowledge base at odysseyfileandservecloud.zendesk.com — NCAOC's own official documents explicitly link to and designate this exact Zendesk domain as "Tyler Technologies File & Serve technical support," so it was treated as a legitimate technical/support source for the system NC actually runs, not a marketing page. That vendor KB was reachable only via a text-extraction proxy (r.jina.ai) because the live site sits behind a Cloudflare bot-challenge that blocked both direct fetch and curl; the extracted content was cross-checked for consistency against NCAOC's own screenshots (e.g., the 26.21 MB and 36.70 MB figures matched exactly across both source classes).
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://odysseyfileandservecloud.zendesk.com/hc/en-us/articles/40875797939469-PDF-Requirements)
  > PDF/A is never mentioned in any NCAOC or Tyler Technologies document reviewed, despite both publishing fairly detailed PDF-preparation guidance (NCAOC's "PDF Best Practices" section in its official filer guide; Tyler's dedicated "PDF Requirements" support page). Adjacent, directly-relevant findings that DO exist: NCAOC instructs filers to flatten every PDF before upload; Tyler's system requires no fillable/interactive form fields and rejects password-protected PDFs (flagged as "the leading cause of on-hold submissions" in the Business Court's guide); and the court's own file-stamping process re-flattens accepted documents, stripping bookmarks/other embedded details in the process. None of this speaks to PDF/A specifically, but it shows the system is already intolerant of some PDF/A-adjacent artifacts (encryption, form fields) independent of PDF/A status — i.e., a naive "convert everything to PDF/A" default would need to also ensure the output has no form fields and no encryption/password layer to avoid the SAME failure modes already documented for ordinary PDFs on this system.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.nccourts.gov/assets/documents/publications/Additional-Information-for-File-&-Serve-Users-Filers-20230616.pdf)
  > Neither NCAOC's official filer guides nor Tyler Technologies' "PDF Requirements"/"PDF Best Practices" pages mention embedded PDF metadata (Title/Author/custom document properties) at all — no requirement to strip it, no requirement to preserve it, and no warning that a metadata-scrubbed file causes upload/processing problems. This is a genuinely separate topic from North Carolina's statutory PII-redaction rule (N.C.G.S. § 132-1.10(d)), which governs VISIBLE content in the document text (SSNs, account numbers, driver's license numbers, etc.), is enforced via a mandatory checkbox certification at submission and an "Auto-redact" tool built into the File & Serve filing UI, and carries civil/criminal penalties for violation — that rule is about document content, not file-level metadata, and does not itself address metadata scrubbing one way or the other.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Which e-filing system is actually live (statewide confirmation)**: As of October 13, 2025, all 100 North Carolina counties use ONE statewide, mandatory platform for District/Superior trial courts: the Enterprise Justice (Odyssey) electronic filing and case management system, operated by Tyler Technologies as part of the state's 'eCourts' program (front-end branded 'File & Serve', hosted at efilenc.tylertech.cloud). Attorneys must e-file; self-represented litigants may opt in. This is NOT county-fragmented like California's ESP model. Two carve-outs sit OUTSIDE this platform: (1) the specialized NC Business Court runs its own separate e-filing portal (ncbc.nccourts.org/filer) with different specs; (2) the NC Supreme Court and Court of Appeals run a distinct legacy appellate e-filing site (ncappellatecourts.org) not migrated into Odyssey ('Appellate activities will continue outside of Odyssey' per NCAOC's own FAQ). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.nccourts.gov/ecourts)
    > North Carolina fully implemented the eCourts conversion in all 100 counties as of October 13, 2025. ALL COUNTIES IN NORTH CAROLINA USE THE ENTERPRISE JUSTICE (ODYSSEY) ELECTRONIC FILING AND CASE MANAGEMENT SYSTEM.
  - **Maximum file size — per document (statewide File & Serve system)**: 26.21 MB per document/filing _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.nccourts.gov/assets/documents/publications/eCourts-FAQS-for-Attorneys-eFiling-20230613.pdf)
    > The file size limit is 26.21 MB (per filing). There can be multiple filings within a single envelope (i.e., per submission).
  - **Maximum file size — per envelope/submission (statewide File & Serve system)**: 36.70 MB per envelope — a single submission can bundle multiple documents/filings up to this combined cap. Confirmed both in NCAOC's own published UI screenshot and independently in Tyler Technologies' own per-state size table. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.nccourts.gov/assets/documents/publications/eFiling-Using-Odyssey-File-&-Serve-Filer-Process-012023.pdf)
    > Max Envelope Size: 36.70 MB / Remaining: 36.70 MB (shown live in the Filings screen of NCAOC's official filer walkthrough); Tyler's own state-by-state table lists 'North Carolina — 26.21 MB [per document] / 36.7 MB [per envelope]'.
  - **Maximum file size — NC Business Court's SEPARATE e-filing system (not the general statewide platform)**: 110 MB per individual document; NO size cap on the total filing queue/submission and no limit on the number of filings in the queue; oversized documents must be split into multiple, clearly labeled parts. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.nccourts.gov/assets/documents/publications/Business-Court-eFiling-Quick-Reference-Guide-20250516.pdf)
    > the file size limit for an individual document is 110 MB; however, please note there is no file size limit for your total filing queue submission nor is there a limit to the number of filings that may be placed into the filing queue. If a document exceeds 110 MB, you will need to split the document into several smaller documents.
  - **Accepted file format (statewide File & Serve system)**: PDF is primary; the live upload screen also lists Word 2007 (.docx) and Word 97-XP (.doc) as accepted types for certain filings. No specific PDF version number (e.g., 1.7) is specified anywhere. PDFs should be produced by Adobe Acrobat or Microsoft Word; Tyler's vendor guidance explicitly discourages Corel WordPerfect's PDF producer. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.nccourts.gov/assets/documents/publications/eFiling-Using-Odyssey-File-&-Serve-Filer-Process-012023.pdf)
    > Accepted file types: Portable Document File (PDF); Word 2007 File (DOCX); Word 97-XP File (DOC) (shown on the official Add-a-Document upload screen); earlier guide states more narrowly: 'Document Format - The following document formats are supported: o Adobe® PDF.'
  - **PDF production/format rules (Tyler Odyssey File & Serve platform NC runs on)**: PDF must NOT be password-protected; must contain NO fillable/interactive form fields (flatten before upload); no unsupported symbol fonts (ZapfDingbats, Wingdings, Symbol); no active hyperlinks/shortcuts; page size 8.5"x11" Portrait; 300 dpi resolution; produced by Adobe Acrobat or Microsoft Word (Corel WordPerfect PDF producer not recommended). Documents with security restrictions or an eSignature 'may cause errors when uploading.' _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://odysseyfileandservecloud.zendesk.com/hc/en-us/articles/40875797939469-PDF-Requirements)
    > The PDF must contain no fill-able text input boxes... Your PDF documents should not be password protected... Documents with security restrictions or limited permissions may cause errors when uploading them to our system... Page size: 8.5" x 11" in Portrait orientation. Page resolution: 300 dpi.
  - **PDF flattening instruction (context for the PDF/A question)**: NCAOC's own official filer guidance instructs users to flatten every PDF before uploading. No PDF/A requirement, preference, or prohibition is stated anywhere in NCAOC's or Tyler's official documentation — the topic is never mentioned. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.nccourts.gov/assets/documents/publications/Additional-Information-for-File-&-Serve-Users-Filers-20230616.pdf)
    > Ensure that all PDFs that are uploaded are flattened.
  - **Filename character/length restrictions**: Under 24 characters; letters and numbers only; no punctuation or special characters (,.'!@#$%^&*-) aside from the period immediately before the ".pdf" extension. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://odysseyfileandservecloud.zendesk.com/hc/en-us/articles/40875797939469-PDF-Requirements)
    > Filename requirements: under 24 characters, only letters and numbers (No punctuation marks or special characters like ,.'!@#$%^&*- aside from the period before the "pdf" extension.)
  - **Bookmark / table-of-contents requirements**: No requirement to add bookmarks. In practice, any bookmarks a filer adds are frequently stripped: NCAOC instructs filers to flatten all PDFs before upload, and separately, the court's own file-stamping process re-flattens the accepted document, which removes bookmarks and other embedded PDF details regardless. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://odysseyfileandservecloud.zendesk.com/hc/en-us/articles/27839143790349-What-Happened-To-My-PDF-Bookmarks-Details)
    > If a filer has to flatten a PDF document prior to submission, that flattening process may eliminate the bookmarks or other special details a filer may have added to their PDF files. Additionally, the court's procedure for adding a file stamp to the document may flatten a PDF, which will remove bookmarks or other details added to a PDF by users.
  - **Searchable-text / OCR requirement**: Not a mandatory filing requirement anywhere in NCAOC's or Tyler's official materials for the statewide system. Tyler's own support knowledge base frames OCR/searchable-text creation strictly as an optional convenience tip for filers who are scanning paper documents — it is not gated or enforced as a system requirement. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://odysseyfileandservecloud.zendesk.com/hc/en-us/articles/360058658872-How-To-Create-a-Text-Searchable-PDF-Document)
    > If using a scanner, check to see if your scanner is equipped with the feature OCR. OCR stands for Optical Character Recognition. This feature will scan your document as text searchable.
  - **Attachment count limit — NC Business Court's SEPARATE e-filing system (not the general statewide platform)**: No limit to the number of attachments per filing/submission on the Business Court's own portal. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.nccourts.gov/assets/documents/publications/Business-Court-eFiling-Quick-Reference-Guide-20250516.pdf)
    > There is no limit to the number of attachments that you may upload.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Numeric attachment/document-count limit for the general statewide File & Serve system (the 100-county Odyssey platform): not documented anywhere found. The system appears to be governed by the 36.7 MB per-envelope size cap rather than a stated count limit, but no NCAOC or Tyler source explicitly confirms 'no count limit' for THIS platform the way the separate Business Court guide does for its own portal., Whether the accepted-format list (PDF / DOCX / DOC) shown in the 2022 official filer-workflow screenshot is uniform across all 100 counties and every filing code, or whether some case types/court locations restrict uploads to PDF only — the separate 'Recommended System Requirements' guide lists only Adobe PDF, creating some ambiguity that couldn't be resolved from public documentation.

---

## North Dakota

- **E-filing system:** Odyssey File & Serve (branded "File & Serve" by the ND Courts) — HTML5 version at northdakota.tylertech.cloud/OfsWeb/Home — for District Courts. The ND Supreme Court runs a separate, smaller, distinct e-filing portal (not the same public-facing system) for appellate filings, reached via ndcourts.gov/supreme-court/filing. (vendor: Tyler Technologies)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** North Dakota is NOT fragmented/county-by-county — confirmed. All district courts statewide use a single Tyler Odyssey File & Serve instance (one portal URL, ndcourts.gov/district-courts/e-filing-portal links to exactly one address for the whole state: https://northdakota.tylertech.cloud/OfsWeb/Home, described as the "Newest Version - Compatible with Safari, Chrome, Firefox, and Internet Explorer"). Electronic filing in district courts is governed by N.D.R.Ct. 3.5 and its Appendix K (a rule of court — excluded from this report per instructions, but the operative practical guidance comes from two AOC-published, currently-linked documents I used as primary sources: "Filer's Guide to Appendix K Rule 3.5 Filing Requirements" and "Common Causes of Filing Format Errors," both hosted directly on ndcourts.gov and linked from the live e-filing-resources page). Separately, the ND Supreme Court operates its own distinct e-filing portal for appellate filings (not the same system attorneys use for trial-court filings) documented at ndcourts.gov/supreme-court/efiling/tips — this is a second, smaller e-filing system, not a county fragmentation, but worth flagging so RaioPDF doesn't conflate district-court and Supreme Court constraints. One vintage source — a Tyler-hosted "Frequently Asked Questions" PDF dated September 2014 (ODY-FS-600-3061 v.5) — is still live at its URL and is ND-specific, but is NOT currently linked from ndcourts.gov's e-filing resources page, so it may be stale (its browser-support text references Internet Explorer 7-10 and Microsoft Silverlight, which is inconsistent with the current "HTML5 version" portal). I used it only where its factual claims (PDF/PDF-A acceptance, no-embedded-file-attachments rule, hyperlink rule) are not contradicted by the current AOC-hosted documents, and flagged it as dated wherever cited.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.ndcourts.gov/Media/Default/Trial%20Courts/Filing%20Errors.pdf)
  > Not required, not preferred, not outright prohibited — but a genuine, ND-documented technical risk exists. A 2014 Tyler-hosted FAQ states District Court File & Serve "only accepts documents in PDF or PDF-A formats" (both allowed, neither singled out as preferred). More importantly, the CURRENT, AOC-hosted "Common Causes of Filing Format Errors" guide explicitly ties PDF/A to a specific failure mode: PDF/A's standard practice of embedding font resources can produce an "unsupported font" Format Error if the embedded font encoding is CID or JBig — i.e., converting to PDF/A is not blanket-safe because some PDF/A producers embed font encodings the conversion pipeline rejects. This is a real, ND-specific, currently-published caveat, not a hypothetical.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.ndcourts.gov/Media/Default/Trial%20Courts/Appendix%20K%20Guide.pdf)
  > No North Dakota court document I reviewed addresses metadata at all — not the AOC's "Filer's Guide to Appendix K Rule 3.5 Filing Requirements" (the operative, comprehensive, currently-linked filing-requirements document), not the "Common Causes of Filing Format Errors" guide, not the Odyssey File & Serve Quick Reference Guide, and not the 2014 FAQ. There is no stated requirement to include or preserve metadata, no recommendation to scrub it before filing, and no indication that metadata-scrubbed files cause problems. This is a genuine silence across every ND-specific source found, not a gap in my search — it simply is not addressed anywhere in the state's e-filing documentation.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Max file size — District Courts (Odyssey File & Serve)**: 25 MB per document / 80 MB per envelope (submission) _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://odysseyfileandservecloud.zendesk.com/hc/en-us/articles/4402363973389-Max-PDF-File-Size-by-State)
    > North Dakota | 25 MB | 80 MB (State / Per Document / Per Envelope columns of Tyler's current max-file-size table)
  - **Max file size — District Courts (older ND-hosted figure, likely stale)**: Court 'recommended' 5 MB per document / 25 MB per envelope (2014 document — contradicted by the current Tyler KB figure of 25MB/80MB above; flagging both since I cannot confirm which the live portal enforces today) _(needs-review)_ -- [source](http://content.tylerhost.net/docs/nd/help/odysseyfileandservefrequentlyaskedquestions.pdf)
    > For optimal manageability, the court recommends that files do not exceed 5 MB per document and 25 MB per envelope.
  - **Max file size — Supreme Court e-filing portal**: 75 MB per document upload; larger files must be emailed to the Clerk instead _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.ndcourts.gov/supreme-court/efiling/tips)
    > The limit on the file size of uploads is 75 MB. When you look at the size of a file, 1,000 KB = 1 MB. So a file size over 75,000 KB would be too large to upload.
  - **Accepted file format — District Courts**: PDF or PDF-A only _(needs-review)_ -- [source](http://content.tylerhost.net/docs/nd/help/odysseyfileandservefrequentlyaskedquestions.pdf)
    > File & Serve only accepts documents in PDF or PDF-A formats.
  - **Accepted file format — Supreme Court**: Native searchable PDF strongly encouraged; if PDF is unavailable, WordPerfect, Word, or ASCII text accepted as fallback _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.ndcourts.gov/supreme-court/efiling/tips)
    > Filing of PDF searchable documents is strongly encouraged. If PDF is unavailable to the filer, only WordPerfect, Word or ASCII documents will be accepted.
  - **OCR / searchable-text — District Courts (risk finding, not a requirement)**: OCR is NOT required — and running OCR over a document is explicitly listed as a typical CAUSE of a rejection-triggering 'Format Error' in the district court system _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.ndcourts.gov/Media/Default/Trial%20Courts/Filing%20Errors.pdf)
    > A document that has Optical Character Recognition (OCR) associated with it, usually determined by a larger file size.
  - **Filename character/length restriction**: Under 24 characters, letters and numbers only, no punctuation/special characters (aside from the period before the .pdf extension) — CAVEAT: this is Tyler's generic Odyssey File & Serve Cloud platform documentation, not an ND-specific court publication; I found no ND court document stating a filename rule, so treat this as 'what the underlying software is documented to require' rather than an ND-AOC-confirmed rule. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://odysseyfileandservecloud.zendesk.com/hc/en-us/articles/40875797939469-PDF-Requirements)
    > Filename requirements: under 24 characters, only letters and numbers (No punctuation marks or special characters like ,.'!@#_$%^&*- aside from the period before the "pdf" extension.)
  - **Bookmark / table-of-contents requirement — District Courts**: No bookmark or table-of-contents requirement appears anywhere in the operative, comprehensive filing-requirements documents _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.ndcourts.gov/Media/Default/Trial%20Courts/Appendix%20K%20Guide.pdf)
    > The filing will be rejected if these guidelines are not followed. [21 numbered guidelines follow — paper size/orientation, party data, signature blocks, page sequence, paragraph numbering, exhibit separation, etc. — none reference bookmarks or a table of contents]
  - **Attachment/document count limit — Supreme Court**: Up to 5 documents per case, per upload session _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.ndcourts.gov/supreme-court/efiling/tips)
    > You can upload documents for one case at a time and up to five documents.
  - **Document-separation rule — District Courts (not a numeric cap, but governs attachment structure)**: Each docketable item (motion, exhibit, service document, affidavit, etc.) must be filed as its own separate PDF within the envelope — combining distinct documents into one PDF, or bundling exhibits into the main pleading's PDF, causes rejection _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.ndcourts.gov/Media/Default/Trial%20Courts/Appendix%20K%20Guide.pdf)
    > Individual documents must be filed separately. For example, documents may not be combined such as Motion & Service Document, Stipulation & Proposed Order, Brief & Exhibits, and Plea Agreement & Proposed Order. ... Exhibits to pleadings must be filed as separate documents.
  - **Document security / encryption prohibition — District Courts**: PDFs must be unsecured/not password-protected; secured or password-protected PDFs are a typical cause of Format Error rejection _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.ndcourts.gov/Media/Default/Trial%20Courts/Filing%20Errors.pdf)
    > Use non-secured document properties (i.e., not password-protected). ... Secured or password-protected PDFs [are a typical cause of format errors].
  - **Embedded file attachments within a PDF — District Courts**: Prohibited — a PDF containing an embedded file attachment (Acrobat's Document > Attach a File) triggers a File Format Error and rejection; combine appendices via Insert Pages instead _(needs-review)_ -- [source](http://content.tylerhost.net/docs/nd/help/odysseyfileandservefrequentlyaskedquestions.pdf)
    > No, it is not acceptable to use the file attachment option within a PDF document. If you create a PDF document that includes embedded file attachments, a "File Format Error" message is displayed when you view the filing status after submittal.
  - **Hyperlinks policy — District Courts**: Internal (within-document) links are permitted; external URLs, shortcuts, and hyperlinks to other documents/websites must be removed and can themselves cause Format Errors _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.ndcourts.gov/Media/Default/Trial%20Courts/Filing%20Errors.pdf)
    > Remove external references in the documents (URLs, shortcuts, etc.). [listed as part of the 'standard document specifications for e-filing cases']

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Metadata policy: no ND court document (FAQ, Filer's Guide, Format Errors guide, or Quick Reference Guide) states any requirement to include, preserve, or remove document metadata, or any indication that metadata-scrubbed files cause problems — reported as 'silent' in metadataScrubStance rather than left fully unaddressed, since multiple comprehensive primary sources were checked., District Courts numeric attachment/document count cap: no ND source states a hard maximum number of documents/attachments per envelope for district court filings (only the separate Supreme Court portal states an explicit 5-document limit); district guidance covers document-separation rules but not a count ceiling., Whether the 24-character/letters-only filename rule is actually enforced by North Dakota's specific Odyssey File & Serve configuration, as opposed to being generic Tyler platform documentation not customized/confirmed for ND — no ND-specific court document states a filename rule at all., Whether the current, controlling per-document/per-envelope file size limit for ND district courts is the Tyler vendor KB's 25MB/80MB figure or some other current value — the only ND-court-hosted figure I found (5MB/25MB, 'recommended') is from a September 2014 document not currently linked from ndcourts.gov's e-filing resources page, so its currency is uncertain.

---

## Ohio

- **E-filing system:** FRAGMENTED — no single statewide e-filing portal for general litigation. Three distinct tiers observed: (1) Supreme Court of Ohio's own "e-Filing Portal" — handles ONLY cases filed directly with the Supreme Court of Ohio (original actions, appeals from courts of appeals, etc.), not trial-court matters. (2) Ohio Court of Claims' "eFileOH" — a separate, narrower statewide-scope system for Court of Claims case types only (claims vs. the state, public records requests, crime victims compensation). (3) Ohio's 88 counties' Common Pleas, Municipal, and Appellate courts each adopt their own local e-filing rules/administrative orders and each procures/operates its own e-filing system independently (analogous to California's county-by-county EFSP model) — e.g., Franklin County Common Pleas runs its own system under its own "Ninth Amended Civil eFiling Administrative Order," and Cuyahoga County's Eighth Appellate District imposes its own file-format rule (Loc.App.R. 13.1) referencing "the Cuyahoga County Clerk of Court's electronic filing procedure." (vendor: Fragmented by court — Tyler Technologies (Odyssey File & Serve, branded "eFileOH") powers the Ohio Court of Claims' system and is offered to counties that choose to contract with Tyler (contact info for other courts to "offer e-filing with Odyssey eFileOH" appears on tylertech.com); Franklin County Common Pleas' portal runs on a platform branded "Tyberacloud" (efile.franklincountyoh.tyberacloud.net); the Supreme Court of Ohio's own e-Filing Portal does not identify its underlying vendor in the Attorney e-Filing User Guide; Cuyahoga County's e-filing procedure/vendor is set by the Cuyahoga County Clerk of Courts and is not named in the Eighth District's local rule. No single vendor serves all of Ohio's trial courts.)
- **Statewide system:** no -- fragmented/county-by-county
- **Notes:** Confirmed via direct comparison of three official Ohio court documents that Ohio's technical e-filing requirements genuinely differ court-to-court: the Supreme Court of Ohio's own portal guide states only "file in PDF, one document per PDF" with no file-size cap, no OCR requirement, and no PDF/A mention; Franklin County Common Pleas Court's own Administrative Order sets a 5MB/25MB size cap and a font/spacing rule found nowhere in the Supreme Court's guide; and Cuyahoga County's Eighth Appellate District's Local Rules impose a searchable-but-not-editable PDF mandate and ban external hyperlinks — a rule that appears in none of the other systems reviewed. This is consistent with Ohio Sup.R. 27's framework, under which the Supreme Court's Technology Standards Committee approves individual courts' own local rules/administrative orders for electronic filing rather than mandating one uniform statewide portal for trial-level courts (this framework description is based on secondary summaries of Sup.R. 27, not a directly quoted primary excerpt — the primary rule text file exceeded fetch size limits). RaioPDF should NOT assume a single "Ohio" technical profile; any Ohio-specific preset should be scoped per-court (Supreme Court of Ohio vs. named county) and should surface the county/court's own current administrative order rather than a generic "Ohio" default.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.fccourts.org/DocumentCenter/View/1148/Civil---Ninth-Amended-Administrative-E-Filing-Order)
  > No requirement, preference, or prohibition of PDF/A (ISO 19005) was found in any of the three official sources examined: the Supreme Court of Ohio's Attorney e-Filing User Guide (specifies plain "PDF" only), Franklin County Common Pleas Court's Ninth Amended Civil eFiling Administrative Order (specifies plain "Portable Document Format (PDF)"), or Cuyahoga County's Eighth Appellate District Local Rules (specifies "searchable, but not editable, PDF format" — still no PDF/A reference). All three describe the format requirement in generic PDF terms with no mention of the PDF/A archival subset, and none flag encryption, form-field, or annotation conflicts with PDF/A.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://appeals.cuyahogacounty.gov/docs/default-source/default-document-library/localrules.pdf)
  > No policy requiring or recommending removal of PDF file metadata (Author/Company/revision history/hidden data) was found in any of the three sources reviewed. Note a related but distinct requirement exists at the Eighth Appellate District: Loc.App.R. 13.2(B) requires filers to remove or redact "personal and private information" (SSNs, financial account numbers, juvenile names, sexual-offense-victim names) from document CONTENT before filing — this is a content-redaction rule, not a file-metadata-property rule, and should not be conflated with the metadata-scrubbing question. No source addressed whether metadata-scrubbed files cause technical problems on submission.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size — Franklin County Common Pleas Court (county-level example; NOT a statewide figure)**: 5 MB per individual PDF file; the combined total of all PDF files in one e-filing submission may not exceed 25 MB _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.fccourts.org/DocumentCenter/View/1148/Civil---Ninth-Amended-Administrative-E-Filing-Order)
    > Size of Filing. Submissions shall be limited to five megabytes (5MB) in size. No combination of PDF files in one transmission may accumulate to more than 25 megabytes (25MB) in size.
  - **Accepted file format — Supreme Court of Ohio e-Filing Portal (Supreme Court cases only, statewide in scope but NOT for trial courts)**: PDF is required for all substantive filings. Each document, together with any exhibits attached to it, must be assembled as a single, separate PDF file — multiple distinct documents (e.g., a notice of appeal and a memorandum in support of jurisdiction) must never be combined into one PDF. No specific PDF version number (e.g., 1.7/2.0) is specified. Only one document can be uploaded per Add-PDF action. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.supremecourt.ohio.gov/docs/e-filing/Guide/e-FilingUserGuide.pdf)
    > Prepare each document (and any associated exhibits) as a single PDF file. Do NOT create a single PDF file containing multiple documents that you are submitting for filing. For example, the notice of appeal and memorandum in support of jurisdiction should be submitted as two separate PDFs.
  - **Accepted file format — Franklin County Common Pleas Court**: PDF required for all filed documents, pleadings, papers, and exhibits, with one carve-out: proposed orders/entries must instead be submitted in Microsoft Word 2007-or-higher-compatible format (.docx), with no mail-merge fields and no picture-boxes of text. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.fccourts.org/DocumentCenter/View/1148/Civil---Ninth-Amended-Administrative-E-Filing-Order)
    > All electronically filed documents, pleadings and papers shall be filed with the Clerk in Portable Document Format (PDF) with the exception of proposed orders. Proposed orders shall be submitted in a Microsoft Word 2007 or higher compatible format (.docx) and shall reference the specific motions to which they apply.
  - **Searchable-text / OCR requirement — Cuyahoga County, Eighth Appellate District Court of Appeals (county/district-specific, NOT statewide)**: REQUIRED — e-filed documents, including any attachments, must be filed as searchable PDFs. The rule additionally requires the PDF be non-editable, and separately bans embedded external hyperlinks (internal links within the same filing are allowed). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://appeals.cuyahogacounty.gov/docs/default-source/default-document-library/localrules.pdf)
    > Format of Electronically Filed (e-filed) Documents. ... E-filed documents, including attachments, shall be filed in searchable, but not editable, PDF format. External electronic links, to material outside the filed document, are strictly prohibited. Internal links to other parts of the same filing are permissible.
  - **Handling of oversized exhibit sets (a size-based splitting rule, distinct from a hard attachment-count cap) — Franklin County Common Pleas Court**: No fixed numeric attachment-count limit is stated. Instead, exhibits that exceed the court's file-size limits must be split into multiple, sequentially labeled parts, each accompanied by a cover page identifying the case and which part of the set it contains. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.fccourts.org/DocumentCenter/View/1148/Civil---Ninth-Amended-Administrative-E-Filing-Order)
    > Exhibits that must be filed separately (ex: ... miscellaneous exhibits accompanying a motion that exceed the filing size limitations, etc.) shall be accompanied by a cover page that contains the full case caption and case number of the case in which they are filed. If filed in multiple parts, exhibits shall be clearly marked to identify which part of the submission they contain (Ex: "Exhibits A through J – Part 1 of 3").

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Statewide maximum file size — no single figure exists because Ohio has no unified statewide e-filing portal for trial courts; the Supreme Court of Ohio's own e-Filing Portal user guide states no numeric file-size cap at all, so even that narrower statewide system has no documented limit within the source reviewed., Filename character/length restrictions — not addressed in any of the three official sources reviewed (Supreme Court of Ohio e-Filing Portal guide, Franklin County Common Pleas Administrative Order, Cuyahoga County Eighth Appellate District Local Rules)., Bookmark or table-of-contents requirements — not addressed in any source reviewed; Cuyahoga's Eighth District rule only addresses hyperlinks (external links prohibited, internal links permitted), not bookmarks/TOC structure., Hard numeric attachment-count limit — not found in any source; Ohio courts examined regulate via file-size caps and exhibit-splitting/labeling instructions rather than a fixed count of attachments., PDF file metadata (Author/Company/hidden revision data) policy — no source found requiring, recommending, or warning against metadata scrubbing; distinct from the content-level personal-information redaction rule found at Cuyahoga's Eighth District (Loc.App.R. 13.2), which governs document text, not file properties., Ohio Court of Claims (eFileOH/Tyler) specific technical specs (file size, PDF/A, OCR, filename, bookmarks, attachment count, metadata) — confirmed this system exists and is Tyler-Technologies-powered, but a dedicated technical-specifications page or user manual with these details was not located within the bounded search effort., Whether the Franklin County Ninth Amended Administrative Order (last confirmed dated via court-stamp 2022-07-29) remains the current, unsuperseded version as of 2026 — no more recent amended order was located, but its currency was not independently confirmed against a live index of Franklin County administrative orders.

---

## Oklahoma (state courts — District Courts, Court of Civil Appeals, Court of Criminal Appeals, Supreme Court)

- **E-filing system:** OUCMS E-Filing Portal (Oklahoma Unified Case Management System), accessed at efile.oscn.net / OSCN.net, administered by the Administrative Office of the Courts under the Oklahoma Supreme Court (vendor: Not named in any official OSCN/AOC source reviewed (Technical Standards, E-Filing Rules, User Guide, FAQ). The underlying case-management platform vendor is not disclosed in these documents, so this field is unconfirmed — do not treat as verified.)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Oklahoma runs ONE state-operated e-filing platform (OUCMS, via OSCN.net, one uniform "Electronic Filing Technical Standards" document from the AOC) rather than county-procured vendors like California — so architecturally it is a single statewide system, not fragmented. HOWEVER it is emphatically not yet universal or mandatory: the founding order (SCAD-2012-36) rolls it out "in other Oklahoma counties on a county-by-county basis as approved by this Court," and the current official E-Filing FAQ (dated 1/28/2025) states e-filing is live in only 13 of Oklahoma's 77 counties: Adair, Canadian, Cleveland, Comanche, Ellis, Garfield, Logan, Oklahoma, Payne, Pushmataha, Roger Mills, Rogers, and Tulsa. Even in those counties e-filing is optional — "Is e-Filing mandatory? A: No. Conventional paper filing is still available." Additional portal-level restrictions worth flagging for RaioPDF: e-filing cannot be used to initiate a new case (existing cases only), and confidential/sealed documents and proposed orders cannot be e-filed at all — those must go to the court clerk's office on paper. Separately, Oklahoma's three federal U.S. District Courts (E.D., W.D., N.D. Okla.) run the unrelated federal CM/ECF/PACER e-filing system with their own distinct technical rules (e.g., the Eastern District publishes its own PDF/A FAQ) — that is a different court system entirely and is out of scope for this state-court research.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://efile.oscn.net/docs/Electronic%20Filing%20Technical%20Standards.pdf)
  > The AOC's "Electronic Filing Technical Standards" (10/22/2024) is the authoritative technical spec and explicitly frames its own scope as covering "file size, attributes, resolution, embedded files, and other technical requirements," yet its actual Document Format section says only: "All e-Documents should be filed in a text-based PDF format." Neither this document, nor Rule 12 ("Form of Electronic Documents") of the Rules for Electronic Filing, nor the E-Filing User Guide, nor the E-Filing FAQ mentions "PDF/A" anywhere. No requirement, preference, or prohibition of PDF/A was found in any official source — the format spec is silent on the ISO archival standard, specifying only "text-based PDF."
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://efile.oscn.net/docs/Electronic%20Filing%20Technical%20Standards.pdf)
  > None of the four official documents reviewed (Electronic Filing Technical Standards, Rule 12 of the Rules for Electronic Filing, the E-Filing User Guide, or the E-Filing FAQ) contains the word "metadata" or any instruction to add, preserve, or strip document metadata before filing. The Technical Standards document's own stated scope ("file size, attributes, resolution, embedded files, and other technical requirements") is the closest brush with the topic, but its 9 enumerated requirements (browser compatibility, document format, document size, hyperlinks, multiple-document filing, bulk filings, proposed orders, confidential/sealed documents, attachments) never address metadata in either direction.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size (per document)**: 10 MB per individual e-Document (PDF file). If a document exceeds 10 MB it must be split into multiple separate e-Documents (e.g., 'Petition Part 1.pdf', 'Petition Part 2.pdf'), each including the case style and case number. No distinct aggregate 'envelope/submission' size cap is stated — instead, combining multiple e-Documents into one PDF, or bulk-filing across cases, is separately prohibited (see Bulk Filings rule), so a submission's effective ceiling is the sum of its individually-compliant (≤10MB) e-Documents. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efile.oscn.net/docs/Electronic%20Filing%20Technical%20Standards.pdf)
    > The maximum file size for an e-Document is 10 megabytes. If an e-Document exceeds this limit, it should be split into separate e-Documents.
  - **Accepted PDF format**: PDF is required, specifically 'text-based PDF format' for all e-Documents. No specific PDF version number (e.g. 1.4, 1.7, 2.0) is specified anywhere in the official technical documentation reviewed. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efile.oscn.net/docs/Electronic%20Filing%20Technical%20Standards.pdf)
    > All e-Documents should be filed in a text-based PDF format. ... All E-Documents shall be filed in a text-based PDF format in compliance with the Electronic Filing Technical Standards.
  - **Searchable-text / OCR requirement**: Preferred/'should' but not absolutely mandatory: e-Documents and attachments/exhibits should be filed as text-searchable PDFs, but if the original cannot be converted to text-searchable, a non-text-searchable PDF is expressly permitted, and non-text images may be submitted as JPEG as a further fallback. There is no hard OCR gate that blocks a filing for lacking searchable text. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efile.oscn.net/docs/eFiling%20User%20Guide%20-%20Filer%20Interface.pdf)
    > Attachments and exhibits should be submitted with the principal E-Filed document as a txt-searchable PDF. If the original attachment or document cannot be converted to a text-searchable PDF, the attachment or document may be submitted in a non-text searchable PDF format.
  - **Attachment count limits**: No numeric cap on the number of attachments/exhibits per filing was found. Instead there is a structural rule: bulk-combining multiple e-Documents (or multiple cases) into a single PDF is prohibited — each attachment/exhibit not folded into the principal document must be filed as its own separate e-Document (individually subject to the 10MB limit) and clearly named to identify the principal document it relates to. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efile.oscn.net/docs/Electronic%20Filing%20Technical%20Standards.pdf)
    > Bulk filings of multiple cases or multiple e-Documents combined into one PDF e-Document cannot be e-Filed. ... Any attachment or exhibit which is filed as a separate E-Document ... shall be ... clearly named to specify the principal Document to which it is related.
  - **System rollout scope (portal availability)**: The portal is live in only 13 of Oklahoma's 77 counties as of the most recent official FAQ (Jan. 2025): Adair, Canadian, Cleveland, Comanche, Ellis, Garfield, Logan, Oklahoma, Payne, Pushmataha, Roger Mills, Rogers, and Tulsa. E-filing is optional even there; paper filing remains available statewide. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efile.oscn.net/docs/EFILING_FAQ.pdf)
    > E-Filing is available for the following counties and these are the only counties where e-Filing will be available: Adair, Canadian, Cleveland, Comanche, Ellis, Garfield, Logan, Oklahoma, Payne, Pushmataha, Roger Mills, Rogers and Tulsa. ... Is e-Filing mandatory? A: No. Conventional paper filing is still available.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Filename character-set / length restrictions — no technical limit (allowed characters or max length) is specified in the Technical Standards, Rule 12, User Guide, or FAQ; the only guidance found is a non-technical naming convention for split files (include case style/number, label parts sequentially), not an enforced restriction., Bookmark or table-of-contents requirements — not addressed at all (neither required nor discussed) in any of the four official OSCN/AOC documents reviewed (Technical Standards, Rule 12, User Guide, FAQ).

---

## Oregon

- **E-filing system:** Odyssey File & Serve (branded by the Oregon Judicial Department as "OJD eFile" / "File and Serve") (vendor: Tyler Technologies)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Oregon has ONE mandatory statewide e-filing system for trial-level courts: Odyssey File & Serve (Tyler Technologies), used by all Oregon Circuit Courts and the Oregon Tax Court. It is NOT fragmented county-by-county like California — OJD contracted Tyler after a competitive bid and rolled Odyssey out court-by-court from 2013–2016, with mandatory e-filing for active OSB members completing statewide by fall 2016; it remains the live statewide system today (portal: oregon.tylerhost.net/ofsweb, and a newer "H5" HTML5 interface at oregon.tylertech.cloud/ofsweb — the FAQ documentation covers both the legacy Silverlight-based site and the new H5 site). Self-represented litigants typically enter through "OJD Guide & File," which then routes into the same File & Serve backend. CAVEAT: the Oregon Supreme Court and Court of Appeals use a separately-branded "Appellate eFile" system; this research focused on the circuit-court/Tax-Court Odyssey File & Serve system (where the overwhelming volume of attorney e-filing happens) and did not separately verify Appellate eFile's technical specs — flagging this rather than assuming the two are identical.
- **PDF/A stance:** preferred -- [source](https://www.courts.oregon.gov/services/online/Documents/eFile/OdysseyFileandServeFAQ.pdf)
  > PDF/A is explicitly named as one of exactly two accepted formats — "text-searchable PDF or PDF-A" — by two separate official Oregon Judicial Department documents (not merely tolerated as an edge case). It is NOT mandatory (plain text-searchable PDF is equally acceptable) and there is no language suggesting OJD favors PDF/A over plain searchable PDF for any archival or other reason — so treat "preferred" here as "explicitly sanctioned/named," not "recommended over the alternative." IMPORTANT CAUTION FOUND: Tyler's own official Oregon-specific FAQ contains a dedicated "Unsupported Fonts" troubleshooting section stating that PDF/A files, "as a standard," embed font resources, and that "document generating tools use non-supported fonts when creating documents, which results in the inability to convert the document into the standard e-filing format" (it specifically calls out the JBig font as unsupported). This is a real, sourced signal that PDF/A conversion is NOT risk-free — a PDF/A converter that embeds non-standard fonts can cause outright rejection/Format Error, independent of the fact that PDF/A itself is nominally accepted. Separately (not PDF/A-specific but relevant to the "encryption conflicts" question), the same FAQ and Tyler's generic PDF-requirements documentation both state that password-protected/secured/permission-restricted PDFs commonly cause upload and conversion errors — so any PDF/A workflow must not carry forward encryption or restricted permissions.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.courts.oregon.gov/services/online/Documents/eFile/OdysseyFileandServeFAQ.pdf)
  > No official Oregon Judicial Department or Tyler Technologies File & Serve technical document reviewed mentions document metadata (author/title/XMP properties) at all, in either direction. Checked: the OJD "Standards for Electronic Filings in Circuit Courts" supplemental guide (rejection-reason catalog), the OJD "File & Serve: Filing Code Quick Reference Guide," the Tyler "Odyssey File & Serve FAQ — State of Oregon" (including its detailed "Format Errors" and "Causes of Typical Format Errors" troubleshooting sections), and Tyler's generic "PDF Requirements" knowledge-base page. None require inclusion of specific metadata, none instruct or recommend scrubbing/removing metadata before filing, and none indicate that a metadata-scrubbed file causes an upload or processing problem. The documented causes of technical "Format Errors" are all structural/content issues (corrupt/zero-byte files, password/security restrictions, non-PDF file types, non-standard image compression, unsupported embedded fonts, off-center/landscape/irregular scans, invalid tables) — metadata is simply never raised as a factor.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size — per document**: 25 MB per document. Oversized documents must be split into separate documents (within the same envelope), each ≤25 MB, filed in order under the same filing code with a Filing Comment noting "part 1 of 2" etc. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.oregon.gov/services/online/Documents/eFile/OdysseyFileandServeFAQ.pdf)
    > The file size may not exceed 25 MB per document. Documents greater than 25MB must be broken down and submitted as separate documents (within the same envelope) that do not exceed 25 MB. Each document should be submitted in order using the same filing code. The filer shall indicate which part of the whole document that the filed document represents (1 of 3, 2 of 3, 3 of 3) within the Filing Comments field.
