  - **Maximum file size — per envelope/submission**: 35 MB per envelope (Oregon), per Tyler's cross-state Odyssey File & Serve size-limit table _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://odysseyfileandservecloud.zendesk.com/hc/en-us/articles/4402363973389-Max-PDF-File-Size-by-State)
    > Oregon — Per Document: 25 MB — Per Envelope: 35 MB. [Header note:] Max File Size is subject to change.
  - **Accepted PDF format/version**: Text-searchable PDF or PDF/A only. Fillable/interactive-form PDFs are explicitly disallowed and must be flattened before filing. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](http://content.tylerhost.net/docs/or/help/OFSOregonFCQRG.pdf)
    > Documents must be submitted in a text-searchable PDF or PDF-A format. Fillable PDF documents should not be submitted using File & Serve. The rule governing document formatting for documents filed through File & Serve can be found at UTCR 21.040.
  - **Searchable-text / OCR requirement**: Required. A PDF that has not been OCR'd (image-only, not text-searchable) is a defined, named rejection reason in the e-filing system itself, distinct from any UTCR rule violation. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.oregon.gov/services/online/Documents/eFile/oeto_OJD-Guidance-Document-eFiling-Standards-EXTERNAL.pdf)
    > 3. Technical Errors (Either by the eFiler or the System) ... PDF Document that is Not Text Searchable — Rejection Description: The PDF document submitted is not text searchable. How to avoid this rejection reason: Make sure the PDF conversion process includes applying Optical Character Recognition (OCR) to the document before submitting the document(s).
  - **Filename character/length restrictions**: Keep filenames short (roughly 24–25 characters including spaces, per two slightly inconsistent Tyler pages) and alphanumeric-only — no punctuation or special characters other than the extension's period. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://odysseyfileandservecloud.zendesk.com/hc/en-us/articles/40875797939469-PDF-Requirements)
    > Filename requirements: under 24 characters, only letters and numbers (No punctuation marks or special characters like ,.'!@#_$%^&*- aside from the period before the "pdf" extension.) ... [separately:] A filename longer than 25 characters will also trigger this error message. Please keep filenames no longer than 25 characters. (Spaces are included in this character limit.)
  - **PDF/A-specific caution — unsupported embedded fonts can cause Format Error / conversion failure**: Tyler's own Oregon troubleshooting FAQ separately identifies PDF/A-generated documents as a recurring source of rejection because PDF/A's font-embedding standard sometimes embeds fonts the system's conversion engine does not support. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.oregon.gov/services/online/Documents/eFile/OdysseyFileandServeFAQ.pdf)
    > Font resources are included in newly created documents. This is a standard with PDF/A files. Document generating tools use non–supported fonts when creating documents, which results in the inability to convert the document into the standard e-filing format. ... The JBig font is not a supported font.
  - **Encrypted / password-protected / permission-restricted PDFs**: Prohibited in practice — a common, named cause of Format Errors and upload failures, independent of and in addition to any PDF/A question. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.oregon.gov/services/online/Documents/eFile/OdysseyFileandServeFAQ.pdf)
    > Your PDF documents should not be password protected. ... Documents with security restrictions or limited permissions may cause errors when uploading them to our system. The most common restriction, as mentioned above, is a password protection on a PDF, though you may also encounter errors if there is an eSignature on your document. [Oregon FAQ, corroborating:] Secured or password-protected PDFs. This includes electronic certificates that prevent a document from being modified. These are typically used on documents containing electronic signatures.
  - **OCR'd files as a secondary source of Format Errors (nuance on the OCR requirement)**: Even though OCR/text-searchability is required (see above), Tyler's own Oregon FAQ separately lists OCR-processed documents among the common causes of technical Format Errors, apparently because OCR increases file size/complexity. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.oregon.gov/services/online/Documents/eFile/OdysseyFileandServeFAQ.pdf)
    > Causes of Typical Format Errors ... A document that has Optical Character Recognition (OCR) associated with it; usually determined by a larger file size.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Bookmark / table-of-contents requirement — no official OJD or Tyler File & Serve technical document reviewed mentions bookmarks or a table-of-contents requirement in either direction (not required, not recommended, not prohibited was ever stated)., Attachment count limit — no explicit numeric cap on the number of documents/attachments per envelope was found in any official source; the only documented envelope-level constraint is the 35 MB total size limit (per the vendor's cross-state size table), not a document count.

---

## Pennsylvania

- **E-filing system:** PACFile (the Pennsylvania Unified Judicial System's electronic filing service, delivered through the UJS Web Portal at ujsportal.pacourts.us) (vendor: No third-party vendor brand (e.g., Tyler/Odyssey, File & ServeXpress) was found attached to PACFile in the official documentation reviewed. PACFile is presented throughout as a service built and operated directly by the Administrative Office of Pennsylvania Courts (AOPC) via the UJS Web Portal — it reads as an in-house AOC system rather than an outsourced e-filing platform.)
- **Statewide system:** no -- fragmented/county-by-county
- **Notes:** Pennsylvania's e-filing landscape is genuinely split — not one uniform statewide portal for every case type, so a single "Pennsylvania e-filing requirements" answer is misleading if presented as blanket-statewide. PACFile (AOPC/UJS Web Portal) IS a true mandatory statewide system for (1) all appellate filings in the Supreme, Superior, and Commonwealth Courts, and (2) criminal-case filings in the Courts of Common Pleas and Philadelphia Municipal Court. But CIVIL filings at the Court of Common Pleas level — the trial-court venue for the bulk of everyday civil litigation, and probably what most solo/small-firm RaioPDF users file most often — are NOT unified under PACFile. The PACFile Overview page itself says filings go to "the Supreme, Superior, Commonwealth, and certain Common Pleas courts" (i.e., only some counties have opted PACFile in for some purposes). The largest counties instead run their own independently-vendored civil e-filing systems: Philadelphia County's First Judicial District operates its own "eFileIT" portal at fjdefile.phila.gov, and Allegheny County's Department of Court Records has run its own separate, mandatory e-filing system since November 13, 2023. Those county-run civil portals were NOT researched in this pass (out of scope/bounded effort) and likely carry their own distinct technical specs. Everything in "constraints" and the PDF/A and metadata fields below describes PACFile only (appellate courts statewide + criminal Common Pleas statewide) — it should not be assumed to apply to a given county's civil e-filing portal without separate verification.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://ujswebportalhelp.pacourts.us/A_Topics/D_PACFile/A_AllCourts/I_Miscellaneous/C_Document%20Requirements%20-%20PACFile.htm)
  > The PACFile "Electronic Document Requirements" page — the most detailed official technical-specs document located, covering format, size, fonts, scanning DPI, security, and filenames — specifies only generic "PDF file format" and never mentions PDF/A (the ISO archival PDF subset) anywhere, on that page or on the Superior Court / Commonwealth Court "Filing Documents tab" help pages or the Appellate FAQ. PDF/A is neither required, preferred, nor flagged as prohibited/problematic (no mention of encryption conflicts, form-field issues, or redaction/annotation stripping tied to PDF/A). Absence across all located official technical-requirements pages is the basis for "silent" rather than an affirmative statement.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://ujswebportalhelp.pacourts.us/A_Topics/D_PACFile/A_AllCourts/I_Miscellaneous/C_Document%20Requirements%20-%20PACFile.htm)
  > The same PACFile Electronic Document Requirements page, plus the Superior/Commonwealth Court Filing Documents help pages and the Appellate FAQ, address file format, size, fonts, DPI, security (no password protection), and filename characters in detail, but contain no mention of document metadata at all — no requirement to include specific metadata (e.g., no case-number-in-metadata mandate), no instruction to scrub or remove metadata before filing, and no warning that metadata-scrubbed files cause processing problems. This is a documentation gap/silence, not an affirmative policy statement either way.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size**: 500 MB maximum per individual document submitted through PACFile. No separate/distinct envelope- or total-submission-level size cap is documented anywhere found — the limit is stated only per document. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://ujswebportalhelp.pacourts.us/A_Topics/D_PACFile/A_AllCourts/I_Miscellaneous/C_Document%20Requirements%20-%20PACFile.htm)
    > The document must be less than 500 MB (megabytes) in size.
  - **Accepted PDF version / file format requirements**: PDF file format is mandatory for all documents; no specific PDF version number (e.g., 1.4, 1.7, 2.0) is specified anywhere in the official documentation. Guidance favors direct electronic conversion from the originating word-processing file over scanning a printed copy, and requires embedding any non-standard fonts during PDF conversion. Documents must NOT be password-protected or otherwise secured — the same requirements page states security features will block processing. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://ujswebportalhelp.pacourts.us/A_Topics/D_PACFile/A_AllCourts/I_Miscellaneous/C_Document%20Requirements%20-%20PACFile.htm)
    > All documents must be saved in the PDF file format.
  - **Filename character/length restrictions**: Document/file names must not contain the following characters: backslash, forward slash, colon, asterisk, question mark, straight quotation marks, or angle brackets (< / >). No maximum filename length was found specified in the official documentation. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://ujswebportalhelp.pacourts.us/A_Topics/D_PACFile/A_AllCourts/I_Miscellaneous/C_Document%20Requirements%20-%20PACFile.htm)
    > The document name must not contain any of the following characters: \ / : * ? " < >

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Per-envelope/total-submission file size cap for PACFile — only a 500 MB per-document limit is documented; no separate envelope-level or total-filing-size cap was found in any official PACFile page reviewed., Searchable-text / OCR requirement for PACFile — not addressed in the Electronic Document Requirements page, the Appellate FAQ, or the Superior/Commonwealth Filing Documents tab help pages; no statement requiring or recommending OCR/searchable text was found., Bookmark or table-of-contents requirement for PACFile filings — not addressed in any official documentation located., Attachment count limit per filing on PACFile — no numeric cap was found; the only related rule found is structural (documents for different filing types cannot be combined into a single file and must be attached separately per filing type), which is not the same as a maximum-attachments constraint., Technical/portal filing requirements (file size, format, PDF/A stance, metadata policy, etc.) for the separate, county-operated CIVIL e-filing systems at the Court of Common Pleas level — e.g., Philadelphia County's First Judicial District eFileIT (fjdefile.phila.gov) and Allegheny County's Department of Court Records e-filing system — were not researched in this pass and are likely to differ from PACFile's specs; these would need their own dedicated research given Pennsylvania's fragmented civil e-filing landscape.

---

## Rhode Island

- **E-filing system:** eFileRI (Odyssey File & Serve) (vendor: Tyler Technologies, Inc.)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Confirmed: Rhode Island runs ONE statewide, mandatory e-filing system — eFileRI, built on Tyler Technologies' Odyssey File & Serve platform (https://efileri.tylertech.cloud) — used by all courts in the Rhode Island Judiciary (Supreme, Superior, Family, District, Workers' Compensation Court, and the Traffic Tribunal). This is NOT a fragmented county-by-county model like California; it is a single Judiciary-wide EFS governed by one statewide rule set (Supreme Court Article X, Rules Governing Electronic Filing, revised September 2023) and one general technical reference (the "Rhode Island Judiciary User Guide for Electronic Filing," still the live linked document on the court's current Electronic Filing Guidelines page as of this research, though its cover page reads "Effective November 5, 2014, Revised August 10, 2017" — the file itself shows an HTTP last-modified date of June 2023, and Article X's 2023 revision still points to it by name as authoritative for technical requirements). Each individual court (Supreme, Superior, Family, District, Workers' Comp, Traffic Tribunal) also publishes its own supplementary e-filing guidelines document that mostly incorporates the general User Guide's technical rules by reference but occasionally states its own numbers — most notably, the Supreme Court's 2021 guidelines set a different (larger) file-size limit than the general User Guide/Superior Court guidelines. Electronic filing is mandatory for attorneys statewide (with narrow waiver/incarceration exceptions) and optional for self-represented litigants, per Article X Rule 1(b)/3.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.courts.ri.gov/Public-Resources/Documents/Electronic%20Filing/RI_Judiciary_User_Guide_for_Electronic_Filing.pdf)
  > The User Guide explicitly names PDF/A as an equally acceptable alternative to standard PDF ("shall be in a searchable portable document format (PDF or PDF-A)") — it is not required over plain PDF, not specifically preferred, and not prohibited; the two formats are presented on equal footing with no stated preference. No source reviewed (User Guide, Article X, Supreme Court guidelines, or Superior Court guidelines) mentions any problem caused by PDF/A specifically — no note of encryption conflicts, form-field issues, or redaction/annotation stripping tied to PDF/A. Two adjacent, EFS-wide (non-PDF/A-specific) rules are worth flagging as related context: (1) "Documents may not be secured, password-protected, or have other features limiting access" (Sec. 4.3.4) — this bans encryption/security on any filed PDF regardless of version, which happens to align with (not conflict with) PDF/A's own spec-level ban on encryption; and (2) fillable/interactive-form PDFs are rejected outright by the system regardless of PDF/A status (Sec. 4.1), with the guide recommending flattening the form to a standard PDF first. Neither of these is evidence that PDF/A itself causes a problem — they are blanket EFS rules that a PDF/A file would need to comply with just like any other PDF.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.courts.ri.gov/Public-Resources/Documents/Electronic%20Filing/RI_Judiciary_User_Guide_for_Electronic_Filing.pdf)
  > None of the primary sources reviewed — the statewide User Guide for Electronic Filing (the comprehensive technical-requirements document), Article X (Rules Governing Electronic Filing), the Supreme Court's E-File Guidelines, or the Superior Court's E-Filing Guidelines — mention document metadata in any way: no requirement to include specific metadata, no instruction or recommendation to scrub/remove metadata before filing, and no warning that metadata-scrubbed (or metadata-laden) files cause rejections or problems. The only privacy-related filing obligation found concerns redacting visible non-public/Personal Identifying Information from the document's *content* itself (Article X, Rule 8(b)(1): "it is the responsibility of the filing party to ensure that non-public information or personally identifiable information is appropriately redacted prior to filing") — this is about on-page content redaction, not file-level metadata scrubbing, and the sources draw no connection between the two.

**Constraints found:**
  - **maxFileSize_general**: General/default EFS rule: a single filing should not exceed 25 MB. If a document is larger, it must be broken into multiple filed parts (each noted in the filing comments, e.g. "Part 2 to Follow"). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.ri.gov/Public-Resources/Documents/Electronic%20Filing/RI_Judiciary_User_Guide_for_Electronic_Filing.pdf)
    > Document Size - A single filing should not be greater than 25 megabytes. Larger documents or filings may be filed in several parts.
  - **maxFileSize_supremeCourtVariant**: Court-specific variation: the Supreme Court's own e-filing guidelines (more recent than the general User Guide) set a DIFFERENT, larger limit: 35 MB per filing/document and 50 MB per envelope. This is a documented inconsistency between the statewide general User Guide (25 MB) and one court's own supplementary guidelines — a builder should not assume a single universal number applies to every RI court. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.ri.gov/Legal-Resources/Documents/Supreme_Court_E-File_Guidelines.pdf)
    > Document Size - A single filing should not be greater than thirty-five (35) megabytes per filing and fifty (50) megabytes per envelope. See Section 7.10 for guidance on submitting filings that exceed the size limitation.
  - **acceptedFileFormat**: PDF or PDF/A only, and must be searchable. Fillable/interactive-form PDFs are explicitly NOT accepted — the system does not support them. Recommended workaround: fill the form, then print/flatten it to a standard (non-interactive) PDF before filing. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.ri.gov/Public-Resources/Documents/Electronic%20Filing/RI_Judiciary_User_Guide_for_Electronic_Filing.pdf)
    > Documents filed in the EFS shall be in a searchable portable document format (PDF or PDF-A). Fillable PDFs will not be accepted as the EFS does not support them. The best way to file a PDF form is to fill it out, save it, print it as a standard PDF, and then file the standard PDF.
  - **searchableTextOcrRequirement**: Genuinely contradictory documented requirement, quoted verbatim because it is what the official guide actually says: the guide requires documents to be in a "searchable" PDF format (Sec. 4.1), but a separate clause in the same section states no OCR data may be contained in or associated with the document (Sec. 4.3.6). Article X, Rule 4(a) independently confirms documents "shall be in a searchable format, as specified by the Rhode Island Judiciary User Guide." A builder should treat the literal 'no OCR data' clause with caution/flag it for legal review rather than silently OCR-stamping filings, since it directly conflicts with the searchable-format mandate in the same document. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.ri.gov/Public-Resources/Documents/Electronic%20Filing/RI_Judiciary_User_Guide_for_Electronic_Filing.pdf)
    > Optical Character Recognition (OCR) - No OCR data shall be contained in or associated with the document.
  - **filenameAndFieldCharacterLimits**: Not a filename-extension restriction per se, but the EFS enforces character-length caps on filing metadata fields that a builder should validate against: first/last name fields limited to 40 characters each, business name field to 80 characters, address line 1 and 2 fields to 60 characters each, and PDF file description names limited to 100 characters. Exceeding any of these causes a submission error. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.ri.gov/Public-Resources/Documents/Electronic%20Filing/RI_Judiciary_User_Guide_for_Electronic_Filing.pdf)
    > Character Length Restrictions – Filing submissions will error out when using the EFS if the filer exceeds certain character length restrictions on some of the fields. First and last name fields are each limited in length to forty (40) characters. The business name field is limited in length to eighty (80) characters. The address lines 1 and 2 fields are each limited in length to 60 characters. The description names of PDF files are limited in length to 100 characters.
  - **bookmarkOrTableOfContents**: No PDF-native bookmark or table-of-contents requirement was found anywhere in the statewide User Guide, Article X, or the Supreme Court's guidelines. The only related provision found is a soft, non-mandatory ('should', not 'shall') recommendation in the Superior Court's own supplementary guidelines specifically for attachments/exhibits: include a separate index document for navigation. This is court-specific (Superior Court only) and advisory, not a statewide hard requirement, and not a PDF-bookmark feature requirement — it describes a separate index document, not embedded PDF bookmarks. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.ri.gov/Legal-Resources/Documents/SuperiorEfilingGuidelines.pdf)
    > All subsequent pleadings, motions, and other papers, shall be submitted individually with related documents submitted as separate files within the same submission or filing (for example, a motion and memorandum or other supporting attachments or exhibits filed in support of a motion). The filing should also include an index to the attachments or exhibits submitted as a separate document, for ease in navigating the submission.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Attachment count limit — no explicit numeric cap on the number of attachments per filing/envelope was found in the statewide User Guide, Article X, or the Supreme Court's/Superior Court's supplementary guidelines. Those sources describe *which* documents must be filed as separate attachments vs. combined into one (e.g., 'categories of items such as bills, receipts, invoices, photographs... may be submitted in one attachment'), but never state a maximum count.

---

## South Carolina

- **E-filing system:** South Carolina Electronic Filing System (eFlex) (vendor: Tybera Development Group)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** South Carolina runs ONE statewide mandatory e-filing system, not a fragmented county-by-county model. It is operated by the South Carolina Judicial Branch on the "eFlex" platform built by Tybera Development Group (confirmed by the manual's "Copyright – Tybera Development Group, Inc." footer and by the live login portal at efile.sccourts.org, which self-identifies as "eFlex" / "South Carolina Statewide E-Filing" and shows a July 2026 maintenance notice, confirming it is the currently-live system, not a decommissioned one). Rollout was phased county-by-county starting with Clarendon County in Dec. 2015, but all participating counties now use this single common platform — it is a single statewide system with a phased-in rollout, not a fragmented multi-vendor model like California. Primary sources used: the official "Complete User Guide – Filer Interface" manual (dated 2015 but confirmed still current — its 8MB/40MB figures are echoed verbatim on the live FAQ page), the official FAQ page, and the numbered Attorney Reference Guides (ARG-01, ARG-03, ARG-04, ARG-16) published at sccourts.org/media/efiling/ARGs/. Federal court e-filing in SC (USDC District of South Carolina CM/ECF, at scd.uscourts.gov) is a SEPARATE, federal-only system and was NOT used as a source here — all findings above are for SC state courts only.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.sccourts.org/media/efiling/ARGs/ARG-03-Preparing_Your_Document_for_E-Filing.pdf)
  > PDF/A (or any PDF/A-adjacent term like "archival PDF") does not appear anywhere in the official E-Filing user manual, the FAQ page, or any of the 26 Attorney Reference Guides reviewed (ARG-01 through ARG-26, including the ones specifically about document preparation — ARG-03 — and large documents — ARG-16). The only PDF-related requirement is that the file be a "searchable Adobe Acrobat PDF" (i.e., a standard text-based PDF produced by Save-As-PDF from a word processor), as opposed to a scanned image-based PDF. No mention was found of PDF/A causing encryption conflicts, form-field issues, or annotation/redaction stripping — the topic is simply absent from the official technical materials, so this cannot be characterized as either a safe or unsafe default based on SC's own documentation.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.sccourts.org/media/efiling/ARGs/ARG-04-Redacting_Personal_Information.pdf)
  > No requirement, recommendation, or prohibition regarding document metadata (XMP/Info dictionary/author/revision history) appears anywhere in the official manual, FAQ, or any Attorney Reference Guide, including ARG-04 (Redacting Personal Information), which is the guide most likely to touch this topic. ARG-04 addresses only PII redaction of document CONTENT (SSN, DOB, financial account numbers, etc.) via a separate "Confidential Reference List" filed alongside the redacted document — it never discusses removing or preserving embedded file metadata. No indication was found either way that metadata-scrubbed files cause problems with the eFlex system.

**Constraints found:**
  - **efilingSystemName**: South Carolina Electronic Filing System (E-Filing), branded "eFlex", built by Tybera Development Group _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.sccourts.org/media/wvpdl2wq/efilingusermanual.pdf)
    > Copyright – Tybera Development Group, Inc. November 2015 ... Complete User Guide – Filer Interface
  - **statewideSystem**: true — single statewide mandatory system operated by the SC Judicial Branch, rolled out county-by-county starting with Clarendon County (Dec. 2015) but now a single platform used across all participating counties/circuits (all counties are now live) _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efile.sccourts.org/)
    > South Carolina Statewide E-Filing ... South Carolina Electronic Filing System (E-Filing System) ... managed by the South Carolina Judicial Branch
  - **maxFileSizePerDocument**: 8 MB per individual document _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.sccourts.org/media/wvpdl2wq/efilingusermanual.pdf)
    > Individual document size is limited to 8 MB and the size limitation for the entire submission is 40 MB.
  - **maxFileSizePerSubmission**: 40 MB per entire submission/envelope _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.sccourts.org/e-filing-for-attorneys/faqs/)
    > Single documents are restricted to 8 megabytes. A total filing cannot exceed 40 megabytes. Larger documents can be broken into smaller increments.
  - **acceptedFileFormat**: PDF required for all documents except Proposed Orders, which must be Microsoft Word (.doc/.docx); Consent Orders requiring a non-E-Filer signature may be submitted as scanned PDFs _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.sccourts.org/media/efiling/ARGs/ARG-01-E-Filing_General_Requirements.pdf)
    > Required File Type: Must be PDF unless it is a proposed order, which must be submitted in Microsoft Word format
  - **pdfVersionRequirement**: No specific PDF version (e.g. 1.4/1.7/2.0) is specified anywhere in the official manual, FAQ, or Attorney Reference Guides — only that the file be a standard Adobe PDF _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.sccourts.org/media/wvpdl2wq/efilingusermanual.pdf)
    > these documents ... need to be submitted as searchable Adobe® Acrobat® PDF files (Portable Document Format)
  - **pdfaRequirement**: silent — PDF/A is never mentioned in the official user manual, FAQ, or any of the 26 Attorney Reference Guides; the only format called for is a standard searchable Adobe PDF (or Word for proposed orders). No indication PDF/A is required, preferred, or causes problems — the topic simply does not appear in the official materials. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.sccourts.org/media/efiling/ARGs/ARG-03-Preparing_Your_Document_for_E-Filing.pdf)
    > Searchable PDF documents have been converted in a word processing program to a PDF format. These are called text-based PDFs. ... each submitted document cannot be larger than 8 megabytes.
  - **searchableTextOcrRequirement**: Recommended/expected where feasible, not strictly mandatory for every document — text-based/searchable PDF is the norm for filer-generated pleadings, but scanned image-based PDFs are explicitly permitted for documents that can't be converted (plats, maps, third-party signatures) and for those the court does not require OCR _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.sccourts.org/e-filing-for-attorneys/faqs/)
    > Do the .pdfs submitted need to be OCR searchable? ... The Court recognizes that certain documents cannot be converted and will always need to be scanned (e.g.--plats, maps). ... However, whenever possible, documents should be converted to .pdf and be OCR searchable before submission.
  - **filenameRestrictions**: No character-set or length limit is specified anywhere in the official materials; guidance is only substantive — name multi-part files so their sequence/relationship is clear (e.g. 'Summons and Complaint-Part 2') _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.sccourts.org/media/efiling/ARGs/ARG-16-Filing_Large_Documents_and_Additional_Parts.pdf)
    > If you have a document larger than 8 MB, it will need to be divided into multiple parts. When you do this, it is helpful to save the individual parts with consistent file names such as "Summons and Complaint-Part 2", "Summons and Complaint-Part 3", etc.
  - **metadataPolicy**: silent — no metadata requirement, recommendation, or removal instruction appears anywhere in the official manual, FAQ, or the 26 Attorney Reference Guides (including the dedicated redaction guide, ARG-04, which addresses PII redaction via a separate Confidential Reference List but never discusses embedded document metadata) _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.sccourts.org/media/efiling/ARGs/ARG-04-Redacting_Personal_Information.pdf)
    > Redaction is the process of editing or removing Personal Identifying Information (PII). ... Redaction is the responsibility of the filer. The court is not responsible for reviewing submissions to ensure that personal information has been redacted.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Bookmark / table-of-contents requirement — no mention found in the official user manual, FAQ, or any of the 26 Attorney Reference Guides; South Carolina's eFlex system does not appear to require or discuss bookmarks/TOC at all, but a further search of the SCEF Rules (Rule 1-Rule 11 series, e.g. rule text on sccourts.org/resources/judicial-community/court-rules/e-filing/) was not exhaustively completed and could theoretically contain a technical-annex reference not surfaced by search., Attachment/document count limit per submission — the system caps submissions by total file SIZE (40 MB) rather than by a stated maximum NUMBER of attached documents/parts; no explicit numeric cap on attachment count was found in any official source, so this is left as a gap rather than asserting 'no limit' as a verified fact., PDF version number (e.g., whether PDF 1.4 through 2.0/PDF 2.0 ISO 32000-2 are all accepted, or whether newer PDF 2.0 files are rejected) — not addressed in any official SC source found; only that the file must open as a standard Adobe-readable PDF.

---

## South Dakota

- **E-filing system:** eFile &amp; Serve (Odyssey File &amp; Serve), accessed via the "eFileSD" login at southdakota.tylerhost.cloud/OfsWeb (vendor: Tyler Technologies (Odyssey File &amp; Serve product; notification emails originate from no-reply@efilingmail.tylertech.cloud, help content hosted at content.tylerhost.net))
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** South Dakota has ONE mandatory statewide e-filing system, not a county-by-county model. It is operated by the South Dakota Unified Judicial System (UJS) — the state's centralized court administration — on the Tyler Technologies Odyssey File & Serve platform, branded "eFile & Serve." All circuits/counties run on the same platform (confirmed via the UJS Court Finder → circuit → county structure feeding into the same eFileSD login and the same Tyler-hosted help content). Registration is by firm, not by county, and self-represented litigants are categorically barred from using it ("No. Self-represented litigants are not eligible to use the e-filing system." — EFSP_FAQ.pdf).

IMPORTANT DATA-QUALITY FLAG: South Dakota's own three official e-filing documents give THREE DIFFERENT sets of numbers for file-size limits (see constraints below) — the FAQ says 5 MB/doc + 25 MB/envelope "(recommended)"; the dedicated eFiling Guidelines document says a hard "Maximum 25 MB per document" + "Maximum 35 MB per envelope"; and the Filer/Firm Administrator manual states both "File size must not exceed 25 MB per document" in one section AND lists "Document exceeds size limits (5 MB per document; 25 MB per envelope)" as an actual Technical rejection reason in another section of the SAME document. This is not a research gap — it's a genuine inconsistency baked into the state's own primary sources. For a tool like RaioPDF, the safest engineering default is to target the smallest number found (5 MB/document, 25 MB/envelope) since that is the figure the system's own documented rejection-reasons table associates with an actual technical rejection.

Other notable technical constraints found, outside the 8 requested fields but relevant to a PDF tool: documents must be black-and-white only (any color, including blue-ink signatures, causes rejection — a photographed/scanned color signature is a real failure mode); external hyperlinks are prohibited and may cause rejection (internal links are fine); embedded file attachments inside a PDF cause a "format error"; password protection / security restrictions must be removed before filing; all pages within one document must share a single orientation (portrait or landscape, not mixed); and scan resolution should exceed 200 DPI.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://media.sd.gov/ujs/fileserve/file_Serve_Filer_Instructions.pdf)
  > No mention of PDF/A (as a format standard) appears anywhere in any of the three official SD UJS e-filing documents reviewed in full: the eFile & Serve FAQ, the 27-page "Filers and Firm Administrators" manual, or the dedicated "eFiling Guidelines" document. The "Document Format" section of the Filer manual (p.8) is the most detailed treatment of file format and only says: "Documents must be in PDF format," "Searchable PDFs are preferred," and gives the file-size limit — no PDF/A requirement, preference, or prohibition is stated. Two adjacent, potentially-relevant data points (not a PDF/A statement themselves, but worth flagging for downstream risk analysis): (1) the system requires all security/password restrictions to be removed before filing ("Avoid password protection" / "Remove all restrictions before filing" — a PDF/A-1 profile also disallows encryption, so there's no apparent conflict there); and (2) the FAQ's rejection-cause list includes "unsupported fonts... Some fonts prevent document processing. Use standard fonts," which is a generic guidance line, not a documented PDF/A-conversion problem — I found no explicit statement tying PDF/A conversion to font, form-field, or annotation/redaction stripping issues in any official SD source.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://media.sd.gov/ujs/fileserve/file_Serve_Filer_Instructions.pdf)
  > No mention of document metadata — no requirement to include specific metadata, no recommendation or requirement to scrub/remove metadata before filing, and no indication that metadata-scrubbed files cause processing problems — appears anywhere in the eFile & Serve FAQ, the 27-page Filer/Firm Administrator manual, or the eFiling Guidelines document. The closest adjacent topics actually covered are redaction (a content-removal, not metadata-removal, requirement — "Filers must submit both a non-redacted version and a redacted version of the document") and a Confidential Information Form/Financial Documents Form regime under SDCL 15-15A-9, both of which are substantive redaction/confidentiality rules rather than PDF metadata (XMP/Info-dictionary) policy.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size per document — per FAQ (labeled "recommended")**: 5 MB per document _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://media.sd.gov/ujs/fileserve/EFSP_FAQ.pdf)
    > What is the maximum file size? • 5 MB per document (recommended) • 25 MG per envelope (recommended)
  - **Maximum file size per envelope — per FAQ (labeled "recommended"; document itself has a typo, "MG")**: 25 MB per envelope _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://media.sd.gov/ujs/fileserve/EFSP_FAQ.pdf)
    > What is the maximum file size? • 5 MB per document (recommended) • 25 MG per envelope (recommended)
  - **Maximum file size — actual documented Technical rejection trigger (conflicts with the dedicated eFiling Guidelines doc, see next two entries)**: 5 MB per document; 25 MB per envelope _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://media.sd.gov/ujs/fileserve/file_Serve_Filer_Instructions.pdf)
    > Technical • ... • Document exceeds size limits (5 MB per document; 25 MB per envelope)
  - **Maximum file size per document — per the same Filer/Firm manual's own Document Format section (conflicts with that manual's own rejection-reasons table above)**: 25 MB per document _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://media.sd.gov/ujs/fileserve/file_Serve_Filer_Instructions.pdf)
    > File size must not exceed 25 MB per document. Refer to eFiling Guidelines for additional information.
  - **Maximum file size — per the dedicated eFiling Guidelines document (numbered guideline #10; hard "Maximum", not labeled recommended; also gives a large-document workaround)**: Maximum 25 MB per document; Maximum 35 MB per envelope. If a document exceeds 25 MB, split it into labeled volumes (Volume 1, Volume 2, etc.) _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://media.sd.gov/ujs/fileserve/e_filing_guidelines.pdf)
    > 10. File Size Limits • Maximum 25 MB per document • Maximum 35 MB per envelope. If a document exceeds 25 MB: • Divide into sections labeled: • Volume 1 • Volume 2, etc.
  - **Accepted file format**: PDF only, one document per PDF file. No specific PDF version number (e.g., 1.4/1.7/2.0) is specified anywhere in official documentation — only the generic requirement that the file be "PDF format." _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://media.sd.gov/ujs/fileserve/file_Serve_Filer_Instructions.pdf)
    > Documents must be in PDF format. Submit a separate PDF for each document.
  - **Searchable text / OCR requirement**: Preferred, not required. Searchable text is explicitly called out as a preference, and the manual notes scanned PDFs are inherently not searchable (implying scanned/non-OCR'd filings are accepted, just not preferred). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://media.sd.gov/ujs/fileserve/file_Serve_Filer_Instructions.pdf)
    > Searchable PDFs are preferred: Scanned PDFs are not searchable. Documents converted from Word or WordPerfect are searchable.
  - **Bookmark / table-of-contents requirement inside filed PDF documents**: None found. Note for disambiguation: the only "Bookmarks" feature documented in the official Filer/Firm manual is an unrelated case-tracking convenience feature in the filer's own dashboard (saving a case number/location/description for quick access), not a requirement to embed PDF navigation bookmarks or a table of contents inside a filed document. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://media.sd.gov/ujs/fileserve/file_Serve_Filer_Instructions.pdf)
    > The bookmarks page displays a list of case numbers, locations, and descriptions for cases you have bookmarked. This information is visible only to you and your firm.
  - **Attachment / document count limit per envelope**: No explicit numeric cap on the number of documents/attachments per envelope was found in any official source. Filers are told to submit each docketable document as a separate PDF and exhibits as separate attachments, and may add as many filings to one envelope as needed via "Add More" — the only practical ceiling documented is the aggregate envelope file-size limit (see file-size entries above). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://media.sd.gov/ujs/fileserve/EFSP_FAQ.pdf)
    > Can I file multiple pleadings in one transaction? Yes. Multiple filings can be submitted in one envelope. ... Each document should be a separate PDF. Documents docketed separately must not be combined. Exhibits should be separate attachments.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Filename character/length restrictions on the uploaded PDF document file itself — no official SD UJS e-filing document (FAQ, 27-page Filer/Firm Administrator manual, or eFiling Guidelines) addresses filename length or allowed characters for the document file being uploaded. (Note: the manual does document unrelated field-length limits — e.g., party name max 40/80 characters, payment-account name max 30 characters — but nothing about the uploaded file's filename.), Specific accepted PDF version/subversion (e.g., PDF 1.4, 1.7, 2.0) — official sources uniformly require just "PDF format" with no version number ever specified.

---

## Tennessee

- **E-filing system:** Fragmented — no single statewide e-filing system for trial courts. Tennessee's own Administrative Office of the Courts (AOC) states plainly: \"there is no statewide Electronic Filing Service Provider (EFSP) or Electronic File Manager (EFM).\" Each trial court (chancery, circuit, criminal, general sessions, probate, juvenile) independently adopts e-filing, and as of the AOC's own assessment only roughly 40 of 300+ trial courts e-file at all. The one exception is the appellate tier: the Supreme Court, Court of Appeals, and Court of Criminal Appeals share a single statewide portal, ImageSoft's TrueFiling (tf3.truefiling.com), governed procedurally by Supreme Court Rule 46. A new unified statewide case-management-and-e-filing system was awarded via RFP (Notice of Award issued December 16, 2025) but was not yet live as of this research (per the AOC's February 2026 status report to the legislature, which describes today's courts as running on "siloed court/case management systems"). (vendor: Multiple, chosen per-court from four AOC pre-approved vendors: Tybera (eFlex) — used by most Tennessee trial courts that e-file (~11+ counties per the AOC's own assessment); Tyler Technologies (Odyssey File & Serve, publicly branded "eFileTN") — used by at least Davidson County Chancery Court; ImageSoft (TrueFiling) — the sole vendor for the unified statewide appellate portal, and also pre-approved for trial courts; Intresys (TurboCourt) — pre-approved but with unconfirmed/limited adoption found. A single new statewide vendor is in procurement but not yet live.)
- **Statewide system:** no -- fragmented/county-by-county
- **Notes:** Treat Tennessee as two separate answers, not one. (1) Appellate courts: one statewide portal (TrueFiling), but its technical constraints are expressed only through Supreme Court Rule 46 (a procedural rule, e.g. "text searchable, if possible" and bookmarks "encouraged") — no standalone AOC/ImageSoft technical-spec page for the Tennessee deployment was found, so per this research's scope (rules of court excluded) those appellate specifics are not reported as constraints, only flagged in gaps. (2) Trial courts: genuinely fragmented like California's county-by-county EFSP model — each court/county picks among four pre-approved vendors, and the two vendors with actual documentation found (Tyler Odyssey/eFileTN and Tybera eFlex) have materially different numeric limits (25MB/35MB vs. 10MB/30MB), which itself is evidence of the fragmentation: there is no single "Tennessee" file-size answer. A caution from this research: one Tybera document found at a Tennessee-titled URL path (FilerInterface.pdf) turned out, on inspection, to be Tybera's generic Arkansas Judiciary manual, not Tennessee-specific — it was discarded rather than cited, and is a reminder that vendor-hosted "state" documentation folders aren't reliably state-specific.
- **PDF/A stance:** prohibited -- [source](https://odysseyfileandservecloud.zendesk.com/hc/en-us/articles/29296932892045-REJECTED-Invalid-File-Extension-When-Uploading-Document)
  > On the Tyler Technologies Odyssey File & Serve platform (the "eFileTN" branded system used by at least Davidson County Chancery Court), PDF/A is not merely discouraged — uploading a PDF/A (or PDF/X) file triggers the same hard rejection as uploading a non-PDF file: "This error is produced whenever a document that is not a PDF - or is a PDF variant that is not accepted by the efiling system (like a PDF/A or PDF/X) - is uploaded to the website." No PDF/A guidance was found at all for Tybera eFlex (the more widely-used TN vendor) or for the appellate TrueFiling system — those are gaps, not confirmed-safe defaults.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://odysseyfileandserve.zendesk.com/hc/en-us/articles/40875795845517-PDF-Requirements)
  > Neither the Tyler Odyssey File & Serve / eFileTN "PDF Requirements" checklist (which is otherwise long and prescriptive — fonts, hyperlinks, filenames, security, page size, creation software) nor the Tybera eFlex Tennessee Filer's Guide mentions metadata anywhere — no instruction to include it, no instruction to remove it, and no warning that a metadata-scrubbed file causes problems. Given how detailed both documents are about everything else a filer could get wrong, the silence reads as a genuine absence of any metadata policy rather than a gap in this research, though it should still be treated as unconfirmed for RaioPDF's purposes, especially for the appellate TrueFiling system and the Intresys TurboCourt vendor, for which no technical documentation was found at all.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Max file size — Tyler Technologies Odyssey File & Serve / "eFileTN" (e.g. Davidson County Chancery Court)**: 25 MB per document; 35 MB per total envelope/submission _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://odysseyfileandserve.zendesk.com/hc/en-us/articles/360047164312-Max-PDF-File-Size-by-State)
    > Tennessee | 25 MB | 35 MB (table columns are "Per Document" and "Per Envelope"; page header notes "Max File Size is subject to change.")
  - **Max file size — Tybera eFlex (the vendor the AOC's own assessment says most e-filing TN courts actually use)**: 10 MB per document; 30 MB per total submission/envelope _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://go.tybera.net/tncis/eflex-resources/FilerQuickGuide.pdf)
    > NOTE: Proposed Orders must be in Word format with a document file extension of doc or docx in order to be editable for the judge/magistrate. All other document types must be PDFs. Each document uploaded to the system must be 10 megabytes or less. Multiple documents can be included in a single submission. The size limitation for an entire submission is 30 megabytes.
  - **Accepted file format — Tyler Odyssey File & Serve / eFileTN**: PDF only, no stated PDF version number (e.g. 1.4/1.7). Must be "created/produced by Adobe Acrobat or Microsoft Word"; Corel WordPerfect PDF Producer explicitly discouraged. No fillable form fields, no unsupported fonts (ZapfDingbats/Wingdings/Symbol), no active hyperlinks, not password protected, no security restrictions/limited permissions. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://odysseyfileandserve.zendesk.com/hc/en-us/articles/40875795845517-PDF-Requirements)
    > Your PDF should be created/produced by Adobe Acrobat or Microsoft Word. (We do not recommend using Corel Word Perfect PDF Producer to create your documents.) ... Documents with security restrictions or limited permissions may cause errors when uploading them to our system.
  - **Accepted file format — Tybera eFlex (Tennessee)**: All document types must be PDF, with one named exception: Proposed Orders must be filed in native Word format (.doc/.docx) so the judge/magistrate can edit them directly. No PDF version specified. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://go.tybera.net/tncis/eflex-resources/FilerQuickGuide.pdf)
    > Proposed Orders must be in Word format with a document file extension of doc or docx in order to be editable for the judge/magistrate. All other document types must be PDFs.
  - **PDF/A handling — Tyler Odyssey File & Serve / eFileTN (detail behind the pdfaStance field below)**: PDF/A (and PDF/X) are not a discouraged-but-tolerated format — the system hard-rejects them at upload as an "invalid file extension" error, identical to rejecting a non-PDF file. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://odysseyfileandservecloud.zendesk.com/hc/en-us/articles/29296932892045-REJECTED-Invalid-File-Extension-When-Uploading-Document)
    > This error is produced whenever a document that is not a PDF - or is a PDF variant that is not accepted by the efiling system (like a PDF/A or PDF/X) - is uploaded to the website.
  - **Searchable text / OCR requirement — Tyler Odyssey File & Serve / eFileTN**: Not stated as a mandatory upload requirement. The system's own PDF Requirements checklist is otherwise explicit and prescriptive (fonts, hyperlinks, security, filename, page size) but never lists searchability as a requirement; OCR only shows up in separate troubleshooting/how-to guidance aimed at filers whose scanned documents caused problems. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://odysseyfileandserve.zendesk.com/hc/en-us/articles/360059030891-How-To-Create-a-Text-Searchable-PDF-Document)
    > If using a scanner, check to see if your scanner is equipped with the feature OCR. OCR stands for Optical Character Recognition. This feature will scan your document as text searchable.
  - **Filename character/length restrictions — Tyler Odyssey File & Serve / eFileTN**: Under 24 characters; letters and numbers only; no punctuation or special characters (comma, period, apostrophe, exclamation point, @, #, $, %, ^, &, *, hyphen) except the single period immediately before the ".pdf" extension. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://odysseyfileandserve.zendesk.com/hc/en-us/articles/40875795845517-PDF-Requirements)
    > Filename requirements: under 24 characters, only letters and numbers (No punctuation marks or special characters like ,.'!@#$%^&*- aside from the period before the "pdf" extension.)
  - **Page size / resolution — Tyler Odyssey File & Serve / eFileTN**: Pages must be exactly 8.5" x 11" portrait orientation; 300 dpi resolution for scanned content. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://odysseyfileandserve.zendesk.com/hc/en-us/articles/40875795845517-PDF-Requirements)
    > Page size: 8.5" x 11" in Portrait orientation. Page resolution: 300 dpi

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Bookmark or table-of-contents requirement: not addressed in any trial-court e-filing vendor's published technical documentation found (Tyler Odyssey/eFileTN or Tybera eFlex). Supreme Court Rule 46 says bookmarks are "encouraged" for appellate e-filings, but that is procedural-rule language, not a portal/technical-spec page, so it is excluded here per the research scope., Attachment count limits: no explicit numeric cap on number of attachments/documents per envelope was found for either Tyler Odyssey File & Serve/eFileTN or Tybera eFlex — both vendors' documentation frames limits only in terms of total file size (35MB/30MB envelope caps), not attachment count., Tybera eFlex (the vendor the AOC's own current-state assessment identifies as used by most Tennessee e-filing courts) technical stance on PDF/A, searchable-text/OCR, filename restrictions, and metadata — not documented in the public Tennessee-specific Filer's Guide found (go.tybera.net/tncis/eflex-resources/FilerQuickGuide.pdf); that guide covers file-size and format (PDF vs. Word) only, and no separate Tennessee-specific Tybera technical-spec/FAQ page was located., ImageSoft TrueFiling (the single statewide system for the Supreme Court, Court of Appeals, and Court of Criminal Appeals): no standalone technical/portal specification page (file size, PDF/A stance, filename rules, OCR, attachment limits, metadata) could be found published by the AOC or by ImageSoft specifically for the Tennessee appellate deployment (tf3.truefiling.com). The only appellate-specific language located lives in Supreme Court Rule 46, a procedural rule, which is out of scope per the research instructions., Intresys TurboCourt: one of the four AOC pre-approved e-filing vendors, but no technical specification, user manual, or FAQ page was found at all within the bounded search effort, and its actual county-level adoption in Tennessee could not be confirmed., Full county-by-county map of which Tennessee trial courts run which vendor (Tybera eFlex vs. Tyler Odyssey/eFileTN vs. TrueFiling vs. TurboCourt): only Davidson County Chancery Court was confirmed as an Odyssey/eFileTN deployment; the AOC assessment cites ~11 counties on Tybera and ~40 of 300+ courts e-filing at all, but a complete current roster was not located.

---

## Texas

- **E-filing system:** eFileTexas.gov (public no-cost filer interface is branded eFile.TXCourts.gov); backend platform is the state's "TexFile" Electronic Filing Manager (vendor: Tyler Technologies — Tyler Odyssey File &amp; Serve / Tyler File &amp; Serve platform (vendor since the 2013 statewide rollout; re-awarded the contract in a 2020 OCA re-procurement))
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Texas has ONE mandatory statewide e-filing system, not a county-by-county model. E-filing has been mandatory for attorneys filing civil, family, probate, and criminal matters in the Supreme Court, Court of Criminal Appeals, Courts of Appeals, and all district/county courts since a phased 2013–2016 rollout completed under a Texas Supreme Court order; some JP courts also participate. The Texas Office of Court Administration (OCA) holds the contract (with Tyler Technologies as the vendor, re-procured 2020) and filers may go through the free portal (eFile.TXCourts.gov) or any OCA-certified third-party Electronic Filing Service Provider (EFSP) — File&ServeXpress, OneLegal, Green Filing, iDocket, Court File America, etc. — all of which route into the same backend. The binding technical rules for the SYSTEM itself (as opposed to Rules of Civil/Appellate Procedure) are published by the Judicial Committee on Information Technology (JCIT), a body created by the Texas Legislature under Tex. Gov't Code ch. 77, in a document titled "Technology Standards" — currently Version 7.0 (November 2021), hosted directly on efiletexas.gov. That document is the strongest available primary source for portal-level technical constraints and is what this research relies on for items 2–6. It notably does NOT state a numeric file-size cap or a metadata policy, and does not give a numeric attachment-count ceiling — see gaps. Older county-clerk FAQ handouts citing "5MB/25MB" size guidance predate the JCIT v7.0 standard and the 2020 platform re-procurement, so were not treated as reliable current constraints.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.efiletexas.gov/documents/Technology-Standards.pdf)
  > The term "PDF/A" never appears in the JCIT Technology Standards (the authoritative technical spec). But its definition of "PDF" cites ISO 19005-1:2005 — the actual ISO number for PDF/A-1 — suggesting the drafters had PDF/A in mind, while a separate, explicit clause in the same section bans embedded fonts ("Documents may not contain embedded fonts"), which directly conflicts with true PDF/A conformance (PDF/A mandates embedding every font used, by definition). This looks like an unresolved drafting inconsistency in the state's own standard rather than a deliberate PDF/A policy either way. Practical implication for RaioPDF: a standard "Save as PDF/A" conversion (which will embed fonts to satisfy the PDF/A spec) risks tripping Texas's own explicit no-embedded-fonts rule, so PDF/A conversion is NOT demonstrably a safe default for Texas e-filing and should not be presented as compliant without flagging this tension.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** unverified
  > No official eFileTexas.gov / txcourts.gov / JCIT source was found that addresses PDF metadata (document properties, author, revision history, XMP data) one way or the other. The only metadata-adjacent, verifiably-sourced requirement in the JCIT Technology Standards concerns redacting sensitive information from the visible content of a document (SSNs, driver's license numbers, financial account numbers, dates of birth, and identifying information of minors, per TRCP 21c) before filing — a content-redaction rule, not a file-metadata-scrubbing rule. Some AI-generated web search summaries asserted a "check your metadata before filing" instruction, but this could not be confirmed against any primary page actually fetched and read, so it is excluded rather than reported as a constraint.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Accepted PDF version / file format requirements**: Every e-filed document must be a single, text-searchable PDF (PDF 1.4 per the standard's definition), one document per PDF file — no 'package' PDFs and no PDF embedded inside another PDF. Page size must be 8.5x11 in., content correctly rotated, and only fonts specified in the PDF spec may be used (no embedded fonts). The file may not contain password protection, encryption, or any other security/feature restriction, and may not contain embedded multimedia (audio/video) or programming/scripts. Scanned source documents must be scanned at 300 DPI before conversion. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.efiletexas.gov/documents/Technology-Standards.pdf)
    > An e-filed document must be in text-searchable PDF, using fonts specified in the PDF specification, on 8.5x11 page size, with the content appropriately rotated... An e-filed document may not contain any security or feature restrictions including password protection or encryption and may not contain embedded multi-media video, audio, or programming... Documents may not contain package PDF's. PDF's should not be embedded inside of another PDF. Documents may not contain embedded fonts. Each document must be a single PDF.
  - **PDF/A requirement**: The statewide technical standard never uses the term 'PDF/A' and does not affirmatively require or forbid it by name. However, its own definition of the required 'PDF' format cites ISO 19005-1:2005 — which is literally the ISO standard defining PDF/A-1 — while a separate clause in the same section flatly bans embedded fonts ('Documents may not contain embedded fonts'). True PDF/A conformance requires every font to be embedded, so a genuinely ISO-19005-1-conformant PDF/A file would violate this standard's own font rule. This is an internal contradiction in the state's own spec, not a considered policy choice, so it should not be read as an endorsement of PDF/A conversion. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.efiletexas.gov/documents/Technology-Standards.pdf)
    > PDF – Portable Document Format – for the purpose of these standards this is PDF 1.4 (ISO 19005-1:2005 – Revised as ISP/NP 19005-1). This standard specifies how to use PDF for long-term preservation of electronic documents... [Section 3.1.E] Documents may not contain embedded fonts.
  - **Searchable-text / OCR requirement**: Text-searchable PDF is mandatory for every e-filed document (not merely preferred). For documents that originate as paper and are scanned, the scan must be at 300 DPI resolution before filing, and the standard states scanned documents should 'preferably' be made searchable using OCR — i.e., OCR is the expected mechanism for meeting the searchable-text mandate on scanned material. A filing that is not text-searchable is a stated ground for rejection. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.efiletexas.gov/documents/Technology-Standards.pdf)
    > An e-filed document must be in text-searchable PDF... Prior to being filed electronically, a scanned document must have a resolution of 300 DPI. Preferably, scanned documents should be made searchable using OCR technology.
  - **Filename character/length restrictions**: Filenames for e-filed documents must contain only alphanumeric characters from the Latin1_General character set — no special characters — and must be restricted to 50 characters or fewer. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.efiletexas.gov/documents/Technology-Standards.pdf)
    > Any e-filed document filename should contain only alphanumeric characters that are part of the Latin1_General character set. No special characters are allowed and the length of the filename should be restricted to 50 characters.
  - **Bookmark or table-of-contents requirements**: Bookmarks are not required for ordinary trial-court filings, and each document must generally be filed as its own single PDF rather than combined. The one carve-out is at the appellate level: an appellate court may require multiple separate PDF documents to be combined into one PDF, in which case bookmarks must be used to mark where each original document begins. Even then, the substantive content/legal effect of the filing may not depend on the bookmarks functioning correctly. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.efiletexas.gov/documents/Technology-Standards.pdf)
    > An appellate court may require that multiple PDF documents be combined into a single PDF document and bookmarks used to separate content appropriately. The content of the document should not depend on bookmarks.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Maximum file size (per document and per envelope/submission) — the current official JCIT Technology Standards and efiletexas.gov publish no numeric byte/MB cap. Older (circa 2016, pre-2020 Tyler-Odyssey-re-procurement) county-court FAQ handouts (e.g., Fayette County Court) attribute a '5MB per document / 25MB per envelope' recommendation to eFileTexas.gov, and separate secondary/aggregator pages describe a '25MB per document / 35MB per envelope' figure, but neither number could be corroborated on efiletexas.gov, efile.txcourts.gov, or txcourts.gov directly, and the two figures conflict — so no figure is reported as a verified constraint., Attachment count limit per envelope — no numeric cap is stated in the JCIT Technology Standards. The standard's own filing-configuration table marks 'Exhibits/Supporting Documents' as allowing 'Multiples' with no stated maximum, but this is not the same as a confirmed upper bound., Metadata policy (any requirement/recommendation to include or strip document metadata before filing) — no explicit statement was found in the JCIT Technology Standards, the efiletexas.gov FAQ, the txcourts.gov JCIT e-filing page, or the TYLA e-filing guide. The Technology Standards only address redaction of sensitive data *within the visible document content* (SSN, DOB, financial account numbers, minors' identifying information under TRCP 21c), which is a distinct requirement from PDF metadata/document-properties scrubbing.

---

## Utah (state courts)

- **E-filing system:** No single branded portal name for the whole system. District/justice trial courts run on an unbranded Administrative Office of the Courts (AOC) "Electronic Filing Manager" integrated with the CORIS case management system; attorneys almost always reach it through the Tybera-built "eFlex" front end (distributed via the Utah State Bar at efiling.utahbar.org), though two other AOC-certified vendor front ends exist. The appellate courts (Supreme Court + Court of Appeals) run a SEPARATE second system called "Utah Appellate E-filing" at appellatefiling.utcourts.gov, requiring its own account. (vendor: Tybera Technology Solutions (a.k.a. Tybera Development Group) built and operates the AOC's core "electronic filing manager" backend under contract, and separately offers its own certified front-end product ("eFlex"). Two other AOC-certified, independently-operated Electronic Filing Service Providers (EFSPs) compete to file into the same backend: GreenFiling, LLC and Judicialink, LLC. Tybera is also the sole listed e-filing service provider for the separate appellate system.)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Utah is NOT fragmented county-by-county like California. There is one mandatory statewide backend for district and justice (trial) courts — the AOC's central Electronic Filing Manager tied to CORIS — so the technical caps and format rules below are uniform statewide. The wrinkle is that, like Texas, Utah does not let attorneys file directly against a bare government portal: they must go through one of a small slate of AOC-certified third-party "Electronic Filing Service Providers" (EFSPs) — Tybera's own "eFlex," GreenFiling, or Judicialink — all of which submit into the identical single back-end system, so the substantive rules don't vary by which EFSP a firm picks. Separately, Utah's appellate courts (Court of Appeals/Supreme Court) run their own distinct e-filing system ("Utah Appellate E-filing"), with its own account/login and its own FAQ, also run by Tybera — an attorney with a district-court eFiling login must register again for appellate e-filing. Both systems require searchable PDF for signed documents and require RTF (never PDF) for documents still needing a judge/clerk signature (proposed orders, judgments, etc.), which will then be system-converted to PDF once signed. Two of the primary sources used here (the "Electronic Filing Guide," Dec 2013/updated 8-2017, and the "eFiling Standards," Dec 7 2015) are old, but they are still the live, currently-linked technical documents on utcourts.gov, and every substantive claim in them that overlaps with the current district FAQ (updated April 2026) and appellate FAQ (Sept 2024) is independently corroborated, so they appear to still reflect the live system despite their age.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.utcourts.gov/content/dam/howto/filing/efiling/district/docs/eFiling_FAQ-Attorneys.pdf)
  > PDF/A (or "archival PDF," ISO 19005) is never mentioned in any of the five official Utah Courts documents reviewed in depth (district FAQ updated April 2026; appellate FAQ Sept 2024; Electronic Filing Guide 2013/2017; district eFiling Standards Dec 2015; "Common Mistakes" attorney training doc). Every one of them specifies only generic "searchable PDF" for signed documents (and RTF, never PDF, for documents awaiting a judge/clerk signature). No PDF/A requirement, preference, or prohibition is stated anywhere, and none of the documents raise PDF/A-adjacent problems (encryption, form-field conversion, redaction stripping) in connection with PDF/A specifically — though note the Standards doc does independently ban embedded form fields and embedded images in the RTF (not PDF) track, for unrelated formatting reasons.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.utcourts.gov/content/dam/howto/filing/efiling/district/docs/Electronic_Filing_Guide.pdf)
  > No official document instructs filers to scrub document metadata (Author/Company/XMP properties, etc.) before filing, and none states that metadata-scrubbed files cause problems. The one arguably-adjacent line is in the 2013/2017 Electronic Filing Guide, under a "Hyperlinks" heading: "No embedded data is allowed in documents electronically filed with the Court" — but in context this sits right after rules banning hyperlinks other than internal/cited-authority links, so it reads as a ban on embedded objects/hyperlinks/OLE content, not a document-metadata (file-properties) scrubbing mandate. Separately and repeatedly, all five documents make clear that redacting personal identifiers (SSNs, DOBs, account numbers) from the VISIBLE BODY TEXT of a document is solely the filer's responsibility and that clerks do not screen for it — that is a content-redaction duty, not a metadata policy, and should not be conflated with metadata scrubbing.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size per document — district/justice trial courts**: 7 MB per document. Documents over 7 MB must be split into sections and re-filed with 'Part X of Y' in the Additional Docket Text field. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.utcourts.gov/content/dam/howto/filing/efiling/district/docs/eFiling_FAQ-Attorneys.pdf)
    > The court efiling system will accept documents with an electronic file size of up to 7 MB. Larger documents must be filed in sections. Be sure you do not scan your documents in color and avoid using colored paper to reduce the size of your documents.
  - **Maximum size for the entire filing/submission (envelope) — district/justice trial courts**: 10 MB total across all documents in one eFiling submission, on top of the 7 MB per-document cap. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.utcourts.gov/content/dam/howto/filing/efiling/district/docs/Attorney_eFiling_Training_Common_Mistakes.pdf)
    > All documents must be in black and white. Color documents do not meet the eFiling specifications. Size limitation under 7MB or 10MB for the entire filing. Scanning your documents in color and using colored paper will increase the size of your documents
  - **Maximum file size per document — appellate courts (separate system)**: 7 MB per document (same numeric cap as trial courts, but a distinct system/account). Larger PDFs must be split into multiple ≤7MB files. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.utcourts.gov/content/dam/howto/filing/efiling/appellate/Appellate-eFiling-FAQ-for-Attorneys.pdf)
    > All documents bearing the signature of the filer must be submitted in searchable PDF format of no more than 7 megabytes. Large PDF documents must be divided into multiple files of no more than 7 megabytes each.
  - **Accepted file format / PDF version requirements**: Any document bearing the filer's signature (motions, pleadings, briefs, memoranda, etc.) must be a searchable PDF; no specific PDF version number or PDF/A designation is specified anywhere — 'searchable PDF' is the entire format spec. Draft documents still needing a judge or clerk signature (proposed orders, judgments, jury instructions, findings of fact, etc.) must instead be filed in Rich Text Format (RTF) — never PDF — formatted per detailed RTF rules (Times/Times New Roman/Arial fonts only, no Wingdings/§/© symbols, no embedded images, no form fields, 1.5in top margin, no page numbers, tables instead of tabs). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.utcourts.gov/content/dam/howto/filing/efiling/district/docs/eFiling_FAQ-Attorneys.pdf)
    > All documents bearing the signature of the filer must be submitted in searchable PDF format. Draft documents, such as orders, to be signed by the court must be submitted in rich text format (RTF). / Documents not requiring a court signature must be saved in Portable Document Format (PDF) before electronic filing... Documents requiring a court signature must be formatted according to Standards and saved in Rich Text Format (RTF) before electronic filing.
  - **Color document restriction**: District/justice trial courts flatly reject color documents ('do not meet the eFiling specifications'); the separate appellate system is more permissive — color is allowed but discouraged, so long as the file still meets the 7 MB size cap. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.utcourts.gov/content/dam/howto/filing/efiling/district/docs/eFiling_FAQ-Attorneys.pdf)
    > Can I submit color documents? No. Color documents do not meet the efiling specifications. Please submit color documents in black and white. [district FAQ] / Can I submit color documents? While not recommended, a document can contain color if it meets the file size requirements. NOTE: The colored cover of a brief is only necessary for the hard copies. [appellate FAQ]
  - **Searchable-text / OCR requirement**: Required for all signed documents in both the trial-court and appellate systems. A raw scan saved straight to PDF (image-only, no text layer) does not satisfy the requirement — filers must run text recognition on it — though the source documents never use the literal word 'OCR.' _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.utcourts.gov/content/dam/howto/filing/efiling/district/docs/eFiling_FAQ-Attorneys.pdf)
    > Are all PDFs searchable? No. PDFs are "searchable" when you can search for words or data within the document. Most word processing applications like Word Perfect or MS Word allow you to convert your text document to a searchable PDF. When you scan a document, the scanner creates an image of the document. The image can be converted to a PDF file, but the result is only an image or picture of the document. An image-only PDF is not searchable.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Filename character/length restrictions on the uploaded PDF file itself — no official AOC document specifies a maximum filename length or disallowed characters for the file being uploaded. (The only documented character rules govern DATA ENTERED into web-form fields — party names, the 'Additional Docket Text'/document-title box — e.g. no punctuation other than hyphens, avoid special characters like §; these are data-entry rules, not filename rules, and were not reported as a constraint for that reason.), Bookmark or table-of-contents requirements — no AOC eFiling FAQ, guide, standards document, or training material (district or appellate) imposes any bookmark or TOC requirement on filed PDFs. (A bookmark rule could conceivably live inside a formal Rule of Appellate Procedure such as URAP 27, but that is a rule of procedure, not a portal/technical spec, and is out of scope per the assignment.), Exact numeric attachment/document count limit per submission or envelope — no official document states a maximum number of documents, exhibits, or attachments allowed in one eFiling submission. The only numeric submission-level cap found is unrelated: a single eFiling submission can collect at most 6 filing fees before the filer must contact the court or pay online separately.

---

## Vermont

- **E-filing system:** Odyssey File & Serve (OFS) — mid-rebrand to "eFile & Serve" (EFS), marketed as "eFileVT" (vendor: Tyler Technologies)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Vermont runs ONE mandatory, statewide e-filing system — this is not a county-by-county / fragmented model like California. Odyssey File & Serve (OFS), hosted and supported by Tyler Technologies, is used in all units and divisions of the Vermont Superior Court plus the Vermont Supreme Court, the Judicial Bureau, and the Environmental Division. As of 2025-2026 the Judiciary is transitioning the platform's branding from "Odyssey File & Serve (OFS)" to "eFile & Serve (EFS)" / "eFileVT" — both names currently refer to the same underlying Tyler-hosted system, with OFS remaining live during the cutover per the Judiciary's own announcement. All attorneys and public-agency personnel are required to e-file; self-represented litigants may opt in but then must continue e-filing for the rest of that case. Confirmed via the AOC's own "Vermont eFiling General Policy and Procedure Guide," the "Odyssey File and Serve FAQs" page, and the "Vermont Supreme Court eFiler Guide" (V1.1, July 2025) — all hosted at vtcourts.gov (formerly vermontjudiciary.org, which now 301-redirects to vtcourts.gov).
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.vtcourts.gov/sites/default/files/documents/VERMONT%20OFS%20Policy%20and%20Procedure%20GUIDE%206-26.pdf)
  > Both the AOC's general "Document Formatting Requirements" section (Policy and Procedure Guide) and the Supreme Court eFiler Guide's equivalent section address PDF requirements in some detail — generic PDF format required, scanned PDFs must be legible, fillable PDFs must be flattened before upload — but neither, nor the FAQ page, nor any other official guide found (Civil/Criminal/Probate/Judicial Bureau filer guides referenced from the same index) ever mentions PDF/A by name, in any direction (not required, not preferred, not warned against). Because the exact section of the manual that would logically state a PDF/A requirement was reviewed directly and is silent, this is coded as "silent" rather than "unverified."
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.vtcourts.gov/sites/default/files/documents/VERMONT%20OFS%20Policy%20and%20Procedure%20GUIDE%206-26.pdf)
  > No official Vermont e-filing guide reviewed (Policy and Procedure Guide, FAQ, Supreme Court eFiler Guide) discusses document metadata (author, revision history, hidden XMP data) or instructs filers to scrub/remove it before filing. The only related instruction found is the "flattening" requirement for form-fillable PDFs, which is about removing interactive form fields/embedded objects so the file becomes a static "flat" PDF — a formatting requirement, not a metadata-privacy instruction. Separately, the confidentiality section of the Policy Guide places the burden on filers to manually redact non-public information (e.g., SSNs) from the visible content and file an unredacted version separately as confidential, but this is a content-redaction rule under the Rules for Public Access to Court Records, not a metadata-scrubbing directive from the e-filing system itself.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size (per document and per envelope/submission)**: 35 MB maximum per individual document; 50 MB maximum per envelope (the bundle of documents filed together in one submission). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.vtcourts.gov/about-vermont-judiciary/electronic-access/electronic-filing/faqs)
    > The document size limit is 35 Megabytes and the envelope size limit is 50 Megabytes. If the document exceeds the size limit, you can compress the file before uploading to File and Serve.
  - **Accepted PDF version / file format requirements**: Every filed document must be a PDF. Documents must be 'flat' — form-fillable PDFs (including all posted court forms) must be flattened (printed to a PDF driver) before upload or the submission fails outright. Each individual document must be its own separate PDF — the portal rejects a filing if multiple documents were scanned/combined into one PDF — while a single multi-page document stays as one PDF. No specific PDF version number (e.g., 1.4/1.7/2.0) is specified anywhere in the official guidance. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.vtcourts.gov/sites/default/files/documents/VERMONT%20OFS%20Policy%20and%20Procedure%20GUIDE%206-26.pdf)
    > All electronically filed documents must be submitted in PDF format... Every individual document in a filing must be submitted as a separate PDF. Filings will not be accepted if multiple filed documents are scanned/uploaded together as one combined PDF. Multi-page documents should be submitted as one PDF. (Vermont eFiling General Policy and Procedure Guide); 'Filers must ensure that scanned PDF documents are viewable and legible and are in a "flat" format... When efiling a form-fillable PDF... you must first save it as a flat file. Otherwise, the filing will fail, and you will need to refile.' (Vermont Supreme Court eFiler Guide)
  - **Searchable-text / OCR requirement**: No OCR or machine-searchable-text mandate exists anywhere in the official guidance.
