The only quality bar stated for a scanned PDF is legibility/viewability — nothing requires the text layer itself to be searchable. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.vtcourts.gov/sites/default/files/documents/VERMONT%20OFS%20Policy%20and%20Procedure%20GUIDE%206-26.pdf)
    > Filers are responsible for ensuring that scanned PDF documents are viewable and legible after scanning.
  - **Filename character/length restrictions**: No rule was found governing the literal OS filename of the uploaded PDF. What IS restricted is the portal's own 'Filing Description' and 'Document Description' metadata text fields entered at upload time — each capped at 100 characters including spaces; going over throws a system error and can delay acceptance. Treat this as a description-field limit, not a filename limit. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.vtcourts.gov/about-vermont-judiciary/electronic-access/electronic-filing/faqs)
    > The Filing Description and Document Description can only be 100 characters in length including spaces. If the text is longer than 100 characters, it will cause an error in OFS and acceptance of the filing could be delayed.
  - **Bookmark or table-of-contents requirements**: Not required for any filing type. The Supreme Court filer guide mentions a table of contents only as an optional convenience when a filer chooses to compile multiple attachments into a single combined document; it is never mandated. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.vtcourts.gov/sites/default/files/documents/VERMONT-SUPREME-COURT-EFILER-GUIDE-July-2025.pdf)
    > Multi-page documents should be submitted as one PDF. Attachments to a motion may be compiled into one document with a table of contents.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Attachment/document count limit per envelope — no numeric ceiling was found anywhere; the guides only confirm multiple documents/filings may be bundled into one envelope and that the per-envelope system-use fee ($5.25 per the general FAQ guide / $14 per-case-per-party fee cited in the newer Supreme Court guide) is charged per envelope, not per document, with no stated maximum document count., Whether any restriction (character set, length) applies to the literal filename of the uploaded PDF file itself, as distinct from the in-portal 'Filing Description'/'Document Description' text fields (100-character cap) — no source addresses the OS-level filename specifically.

---

## Virginia

- **E-filing system:** Fragmented — no single statewide e-filing portal. Trial-level (circuit court) civil e-filing runs on two parallel, non-interoperable systems depending on which court you're filing in: (1) VJEFS — Virginia Judiciary E-Filing System, built and administered by the Office of the Executive Secretary (OES) of the Supreme Court of Virginia, live in a court-by-court rollout (73 participating circuit courts as of the current published User's Guide); and (2) eFileVA — Tyler Technologies' Odyssey File & Serve, used by circuit courts that run Tyler's case management system instead of participating in VJEFS (e.g., Virginia Beach, Rockingham, Williamsburg/James City, York-Poquoson). Separately, appellate filings (Supreme Court of Virginia and Court of Appeals of Virginia) go through a third, distinct system: VACES — Virginia Appellate Courts Electronic System. (vendor: VJEFS: in-house build for OES. eFileVA: Tyler Technologies (Odyssey File &amp; Serve). VACES: in-house build for OES/Supreme Court of Virginia.)
- **Statewide system:** no -- fragmented/county-by-county
- **Notes:** Virginia is a hybrid case, not a clean "one statewide system" (Florida/Texas) or "fully vendor-fragmented" (California) state. For circuit courts (where the vast majority of civil litigation is filed), a locality is on EITHER VJEFS OR eFileVA — never both — so the technical constraints an attorney faces literally depend on which courthouse they're filing in. VACES is a fully separate, mandatory system for the two appellate courts with its own (more detailed and stricter) technical rules. RaioPDF should treat these as three separate constraint profiles, not one. Caveat on document vintage: the VJEFS User's Guide is dated "Rev: 7/16" (July 2016) and the VJEFS Terms and Conditions/EULA is dated "Rev: 5/14" (May 2014), yet both are the current documents actively linked from the live vacourts.gov VJEFS page today — I could not find a newer revision, so this is the official current source despite its age, but the 10-year gap is worth an independent-review flag before treating the 10MB figure as certainly still accurate. I could not find an official (non-vendor) Virginia-court-hosted technical specification page for eFileVA/Tyler within the research budget — efileva.com and Tyler's own hosted pages are vendor marketing/product pages and were excluded per instructions, so eFileVA constraints are listed as a gap rather than guessed from Tyler's generic Odyssey documentation for other states.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.courts.state.va.us/static/online/vjefs/usersmanual.pdf)
  > Read in full: the VJEFS User's Guide, the VJEFS Terms and Conditions of Use (EULA), and the VACES Guidelines and User's Manual (Introduction, Opening Briefs, Appendices, All Other Pleadings sections). None of them mention "PDF/A" anywhere. VJEFS's only format language is "Adobe Reader® or equivalent software to view Portable Document Format (PDF) documents" and "VJEFS only accepts PDF documents up to 10MB" — generic PDF, no version/subset specified. VACES's only format language is "All electronically filed documents must be in PDF format and must be text searchable" — again generic PDF with a searchability requirement, no PDF/A specification, preference, or prohibition. No indication in any reviewed document of PDF/A causing encryption conflicts, form-field issues, or annotation/redaction stripping.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.courts.state.va.us/static/online/vjefs/usersmanual.pdf)
  > Same three documents reviewed in full (VJEFS User's Guide, VJEFS EULA, VACES Guidelines and User's Manual) contain no mention of document metadata at all — no requirement to include specific metadata fields, no instruction or recommendation to scrub/remove metadata before filing, and no indication that metadata-scrubbed files cause upload, acceptance, or display problems in either system.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Max file size per document — VJEFS (circuit court civil e-filing)**: 10 MB per PDF document _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.state.va.us/static/online/vjefs/usersmanual.pdf)
    > NOTE: VJEFS only accepts PDF documents up to 10MB.
  - **Accepted file format — VJEFS**: PDF only; no specific PDF version/subset specified _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.state.va.us/static/online/vjefs/usersmanual.pdf)
    > NOTE: VJEFS only accepts PDF documents.
  - **Max file size per document / per submission — VACES (appellate e-filing)**: 150 MB per PDF; documents exceeding that must be split into separate volumes. Up to 25 documents per submission. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://eapps.courts.state.va.us/help/robo/vaces/VACES.htm)
    > Document submissions exceeding 150 MB Portable Document File (PDF) size limit must be uploaded as separate volumes." ... "The system allows users to submit up to twenty-five documents with each submission.
  - **Searchable-text/OCR requirement — VACES (appellate e-filing)**: Required: all filed PDFs must be text-searchable; briefs may not be produced by scanning; appendices of paper-source documents must be run through OCR _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://eapps.courts.state.va.us/help/robo/vaces/VACES.htm)
    > All electronically filed documents must be in PDF format and must be text searchable." ... "The brief must not be created by using a scanner to produce the PDF file." ... "Appendices must be scanned with an Optical Character Recognition (OCR) feature.
  - **Searchable-text/OCR requirement — VJEFS (circuit court civil e-filing)**: Not required — no searchable-text or OCR mandate found in the VJEFS User's Guide or Terms and Conditions _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.state.va.us/static/online/vjefs/termsandconditions.pdf)
    > In addition to the above, the following are also required in order to file documents: ... Access to a scanner to create images of non-computerized documents, such as exhibits.
  - **Bookmark / table-of-contents requirement — VACES (appellate briefs and appendices)**: Required for briefs (cover page, Table of Contents, Table of Authorities, all entries — outline-format bookmarks) and appendices (bookmarked per Table of Contents heading); explicitly NOT required for other pleadings _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://eapps.courts.state.va.us/help/robo/vaces/VACES.htm)
    > The cover page, Table of Contents, Table of Authorities, and all entries therein must be bookmarked to the appropriate page. The bookmarks must be placed in an outline format." ... "Bookmarks and thumbnail page numbering are not required.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Filename character/length restrictions — not addressed anywhere in the VJEFS User's Guide, VJEFS Terms and Conditions (EULA), or VACES Guidelines and User's Manual; no official Virginia-court source found specifying filename constraints for any of the three systems., Bookmark/table-of-contents requirement for VJEFS (circuit-court civil e-filing) specifically — not addressed in the VJEFS User's Guide or EULA (VACES, the separate appellate system, does mandate bookmarks for briefs/appendices — see constraints array)., Attachment/document count limit for VJEFS (circuit-court civil e-filing) specifically — the User's Guide describes an open-ended 'Add More Exhibits' upload flow with no stated numeric cap; no official source found giving a maximum attachment/document count for VJEFS (VACES caps submissions at 25 documents — see constraints array)., All eight technical fields for eFileVA (Tyler Technologies Odyssey File & Serve), used by the subset of Virginia circuit courts that do not participate in VJEFS — no official, non-vendor Virginia-court-hosted technical specification page could be located within the research budget; efileva.com and Tyler-hosted pages are vendor product/marketing pages and were excluded per instructions rather than used as a substitute source.

---

## Washington State

- **E-filing system:** FRAGMENTED — no single statewide e-filing portal for trial courts. Three distinct systems identified: (1) Odyssey File &amp; Serve / "eFileWA" — the statewide-standardized system for Courts of Limited Jurisdiction (district/municipal courts, governed by the published CLJ-CMS Code &amp; Technical Standards) and also used by most Superior Courts that have adopted Tyler's Odyssey case management system; (2) Washington State Appellate Courts' Portal (ac.courts.wa.gov) — a separate, statewide system used only by the WA Supreme Court and the three divisions of the Court of Appeals; (3) King County Superior Court's own proprietary e-filing application, referred to on its own pages as the "KC Script Portal" / "E-Filing &amp; Case Access" — confirmed NOT to be eFileWA/Odyssey. King County District Court runs yet another county-specific e-filing resource page with its own stated limits. (vendor: Tyler Technologies (Odyssey File &amp; Serve) powers eFileWA for Courts of Limited Jurisdiction statewide and for most Superior Courts running Odyssey. The Washington State Appellate Courts' Portal's vendor is not identified in the official documentation found (appears to be an AOC-built portal integrated with ACORDS/JIS, historically Flash-based). King County Superior Court's "KC Script Portal" and King County District Court's e-filing application appear to be locally procured/operated, not Tyler Odyssey.)
- **Statewide system:** no -- fragmented/county-by-county
- **Notes:** Washington is a hybrid, not a single statewide portal (unlike Florida's ePortal) and not a fully county-fragmented free-for-all (unlike California). The state has standardized district/municipal court (CLJ) e-filing under eFileWA/Odyssey with a published statewide Code & Technical Standards document, and Superior Courts have largely (but not universally) folded into the same Odyssey/eFileWA platform as counties migrate onto Tyler's Odyssey case management system. King County — the state's largest county — is the clearest exception: its Superior Court runs its own separate e-filing application (the page calls it the "KC Script Portal"), and King County District Court likewise has its own e-filing resource page with its own stated limits, distinct from both eFileWA and the Superior Court system. The appellate courts (Supreme Court + Court of Appeals) run an entirely separate statewide portal. A firm using RaioPDF in Washington needs to know which of these three systems its target court actually uses — the technical constraints below differ system-to-system and are NOT interchangeable. A full county-by-county audit of which Superior Courts have or haven't migrated to Odyssey was outside this research's bounded scope (see gaps).
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.courts.wa.gov/subsite/cljcms/docs/CLJ-CMS%20eFile%20Code%20and%20Technical%20Standards.pdf)
  > None of the four official documents read (CLJ-CMS Code & Technical Standards for eFileWA; the WA Appellate Courts' Portal eFiling FAQ and Filing Instructions; King County's Superior Court "KC Script Portal" page; King County District Court's e-Filing Resources page) mentions PDF/A by name, in either a required, preferred, or prohibited sense — despite the CLJ-CMS document being unusually detailed about document formatting (9 numbered document standards). The closest adjacent signal is from the CLJ-CMS standard, which explicitly prohibits any "security or feature restrictions including password protection or encryption" and prohibits embedded multimedia/programming — a PDF/A file that happens to carry incompatible encryption or interactive form/JS elements could collide with that rule, but this is an inference, not a stated PDF/A policy. Separately, King County Superior Court's own page states its portal "is currently compatible with Adobe Acrobat 9 software" and instructs filers to set PDF-conversion tools to "version 9 or less" — an old PDF-version ceiling (Acrobat 9 = PDF 1.7 era, 2008) that could plausibly be friction-prone for some modern PDF/A-2 or PDF/A-3 conformance levels, but again the page never says so explicitly, so this cannot be reported as a stated PDF/A stance.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent
  > No official WA e-filing technical document found addresses embedded file metadata (author name, revision history, XMP/document-properties data) — neither requiring its inclusion, recommending its removal, nor flagging problems from removing it. The one Washington rule that is adjacent but distinct is GR 22, which requires attorneys to redact sensitive personal identifiers (SSNs, financial account numbers, driver's license numbers, a minor's date of birth) from the visible content of a filed document before filing — this is a content-redaction rule of court, not a technical metadata-scrubbing requirement of the e-filing system itself, so per the research brief it is noted here only as context and is not reported as a "metadata policy" constraint.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Max file size — eFileWA / Odyssey File & Serve (statewide CLJ-CMS standard; also used by most Superior Courts on Odyssey)**: 35 MB per document (hard cap; exceeding it produces an actual rejection) _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.wa.gov/subsite/cljcms/docs/CLJ-CMS%20eFile%20Code%20and%20Technical%20Standards.pdf)
    > Any eFiled document's size shall not exceed 35 megabytes (35 MB) in size, must be on 8.5 x 11 paper, and content should be appropriately rotated for viewing.
  - **Max file size — Washington State Appellate Courts' Portal (Supreme Court + Court of Appeals, statewide)**: 60 MB per file; 600 MB combined total per submission; no cap on number of documents _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://ac.courts.wa.gov/content/help/eFilingFAQs.pdf)
    > There is no limit to the number of documents you can file; however, there is a limit to the size of each document, and to the total size of all documents being uploaded. The combined size of all uploaded files cannot be more than 600 MB. There is also a 60 MB limit for the size of each file.
  - **Max file size — King County District Court e-filing (county-specific, distinct from eFileWA)**: 50 MB document size limit _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://districtcourt.kingcounty.gov/help/e-filing-resources)
    > 50 MB document size limit
  - **Accepted file format — eFileWA / Odyssey File & Serve (CLJ-CMS)**: PDF only; no other file types accepted; no specific PDF version number specified _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.wa.gov/subsite/cljcms/docs/CLJ-CMS%20eFile%20Code%20and%20Technical%20Standards.pdf)
    > Odyssey File & Serve accepts PDF documents only. All other file types will not be accepted.
  - **Accepted file format / PDF version — Washington State Appellate Courts' Portal**: PDF format required for all uploads _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://ac.courts.wa.gov/content/help/qsgFilingInstructions.pdf)
    > All files must be in PDF format and cannot exceed 60 MB.
  - **Accepted file format / PDF version — King County Superior Court ('KC Script Portal')**: PDF or TIFF; portal stated to be compatible only up to Adobe Acrobat 9-generation PDFs — filers told to set their scanner/PDF-conversion software to 'version 9 or less' _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://kingcounty.gov/en/dept/dja/courts-jails-legal-system/court-forms-document-filing/filing/e-filing)
    > The KC Script Portal is currently compatible with Adobe Acrobat 9 software... verify that your scanner or .pdf conversion software is set to version 9 or less.
  - **Searchable text / OCR requirement — eFileWA / Odyssey File & Serve (CLJ-CMS)**: Required for scanned documents: must be scanned at 300 DPI and made text-searchable via OCR; a non-searchable PDF is an enforced, named rejection reason _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.wa.gov/subsite/cljcms/docs/CLJ-CMS%20eFile%20Code%20and%20Technical%20Standards.pdf)
    > If a document needs to be scanned, the document must have a resolution of 300 DPI. Every document scanned should be made searchable using Optical Character Recognition (OCR) technology. [...] PDF document is not text searchable [listed as a Technical Rejection Code]
  - **Scan resolution guidance — King County District Court**: 200-300 DPI resolution recommended for scanned documents _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://districtcourt.kingcounty.gov/help/e-filing-resources)
    > 200-300 DPI resolution
  - **Filename character/length restrictions — eFileWA / Odyssey File & Serve (CLJ-CMS)**: No special characters (examples given: &, *, #, @); filename must not exceed 50 characters _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.wa.gov/subsite/cljcms/docs/CLJ-CMS%20eFile%20Code%20and%20Technical%20Standards.pdf)
    > The filename for the document shall not contain special characters (i.e. &,*,#,@) or exceed 50 characters.
  - **Filename restrictions — Washington State Appellate Courts' Portal**: No special characters; keep filenames short and simple (no specific numeric character cap stated) _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://ac.courts.wa.gov/content/help/qsgFilingInstructions.pdf)
    > Do not use special characters in the file names and keep the file names short and simple.
  - **Bookmark / table-of-contents requirement — eFileWA / Odyssey File & Serve (CLJ-CMS)**: Not required — and affirmatively restricted: the standard requires a PDF NOT be dependent on internal bookmarks for navigation/completeness, and bars embedding other documents inside a filed PDF _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.wa.gov/subsite/cljcms/docs/CLJ-CMS%20eFile%20Code%20and%20Technical%20Standards.pdf)
    > PDFs shall not have other documents embedded and not be dependent on bookmarks within the document.
  - **Attachment / document count limit — Washington State Appellate Courts' Portal**: No limit on the number of documents in one filing session; only the per-file (60MB) and total (600MB) size caps apply _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://ac.courts.wa.gov/content/help/eFilingFAQs.pdf)
    > There is no limit to the number of documents you can file; however, there is a limit to the size of each document, and to the total size of all documents being uploaded.
  - **One-document-per-PDF packaging rule — eFileWA / Odyssey File & Serve (CLJ-CMS)**: Each filed document must be submitted as its own individual PDF file (functions as a de facto attachment-packaging constraint distinct from a numeric cap) _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.wa.gov/subsite/cljcms/docs/CLJ-CMS%20eFile%20Code%20and%20Technical%20Standards.pdf)
    > Documents shall be filed as an individual PDF.
  - **Encryption / security-restriction prohibition (adjacent to the PDF/A safety question) — eFileWA / Odyssey File & Serve (CLJ-CMS)**: Prohibited: filed documents must be free of any password protection, encryption, or feature restriction that would block the court user from viewing the file; embedded multimedia/video/audio/programming is also prohibited _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courts.wa.gov/subsite/cljcms/docs/CLJ-CMS%20eFile%20Code%20and%20Technical%20Standards.pdf)
    > All eFiled documents shall be free of any security or feature restrictions including password protection or encryption that will prohibit the court user from viewing the document. Any eFiled document shall not contain any embedded multi-media video, audio, or programming.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Exact per-document and per-envelope file size limit for King County Superior Court's own 'KC Script Portal' — its official page describes PDF/TIFF format and an Adobe Acrobat 9 compatibility ceiling but does not state a numeric size cap; King County's more detailed 'E-Filing User Tips' PDF could not be fetched (blocked by a Cloudflare bot-challenge), so this could not be verified from a primary source., Attachment / document count limit for eFileWA / Odyssey File & Serve (CLJ-CMS) — the statewide Code & Technical Standards document does not state a numeric cap on the number of documents/attachments per filing (only the Appellate Courts' Portal explicitly states no limit)., Whether Washington's ~30 Superior Courts that use Odyssey follow the exact same CLJ-CMS Code & Technical Standards found here, or a parallel Superior-Court-specific standards document (references to a separate 'SC-CMS'/Odyssey Portal registration process were found, but no equivalent Superior-Court technical-standards PDF could be located within the bounded search effort)., A full county-by-county map of which Superior Courts run eFileWA/Odyssey versus a locally procured system (King County is confirmed as an exception; whether other counties also run their own separate systems was not exhaustively checked)., Bookmark/table-of-contents requirements for the Appellate Courts' Portal and for King County's systems — not addressed in any of the documents found (only the eFileWA/CLJ-CMS standard addresses bookmarks at all, and only to restrict reliance on them).

---

## West Virginia

- **E-filing system:** WV E-File (the "CourtPLUS Initiative") — the single statewide, mandatory e-filing/case-management portal for all Circuit and Family (trial) courts, live in all 55 counties as of July 15, 2024. NOTE: this is NOT the system used for appellate matters — see systemNotes. (vendor: Not disclosed in any official WV E-File/CourtPLUS documentation reviewed (the AOC brands it only as "CourtPLUS"/"WV E-File," no third-party vendor named). Separately, the appellate-court e-filing provider has been File & ServeXpress (FSX) since 2022, with an April 2025 courtswv.gov announcement of a new partnership with Tyler Technologies for a replacement appellate e-filing/public-access system — current live status as of this research (2026-07-02) is unconfirmed. See systemNotes and gaps.)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** West Virginia is NOT fragmented county-by-county like California. It runs ONE unified statewide e-filing/case-management portal for trial-level courts — "WV E-File," part of the "CourtPLUS Initiative" sponsored by the WV Supreme Court of Appeals — confirmed live in all 55 counties as of July 15, 2024 (courtswv.gov status page: "As of Monday, July 15, 2024, the CourtPLUS E-File system is live throughout the entire state of West Virginia."). This portal (efile.courtswva.com) handles civil and criminal filings in Circuit and Family Courts and is the system virtually all WV attorneys use day to day — it is the system this report focuses on.

However, WV DOES bifurcate by court level: appellate matters (Supreme Court of Appeals, Intermediate Court of Appeals, and the Mass Litigation Panel) file through a separate, differently-built system, historically File & ServeXpress (FSX) since July 1, 2022. A courtswv.gov post from April 2025 ("Supreme Court Partners with Tyler Technologies on New Appellate E-Filing and Public Access Systems") announced FSX being replaced by a Tyler Technologies system targeted for "late summer" 2025, but I could not confirm from an official primary source whether that cutover has actually completed, nor find that new system's technical specs, within this research pass — flagged as a gap rather than guessed. The technical constraints below (file size, page dimensions, attachment count) come from the trial-court WV E-File/CourtPLUS documentation only, not from either appellate system.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://efile.courtswva.com/Pages/Faq/Questions.aspx)
  > No official WV E-File/CourtPLUS source mentions PDF/A at all, in either direction. I reviewed the complete FAQ question index (every question title on the portal's FAQ page — none concern PDF/A, file conversion, or archival format), the official "Introduction to CourtPLUS, E-File & Vault" reference FAQ, and the step-by-step filing guides (e.g., "Steps to E-File a Supporting Document") — none reference PDF/A, encryption conflicts, form-field stripping, or any archival-format issue. Absence across this document set is the finding: PDF/A is neither required, preferred, nor flagged as problematic — it is simply never addressed.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://efile.courtswva.com/Pages/Faq/Questions.aspx)
  > Same document set as the PDF/A finding (full FAQ index, the Introduction FAQ reference document, and the step-by-step filing guides) contains no question or guidance addressing document metadata — no instruction to include particular metadata fields, no recommendation to scrub metadata before filing, and no warning that metadata-scrubbed files cause upload or processing problems. This is a genuine silence, not a confirmed "no requirement" statement from the AOC.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size (per document)**: 10 MB maximum per uploaded document in WV E-File; explicitly no limit on the number of documents in a filing. If a document exceeds 10 MB, the filer must compress it or split it into sequential parts (e.g., 'Memorandum of Law Part 1,' 'Part 2'). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courtswv.gov/sites/default/pubfilesmnt/2024-12/FAQ%20-%20Introduction%20to%20CourtPLUS%20E-File%20Vault.pdf)
    > Maximum upload file size: 10 MB, per document. *No limit on number of documents*
  - **Maximum file size — filer-facing guidance**: The portal's own FAQ restates the 10 MB single-document cap and instructs filers to compress or split oversized documents into numbered parts rather than upload one large file. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efile.courtswva.com/Pages/Faq/Answer.aspx?ID=f36de533-a791-44fa-bd2b-06ace1828453)
    > The file size limit is 10 MB to file a single document in E-File... If the document is over 10 MB, the document must be compressed or split into smaller sections.
  - **Accepted page dimensions / PDF format guidance**: Uploaded PDFs must not exceed standard Letter (8.5x11 in), Legal (8.5x14 in), or Tabloid (11x17 in) page dimensions; the same FAQ tells filers to check this via Adobe Reader's 'Document Properties' before uploading. No specific PDF spec/version number (e.g., PDF 1.4–2.0) is documented anywhere in the portal's official materials. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efile.courtswva.com/Pages/Faq/Answer.aspx?ID=f36de533-a791-44fa-bd2b-06ace1828453)
    > Documents cannot exceed 8.5 x 11 inches (letter), 8.5 x 14 inches (legal), or 11 x 17 inches (tabloid).
  - **Attachment / document count limit**: No cap on the number of documents that can be included in a single WV E-File case filing — only the per-document 10 MB size cap applies. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.courtswv.gov/sites/default/pubfilesmnt/2024-12/FAQ%20-%20Introduction%20to%20CourtPLUS%20E-File%20Vault.pdf)
    > *No limit on number of documents*

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Accepted PDF version/spec number (e.g., minimum or maximum PDF format version) — not documented in any official WV E-File/CourtPLUS FAQ or guide found; only page-dimension guidance was located., Searchable-text / OCR requirement — no official WV E-File/CourtPLUS source (FAQ index or guides) addresses whether uploaded PDFs must be text-searchable or OCR'd., Filename character/length restrictions — not documented in any official source reviewed., Bookmark or table-of-contents requirements for trial-court e-filings — not documented in official WV E-File/CourtPLUS materials (bookmark/TOC rules exist for appellate briefs under the Rules of Appellate Procedure, but that is a rule of court and explicitly out of scope for this technical-portal research)., Appellate-court e-filing system current status and technical specs — courtswv.gov announced in April 2025 that Tyler Technologies would replace File & ServeXpress for the Supreme Court of Appeals, Intermediate Court of Appeals, and Mass Litigation Panel, targeting a 'late summer 2025' launch; I could not confirm whether this transition is complete as of the research date (2026-07-02) or locate the resulting system's technical constraints within the research budget.

---

## Wisconsin

- **E-filing system:** Wisconsin Circuit Court eFiling (portal at efiling.wicourts.gov; informational hub at wicourts.gov/ecourts/efilecircuit) (vendor: Built and operated in-house by the Wisconsin Court System / Consolidated Court Automation Programs (CCAP) — not a third-party commercial vendor platform (confirmed NOT Tyler Odyssey; distinct from states like TX/IL/IN/GA/OR that run on Tyler's Odyssey File & Serve))
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Wisconsin has ONE statewide, mandatory e-filing system for circuit (trial) courts — not a fragmented county-by-county model like California. It runs under Wis. Stat. 801.18 and Supreme Court Petitions 14-03 and 20-07 (see the "Rules & requirements" page). A separate portal, Appellate Court eFiling, exists for the Court of Appeals/Supreme Court and has its own (thinner) documentation; I focused on Circuit Court eFiling since that's the day-to-day trial-court system attorneys use. Primary hub pages consulted: wicourts.gov/ecourts/efilecircuit/tech.htm (rules & requirements), .../faq.htm (FAQ), and the Zendesk-hosted eFile Support knowledge base (efilinghelp.zendesk.com) that wicourts.gov's own doc links now redirect to.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.wicourts.gov/ecourts/efilecircuit/tech.htm)
  > No occurrence of "PDF/A" anywhere on wicourts.gov or its eFile Support knowledge base (checked the Rules & Requirements page, the FAQ, the file-prep guide, and a site-restricted search for the literal string "PDF/A"). The system's only stated format rule is submission "in PDF format" (or .docx when a court official is expected to edit the document) — no PDF conformance level, version number, or PDF/A requirement is specified anywhere in the official documentation.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** recommended -- [source](https://www.wicourts.gov/ecourts/efilecircuit/faq.htm)
  > The official FAQ raises metadata unprompted and frames scrubbing as an available privacy safeguard, not a requirement: &quot;Both acceptable document formats (.pdf and .docx) may contain metadata such as authors, comments, versions, hidden text, and/or other personal information. If this metadata exists on your filed document, it is viewable by others with access to that document. It is possible to 'scrub' this metadata before submitting it to the eFiling system.&quot; No language requires scrubbing, and no language warns that scrubbed files cause problems.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size (per document)**: 50 MB per document. No separate/distinguishable envelope- or submission-level cap was found in official documentation — only the per-document limit is stated. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.wicourts.gov/ecourts/efilecircuit/tech.htm)
    > Documents larger than 50 MB must be split into smaller files before uploading them to the eFiling Website.
  - **Accepted file format / PDF version**: PDF is the default required format for e-filed documents. Microsoft Word 2007+ (.docx) is accepted ONLY for documents/forms a court official is expected to edit further. No specific PDF version number (e.g., 1.7, 2.0) is specified. Maximum page size is 12"x18". Active content — JavaScript, macros, document security (i.e., encryption/password protection), and digital signatures — must be omitted from the file. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.wicourts.gov/ecourts/efilecircuit/tech.htm)
    > All documents should be submitted in PDF format unless they require editing by a court official... Omit all JavaScript, macros, document security, and digital signatures (active content).
  - **Searchable text / OCR requirement**: Not required. Text-searchable PDFs are recommended when feasible, but the system explicitly accepts non-searchable (e.g., scanned) PDFs — no OCR pass is mandated before filing. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.wicourts.gov/ecourts/efilecircuit/faq.htm)
    > Although it is not required, we do recommend that when possible, you provide text-searchable PDFs so that other parties on your case can easily access information by searching for keywords and phrases... If you are unable to provide a text-searchable version of your PDF... a non-searchable PDF is sufficient.
  - **Bookmarks / table of contents**: Not required for Circuit Court eFiling — no official page states bookmarks or a TOC are mandatory for any filing type. The only related official guidance found is instructional (not a requirement) and scoped to the separate Appellate Court eFiling system: it explains how to add Word-generated bookmarks to a brief or appendix, with a caution that printing-to-PDF (rather than 'Save As PDF') strips the bookmarks. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://efilinghelp.zendesk.com/hc/en-us/articles/25580840936973-Appellate-court-eFiling-Adding-bookmarks-and-links-to-a-brief-or-appendix)
    > This article explains how to use Microsoft Word 2010 or later to add bookmarks... Do not use the Print menu to create the PDF, as the bookmarks will not be retained in the resulting PDF.
  - **Document formatting margins (adjacent technical constraint)**: Every e-filed document needs a blank 1/2-inch top margin on every page reserved for the court's applied header/stamp; documents requiring a court official's electronic signature need an additional blank 3-inch top margin on page 1 specifically. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.wicourts.gov/ecourts/efilecircuit/tech.htm)
    > a blank 1/2" top margin ... Documents needing official signatures must include a blank 3" top margin on page 1 plus the standard 1/2" on subsequent pages.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Filename character/length restrictions — no official wicourts.gov or eFile-Support-KB page states a character set or length limit for uploaded filenames; a widely-repeated '25 character' figure traces to Tyler Odyssey File & Serve documentation for OTHER states, not to Wisconsin's (custom-built, non-Odyssey) system, so it was excluded rather than reported as a Wisconsin fact., Attachment/document count limit per envelope or per case filing — no official source states a maximum number of documents or attachments per submission. One county's own supplementary PDF guide (Manitowoc County) advises filing each document separately rather than combining them into one PDF, but that is county-issued guidance, not a statewide AOC technical specification, so it was not included as a constraint., Whether there is a distinct maximum size for the total envelope/submission (as opposed to the confirmed 50 MB per-document limit) — not addressed in any official page found.

---

## Wyoming

- **E-filing system:** Electronic Filing System (EFS) hosted by File &amp; ServeXpress (FSX) — used by all Wyoming trial courts (District, Circuit, and Chancery Courts). The Wyoming Supreme Court (appellate level) runs a SEPARATE, distinct portal called the Appellate C-Track and Electronic Filing Portal (CTEF) — not FSX. (vendor: File &amp; ServeXpress (FSX) — confirmed as the state-selected, single vendor for all Wyoming trial-court eFiling (District/Circuit/Chancery). The Supreme Court's CTEF portal's underlying vendor is not identified in its manual (appears to be a Journal Technologies/"C-Track" branded system, separate from FSX) — not independently confirmed.)
- **Statewide system:** yes
- **Notes:** Wyoming is NOT county-fragmented like California — there is one statewide e-filing vendor (File & ServeXpress) for all trial courts (District, Circuit, Chancery) across all counties, governed by a single statewide rule set ("Wyoming Rules for Electronic Filing and Service," effective April 2025, amended through Jan 2026; Rule 1(b)(2) explicitly forbids any individual trial court from adopting its own local eFiling rules). eFiling through this system became mandatory for Wyoming-licensed attorneys as of October 1, 2024 (confirmed via secondary source; not independently re-verified against a primary source in this pass). HOWEVER, the system is bifurcated by court level, not by county: the Wyoming Supreme Court (appeals) runs its own separate portal, CTEF (Appellate C-Track and Electronic Filing Portal, v1.0, published Feb 2026), which is a distinct system with its own manual, its own case-number format (S-##-#### / D-##-####), and — notably — almost none of the granular technical format specifications (file size caps, header-space rules, format conversion rules) that the trial-court Rules/FSX manual spell out. All the concrete technical constraints below (file size, format, searchable text) come from the trial-court EFS/FSX documentation, which is what the overwhelming majority of Wyoming attorney filings go through. Treat the CTEF/Supreme Court portal as a separate, thinner-documented system if RaioPDF ever needs appellate-specific behavior. Also notable: proposed orders must be filed as editable Microsoft Word (.docx), NOT PDF, except proposed stipulated orders which may be PDF — a case where the system actively disfavors PDF for a specific document type.
- **PDF/A stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.wyocourts.gov/app/uploads/2025/01/WY-Electronic-Filing-Service-Rules-Eff.-Jan-2026.pdf)
  > PDF/A is never mentioned in any of the three primary documents reviewed: the Wyoming Rules for Electronic Filing and Service (Rule 8, "Format requirements" — the section that would logically address it), the FSX "Wyoming eFiling Manual for Attorneys" (Rev. 11.2025), or the Wyoming Supreme Court's CTEF Manual (v1.0, Feb 2026). The rules require conversion to plain ".pdf" and define ".pdf" simply as "Portable Document Format, a proprietary file format developed by Adobe Systems, Inc." with no archival-subset (PDF/A) requirement, preference, or prohibition, and no warning about PDF/A causing encryption, form-field, or redaction/annotation problems.
- **Metadata-scrub stance:** silent -- [source](https://www.wyocourts.gov/app/uploads/2025/01/WY-Electronic-Filing-Service-Rules-Eff.-Jan-2026.pdf)
  > No mention of document metadata (author, company, tracked-changes, embedded properties) — as a requirement to include, a recommendation to remove, or a warning about metadata-scrubbed files causing problems — appears anywhere in the Wyoming Rules for Electronic Filing and Service, the FSX Attorney eFiling Manual, or the Supreme Court CTEF Manual. The rules do address confidentiality (Rule 10, "Privacy protections and access restrictions"), but only via visible-content redaction and portal-level "Restricted" labeling in the Document Title / Note-to-Clerk fields — never via file metadata.

**Constraints found:**
  - **Maximum file size — per document**: 150 megabytes (MB) per eFiled document. Oversized documents must be split into multiple files, each ≤150MB, tagged in the 'Note to Clerk' field (e.g., 'Motion for Summary Judgment, part 1 of 2') and linked via the EFS's main/supporting 'electronic stapling' function. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.wyocourts.gov/app/uploads/2025/01/WY-Electronic-Filing-Service-Rules-Eff.-Jan-2026.pdf)
    > The size of any eFiled document must not exceed 150 megabytes. A document that exceeds the size limit must be broken down and submitted as separate files that do not exceed 150 megabytes.
  - **Maximum file size — per transaction/envelope**: The FSX Attorney Manual states the entire transaction (all documents filed together) must also not exceed 150MB total — i.e., the envelope-wide cap is the same 150MB figure, not an additive multiple of the per-document cap. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.fileandservexpress.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/WY-eFiling-Manual-for-Attorneys_Rev-11.2025-1-1.pdf)
    > Each document must adhere to a file size limit of 150 megabytes (MB). Multiple documents can be filed at the same time, as long as the entire transaction does not exceed the limit of 150MB.
  - **Accepted PDF version / file format requirements**: PDF (defined simply as Adobe's Portable Document Format, with no version number specified) is the required end-state format for filed documents. The FSX upload tool itself accepts a broader set of formats at intake — DOC, DOCX, TXT, RTF, PDF, GIF, TIF, TIFF, BMP, JPG, JPEG — but a document that is not an attachment/exhibit must not be embedded inside another PDF, and PROPOSED ORDERS are the opposite of the general rule: they must be filed as editable Microsoft Word (not PDF), except proposed stipulated orders (signed by parties), which may be PDF. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.wyocourts.gov/app/uploads/2025/01/WY-Electronic-Filing-Service-Rules-Eff.-Jan-2026.pdf)
    > '.pdf' means Portable Document Format, a proprietary file format developed by Adobe Systems, Inc. ... Except as set forth in subsection (b)(4), proposed orders filed for the consideration of the presiding judge shall be filed in an editable Microsoft Word document format. ... Proposed stipulated orders, which are signed by the parties, may be filed in .pdf format.
  - **Searchable text / OCR requirement**: Not mandatory — only a soft preference. Filers are told to convert natively to PDF rather than scan, 'when feasible,' specifically to preserve searchable text, but scanning a document (producing a non-searchable image-only PDF) is not prohibited and no OCR step is mandated. _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.wyocourts.gov/app/uploads/2025/01/WY-Electronic-Filing-Service-Rules-Eff.-Jan-2026.pdf)
    > When feasible, an eFiled document should be directly converted to .pdf rather than scanned to make the document searchable.
  - **Character limits on FSX portal metadata/title fields (distinct from the uploaded file's own filename)**: FSX enforces hard character caps on several data-entry fields tied to a filing (the system blocks further typing once the limit is hit): Document Title = 250 characters; Case Name/caption = 200 characters; Organization Name = 100 characters; Party First Name = 30; Party Middle Name = 20; Party Last Name = 55. No published restriction was found on the name of the underlying computer file being uploaded (see gaps). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.fileandservexpress.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/11/WY-eFiling-Manual-for-Attorneys_Rev-11.2025-1-1.pdf)
    > FSX imposes character limits on certain information fields. The following fields are subject to these predefined constraints: Case Name (or case caption) = 200 characters, Document Title = 250 characters, Organization Name = 100, Party First Name = 30 characters, Party Middle Name = 20 characters, Party Last Name = 55 characters. The system prevents additional characters from being entered once the limit is reached.
  - **Document formatting requirements (adjacent context, not one of the 8 requested fields but load-bearing for PDF prep)**: Before conversion to PDF, each document must be 8½" x 11" (attachments/appendices resized to match), use a font no smaller than 12-point, be clearly legible, and leave a blank header space of at least 3 inches from the top of the first page for the court's file stamp/judge's banner (court reporters filing transcripts are exempt from the header rule). _(needs-review)_ -- [source](https://www.wyocourts.gov/app/uploads/2025/01/WY-Electronic-Filing-Service-Rules-Eff.-Jan-2026.pdf)
    > Filers must leave a blank header that extends at least 3-inches from the top of the first page of each eFiled document for use by the EFS and clerk. ... Before conversion to .pdf, each document must: (A) Be 8 ½" by 11" in its original form... (B) Have a font of not less than 12-point; and (C) Be clearly legible.

**Gaps (no reliable source found):** Bookmark or table-of-contents requirements for eFiled PDFs — no mention found in the Rules, the FSX Attorney Manual, or the Supreme Court CTEF Manual, Explicit numeric attachment/document-count limit per filing or transaction — only an aggregate 150MB size cap was found (Rule 8(a)(2); FSX Manual p.15); no count-based limit is stated, Character/length or special-character restrictions on the name of the actual uploaded computer file itself (as opposed to the portal's internal 'Document Title' data-entry field, which does have a stated 250-character cap) — not addressed in any source reviewed, Specific PDF version/specification number (e.g., PDF 1.4, 1.7, ISO 32000) accepted by the FSX system — sources require '.pdf' generically with no version specified
